when you say she's a programmer , she did do some , but the real thing is to have said the future is going to be much , much more than this .	當你說她是程式設計師時 , 她會做一些事 , 但真正的目的是要說未來會遠遠超過這個 。
now , a hundred years later , this guy comes along , alan turing , and in 1936 , and invents the computer all over again .	一百年後 , 這個傢伙出現了 , 艾倫•圖靈 , 1936年 , 再次發明了電腦 。
now , of course , babbage's machine was entirely mechanical .	當然 , 巴貝奇的機器完全機械化 。
turing's machine was entirely theoretical .	土耳其的機器完全是理論的 。
both of these guys were coming from a mathematical perspective , but turing told us something very important .	兩位都來自數學的觀點 , 但圖靈告訴我們很重要的東西 。
he laid down the mathematical foundations for computer science , and said , " it doesn't matter how you make a computer . "	他為電腦科學奠定了數學基礎 , 說: 「 不論你如何製作電腦 , 都不重要 。 」
it doesn't matter if your computer's mechanical , like babbage's was , or electronic , like computers are today , or perhaps in the future , cells , or , again , mechanical again , once we get into nanotechnology .	不管是電腦的機械裝置 , 像是babbage , 或電子裝置 , 像是現今的電腦 , 或是未來的細胞 , 或者 , 細胞 , 或者 , 再一次 , 一旦我們進入奈米科技 。
we could go back to babbage's machine and just make it tiny . all those things are computers .	我們可以回到babbage的機器 , 讓它變得很小 , 所有的東西都是電腦 。
there is in a sense a computing essence .	有一種計算的本質 。
this is called the church–turing thesis .	這就是所謂的教會論文 。
and so suddenly , you get this link where you say this thing babbage had built really was a computer .	所以 , 突然間 , 你看到了這個連結 , 你說這個巴貝奇建造出來的東西 , 其實是一台電腦 。
in fact , it was capable of doing everything we do today with computers , only really slowly .	事實上 , 它能夠做到我們今天用電腦做的每一件事 , 只有很慢 。
to give you an idea of how slowly , it had about 1k of memory .	給你一個概念 , 它有大約1k的記憶 。
it used punch cards , which were being fed in , and it ran about 10 , 000 times slower the first zx81 .	它用打孔卡 , 被餵食 , 它跑的速度大約是第一zx81的一萬倍 。
it did have a ram pack .	它的確有一包 。
you could add on a lot of extra memory if you wanted to .	如果你想要的話 , 你可以加上額外的記憶 。
so , where does that bring us today ?	所以 , 今天這會帶給我們什麼 ?
so there are plans .	所以有計畫 。
over in swindon , the science museum archives , there are hundreds of plans and thousands of pages of notes written by charles babbage about this analytical engine .	在瑞士 , 科學博物館檔案 , 有數百個計劃和數以千計的筆記 , 由查爾斯•巴貝奇所寫 , 關於這個分析引擎 。
one of those is a set of plans that we call plan 28 , and that is also the name of a charity that i started with doron swade , who was the curator of computing at the science museum , and also the person who drove the project to build a difference engine , and our plan is to build it .	其中一個是我們稱之為28計劃的一組計劃 , 這也是我從doronswaade開始的名字 , 他是科學博物館裡的計算計劃的策展人 , 也是推動這個計劃來建造一個不同的引擎的人 , 我們的計劃就是建造它 。
here in south kensington , we will build the analytical engine .	在南肯辛頓這裡 , 我們會建造分析引擎 。
the project has a number of parts to it .	這個專案計畫有許多部分 。
one was the scanning of babbage's archive .	第一是巴貝奇的檔案掃描 。
that's been done . the second is now the study of all of those plans to determine what to build .	這已經完成了 。 第二個是研究這些計畫的目的 , 來決定要建造什麼 。
the third part is a computer simulation of that machine , and the last part is to physically build it at the science museum .	第三部分是模擬這台機器的電腦模擬 , 最後一部分是將它在科學博物館裡建造 。
when it's built , you'll finally be able to understand how a computer works , because rather than having a tiny chip in front of you , you've got to look at this humongous thing and say , " ah , i see the memory operating , i see the cpu operating , i hear it operating . i probably smell it operating . "	當它被建造出來時 , 你終於能夠了解電腦如何運作 , 因為與其在你面前有一小塊晶片 , 你必須看出這個龐大的東西 , 然後說: 「 啊 , 我看到記憶運作 , 我看到cpu在運作 , 我聽見它運作 。 我可能聞到它 。 」
but in between that we're going to do a simulation .	但在這之間 , 我們要做一個模擬 。
babbage himself wrote , he said , as soon as the analytical engine exists , it will surely guide the future course of science .	巴貝奇自己寫信 , 他說 , 只要分析引擎就存在 , 它一定會引導未來的科學課程 。
of course , he never built it , because he was always fiddling with new plans , but when it did get built , of course , in the 1940s , everything changed .	當然 , 他從來沒有打造過它 , 因為他一直在打造新計畫 , 但在1940年代 , 一切都變了 。
now , i'll just give you a little taste of what it looks like in motion with a video which shows just one part of the cpu mechanism working .	現在 , 我會給你們一些味道 , 關於它在動作上看起來的樣子 , 影片上顯示了cpu的運作的一部分 。
so this is just three sets of cogs , and it's going to add . this is the adding mechanism in action , so you imagine this gigantic machine .	這僅僅是三組的認知 , 它會增加 。 這是加入的機制 , 所以你想像一下這個巨大的機器 。
so , give me five years .	所以 , 給我五年 。
before the 2030s happen , we'll have it .	在2030年代發生之前 , 我們就有了 。
thank you very much .	非常謝謝各位 。
in this imagefilled talk , yann arthusbertrand displays his three most recent projects on humanity and our habitat stunning aerial photographs in his series " the earth from above , " personal interviews from around the globe featured in his web project " 6 billion others , " and his soontobereleased movie , " home , " which documents human impact on the environment through breathtaking video .	在這個影像填寫的演說中 , 雅恩•亞斯伯特展現了他三個最近的專案 , 關於人類和我們的棲息地 , 在他的系列中 , 《天空攝影》中 , 《天空攝影》 , 來自世界各地的個人訪問 , 他的網頁寫到 「 六十億人 」 , 他的電影 , 「 家 」 , 透過呼吸影片 , 來記錄人類對環境的影響 。
art , climate change , environment , film , future , humanity , media , photography	藝術、氣候變遷、環境、電影、未來、人性、媒體、攝影 。
yann arthusbertrand captures fragile earth in wideangle	雅恩•阿姆斯堡捕捉到廣泛角落的脆弱地球 , 在廣泛角度上捕捉了地球 。
i have a big impact on the planet to travel here by plane .	我對地球有很大的影響 , 可以透過飛機來到這裡 。
i emitted , in the atmosphere , nine tons of co2 ; that is the weight of two elephants .	我在大氣中排放出九噸的二氧化碳 , 那是兩隻大象的重量 。
i came here to speak about ecology , and i emitted as much co2 as a frenchman in one year .	我來這裡談談生態學 , 一年內我將二氧化碳排放為法國人 。
so what do i have to do ?	所以 , 我該怎麼做 ?
i have to kill a frenchman when i come back at home ?	當我回家時 , 我得要殺掉法國人嗎 ?
i have to do my carbon offset in another way , like i do every time .	我必須以另一種方式抵抗碳 , 就像我每次都要做 。
in fact my work is to show our impact on our planet .	事實上 , 我的作品是要展現我們對地球的影響 。
i'm going to show you some examples of the last pictures i've done in the last year .	我要給你們看一些例子 , 說明我去年拍攝的最後一張照片 。
alberta sand oil , a lot of pollution .	亞伯塔沙油 , 很多污染 。
you know the problem ; we don't want to believe what we know .	你知道問題 , 我們不想相信我們所知道的 。
in alberta people work nonstop , 24 hours by seven to extract as much oil as they can .	在亞伯達人的工作中 , 有24小時 , 七個小時的時間來抽取石油 。
we know about the end of oil .	我們知道石油的末端 。
oil sand is not a longterm solution .	石油沙不是長期的解決方案 。
but we use three times more oil than we find every year .	但我們用的石油比每年多三倍 。
we don't want to believe what we know .	我們不想相信我們所知道的 。
coral reef in new caledonia .	新加利亞的珊瑚礁 。
100 percent of the coral may be wiped out before 2050 because of global warming .	百分之百的珊瑚可能因為全球暖化而消滅 。
and you know how coral are very sensitive to temperature , and are very important for the biodiversity of the sea .	你知道珊瑚對溫度非常敏感 , 對海洋生物多樣性非常重要 。
north pole . i've done this picture last summer .	北極 , 去年夏天我拍了這張照片 。
it was impossible to do this picture 15 years ago .	15年前拍攝這張照片是不可能的
now there is a new way open between atlantic and pacific .	大西洋和太平洋之間有一種新的開放方式 。
the thickness of the arctic decreased more than 40 percent since 1960 .	北極的厚度從1960年開始減少了超過40% 。
there is a new face of kilimanjaro without ice .	kilijaro沒有冰 , 出現了新的面孔 。
it lost 80 percent of its ice .	它損失了80%的冰 。
according to scientists , in 100 years all the mountain glacier will be gone .	根據科學家的說法 , 在100年內 , 所有的山冰會消失 。
glaciers are very important for the life on earth .	冰河對地球生命很重要 。
like al gore told you , two billion people live on the water from the glacier of himalaya .	就像高爾說過的 , 二十億人住在喜馬拉雅冰河的水上 。
return of fish men .	回到魚販 。
one fifth of human kind depend on fish to live .	人類有五分之一依賴魚類生存 。
today now 70 percent of the fish stock are overexploited .	現今 , 70%的魚類存量過度開發 。
according to fao , if we don't change our system of fishing the main sea resources will be gone in 2050 .	根據fao的說法 , 如果我們不改變我們的捕魚系統 , 2050年的主要海洋資源會消失 。
we don't want to believe what we know .	我們不想相信我們所知道的 。
the beautiful picture , by [unclear] in africa .	美麗的照片是非洲的 。
one human of six have not enough to eat in the world .	六個人中就有一個人沒有足夠的食物可以在世界上吃 。
one billion people have not enough to eat .	十億人沒有足夠的食物可吃 。
in africa , corn is one of the main foods in many places .	在非洲 , 玉米是許多地方的主要食物之一 。
here in america , 90 percent of the corn cultivated is used to feed animals or to do oil .	在美國 , 90%的玉米耕種被用來餵養動物或做油 。
palm tree plantation in borneo .	在婆羅的棕櫚樹種植園 。
every year we lose 50 thousand square miles in deforestation .	每年我們損失了五萬平方英哩的森林砍伐 。
refugee camp in darfur .	達佛的難民營 。
today we have 20 million refugees in the world .	現今 , 世界上有兩千萬難民 。
according to the u . n . , we speak about 250 million refugees in 2050 .	根據聯合國 , 我們在2050年談了2億5千萬難民 。
i always show my pictures in the street .	我總是在街上展示我的照片 。

12th man: if i was to go back to iraq and speak to the people , i'd have to bow down and kiss their feet .	第十二個男人:如果我要回到伊拉克 , 和人民說話 , 我就得把他們的腳降低 。
just as that woman tried to kiss my feet when we were taking her sons .	正如那個女人試圖親吻我兒子時的腳 。
and i feel humbled by their strength .	他們的力量讓我感到謙卑 。
and i will forever feel a need to make reparations to iraq .	我永遠覺得需要對伊拉克作出聲明 。
second woman: dad , mom , i grew up .	第二個女人:爸爸 , 我長大了 。

at the moment , my family is very poor , my life here in shenzhen is just about showing myself that i can earn more and to let my parents stay and have something to live on .	此刻 , 我的家人非常貧窮 , 我生活在深圳 , 只是為了向自己展示 , 我能多賺點錢 , 讓我的父母能留下來 , 活下去 。

now i am going to speak to you about my movie .	現在我要跟你們談談我的電影 。
for the last three years , i was shooting the earth for the movie .	過去三年 , 我為這部電影拍攝地球 。
the name of the movie is " home " " maison . "	這部電影的名字是 「 家 」 。
it is about the state of the planet .	它和地球的狀態有關 。
it's a fantastic story of life on the earth .	這是地球上生命的奇妙故事 。

video: this earth is four and a half billion years old .	影片:地球是四十五億年的歷史 。
these plants , several hundred million years old .	這些植物 , 幾億年前 。
and we humans have been walking upright for only 200 thousand years .	我們人類直立行走了20萬年 。
we've managed to adapt , and have conquered the whole planet .	我們已經成功適應了 , 並且征服了整個地球 。
for generations , we've been raising our children , not unlike millions of other species living beside us .	世代以來 , 我們一直在養育我們的孩子 , 而不是其他數百萬種生活在我們身邊 。
for the past 30 years i've been closely watching the earth and its dwellers from high up in the sky .	過去30年來 , 我親眼目睹地球和它在天空中從高空而來 。
our life is tied to the wellbeing of our planet .	我們的生命與地球的幸福有關 。
we depend on water , forests , deserts , oceans .	我們依賴水、森林、沙漠、海洋 。
fishing , breeding , farming are still the world's foremost human occupations .	捕魚、繁殖 , 農業仍然是世界上最重要的人類職業 。
and what binds us together is far greater than what divides us .	把我們的結合在一起遠遠比我們分裂的更大 。
we all share the same need for the earth's gifts the same wish to rise above ourselves , and become better .	我們都對地球的禮物有同樣的需求 , 希望能在我們自己上升 , 變得更好 。
and yet we carry on raising walls to keep us apart .	然而 , 我們仍然在養育牆壁來讓我們分裂 。
today our greatest battle is to protect the natural offerings of our planet .	現今 , 我們最大的戰役是要保護地球的自然提供 。
in less than 50 years we've altered it more thoroughly than in the entire history of mankind .	在短短的五十年內 , 我們徹底改變了它 , 遠遠超過人類的整個歷史 。
half of the world's forests have vanished .	世界一半的森林消失了 。
water resources are running low .	水資源的消耗量低 。
intensive farming is depleting soils .	密集農業正在耗盡土壤 。
our energy sources are not sustainable .	我們的能源不是永續的 。
the climate is changing .	氣候正在改變 。
we are endangering ourselves .	我們在危害我們自己 。
we're only trying to improve our lives .	我們只想改善我們的生活 。
but the wealth gaps are growing wider .	但財富差距越來越大 。
we haven't yet understood that we're going at a much faster pace than the planet can sustain .	我們還沒有了解到 , 我們的速度比地球還快得多 。
we know that solutions are available today .	我們知道今天的解決方案是可行的 。
we all have the power to change this trend for the better .	我們都有能力改變這種趨勢 , 讓它變得更好 。
so what are we waiting for ?	所以 , 我們還在等什麼 ?

in this accessible talk from tedxboston , richard resnick shows how cheap and fast genome sequencing is about to turn health care upside down .	在這場tedxboston的演講中 , 理查德•雷尼克的演講顯示 , 基因序列的便宜和快速基因序列將會減少健康照護 。
dna , biotech , health care , science , technology	dna、生物科技、醫療保健、科學、科技、技術、技術、基因、
richard resnick: welcome to the genomic revolution	理查德•雷尼克:歡迎來到基因革命 。
ladies and gentlemen , i present to you the human genome .	各位先生女士 , 我向你們展示人類基因組 。
chromosome one , top left .	染色體一 , 左上角 。
bottom right are the sex chromosomes .	右下方是性染色體 。
women have two copies of that big x chromosome ; men have the x and , of course , that small copy of the y .	女性有兩份大的x染色體 ; 男性有x , 當然 , y的複製品 。
sorry boys , but it's just a tiny little thing that makes you different .	抱歉 , 男孩 , 但這只是一件小事 , 讓你變得不一樣 。
so if you zoom in on this genome , then what you see , of course , is this double helix structure the code of life spelled out with these four biochemical letters , or we call them bases , right: a , c , g and t .	所以如果你放大這個基因組 , 那麼你會看到的是這雙螺旋結構 , 生命的密碼和這四個生物化學字母拼湊出來 , 或者我們稱它們為基礎 , 即a , c , g和t 。
how many are there in the human genome ? three billion .	人類基因組中有多少 ? 三十億 。
is that a big number ?	這是個很大的數字嗎 ?
well , everybody can throw around big numbers .	嗯 , 每個人都可以隨意丟出大數字 。
but in fact , if i were to place one base on each pixel of this 1280 by 800 resolution screen , we would need 3 , 000 screens to take a look at the genome .	但事實上 , 如果我把每一塊像素放在1280年到800次的解析度螢幕上 , 我們需要3000個螢幕來觀察基因組 。
so it's really quite big .	所以這真的很大 。
and perhaps because of its size , a group of people all , by the way , with y chromosomes decided they would want to sequence it .	或許是因為它的大小 , 一群人 , 順便一提 , y染色體決定要將它定序 。
and so 15 years , actually , and about four billion dollars later , the genome was sequenced and published .	所以 , 15年後 , 大約40億美金後 , 基因組序列和出版 。
in 2003 , the final version was published , and they keep working on it .	在2003年 , 最後的版本被發表 , 他們繼續努力 。
that was all done on a machine that looks like this .	全部的機器看起來就像這樣 。
it costs about a dollar for each base a very slow way of doing it .	每一鹼基要花一塊錢 , 都要花很慢的方式來做這件事 。
well folks , i'm here to tell you that the world has completely changed and none of you know about it .	各位 , 我來這裡要告訴各位 , 世界已經完全改變了 , 沒有人知道 。
so now what we do is we take a genome , we make maybe 50 copies of it , we cut all those copies up into little 50base reads , and then we sequence them , massively parallel .	我們現在做的是將一個基因組做成50個複製 , 我們把所有複製成50個大片 , 然後我們將它們定序 , 大量平行 。
and then we bring that into software , and we reassemble it and we tell you what the story is .	然後我們將它帶入軟體中 , 然後重新組合它 , 告訴你們故事是什麼 。
and so just to give you a picture of what this looks like , the human genome project: 3 gigabases , right .	給你們看一張圖片 , 人類基因組計畫:3gabases , 沒錯 。
one run on one of these machines: 200 gigabases in a week .	一台機器在其中一台:一週200個gbabes 。
and that 200 is going to change to 600 this summer , and there's no sign of this pace slowing .	今年夏天將改變到6000年 , 這種速度沒有跡象 。
so the price of a base , to sequence a base , has fallen 100 million times .	所以基地的價格下降了一億倍 。
that's the equivalent of you filling up your car with gas in 1998 , waiting until 2011 , and now you can drive to jupiter and back twice .	這等同於你在1998年裝滿氣體 , 等到2011年 , 現在你就可以開木星兩次 。
world population , pc placements , the archive of all the medical literature , moore's law , the old way of sequencing , and here's all the new stuff .	世界人口、pc地點、所有醫療文獻的檔案、摩爾定律、舊的方式 , 以及新的東西 。
guys , this is a log scale ; you don't typically see lines that go up like that .	各位 , 這是登革規模 ; 通常你不會看到那樣的線條 。
so the worldwide capacity to sequence human genomes is something like 50 , 000 to 100 , 000 human genomes this year .	所以 , 全球定序人類基因組的能力 , 今年大約是五萬到十萬人基因組 。
and we know this based on the machines that are being placed .	我們都知道 , 基於被安置的機器 。
this is expected to double , triple or maybe quadruple year over year for the foreseeable future .	預期會有兩倍、三倍 , 或可能是一年多的四倍 , 預見的未來 。
in fact , there's one lab in particular that represents 20 percent of all that capacity .	事實上 , 有一間特別的實驗室 , 代表所有這些能力的20% 。
it's called the beijing genomics institute .	它叫做 「 北京基因組學 」 。
the chinese are absolutely winning this race to the new moon , by the way .	順帶一提 , 中國絕對贏得了這個競賽 。
what does this mean for medicine ?	這對醫學有什麼意義 ?
so a woman is age 37 .	所以一個女人37歲 。
she presents with stage 2 estrogen receptorpositive breast cancer .	她有第二階段的雌激素接受乳癌 。
she is treated with surgery , chemotherapy and radiation .	她被手術、化療和輻射治療 。
two years later , she comes back with stage three c ovarian cancer .	兩年後 , 她得了三階段的卵巢癌 。
unfortunately , treated again with surgery and chemotherapy .	不幸的是 , 再次接受手術和化療 。
she comes back three years later at age 42 with more ovarian cancer , more chemotherapy .	三歲後 , 她回到42歲 , 有更多卵巢癌 , 更多的化療 。
six months later , she comes back with acute myeloid leukemia .	六個月後 , 她帶著急性骨髓的白血病回來 。
she goes into respiratory failure and dies eight days later .	她進入呼吸道失敗 , 八天後死亡 。
so first , the way in which this woman was treated , in as little as 10 years , will look like bloodletting .	首先 , 這個女人被治療的方式 , 只要十年 , 就會看起來像血液一樣 。
and it's because of people like my colleague , rick wilson , at the genome institute at washington university , who decided to take a look at this woman postmortem .	因為像我這樣的同事rickwilson , 在華盛頓大學的基因組研究所 , 他決定看這位婦女後期 。
and he sequenced , he took skin cells , healthy skin , and cancerous bone marrow , and he sequenced the whole genomes of both of them in a couple of weeks , no big deal .	他定序、皮膚細胞、健康皮膚、癌症骨髓 , 並在幾個星期內進行完整的基因組 , 沒有什麼大不了的 。
and then he compared those two genomes in software , and what he found , among other things , was a deletion , a 2 , 000base deletion across three billion bases in a particular gene called tp53 .	接著 , 他將這兩種基因組的軟體做比較 , 他發現在其他情況中 , 是一個耗損 , 一個在三十億個鹼基的基因 , 叫做tp53 。
if you have this deleterious mutation in this gene , you're 90 percent likely to get cancer in your life .	如果你在這個基因中有這種全面的突變 , 你的生命中有90%可能罹患癌症 。
so unfortunately , this doesn't help this woman , but it does have severe , profound if you will , implications to her family .	不幸的是 , 這並不能幫助這位女士 , 但這對她的家人來說是很嚴重的 , 深刻的影響 。
i mean , if they have the same mutation , and they get this genetic test , and they understand it , then they can go and get regular screens , and they can catch cancer early and potentially live a significantly longer life .	我的意思是 , 如果他們有相同的突變 , 他們得到了這個基因測試 , 並且他們了解了 , 那麼他們就可以定期的檢查 , 然後他們可以早期發現癌症 , 可能更長壽 。
let me introduce you now to the beery twins , diagnosed with cerebral palsy at the age of two .	現在讓我向你們介紹啤酒雙胞胎 , 診斷出兩歲的腦麻 。
their mom is a very brave woman who didn't believe that the symptoms weren't matching up , and through some heroic efforts and a lot of internet searching , she was able to convince the medical community that , in fact , they had something else .	她們的母親是個非常勇敢的女人 , 她不相信症狀並不符合 , 透過一些英雄式的努力和許多網路搜尋 , 她能夠說服醫學界 , 事實上 , 她們有別的東西 。
what they had was doparesponsive dystonia .	他們的做法是 「 反對障礙症 」 。
and so they were given ldopa , and their symptoms did improve , but they weren't totally asymptomatic .	所以他們得到了對比 , 他們的症狀確實改善了 , 但他們並不完全是症狀 。
turns out the gentleman in this picture is a guy named joe beery , who was lucky enough to be the cio of a company called life technologies .	結果是這張照片裡的男士喬依•貝瑞 , 他很幸運地成為一家叫做生命科技公司的協會 。
they're one of the two companies that makes these massive whole genome sequencing tools .	他們是製造這些大量基因組定序工具的公司之一 。
and so what he did was he got his kids sequenced .	所以他做的是讓他的孩子進行基因序列 。
and what they found was a series of mutations in a gene called spr , which is responsible for producing serotonin , among other things .	他們發現的是一系列的突變 , 叫做spr , 負責產生血清素的基因 。
so on top of ldopa , they gave these kids a serotonin precursor drug , and they're effectively normal now .	所以 , 除了對象之外 , 他們會給這些孩子一種血清素先驅藥 , 現在他們很正常 。
guys , this would never have happened without whole genome sequencing .	各位 , 沒有完整的基因組定序永遠不會發生這種事 。

today it's $10 , 000 . next year it's $1 , 000 .	今天是一萬美金 。 明年是一千美金 。
the year after it's $100 , give or take a year .	一百美金後的一年 , 或花一年 。
that's how fast this is moving .	這就快轉了 。
so here's little nick likes batman and squirt guns .	尼克喜歡蝙蝠俠和松鼠槍 。
and it turns out nick shows up at the children's hospital with this distended belly like a famine victim .	結果發現 , 尼克在兒童醫院裡 , 帶著這種漸進的肚子 , 像是饑荒受害者 。
and it's not that he's not eating , it's that when he eats , his intestine basically opens up and feces spill out into his gut .	並不是說他不吃東西 , 而是當他吃東西的時候 , 他的腸子基本上會打開來餵食 , 流進他的腸子裡 。
so a hundred surgeries later , he looks at his mom and says , " mom , please pray for me . i'm in so much pain . "	一百次手術後 , 他看著他的媽媽 , 說: 「 媽 , 為我禱告 , 我很痛苦 。 」
his pediatrician happens to have a background in clinical genetics and he has no idea what's going on , but he says , " let's get this kid's genome sequenced . "	他的小兒科醫生剛好在臨床遺傳學的背景 , 他完全不知道發生什麼事 , 但他說: 「 讓我們把這個孩子的基因序列拿出來 。 」
and what they find is a singlepoint mutation in a gene responsible for controlling programmed cell death .	他們發現 , 一個單點突變的基因負責控制細胞死亡 。
so the theory is that he's having some immunological reaction to what's going on to the food essentially , and that's a natural reaction , which causes some programmed cell death .	所以 , 理論是 , 他對於食物本質上 , 會有一些免疫反應 , 而這是一種自然的反應 , 造成了一些植入細胞死亡 。

daniel kraft demos his marrow miner a new device that quickly harvests lifesaving bone marrow with minimal pain to the donor . he emphasizes that the adult stem cells found in bone marrow can be used to treat many terminal conditions , from parkinson's to heart disease .	丹尼爾克拉夫示範他的骨髓開採了一個新的裝置 , 快速收集骨髓 , 讓捐贈者的最小疼痛 。 他強調骨髓中發現的成人幹細胞可以被用來治療許多終端疾病 , 從帕金森氏症到心臟疾病 。

we're sending his marrow across the country to save the life of a child with leukemia .	我們把他的骨髓送到全國 , 來拯救白血病孩童的性命 。
so actually how do we harvest this bone marrow ?	所以 , 我們要如何收集這塊骨髓 ?
well we have a whole o . r . team , general anesthesia , nurses , and another doctor across from me .	我們有一整個o.r , 一般麻醉 , 護士 , 還有另一位從我身上穿過的醫生 。
bob's on the table , and we take this sort of small needle , you know , not too big .	巴布在桌子上 , 我們拿著這種小針頭 , 你知道的 , 不是太大 。
and the way we do this is we basically place this through the soft tissue , and kind of punch it into the hard bone , into the tuchus that's a technical term and aspirate about 10 mls of bone marrow out , each time , with a syringe .	我們的做法基本上是把這些東西放到軟組織中 , 把它注入硬骨 , 進入黏液 , 一種技術術語 , 每次都會用針筒吸出大約10隻骨髓 。
and hand it off to the nurse . she squirts it into a tin .	把它交給護士 , 她將它安排成一小塊 。
hands it back to me . and we do that again and again .	把它交給我 。 我們再一次這樣做 。
about 200 times usually .	通常是兩百次 。
and by the end of this my arm is sore , i've got a callus on my hand , let alone bob , whose rear end looks something more like this , like swiss cheese .	在這張手臂的結尾 , 我手上有一通電話 , 更不用說鮑伯 , 他的屁股看起來比較像這樣 , 像是瑞士起士 。
so i'm thinking , you know , this procedure hasn't changed in about 40 years .	所以我在想 , 你知道的 , 這個手術在40年內並沒有改變 。
and there is probably a better way to do this .	這樣做可能有更好的方法 。
so i thought of a minimally invasive approach , and a new device that we call the marrow miner .	所以我想了一個極少入侵的方法 , 一個我們稱之為骨髓礦工的新裝置 。
and the marrow miner , the way it works is shown here .	骨髓礦工 , 它的運作方式在這裡 。
our standard seethrough patient .	我們的標準視診病人 。
instead of entering the bone dozens of times , we enter just once , into the front of the hip or the back of the hip .	與其進入骨頭數十次 , 我們只需要進入一次 , 進入髖骨的前面 , 或髖骨的後面 。
and we have a flexible , powered catheter with a special wire loop tip that stays inside the crunchy part of the marrow and follows the contours of the hip , as it moves around .	我們有彈性、有動力的導管 , 帶有特殊的電線圈圈 , 留在粗糙的骨髓中 , 跟著臀部的轉動 。
so it enables you to very rapidly aspirate , or suck out , rich bone marrow very quickly through one hole .	所以這使得你能迅速地迅速地呼吸 , 或吸收豐富的骨髓 , 迅速地穿過一個洞 。
we can do multiple passes through that same entry .	我們可以通過同樣的入口來傳遞多個訊息 。
and , so , very quickly , bob can just get one puncture , local anesthesia , and do this harvest as an outpatient .	所以 , 很快地 , 鮑勃可以刺穿當地的麻醉 , 做這種收穫是非耐心的 。
so i did a few prototypes . i got a small little grant at stanford .	所以我做了一些原型 。 我在史丹佛得到了一個小小的補助 。
and played around with this a little bit .	再玩一下這個 。
and our team members developed this technology .	我們的團隊成員開發了這項技術 。
and eventually we got two large animals , and pig studies .	最終 , 我們得到兩個大型動物 , 豬研究 。
and we found , to our surprise , that we not only got bone marrow out , but we got 10 times the stem cell activity in the marrow from the marrow miner , compared to the normal device .	我們發現 , 驚訝的是 , 我們不僅得到了骨髓 , 我們還得到了10倍來自骨髓礦工的幹細胞活動 , 相較於正常的裝置 。
this device was just fda approved in the last year .	這個裝置在去年被核准了 。
here is a live patient . you can see it following the flexible curves around .	這裡是現場病人 。 你可以看到它遵循靈活的曲線 。
there will be two passes here , in the same patient , from the same hole .	在同一個病人身上 , 會有兩條路過來 , 來自同一個洞 。
this was done under local anesthesia , as an outpatient .	這在地方麻醉劑的作用下 , 作為一種外在的力量 。
and we got , again , about three to six times more stem cells than the standard approach done on the same patient .	同樣的 , 我們得到的幹細胞 , 比同一個病人的標準方法要多三到六倍 。
so why should you care ? bone marrow is a very rich source of adult stem cells .	為什麼要在乎呢 ? 骨髓是成人幹細胞的豐富來源 。
you all know about embryonic stem cells .	你們都知道胚胎幹細胞 。
they've got great potential but haven't yet entered clinical trials .	他們有很大的潛力 , 但還沒有進入臨床試驗 。
adult stem cells are throughout our body , including the bloodforming stem cells in our bone marrow , which we've been using as a form of stemcell therapy for over 40 years .	成人幹細胞在我們的身體中 , 包括骨髓內的血液幹細胞 , 我們一直以來使用這種幹細胞療法 , 治療超過40年 。
in the last decade there's been an explosion of use of bone marrow stem cells to treat the patient's other diseases such as heart disease , vascular disease , orthopedics , tissue engineering , even in neurology to treat parkinson's and diabetes .	在過去十年 , 骨髓幹細胞被大量使用 , 來治療病人的其他疾病 , 比如心臟疾病、血管疾病、組織工程 , 甚至神經學治療帕金森氏症和糖尿病 。
we've just come out , we're commercializing , this year , generation 2 . 0 of the marrow miner .	我們剛剛出來 , 今年我們將商業化 , 第2.0個骨髓礦工 。
the hope is that this gets more stem cells out , which translates to better outcomes .	希望這能得到更多幹細胞 , 轉化成更好的結果 。
it may encourage more people to sign up to be potential livesaving bone marrow donors .	它可能會鼓勵更多人登記成為拯救生命的骨髓捐助者 。
it may even enable you to bank your own marrow stem cells , when you're younger and healthier , to use in the future should you need it .	它甚至可能讓你可以銀行你自己的骨髓幹細胞 , 當你年輕時 , 用在未來 , 你應該需要它 。
and ultimately and here's a picture of our bone marrow transplant survivors , who come together for a reunion each year at stanford .	最終 , 這張照片是我們的骨髓移植者 , 每年在史丹佛 , 他們聚集在一起 。
hopefully this technology will let us have more of these survivors in the future .	希望這項技術能讓我們未來有更多這些倖存者 。
physicist and surfer garrett lisi presents a controversial new model of the universe that just maybe answers all the big questions . if nothing else , it's the most beautiful 8dimensional model of elementary particles and forces you've ever seen .	物理學家和衝浪者蓋瑞特•里西提出一個有爭議的宇宙模型 , 可能只能回答所有大問題 。 如果沒有 , 它是你所見過最美麗的八度空間粒子和力的模型 。
physics , science , technology	物理 , 科學 , 科技 , 科技 ,
garrett lisi on his theory of everything	garretlisi在他所有事物理論的理論上 , 解釋了他的想法 。
whoa , dude . check out those killer equations . sweet .	哇 , 老兄 。 看看那些殺手方程式 。 甜 。
actually , for the next 18 minutes i'm going to do the best i can to describe the beauty of particle physics without equations .	事實上 , 接下來的18分鐘 , 我要盡我所能地描述粒子物理的美麗 , 沒有方程式 。
it turns out there's a lot we can learn from coral .	結果發現 , 珊瑚有很多我們可以學到的 。
coral is a very beautiful and unusual animal .	珊瑚是非常美麗且不尋常的動物 。
each coral head consists of thousand of individual polyps .	每個珊瑚的頭都是成千上萬個珊瑚蟲 。
these polyps are continually budding and branching into genetically identical neighbors .	這些複合劑持續在基因上分支成一模一樣的鄰居 。
if we imagine this to be a hyperintelligent coral , we can single out an individual and ask him a reasonable question .	如果我們想像這是個高智能的珊瑚 , 我們可以把一個人分開 , 問他一個合理的問題 。
we can ask how exactly he got to be in this particular location compared to his neighbors if it was just chance , or destiny , or what ?	我們可以問他在這個特定的地點與他的鄰居相比 , 如果他有機會 , 或是命運 , 或什麼 ?
now , after admonishing us for turning the temperature up too high , he would tell us that our question was completely stupid .	在我們把溫度調高之後 , 他會告訴我們 , 我們的問題很愚蠢 。
these corals can be quite kind of mean , you see , and i have surfing scars to prove that .	這些珊瑚可以是很有意義的 , 你看 , 我有衝浪的傷疤來證明這一點 。
but this polyp would continue and tell us that his neighbors were quite clearly identical copies of him .	但這複製劑會繼續告訴我們 , 他的鄰居非常相同 。
that he was in all these other locations as well , but experiencing them as separate individuals .	他也在其它的地點裡 , 但他們是獨立的個體 。
for a coral , branching into different copies is the most natural thing in the world .	對珊瑚而言 , 分支成不同的複製品是世上最自然的東西 。
unlike us , a hyperintelligent coral would be uniquely prepared to understand quantum mechanics .	不像我們 , 超級智能珊瑚會特別準備好了解量子力學 。
the mathematics of quantum mechanics very accurately describes how our universe works .	量子力學的數學準確描述宇宙是如何運作的 。
and it tells us our reality is continually branching into different possibilities , just like a coral .	它告訴我們 , 我們的現實不斷地擴展到不同的可能性 , 就像珊瑚一樣 。
it's a weird thing for us humans to wrap our minds around , since we only ever get to experience one possibility .	這對我們人類來說是一件很奇怪的事 , 因為我們只能體驗到一個可能性 。
this quantum weirdness was first described by erwin schrödinger and his cat .	這種量子的奇蹟首先被赫丁格和他的貓所描述 。
the cat likes this version better .	貓比較喜歡這個版本 。
in this setup , schrödinger is in a box with a radioactive sample that , by the laws of quantum mechanics , branches into a state in which it is radiated and a state in which it is not .	在這組合中 , 薛丁格是一個放射性樣本 , 由量子力學定律 , 分布到一個放射性狀態 , 而不是放射的狀態 。
in the branch in which the sample radiates , it sets off a trigger that releases poison and schrödinger is dead .	在這個分支中 , 樣本放射 , 釋放毒藥和薛丁格的觸發器已經死了 。
but in the other branch of reality , he remains alive .	但在現實中 , 他仍然活著 。
these realities are experienced separately by each individual .	每個個體都能感受到這些現實 。
as far as either can tell , the other one doesn't exist .	儘管如此 , 另一隻也不存在 。
this seems weird to us , because each of us only experiences an individual existence , and we don't get to see other branches .	這對我們來說很怪異 , 因為我們每一個人只經歷一個個體存在 , 而我們卻沒有看到其他的分支 。
it's as if each of us , like schrödinger here , are a kind of coral branching into different possibilities .	就像我們每個人 , 像這裡的薛丁格 , 都是一種珊瑚分裂成不同的可能性 。
the mathematics of quantum mechanics tells us this is how the world works at tiny scales .	量子力學的數學告訴我們這個世界是如此的微小 。
it can be summed up in a single sentence: everything that can happen , does .	它可以用單一句話來總結:所有可能發生的事 , 都會發生 。
but this does not mean everything happens .	但這並不意味著一切都會發生 。
the rest of physics is about describing what can happen and what can't .	其餘的物理則是描述可能發生的事以及無法發生的事 。
what physics tells us is that everything comes down to geometry and the interactions of elementary particles .	物理告訴我們 , 所有東西都來到幾何和基本粒子的互動 。
and things can happen only if these interactions are perfectly balanced .	唯有這些互動是完全平衡的 。
now i'll go ahead and describe how we know about these particles , what they are and how this balance works .	現在我要描述我們對這些粒子的了解 , 它們是什麼 , 以及平衡的運作方式 。
in this machine , a beam of protons and antiprotons are accelerated to near the speed of light and brought together in a collision , producing a burst of pure energy .	在這台機器中 , 質子和反質子的光線加速到接近光速的速度 , 並聚集在一起 , 產生出純能量 。
this energy is immediately converted into a spray of subatomic particles , with detectors and computers used to figure out their properties .	這種能量馬上被轉換成亞原子粒子的噴霧 , 用偵測器和電腦來找出它們的特性 。
this enormous machine the large hadron collider at cern in geneva has a circumference of 17 miles and , when it's operating , draws five times as much power as the city of monterey .	這個巨大的機器 , 大型強子對撞機──在日內瓦的cern有一個十七英哩的圈子 , 當它在運作時 , 會把五倍的能量畫成蒙特瑞市 。
we can't predict specifically what particles will be produced in any individual collision .	我們不能明確地預測粒子在任何個體碰撞中會產生什麼 。
quantum mechanics tells us all possibilities are realized .	量子力學告訴我們所有可能性都已經實現了 。
but physics does tell us what particles can be produced .	但物理告訴我們 , 粒子可以產生什麼 。
these particles must have just as much mass and energy as is carried in by the proton and antiproton .	這些粒子需要的質量和能量就等於質子和反質子 。
any particles more massive than this energy limit aren't produced , and remain invisible to us .	任何比這個能量限制更大的粒子都不會產生 , 對我們來說仍然是看不見的 。
this is why this new particle accelerator is so exciting .	這就是為什麼這個新粒子加速器如此令人興奮 。
it's going to push this energy limit seven times beyond what's ever been done before , so we're going to get to see some new particles very soon .	它會把這個能源限制推到前七次之外 , 所以我們很快就會看到一些新的粒子 。
but before talking about what we might see , let me describe the particles we already know of .	但在談到我們所見到的之前 , 讓我描述一下我們已經知道的粒子 。
there's a whole zoo of subatomic particles .	有一大堆亞原子粒子 。
most of us are familiar with electrons .	我們大部分人都熟悉電子 。
a lot of people in this room make a good living pushing them around .	這間房間裡有很多人 , 讓它們能過得很好 。
but the electron also has a neutral partner called the neutrino , with no electric charge and a very tiny mass .	但電子也有中性夥伴 , 稱為中子 , 沒有電荷和極小的質量 。
in contrast , the upanddown quarks have very large masses , and combine in threes to make the protons and neutrons inside atoms .	相對的 , 上游的夸克有很大的質量 , 三分之三的組合 , 使原子和中子內部的質子和中子 。
all of these matter particles come in left and righthanded varieties , and have antiparticle partners that carry opposite charges .	所有這些物質粒子都出現在左邊和右邊的品種 , 帶著相反載荷的抗粒子 。
these familiar particles also have less familiar second and third generations , which have the same charges as the first but have much higher masses .	這些熟悉的粒子也比較不熟悉的第二代和第三代 , 相同的載荷和第一代相同 , 質量較高 。
these matter particles all interact with the various force particles .	這些物質粒子都和各種粒子互動 。
the electromagnetic force interacts with electrically charged matter via particles called photons .	電磁力通過稱為光子的粒子 , 與電荷相互作用 。
there is also a very weak force called , rather unimaginatively , the weak force , that interacts only with lefthanded matter .	還有一種非常微弱的力量 , 叫做 , 非常不可思議 , 弱力 , 只與左撇子相互作用 。
the strong force acts between quarks which carry a different kind of charge , called color charge , and come in three different varieties: red , green and blue .	夸克的強力作用 , 帶有不同的載荷 , 稱為色荷 , 三種不同的顏色:紅、綠、藍 。
you can blame murray gellmann for these names they're his fault .	你可以怪罪murraygellmann的名字 , 他們是他的錯 。
finally , there's the force of gravity , which interacts with matter via its mass and spin .	最後 , 有引力的力量 , 會透過它的質量和旋轉來與物質互動 。
the most important thing to understand here is that there's a different kind of charge associated with each of these forces .	最重要的是 , 每一種力量都有不同的指控 。
these four different forces interact with matter according to the corresponding charges that each particle has .	這四種不同的力量 , 根據每個粒子所擁有的對應電荷來互動 。
a particle that hasn't been seen yet , but we're pretty sure exists , is the higgs particle , which gives masses to all these other particles .	尚未見過的粒子 , 但我們很確定存在 , 就是希格斯粒子 , 給予所有其他粒子質量 。
the main purpose of the large hadron collider is to see this higgs particle , and we're almost certain it will .	大型強子對撞機的主要目的是看到希格斯粒子 , 我們幾乎確定它會 。
but the greatest mystery is what else we might see .	但最偉大的奧秘是我們看到的 。
and i'm going to show you one beautiful possibility towards the end of this talk .	接下來我要給你們看一個美麗的可能性 , 關於這場演說的尾聲 。
now , if we count up all these different particles using their various spins and charges , there are 226 .	如果我們用不同的旋轉和載荷來計算這些不同的粒子 , 就會有226個 。
that's a lot of particles to keep track of .	有很多粒子可以追蹤 。
and it seems strange that nature would have so many elementary particles .	很奇怪 , 大自然會有這麼多基本粒子 。
but if we plot them out according to their charges , some beautiful patterns emerge .	但如果我們根據他們的指控來繪製它們 , 有些美麗的圖案就會出現 。
the most familiar charge is electric charge .	最熟悉的電荷是電荷 。
electrons have an electric charge , a negative one , and quarks have electric charges in thirds .	電子有負電 , 負電 , 夸克有三分之三的電荷 。
so when two up quarks and a down quark are combined to make a proton , it has a total electric charge of plus one .	所以當兩個夸克和一個下夸克結合成一個質子時 , 它總有一連串的電荷 。
these particles also have antiparticles , which have opposite charges .	這些粒子也有反粒子 , 也有相反的載荷 。
now , it turns out the electric charge is actually a combination of two other charges: hypercharge and weak charge .	結果發現 , 電荷實際上是兩個載荷結合:超載和弱載荷 。
if we spread out the hypercharge and weak charge and plot the charges of particles in this twodimensional charge space , the electric charge is where these particles sit along the vertical direction .	如果我們散播超電荷和弱電荷 , 將粒子的載荷畫在這個二維電荷空間中 , 電荷就是這些粒子在垂直方向的位置 。
the electromagnetic and weak forces interact with matter according to their hypercharge and weak charge , which make this pattern .	電磁力和弱力相互作用 , 根據超電荷和弱電荷 , 產生這個模式 。
this is called the unified electroweak model , and it was put together back in 1967 .	這被稱為 「 傾斜模式 」 , 它在1967年被整合起來 。
the reason most of us are only familiar with electric charge and not both of these is because of the higgs particle .	我們大部分人只熟悉電荷 , 而不是兩者都是因為希格斯粒子 。
the higgs , over here on the left , has a large mass and breaks the symmetry of this electroweak pattern .	左邊的希格斯有一個很大的質量 , 打破了電子模式的對稱性 。
it makes the weak force very weak by giving the weak particles a large mass .	它讓弱力變得很弱 , 是因為給予弱粒子一個大質量 。
since this massive higgs sits along the horizontal direction in this diagram , the photons of electromagnetism remain massless and interact with electric charge along the vertical direction in this charge space .	由於這個巨大的希格斯粒位置沿著地平線的方向 , 電磁學的光子仍然是無質量的 , 和電荷在這個載荷空間的垂直方向相互作用 。
so the electromagnetic and weak forces are described by this pattern of particle charges in twodimensional space .	所以電磁力和弱力被二維空間中的粒子載荷所描述 。
we can include the strong force by spreading out its two charge directions and plotting the charges of the force particles in quarks along these directions .	我們可以把強力納入其中 , 藉由推廣兩個載荷方向 , 將引力粒子標記在這些方向上 。
the charges of all known particles can be plotted in a fourdimensional charge space , and projected down to two dimensions like this so we can see them .	所有已知粒子的載荷可以在四維空間中繪製 , 並投射到像這樣的二維空間 , 這樣我們就能看見它們 。
whenever particles interact , nature keeps things in a perfect balance along all four of these charge directions .	每當粒子互動時 , 大自然就會在四個載荷方向保持平衡 。
if a particle and an antiparticle collide , it creates a burst of energy and a total charge of zero in all four charge directions .	如果粒子和抗粒子碰撞 , 它會造成四個載荷方向的能量和全部載荷 。
at this point , anything can be created as long as it has the same energy and maintains a total charge of zero .	此時此刻 , 任何東西都可以產生相同的能量 , 並維持無數的載荷 。
for example , this weak force particle and its antiparticle can be created in a collision .	例如 , 這種弱力粒子和它的抗粒子可以在碰撞中產生 。
in further interactions , the charges must always balance .	在進一步的互動中 , 載荷必須保持平衡 。
one of the weak particles could decay into an electron and an antineutrino , and these three still add to zero total charge .	其中一個微弱的粒子可以腐爛成一個電子 , 和一個反中子 , 這三個粒子仍然加入零電荷 。
nature always keeps a perfect balance .	自然總是保持完美的平衡 。
so these patterns of charges are not just pretty .	所以這些載荷的模式並不只是漂亮的 。
they tell us what interactions are allowed to happen .	他們告訴我們什麼樣的互動被允許發生 。
and we can rotate this charge space in four dimensions to get a better look at the strong interaction , which has this nice hexagonal symmetry .	我們可以在四維空間中旋轉這個載荷空間 , 來更好地觀察強烈的互動 , 強烈的交互作用 , 這種六角形的對稱性 。
in a strong interaction , a strong force particle , such as this one , interacts with a colored quark , such as this green one , to give a quark with a different color charge this red one .	在強烈的互動中 , 強力粒子 , 比如這個 , 和有顏色的夸克互動 , 比如這個綠色的夸克 , 給一個夸克 , 上面有不同的顏色 , 上面有紅色的 。
and strong interactions are happening millions of times each second in every atom of our bodies , holding the atomic nuclei together .	強烈的互動每秒都在發生數百萬次 , 發生在我們身體的每個原子裡 , 把原子核結合在一起 。
but these four charges corresponding to three forces are not the end of the story .	但這四種載荷相對應三種力量並不是故事的終結 。
we can also include two more charges corresponding to the gravitational force .	我們也可以把兩個載荷與重力相對應 。
when we include these , each matter particle has two different spin charges , spinup and spindown .	當我們包含這些粒子時 , 每一個粒子都有兩個不同的旋轉載荷、旋轉和旋轉 。
so they all split , and give a nice pattern in sixdimensional charge space .	所以他們都分開了 , 在六度載荷空間中給一個好的圖案 。
we can rotate this pattern in six dimensions , and see that it's quite pretty .	我們可以在六維空間中旋轉這個模式 , 看它很漂亮 。
right now , this pattern matches our best current knowledge of how nature is built at the tiny scales of these elementary particles .	目前 , 這種模式符合我們目前最好的知識 , 了解大自然是如何在這些基本粒子的微小尺度上建造出來的 。
this is what we know for certain .	這就是我們所知道的 。
some of these particles are at the very limit of what we've been able to reach with experiments .	有些粒子是極限的 , 是我們實驗所能達到的 。
from this pattern , we already know the particle physics of these tiny scales . the way the universe works with these tiny scales is very beautiful .	從這個模式 , 我們已經知道這些微小的尺度的粒子物理 。 宇宙和這些微小的尺度是非常美麗的 。
but now i'm going to discuss some new and old ideas about things we don't know yet .	現在我要談談一些我們還不知道的新舊點子 。
we want to expand this pattern using mathematics alone , and see if we can get our hands on the whole enchilada .	我們想要用數學來拓展這個模式 , 看看我們能否把手放在整個奇拉達上 。
we want to find all the particles and forces that make a complete picture of our universe .	我們想要找到所有能完成宇宙的粒子和力 。
and we want to use this picture to predict new particles that we'll see when experiments reach higher energies .	我們想要用這張照片來預測新的粒子 , 我們會看到什麼實驗能達到更高的能量 。
so there's an old idea in particle physics that this known pattern of charges , which is not very symmetric , could emerge from a more perfect pattern that gets broken similar to how the higgs particle breaks the electroweak pattern to give electromagnetism .	粒子物理學有一個古老的概念 , 這種已知的載荷型態 , 不對稱性 , 可以從更完美的模式中產生 , 就像希格斯粒子破壞了電磁圖案 , 產生電磁作用 。
in order to do this , we need to introduce new forces with new charge directions .	為了做到這一點 , 我們需要引進新的載荷方向 。
when we introduce a new direction , we get to guess what charges the particles have along this direction , and then we can rotate it in with the others .	當我們介紹一個新的方向時 , 我們會猜測在這個方向上有哪些粒子 , 然後我們就可以把它轉動到另一個方向 。
if we guess wisely , we can construct the standard charges in six charge dimensions as a broken symmetry of this more perfect pattern in seven charge dimensions .	如果我們明智地猜測 , 我們就能在六度載荷空間中建立標準載荷 , 作為這類更完美的七度載荷系統的對稱性 。
this particular choice corresponds to a grand unified theory introduced by pati and salam in 1973 .	這特定的選擇與1973年由pati和salam提出的統一理論有關 。
when we look at this new unified pattern , we can see a couple of gaps where particles seem to be missing .	當我們觀察這個新的統一模式時 , 我們可以看到一些缺失的空隙 。
this is the way theories of unification work .	這就是統一理論運作的方式 。
a physicist looks for larger , more symmetric patterns that include the established pattern as a subset .	物理學家尋找更大、更對稱的模式 , 包括後代建立的模式 。
the larger pattern allows us to predict the existence of particles that have never been seen .	更大的模式讓我們能夠預測從未見過的粒子存在 。
this unification model predicts the existence of these two new force particles , which should act a lot like the weak force , only weaker .	這種統一的模型預測了這兩個新勢力粒子的存在 , 它應該很像弱力 , 只有弱力 。
now we can rotate this set of charges in seven dimensions and consider an odd fact about the matter particles: the second and third generations of matter have exactly the same charges in sixdimensional charge space as the first generation .	現在 , 我們可以在七維空間中旋轉這組載荷 , 並考慮關於粒子的奇怪事實:第二代和第三代的物質在六度載荷空間中有完全相同的載荷 。
these particles are not uniquely identified by their six charges .	這些粒子並不獨特地被它們的六個載荷所識別 。
they sit on top of one another in the standard charge space .	在標準載荷空間中 , 他們坐在彼此的上方 。
however , if we work in eightdimensional charge space , then we can assign unique new charges to each particle .	然而 , 如果我們在八度載荷空間中工作 , 我們就能把每個粒子獨特的新載荷給每個粒子 。
then we can spin these in eight dimensions , and see what the whole pattern looks like .	接著 , 我們可以在八度空間中旋轉 , 看看整個模式是什麼樣子 。
here we can see the second and third generations of matter now related to the first generation by a symmetry called " triality . "	這裡我們可以看到第二代和第三代的物質 , 與第一代的對稱性有關 , 叫做 「 實驗性 」 。
this particular pattern of charges in eight dimensions is actually part of the most beautiful geometric structure in mathematics .	這種在八度空間中的載荷模式其實是數學中最美麗的幾何結構之一 。
it's a pattern of the largest exceptional lie group , e8 .	它是最多例外謊言團體的模式e8 。
this lie group is a smooth , curved shape with 248 dimensions .	這個謊言團體是平滑彎曲的形狀有248度 。
each point in this pattern corresponds to a symmetry of this very complex and beautiful shape .	這種模式的每一個點都對應到這種非常複雜且美麗的形狀的對稱性 。
one small part of this e8 shape can be used to describe the curved spacetime of einstein's general relativity , explaining gravity .	這個e8形狀的一小部分可以用來描述愛因斯坦的廣義相對論 , 解釋重力 。
together with quantum mechanics , the geometry of this shape could describe everything about how the universe works at the tiniest scales .	有了量子力學 , 這種形狀的幾何形狀可以描述宇宙在最小的尺度下運作的一切 。
the pattern of this shape living in eightdimensional charge space is exquisitely beautiful , and it summarizes thousands of possible interactions between these elementary particles , each of which is just a facet of this complicated shape .	生活在八度載荷空間的這種形狀的形狀非常美麗 , 它總結了數千個基本粒子之間的互動 , 每一個形狀都是這個複雜的形狀 。
as we spin it , we can see many of the other intricate patterns contained in this one .	隨著我們旋轉 , 我們可以看到許多複雜的圖案包含在這個圖案中 。
and with a particular rotation , we can look down through this pattern in eight dimensions along a symmetry axis and see all the particles at once .	有了特定的旋轉 , 我們可以在八度空間中觀察這個模式 , 同時觀察到所有粒子 。
it's a very beautiful object , and as with any unification , we can see some holes where new particles are required by this pattern .	它是一個非常美麗的物體 , 如同任何統一 , 我們可以看到一些新粒子被這個模式所需要 。
there are 20 gaps where new particles should be , two of which have been filled by the patisalam particles .	那裡有20個空隙 , 新粒子應該是其中兩個被愛國分子填滿 。
from their location in this pattern , we know that these new particles should be scalar fields like the higgs particle , but have color charge and interact with the strong force .	從它們在這個模式的位置 , 我們知道這些新粒子應該像希格斯粒子一樣 , 但有顏色載荷 , 和強力交互作用 。
filling in these new particles completes this pattern , giving us the full e8 .	這些新粒子填滿了這個模式給我們全e8
this e8 pattern has very deep mathematical roots .	這個e8圖案有很深的數學根 。
it's considered by many to be the most beautiful structure in mathematics .	它被許多人認為是數學中最美麗的結構 。
it's a fantastic prospect that this object of great mathematical beauty could describe the truth of particle interactions at the smallest scales imaginable .	這是一個很棒的前景 , 就是這個偉大的數學美麗的物體 , 可以用最小的尺度來描述粒子互動的真相 。
and this idea that nature is described by mathematics is not at all new .	大自然被數學描述的這個想法完全不是新的想法 。
in 1623 , galileo wrote this: " nature's grand book , which stands continually open to our gaze , is written in the language of mathematics .	在1623年 , 伽利略寫了這篇文章: 「 大自然的偉大書 , 一直打開我們的眼神 , 寫在數學的語言中 。
its characters are triangles , circles and other geometrical figures , without which it is humanly impossible to understand a single word of it ; without these , one is wandering around in a dark labyrinth . "	它的角色是三角形、圓圈和其他幾何形狀的角色 , 沒有這種形狀 , 無法了解單一字 ; 沒有這些 , 一個是深色迷宮的周圍 。 」
i believe this to be true , and i've tried to follow galileo's guidance in describing the mathematics of particle physics using only triangles , circles and other geometrical figures .	我相信這是真的 , 我試著遵循伽利略的指導 , 用三角形、圓形和其他幾何形狀來描述粒子物理 。
of course , when other physicists and i actually work on this stuff , the mathematics can resemble a dark labyrinth .	當然 , 當其他物理學家和我實際研究這些東西時 , 數學可以組成一個暗迷宮 。
but it's reassuring that at the heart of this mathematics is pure , beautiful geometry .	但 , 確保在數學的核心是純粹、美麗的幾何形狀 。
joined with quantum mechanics , this mathematics describes our universe as a growing e8 coral , with particles interacting at every location in all possible ways according to a beautiful pattern .	與量子力學結合 , 這個數學將我們的宇宙描述為生長的e8珊瑚 , 粒子在每個位置相互作用 , 根據美麗的圖案 。
and as more of the pattern comes into view using new machines like the large hadron collider , we may be able to see whether nature uses this e8 pattern or a different one .	更重要的是 , 使用像大型強子對撞機這樣的新機器 , 我們也許能看到大自然是否使用e8圖案 , 或另一個圖案 。
this process of discovery is a wonderful adventure to be involved in .	這個發現的過程是個很棒的冒險 。
if the lhc finds particles that fit this e8 pattern , that will be very , very cool .	如果lhc找到符合e8圖案的粒子 , 那會非常、非常酷 。
if the lhc finds new particles , but they don't fit this pattern well , that will be very interesting , but bad for this e8 theory .	如果lhc發現新的粒子 , 但它們不符合這個模式 , 那會很有趣 , 但對這個e8理論來說不好 。
and , of course , bad for me personally .	當然 , 對我個人來說不好 。
now how bad would that be ?	那會多糟 ?
well , pretty bad .	嗯 , 真的很糟 。
but predicting how nature works is a very risky game .	但預測大自然如何運作是個很危險的遊戲 。
this theory and others like it are long shots .	這種理論和其它類似的理論是長的 。
one does a lot of hard work knowing that most of these ideas probably won't end up being true about nature .	許多努力都知道 , 大部分這些想法可能不會成真 。
that's what doing theoretical physics is like: there are a lot of wipeouts .	理論物理就是這樣:有很多的線條 。
in this regard , new physics theories are a lot like startup companies .	在這個領域 , 新的物理理論就像新創公司一樣 。
as with any large investment , it can be emotionally difficult to abandon a line of research when it isn't working out .	就如同任何大型投資 , 情緒上來說 , 要拋棄一行不通的研究線條 。
but in science , if something isn't working , you have to toss it out and try something else .	但在科學上 , 如果有東西行不通 , 你就得試試別的 。
now , the only way to maintain sanity and achieve happiness in the midst of this uncertainty is to keep balance and perspective in life .	現在 , 唯一能維持正直並達成快樂的方法 , 就是維持生活的平衡和觀點 。
i've tried the best i can to live a balanced life .	我盡全力去過平衡生活 。
i try to balance my life equally between physics , love and surfing my own three charge directions .	我試著平衡我的生活 , 包括物理、愛 , 以及衝浪我自己的三個載荷方向 。
this way , even if the physics i work on comes to nothing , i still know i've lived a good life .	這樣一來 , 即使我工作的物理什麼都沒出現 , 我仍然知道我過著美好的生活 。
and i try to live in beautiful places .	我試著生活在美麗的地方 。
for most of the past ten years i've lived on the island of maui , a very beautiful place .	過去十年來 , 我住在毛伊島 , 一個非常美麗的地方 。
now it's one of the greatest mysteries in the universe to my parents how i managed to survive all that time without engaging in anything resembling fulltime employment .	它是宇宙中最偉大的謎之一 , 讓我的父母 , 我如何能一直存活下來 , 卻沒有全職工作機會 。
i'm going to let you in on that secret .	我要給你們看那個秘密 。
this was a view from my home office on maui .	這是我在maui的家庭辦公室的景象 。
and you may have noticed that these beautiful views are similar , but in slightly different places .	你可能已經注意到這些美麗的觀點是相似的 , 但有些不同的地方 。
that's because this used to be my home and office on maui .	那是因為它以前是我的家 , 在maui的辦公室 。
i've chosen a very unusual life .	我選擇了一個非常不尋常的人生 。
but not worrying about rent allowed me to spend my time doing what i love .	但不用擔心房租讓我花時間做我愛的事 。
living a nomadic existence has been hard at times , but it's allowed me to live in beautiful places and keep a balance in my life that i've been happy with .	有時 , 過著遊牧的存在很困難 , 但這讓我能生活在美麗的地方 , 保持平衡 , 讓我很開心 。
it allows me to spend a lot of my time hanging out with hyperintelligent coral .	它讓我能花很多時間和超級智慧的珊瑚在一起 。
but i also greatly enjoy the company of hyperintelligent people .	但我也很享受超級聰明人的公司 。
so i'm very happy to have been invited here to ted .	我很高興能被邀請到ted 。
chris anderson: i probably understood two percent of that , but i still absolutely loved it . so i'm going to sound dumb .	克里斯•安德森:我可能了解這點的百分之二 , 但我仍然很喜歡它 。 所以我會聽起來很笨 。
your theory of everything garrett lisi: i'm used to coral .	所有有關garretlisi的理論:我習慣珊瑚 。
ca: that's right . the reason it's got a few people at least excited is because , if you're right , it brings gravity and quantum theory together .	克里斯:沒錯 , 原因很少人會感到興奮 , 因為如果你是對的 , 它會把引力和量子理論結合在一起 。
so are you saying that we should think of the universe , at its heart that the smallest things that there are , are somehow an e8 object of possibility ?	所以 , 你是說 , 我們應該想到宇宙 , 在它的核心中 , 最小的東西 , 是有可能的e8物體 ?
i mean , is there a scale to it , at the smallest scale , or . . . ?	我的意思是 , 在最小的尺度 , 還是......
gl: well , right now the pattern i showed you that corresponds to what we know about elementary particle physics that already corresponds to a very beautiful shape .	格林:現在我給你們看的圖案 , 與我們所知的基本粒子物理學相對應的圖案 , 已經對應到非常美麗的形狀 。
and that's the one that i said we knew for certain .	這就是我說我們知道的 。
and that shape has remarkable similarities and the way it fits into this e8 pattern could be the rest of the picture .	這種形狀有著驚人的相似性 , 它融入e8圖案中的方式可能是其餘的圖片 。
and these patterns of points that i've shown for you actually represent symmetries of this highdimensional object that would be warping and moving and dancing over the space time that we experience .	而這些我為你們展示的點圖案 , 實際上代表了這個高維的物體的對稱性 , 會隨著時間扭曲、移動、跳舞的對稱性 。
and that would be what explains all these elementary particles that we see .	這就是我們所看到的基本粒子 。
ca: but a string theorist , as i understand it , explains electrons in terms of much smaller strings vibrating i know you don't like string theory vibrating inside it .	克:但像我所了解的 , 弦理論學家解釋電子以更小的弦震動 , 我知道你不喜歡弦理論在裡面震動 。
how should we think of an electron in relation to e8 ?	我們該如何看待e8的電子呢 ?
gl: no , it would be one of the symmetries of this e8 shape .	蓋爾:不 , 它會是這個e8形狀的對稱之一 。
so what's happening is , as the shape is moving over spacetime , it's twisting . and the direction it's twisting as it moves is what particle we see . so it would be ca: the size of the e8 shape , how does that relate to the electron ?	所以 , 當這個形狀在時空移動時 , 它會扭轉 。 當它移動時 , 它的方向是扭曲的 。 所以它會是ca:e8形狀的大小 , 它和電子有什麼關係 ?
i kind of feel like i need that for my picture .	我覺得我需要這張照片 。
is it bigger ? is it smaller ?	它比較大嗎 ? 它比較小嗎 ?
gl: well , as far as we know electrons are point particles , so this would be going down to the smallest possible scales .	蓋爾:嗯 , 據我們所知 , 電子是點粒子 , 所以這會降到最小的尺度 。
so the way these things are explained in quantum field theory is , all possibilities are expanding and developing at once .	所以 , 這些東西在量子場理論中解釋的方式是 , 所有的可能性同時擴展和發展 。
and this is why i use the analogy to coral .	這就是為什麼我用比喻為珊瑚 。
and in this way , the way that e8 comes in is it will be as a shape that's attached at each point in spacetime .	如此一來 , e8在時空中形成的形狀 , 將成為連接的形狀 。
and , as i said , the way the shape twists the directional along which way the shape is twisting as it moves over this curved surface is what the elementary particles are , themselves .	正如我所說的 , 形狀會改變方向 , 隨著它在曲線的表面上移動時 , 形狀會扭轉 , 就是基本粒子本身 。
so through quantum field theory , they manifest themselves as points and interact that way .	透過量子場理論 , 他們把自己當成點 , 交互作用 。
i don't know if i'll be able to make this any clearer .	我不知道我能不能讓它更清楚 。
ca: it doesn't really matter .	克:這一點都不重要 。
it's evoking a kind of sense of wonder , and i certainly want to understand more of this .	它引發一種奇妙感 , 我肯定想了解更多 。
but thank you so much for coming . that was absolutely fascinating .	非常謝謝你們來這裡 。 這真是令人著迷 。
the legendary chimpanzee researcher jane goodall talks about tacare and her other community projects , which help people in booming african towns live sidebyside with threatened animals .	傳奇的黑猩猩研究員珍.古德會談到tacare以及其他社區專案 , 它協助非洲非洲人口繁榮 , 和受到威脅的動物住在附近 。

jane goodall helps humans and animals live together	珍•古德能協助人類和動物一起生活 , 一起生活 。
good afternoon , good evening , whatever .	午安 , 晚安 , 等等 。
we can go , jambo , guten abend , bonsoir , but we can also ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh .	我們可以去 , 詹姆布 , 古巴德 , 邦諾爾 , 但我們也可以 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 喔 , ~ ~
that is the call that chimpanzees make before they go to sleep in the evening .	這就是黑猩猩在晚上睡覺之前所打的電話 。
you hear it going from one side of the valley to the other , from one group of nests to the next .	從山谷的一邊到另一邊 , 從一群巢穴到下一代 。
and i want to pick up with my talk this evening from where zeray left off yesterday .	今天晚上我要來談談的主題是從昨天剩下的地點 。
he was talking about this amazing , threeyearold australopithecine child , selam .	他談到這個驚人的三歲小孩塞萊姆 。
and we've also been hearing about the history , the family tree , of mankind through dna genetic profiling .	我們也聽過歷史 , 家庭樹 , 透過dna基因改造的人類 。
and it was a paleontologist , the late louis leakey , who actually set me on the path for studying chimpanzees .	這是一位古生物學家 , 最近的路易易斯利華 , 他讓我走上研究黑猩猩的道路 。
and it was pretty extraordinary , way back then .	當時的狀況非常驚人 。
it's kind of commonplace now , but his argument was because he'd been searching for the fossilized remains of early humans in africa .	現在有點常見 , 但他的論點是 , 因為他一直在尋找非洲早期人類的化石 。
and you can tell an awful lot about what those beings looked like from the fossils , from the shape of the muscle attachments , something about the way they lived from the various artifacts found with them .	對於化石的樣子 , 你可以從肌肉附著的形狀來判斷它們的外觀 。 關於它們和它們的不同人造生存的方式 。
but what about how they behaved ? that's what he wanted to know .	但他們的行為呢 ? 這就是他想要知道的 。
and of course , behavior doesn't fossilize .	當然 , 行為並沒有化石 。
he argued and it's now a fairly common theory that if we found behavior patterns similar or the same in our closest living relatives , the great apes , and humans today , then maybe those behaviors were present in the apelike , humanlike ancestor some seven million years ago .	他主張這是個相當普遍的理論如果我們發現相似的行為模式 , 和我們最接近的親戚 , 偉大的猿人 , 現今的人類 , 可能這些行為出現在七百萬年前 , 人類的祖先身上
and therefore , perhaps we had brought those characteristics with us from that ancient , ancient past .	因此 , 也許我們把這些特徵帶到古老、古老的過去 。
well , if you look in textbooks today that deal with human evolution , you very often find people speculating about how early humans may have behaved , based on the behavior of chimpanzees .	嗯 , 如果你看今天的教科書處理人類演化 , 你經常會發現人們推測人類早期的行為 , 基於黑猩猩的行為 。
they are more like us than any other living creature , and we've heard about that during this ted conference .	它們比任何其他生物更像我們 , 我們在ted大會上聽過這一點 。
so it remains for me to comment on the ways in which chimpanzees are so like us , in certain aspects of their behavior .	所以這對我來說 , 對於黑猩猩和我們一樣 , 在某些層面上 , 仍然保持著評論 。
every chimpanzee has his or her own personality .	每隻黑猩猩都有自己的個性 。
of course , i gave them names . they can live to be 60 years or more , although we think most of them probably don't make it to 60 in the wild .	當然 , 我給他們名字 , 他們可以活到六十年或更久 , 雖然我們認為大部分的名字可能不會在野外60歲 。
mr . wurzel . the female has her first baby when she's 11 or 12 .	沃爾茲先生 , 雌性最初的寶寶11或12歲 。
thereafter , she has one baby only every five or six years , a long period of childhood dependency when the child is nursing , sleeping with the mother at night , and riding on her back .	在那裡 , 她的嬰兒每五到六年就有一個嬰兒 , 長期的兒童依賴 , 孩子在晚上和母親睡覺 , 背上騎著 。
and we believe that this long period of childhood is important for chimpanzees , just as it is for us , in relation to learning .	我們相信 , 長久以來的童年時期對黑猩猩很重要 , 就如同對我們一樣 , 與學習有關 。
as the brain becomes ever more complex during evolution in different forms of animals , so we find that learning plays an ever more important role in an individual's life history .	當大腦在不同形式的動物演化過程中變得更複雜時 , 我們發現學習在個人的人生史中扮演著更重要的角色 。
and young chimpanzees spend a lot of time watching what their elders do .	年輕的黑猩猩花很多時間觀察他們的長輩所做的事 。
we know now that they're capable of imitating behaviors that they see .	我們現在知道牠們有能力模仿牠們所看到的行為 。
and we believe that it's in this way that the different toolusing behaviors that have now been seen in all the different chimpanzee populations studied in africa how these are passed from one generation to the next , through observation , imitation and practice , so that we can describe these toolusing behaviors as primitive culture .	我們相信 , 這種方式就是 , 目前在非洲所有不同的黑猩猩族群中所看到的各種不同的工具行為 , 研究這些人是如何從一個世代到下一個世代 , 通過觀察、模仿和實踐 , 來描述這些工具行為為原始文化 。
chimpanzees don't have a spoken language . we've talked about that .	黑猩猩沒有說話的語言 , 我們已經談過了 。
they do have a very rich repertoire of postures and gestures , many of which are similar , or even identical , to ours and formed in the same context . greeting chimpanzees embracing .	牠們的確有很豐富的姿勢和姿勢 , 許多姿勢都相似 , 甚至相同 , 與我們相同 , 在同樣的情境中形成 。 打招呼黑猩猩擁抱 。
they also kiss , hold hands , pat one another on the back .	他們也親吻 , 握手 , 拍手 。
and they swagger and they throw rocks .	它們會變動 , 丟石頭 。
in chimpanzee society , we find many , many examples of compassion , precursors to love and true altruism .	在黑猩猩社會中 , 我們發現許多同情心的例子 , 前提者要愛和真正利他主義 。
unfortunately , they , like us , have a dark side to their nature .	不幸的是 , 像我們一樣 , 他們的天性很暗 。
they're capable of extreme brutality , even a kind of primitive war .	他們有能力極端殘暴 , 甚至是原始的戰爭 。
and these really aggressive behaviors , for the most part , are directed against individuals of the neighboring social group .	這些非常積極的行為 , 大部分時候都被指控 , 對抗鄰近社會群體的個體 。
they are very territorially aggressive .	牠們是非常積極的 。
chimpanzees , i believe , more than any other living creature , have helped us to understand that , after all , there is no sharp line between humans and the rest of the animal kingdom .	黑猩猩 , 我相信 , 比起任何其他生物 , 已經協助我們了解到 , 畢竟 , 人類和動物王國之間沒有尖銳的線條 。
it's a very blurry line , and it's getting more blurry all the time as we make even more observations .	這是一個非常模糊的線 , 隨著我們觀察到更多的模糊越來越模糊 。
the study that i began in 1960 is still continuing to this day .	我在1960年開始的研究仍然持續到今天 。
and these chimpanzees , living their complex social lives in the wild , have helped more than anything else to make us realize we are part of , and not separated from , the amazing animals with whom we share the planet .	這些黑猩猩生活在野外複雜的社交生活 , 協助我們了解到 , 我們是其中的一部分 , 而不是孤立的 , 和我們共享這個星球的神奇動物 。
so it's pretty sad to find that chimpanzees , like so many other creatures around the world , are losing their habitats .	所以 , 發現黑猩猩很遺憾 , 就像世界上許多其他生物一樣 , 正在失去牠們的棲息地 。
this is just one photograph from the air , and it shows you the forested highlands of gombe .	這只是空氣中的一張照片而已 , 它顯示了戈米貝的森林高地 。
and it was when i flew over the whole area , about 16 years ago , and realized that outside the park , this forest , which in 1960 had stretched almost unbroken along the eastern shore of lake tanganyika , which is where the tiny , 30squaremile gombe national park lies , that a question came to my mind .	那時 , 我飛越整個區域 , 大約十六年前 , 發現公園外面 , 這片森林 , 在1960年 , 幾乎沒有破壞 , 沿著坦班尼卡湖湖的東岸 , 那裡很小 , 三十平方英雄的國家公園清單 , 這個問題讓我想到了 。
" how can we even try to save these famous chimpanzees , when the people living around the national park are struggling to survive ? "	「 我們要如何拯救這些知名的黑猩猩 , 當住在國家公園附近的人掙扎求生存 ? 」
more people are living there than the land could possibly support .	更多人住在那兒 , 比土地還多 。
the numbers increased by refugees pouring in from burundi and over the lake from congo .	難民的數量增加 , 來自緬甸和來自剛果湖泊的難民數 。
and very poor people they couldn't afford to buy food from elsewhere .	非常貧窮的人無法從其他地方買到食物 。
this led to a program , which we call tacare .	這導致了一個計畫 , 我們稱之為tacare 。
it's a very holistic way of improving the lives of the people living in the villages around the park .	這是一種非常全面的改善生活在公園附近的村民的生活方式 。
it started small with 12 villages . it's now in 24 .	它從十二個村莊開始 。 現在是二十四個 。
there isn't time to go into it , but it's including things like tree nurseries , methods of farming most suitable to this now very degraded , almost desertlike land up in these mountains .	沒有時間深入研究 , 但它包含了樹木護士 , 目前最適合耕種的方法 , 幾乎是破壞了 , 幾乎像沙漠般的土地在這些山上 。
ways of controlling , preventing soil erosion .	控制的方式 , 預防土壤侵蝕 。
ways of reclaiming overused farmland , so that within two years they can again be productive .	恢復過度農田的方法 , 這樣在兩年之內 , 就能再有生產力 。
working to help the villagers obtain fresh water from wells .	為了幫助村民從井中取得淡水 。
perhaps build some schoolrooms .	也許建造一些學校房子 。
most important of all , i believe , is working with small groups of women , providing them with opportunities for microcredit loans .	最重要的是 , 我相信 , 與小群體的女性合作 , 提供她們機會給微型貸款 。
and we've got , as is the case around the world , about 95 percent of all loans returned .	如同全世界的案例 , 大約百分之九十五的貸款回來了 。
empowering women , working with education , providing scholarships for girls so they can finish secondary school , in the clear understanding that , all around the world , as women's education improves , family size drops .	讓女性能夠接受教育 , 提供獎學金給女孩 , 這樣她們才能完成中等學校 , 很明顯地 , 全世界的教育都在改善 , 家庭規模也會下降 。
we provide information about family planning and about hiv/aids .	我們提供家庭規劃和愛滋病的資訊 。
and as a result of this program , something's happening for conservation .	由於這個計畫 , 保育正在進行中 。
what's happening for conservation is that the farmers living in these 24 villages , instead of looking on us as a bunch of white people coming to study a whole bunch of monkeys and by the way , many of the staff are now tanzanian but when we began the tacare program , it was a tanzanian team going into the villages .	保育的情況是 , 住在這24個村落的農夫 , 而不是把我們當成一群白人來研究一大群猴子 , 順便一提 , 許多員工現在是坦尚尼亞 , 但當我們開始計劃時 , 它是一個坦尚尼亞的團隊進入村落 。
it was a tanzanian team talking to the villagers , asking what they were interested in .	那是一個坦尚尼亞的團隊和村民談話 , 問他們感興趣的是什麼 。
were they interested in conservation ? absolutely not .	他們有興趣保育嗎 ? 絕對不是 。
they were interested in health ; they were interested in education .	他們對健康有興趣 , 他們對教育有興趣 。
and as time went on , and as their situation began to improve , they began to understand ever more about the need for conservation .	隨著時間過去 , 當他們的情況開始改善 , 他們開始更加了解保育的需求 。
they began to understand that as the upper levels of the hills were denuded of trees , so you've got this terrible soil erosion and mudslides .	他們開始了解山丘的上層是樹木被砍伐的 , 所以土壤侵蝕和泥土 。
today , we are developing what we call the greater gombe ecosystem .	現今 , 我們正在發展我們所謂的更大的gombe生態系統 。
this is an area way outside the national park , stretching out into all these very degraded lands .	這個區域在國家公園外延伸出去 , 延伸到這些非常惡劣的土地上 。
and as these villages have a better standard of life , they are actually agreeing to put between 10 percent and 20 percent of their land in the highlands aside , so that once again , as the trees grow back , the chimpanzees will have leafy corridors through which they can travel to interact as they must for genetic viability with other remnant groups outside the national park .	隨著這些村落有更好的生活標準 , 他們其實同意把百分之十到二十的土地放到高地之外 , 所以 , 隨著樹木長回來 , 黑猩猩就會有葉廊穿過 , 讓它們可以在國家公園外的其他遺傳團體進行基因改善 。
so tacare is a success .	所以tacare是成功的 。
we're replicating it in other parts of africa , around other wilderness areas which are faced with extreme population pressure .	我們把它複製在非洲的其他地方 , 在其他極端人口壓力的野外地區 。
the problems in africa , however , as we've been discussing for the whole of these first couple of days of ted , are major problems .	然而 , 在非洲 , 我們一直在討論ted的前幾天問題 , 都是主要的問題 。
there is a great deal of poverty .	有很大的貧窮 。
and when you get large numbers of people living in land that is not that fertile , particularly when you cut down trees , and you leave the soil open to the wind for erosion , as desperate populations cut down more and more trees , so that they can try and grow food for themselves and their families , what's going to happen ? something's got to give .	當你有大量的居民住在陸地 , 不是肥沃 , 特別是當你砍樹時 , 土壤就會開放給被侵蝕的土地 , 當絕望的人口減少更多的樹木 , 這樣他們就能試著為自己和家人種食物 , 有什麼事情會發生 。
and the other problems in not only africa , but the rest of the developing world and , indeed , everywhere what are we doing to our planet ?	另外一個問題不僅僅是非洲 , 還有其他開發中國家 , 的確 , 我們對地球所做的一切都一樣 。
you know , the famous scientist , e . o . wilson said that if every person on this planet attains the standard of living of the average european or american , we need three new planets .	你知道 , 著名的科學家e.o.wilson說 , 如果地球上每個人生活的標準是歐洲人或美國人 , 我們需要三個新的行星 。
today , they are saying four . but we don't have them . we've got one .	現今 , 他們說的是四個 。 但我們沒有他們 。 我們有一個 。
and what's happened ? i mean , the question here is , here we are , arguably the most intelligent being that's ever walked planet earth , with this extraordinary brain , capable of the kind of technology that is so well illustrated by these ted conferences , and yet we're destroying the only home we have .	到底發生了什麼事 ? 我的意思是 , 問題是 , 我們在這裡 , 說是最聰明的生物 , 可以走過地球 , 帶著這種非凡的大腦 , 可以用這些ted大會來說明 , 這樣科技才會被我們破壞 。
the indigenous people around the world , before they made a major decision , used to sit around and ask themselves , " how does this decision affect our people seven generations ahead ? "	世界各地的原住民 , 在他們做出重大的決定之前 , 常常坐在旁邊問自己: 「 這決定如何影響我們七個世代 ? 」
today , major decisions and i'm not particularly talking about africa here , but the developed world major decisions involving millions of dollars , and millions of people , are often based on , " how will this affect the next shareholders' meeting ? "	今天 , 主要的決策 , 我並不特別談論非洲 , 但已開發國家的主要決策 , 涉及數百萬美金 , 數百萬人 , 通常是基於 「 這會如何影響下一股東的會議 ? 」
and these decisions affect africa .	這些決定影響了非洲 。
as i began traveling around africa talking about the problems faced by chimpanzees and their vanishing forests , i realized more and more how so many of africa's problems could be laid at the door of previous colonial exploitation .	當我開始在非洲各地旅行 , 談到黑猩猩所面臨的問題 , 以及它們消失的森林 , 我越來越了解到 , 許多非洲的問題可以在過去殖民地爆發的大門上 。
so i began traveling outside africa , talking in europe , talking in the united states , going to asia .	所以我開始在非洲外面旅行 , 在歐洲談話 , 在美國談話 , 去亞洲 。
and everywhere there were these terrible problems .	到處都有這些可怕的問題 。
and you know the kind i'm talking about . i'm talking about pollution .	你知道我在說的那種 , 我在說的是污染 。
the air that we breathe that often poisons us .	我們呼吸的空氣經常毒害我們 。
the earth is poisoning our foods .	地球正在毒害我們的食物 。
the water water is perhaps one of the most crucial issues that we're going to face in this century and everywhere water is being polluted by agricultural , industrial and household chemicals that still are being sprayed around the world , seemingly with the inability to profit from past experience .	水可能是我們本世紀所面臨的最關鍵議題之一 , 到處都是來自農業、工業和家庭用的化學物質 , 仍然在世界各地被噴殺 , 似乎無法從過去的經驗中獲利 。
the mangroves are being cut down ; the effects of things like the tsunami get worse .	紅樹林被砍伐 ; 像海嘯這樣的效應變得更糟 。
we've talked about the soil erosion .	我們談過土壤侵蝕 。
we have the reckless burning of fossil fuels along with other greenhouse gasses , so called , leading to climate change .	我們有無能為力的化石燃料和其他溫室氣體燃燒 , 因此 , 導致氣候變遷 。
finally , all around the world , people have begun to believe that there is something going on very wrong with our climate .	最後 , 世界各地 , 人們開始相信氣候有問題 。
all around the world climates are mixed up .	全世界的氣候都混合在一起 。
and it's the poor people who are affected worse .	貧窮的人會受到更嚴重的影響 。
it's africa that already is affected .	非洲已經受到影響了 。
in many parts of subsaharan africa , the droughts are so much worse .	在撒哈拉以南非洲的許多地區 , 乾旱越來越嚴重 。
and when the rain does come , it so often leads to flooding and added distress , and the cycle of poverty and hunger and disease .	當下雨來臨時 , 通常會導致洪水、加上苦惱 , 以及貧窮、飢餓和疾病的循環 。
and the numbers of people living in an area that the land cannot support , who are too poor to buy food , who can't move away because the whole land is degraded .	住在土地無法支援的地區 , 人口數量太貧窮 , 無法購買食物 , 因為整個土地都被降解了 。
and so you get desertification creeping , creeping , creeping as the last of the trees are cut down .	所以你會得到沙漠化 , 哭泣 , 哭泣 , 彷彿最後一棵樹被砍伐了 。
and this kind of thing is not just in africa . it's all over the world .	這種事不僅僅是在非洲 , 世界各地 。
so it wasn't surprising to me that as i was traveling around the world i met so many young people who seemed to have lost hope .	所以 , 我並不意外 , 當我在世界各地旅行時 , 我遇到許多似乎失去希望的年輕人 。
we seem to have lost wisdom , the wisdom of the indigenous people .	我們似乎失去了智慧 , 原住民的智慧 。
i asked a question . " why ? "	我問了一個問題 。 為什麼 ?
well , do you think there could be some kind of disconnect between this extraordinarily clever brain , the kind of brain that the ted technologies exemplify , and the human heart ? talking about it in the nonscientific term , in terms of love and compassion . is there some disconnect ?	嗯 , 你認為這個非凡聰明的大腦之間有某種差異嗎 ? ted科技的表現和人的心 ? 用非科學的角度來說 , 愛和同理心 , 有沒有什麼差別 ?
and these young people , when i talk to them , basically they were either depressed or apathetic , or bitter and angry . and they said more or less the same thing , " we feel this way because we feel you've compromised our future and there's nothing we can do about it . "	而這些年輕人 , 當我和他們談話時 , 基本上他們不是憂鬱或冷漠 , 或痛苦 , 或生氣 。 他們說了同樣的話: 「 我們覺得你已經妥協了我們的未來 , 沒有我們能做的事 。 」
we have compromised their future .	我們已經妥協了他們的未來 。
i've got three little grandchildren , and every time i look at them and i think how we've harmed this beautiful planet since i was their age , i feel this desperation .	我有三個小孫子 , 每當我看著他們 , 我想我們從小就傷害了這個美麗的星球 , 我感受到這種絕望 。
and that led to this program we call roots and shoots , which began right here in tanzania and has now spread to 97 countries around the world .	那就導致了這個計畫我們稱之為根與芽 , 由於坦尚尼亞開始 , 現在已散播到全世界的97個國家 。
it's symbolic . roots make a firm foundation .	它是象徵性的 。 根是建立公司基金會 。
shoots seem tiny ; to reach the sun they can break through a brick wall .	射擊似乎很小 , 能抵達太陽 , 能穿過磚牆 。
see the brick wall as all these problems we've inflicted on the planet , environmental and social . it's a message of hope .	把磚牆當作我們在地球上所遇到的問題 , 環境和社會的問題 。 這是希望的訊息 。
hundreds and thousands of young people around the world can break through and can make this a better world for all living things .	全世界成千上萬的年輕人可以突破 , 讓這個更美好的世界 , 讓所有生物都能活得更好 。
the most important message of roots and shoots: every single one of us makes a difference , every single day .	根與芽的最重要訊息:我們每一個人都能改變 , 每天都能改變 。
we have a choice . every one of us in this room , we have a choice as to what kind of difference we want to make .	我們有選擇 。 在座的每一個人 , 我們都有選擇要做出什麼樣的改變 。
the very poor have no choice . it's up to us to change things so that the poor have choice as well .	非常貧窮的人沒有選擇 。 由我們決定改變事情 , 讓窮人也有選擇 。
the roots and shoots groups all choose three projects .	根和芽團體都選擇了三個計畫 。
it depends on how old they are , and which country , whether they're in a city or rural , as to what kinds of projects .	這取決於他們有多老 , 哪個國家 , 不管他們住在城市或鄉下 , 什麼類型的專案 。
but basically , we have programs now from preschool right through university , with more and more adults starting their own roots and shoots groups .	但基本上 , 我們有從學前兒童到大學的專案 , 越來越多的成人開始自己的根與芽 。
and every group chooses , between them , three different kinds of project to make this a better world , recognizing that all these different problems are interconnected and impinge on each other .	每個團體都選擇了三種不同的專案 , 讓這個更美好的世界變得更好 , 認知到所有這些不同的問題都互相連結並實現 。
so one of their projects will be to help their own human community .	其中一項計畫是幫助他們自己的人類社區 。
and then , if they're able , they may raise money to help communities in other parts of the world .	如果他們能的話 , 他們就能募到錢來協助世界其他地方的社區 。
one of their projects will be to help animals not just wildlife , domestic animals as well .	其中一項計畫是要幫助動物 , 不只是野生動物 , 家族動物 。
and one of their projects will be to help the environment that we all share .	其中一項計畫是要協助我們所有人共享的環境 。
and woven throughout all of this is a message of learning to live in peace and harmony within ourselves , in our families , in our communities , between nations , between cultures , between religions and between us and the natural world .	所有這一切都是關於學習和平和和諧的訊息 , 在我們自己的家庭、我們的社區、文化、宗教、我們之間、和自然界之間的連結 。
we need the natural world . we cannot go on destroying it at the rate we are .	我們需要自然世界 。 我們不能以我們現在的速度來摧毀它 。
we not do have more than this one planet .	我們沒有超過這個星球 。
just picking one or two of the projects right here in africa that the roots and shoots groups are doing , one or two projects only in tanzania , in uganda , kenya , south africa , congobrazzaville , sierra leone , cameroon and other groups . and as i say , it's in 97 countries around the world .	在非洲 , 選出一兩項專案 , 包括根與槍擊團體 , 一到兩項專案 , 只在坦尚尼亞、肯亞、南非、剛果廣場、獅子山共和國、喀麥隆 , 以及其他團體 。 如我所說 , 它在世界上97個國家 。
of course , they're planting trees . they're growing organic vegetables .	當然 , 他們種植樹木 , 種植有機蔬菜 。
they're working in the refugee camps , with chickens and selling the eggs for a little amount of money , or just using them to feed their families , and feeling a sense of pride and empowerment , because they're no longer helpless and depending on others with their vegetables and their chickens .	他們在難民營工作 , 有雞肉賣卵 , 或只用它們餵飽他們的家庭 , 感受到驕傲和賦權 , 因為他們不再無助 , 依賴他們的蔬菜和雞 。
it's being used in uganda to give some psychological help to exchild soldiers .	它被用在烏干達 , 給予士兵一些心理協助 。
doing projects like this is bringing them out of themselves .	像這樣做 , 會讓他們脫離自己 。
once again , they're useful members of society .	再一次 , 他們是社會中有用的成員 。
we have this program in prisons as well .	我們在監獄也有這個計畫 。
so , there's no time for more roots and shoots now .	所以 , 現在沒有更多的根和芽時間了 。
but oh , they're also working on hiv/aids .	但 , 喔 , 他們也致力於愛滋病/愛滋病 。
that's a very important component of roots and shoots , with older kids talking to younger ones .	這是根與芽的重要元素 , 與較年長的孩子對談 ,
and unwanted pregnancies and things like that , which young people listen to better from other youth , rather than adults .	未曾預期的懷孕之類的 , 年輕人會傾聽別人的心聲 , 而非成人 。
hope . that's the question i get asked as i'm going around the world: " jane , you've seen so many terrible things , you've seen your chimpanzees decrease in number from about one million , at the turn of the century , to no more than 150 , 000 now , and the same with so many other animals .	希望 。 這是我在世界各地被問的問題: 「 珍 , 你見過這麼多可怕的事情 , 你見過你的黑猩猩數量從本世紀的一百萬 , 降低到現在已經超過十五萬人了 , 和許多其他動物一樣 。
forests disappearing , deserts where once there was forest .	森林消失 , 曾經有森林的沙漠 。
do you really have hope ? " well , yes .	你真的有希望嗎 ? 」 嗯 , 是的 。
you can't come to a conference like ted and not have hope , can you ?	你不能參加像ted這樣的會議 , 沒有希望 , 對吧 ?
and of course , there's hope . one is this amazing human brain .	當然 , 還有希望 。 其中一個是這個神奇的人類大腦 。
and i mean , think of the technologies .	我的意思是 , 想想科技 。
and i've just been so thrilled , finally , to come to people talking about compost latrines .	我一直很興奮 , 終於 , 能來到人們談論堆肥廁所 。
it's one of my hobbyhorses .	這是我的嗜好之一 。
we just flush all this water down the lavatory , it's terrible .	我們把所有的水沖到電梯裡 , 很糟糕 。
and then talking about renewable energy desperately important .	接著談到可再生能源 , 迫切重要 。
do we care about the planet for our children ?	我們在乎我們的孩子這個星球嗎 ?
how many of us have children or grandchildren , nieces , nephews ?	有多少人有小孩或孫子、姪子、姪子 ?
do we care about their future ?	我們關心他們的未來嗎 ?
and if we care about their future , we , as the elite around the world , we can do something about it . we can make choices as to how we live each day .	如果我們關心他們的未來 , 我們身為全世界菁英的菁英 , 我們可以做點什麼 。 我們可以做出選擇 , 來做我們每天的生活 。
what we buy . what we wear .	我們買什麼 , 我們穿什麼 。
and choose to make these choices with the question , how will this affect the environment around me ?	選擇用這個問題來做這些選擇 , 這會如何影響我周遭的環境 ?
how will it affect the life of my child when he or she grows up ?	當他或她長大後 , 它會如何影響我的孩子 ?
or my grandchild , or whatever it is .	或者是我的孫子 , 或其它的東西 。
so the human brain , coupled with the human heart , and we join hands around the world .	所以 , 人類的大腦 , 和人類的心情結合 , 我們加入世界各地 。
and that's what ted is helping so well with , and google who help us , and esri are helping us with mapping in gombe national park .	這就是ted的幫助 , google幫助我們 , esri協助我們 , 協助我們繪製gombe國家公園的地圖 。
all of these technologies we can use .	所有我們能使用的科技 。
now let's link them , and it's beginning to happen , isn't it ?	現在讓我們把它們連結起來 , 開始了 , 不是嗎 ?
you've heard about it this afternoon . it's beginning to happen .	你今天下午已經聽說過 , 已經開始發生了 。
this change , this change . to see change that we must have if we care about the future .	這種改變 , 這種改變 。 若我們關心未來 , 我們必須看到改變 。
and the next reason for hope nature is amazingly resilient .	希望大自然的下一個理由是令人驚訝的韌性 。
you can take an area that's absolutely destroyed , with time and perhaps some help it can regenerate .	你可以把一個絕對被摧毀的區域 , 用時間 , 或一些幫助來恢復 。
and an example is the tacare program .	一個例子是醫療保健計畫 。
i told you , where a seemingly dead tree stump if you stop hacking them for firewood , which you don't need to because you have wood lots , then in five years you can have a 30foot tree .	我告訴你們 , 看似已死的樹木 , 如果你停止砍伐它們 , 不用砍伐它們 , 因為你有很多木頭 , 然後在五年內 , 你可以有三十英呎的樹木 。
and animals , almost on the brink of extinction , can be given a second chance . that's my next book .	而動物 , 幾乎在絕種的邊緣 , 可以得到第二次機會 。 這是我的下一本書 。
it's inspiring . and it brings me to my last category of hope , and we've heard about this so much in the last two days: this indomitable human spirit . this determination of people , the resilience of the human spirit , so that people who you would think would be battered by poverty , or disease , or whatever , can pull themselves up out of it , sometimes with a helping hand , and take their part in society , and take their part in changing the world .	它很鼓舞人心 。 它帶我到我最後的希望類別 , 在過去的兩天 , 我們都聽過這麼多的希望:這種不屈不撓的人類精神 。 這種決心 , 人類精神的韌性 , 這樣你認為會被貧窮或疾病所困擾 , 或其他的人們 , 可以把自己從中拉出來 , 有時 , 用協助 , 把他們的部分帶到社會中 , 讓他們改變世界 。
and just to think of one or two people out of africa who are just really inspiring .	想想看 , 一到兩位非洲的人 , 他們真的很鼓舞人心 。
we could make a very long list , but obviously nelson mandela , emerging from 17 years of hard physical labor , 23 years of imprisonment , with this amazing ability to forgive , so that he could lead his nation out the evil regime of apartheid without a bloodbath .	我們可以列出很長的清單 , 但很顯然 , 曼德拉的名單來自十七年的硬體勞工 , 23年的監獄 , 有了很棒的寬恕 , 讓他能帶領他的國家離開種族隔離的邪惡政權 , 沒有血浴 。
