ken sarowiwa , in nigeria , who took on the giant oil companies , and although people around the world tried their best , was executed .	奈及利亞的薩朗瓦 , 帶著巨型的石油公司 , 儘管全世界的人都盡力 , 被處決了 。
people like this are so inspirational .	像這樣的人是如此的靈感 。
people like this are the role models we need for young africans .	像這樣的人是我們非洲年輕人所需要的榜樣 。
and we need some environmental role models as well , and i've been hearing some of them today .	我們也需要一些環保的榜樣 , 我今天也聽到了其中一些 。
so i'm really grateful for this opportunity to share this message again , with everyone at ted .	所以我很感激這個機會 , 再次與ted的每個人分享這個訊息 。
and i hope that some of us can get together and talk about some of these things , especially the roots and shoots program .	我希望我們當中有些人能聚集起來討論其中的一些事情 , 特別是根與芽計劃 。
and just a last word on that the young woman who's running this entire conference center , i met her today .	最後一個字是那個跑完這整個會議中心的年輕女子 , 我今天見到她 。
she came up so excited , with her certificate . she was [in] roots and shoots .	她很興奮 , 得到她的證書 。 她是根和槍 。
she was in the leadership in dar es salaam .	她在達斯薩拉姆的領導階層 。
she said it's helped her to do what she's doing .	她說 , 做她正在做的事是有幫助的 。
and it was very , very exciting for me to meet her and see just one example of how young people , when they are empowered , given the opportunity to take action , to make the world a better place , truly are our hope for tomorrow .	對我來說 , 我非常興奮地見到她 , 看到一個例子 , 說明了年輕人如何被賦權力的例子 , 因為他們有機會採取行動 , 讓世界變得更美好 , 真正是我們明天的希望 。
artist dianna cohen shares some tough truths about plastic pollution in the ocean and in our lives and some thoughts on how to free ourselves from the plastic gyre .	藝術家黛安娜•柯恩分享了一些關於海洋中的塑膠污染的艱難事實 , 在我們的生命中 , 以及一些想法 , 關於如何讓自己脫離塑膠圈 。
consumerism , global issues , green , mission blue , oceans , plastic	消費主義、全球議題、綠色、使命藍色、海洋、塑膠、塑膠 。
dianna cohen: tough truths about plastic pollution	黛安娜•柯恩:關於塑膠污染的困難真相 。
i'm a visual artist , and i'm also one of the cofounders of the plastic pollution coalition .	我是視覺藝術家 , 我也是塑膠污染聯盟的共同創辦人之一 。
i've been working with plastic bags , which i cut up and sew back together as my primary material for my artwork for the last 20 years .	我一直在研究塑膠袋 , 我把塑膠袋剪下來 , 縫合起來 , 做為我過去二十年來的藝術作品 。
i turn them into two and threedimensional pieces and sculptures and installations .	我把它們變成兩片、三度空間的碎片、雕塑和裝置 。
upon working with the plastic , after about the first eight years , some of my work started to fissure and break down into smaller little bits of plastic .	和塑膠合作了大約八年後 , 我的一些作品開始有裂縫 , 分解成更小的塑膠 。
and i thought , " great .	我心想: 「 太棒了 。
it's ephemeral just like us . "	它就像我們一樣 。 」
upon educating myself a little further about plastics , i actually realized this was a bad thing .	在我更深入地研究塑膠 , 我發現這是一件壞事 。
it's a bad thing that plastic breaks down into smaller little bits , because it's always still plastic .	塑膠會分解成更小的部分 , 因為它永遠都是塑膠 。
and what we're finding is that a lot of it is in the marine environment .	我們發現 , 很多都是在海洋環境中 。
i then , in the last few years , learned about the pacific garbage patch and the gyre .	接著 , 在過去幾年 , 我學到太平洋垃圾堆和蓋瑞 。
and my initial reaction and i think this is a lot of people's first reaction to learning about it is , " oh my god !	我最初的反應是 , 很多人的第一個反應是: 「 天啊 !
we've got to go out there and clean this thing up . "	我們必須去清理這個東西 。 」
so i actually developed a proposal to go out with a cargo ship and two decommissioned fishing trawlers , a crane , a chipping machine and a coldmolding machine .	所以我開發了一個提案 , 和一艘貨船出去 , 和兩艘退休的捕魚拖網 , 一台拖車 , 一台拖車 , 一台冰冷的機器 。
and my intention was to go out to the gyre , raise awareness about this issue and begin to pick up the plastic , chip it into little bits and cold mold it into bricks that could potentially be used as building materials in underdeveloped communities .	我的意圖是走到蓋爾 , 提高對這個問題的認知 , 開始把塑膠 , 切成碎片 , 將它冷成一些磚塊 , 可以被用來當作已開發的社區建造材料 。
i began talking with people who actually had been out to the gyre and were studying the plastic problem in the marine environment and upon doing so , i realized actually that cleaning it up would be a very small drop in the bucket relative to how much is being generated every day around the world , and that actually i needed to back up and look at the bigger picture .	我開始和那些真的去過蓋爾的人們談話 , 研究海洋環境中的塑膠問題 , 然後在做這件事時 , 我意識到 , 清理它會是非常小的一滴 , 和全世界每天所產生的塑膠相比 , 我需要回頭看更大的照片 。
and the bigger picture is: we need to find a way to turn off the faucet .	更大的圖片是:我們需要找到一個方法來關掉公平面 。
we need to cut the spigot of singleuse and disposable plastics , which are entering the marine environment every day on a global scale .	我們需要切斷單一、可分配的塑膠 , 每天進入海洋環境 , 以全球性的規模 。
so in looking at that , i also realized that i was really angry .	所以 , 看著這一點 , 我也發現我真的很生氣 。
i wasn't just concerned about plastic that you're trying to imagine out in the middle of the pacific ocean of which i have learned there are now 11 gyres , potentially , of plastic in five major oceans in the world .	我不只關心塑膠 , 你在太平洋的正中部 , 我還知道現在有11個健身 , 可能是世界上五大海洋的塑膠 。
it's not just that gyre of plastic that i'm concerned about it's the gyre of plastic in the supermarket .	不只是我所關心的塑膠垃圾 , 而是超市的塑膠垃圾蓋 。
i'd go to the supermarket and all of my food is packaged in plastic .	我會去超市 , 我所有的食物都是塑膠包裝的 。
all of my beverages are packaged in plastic , even at the health food market .	我所有的飲料都是塑膠的包裝 , 甚至是健康食品市場 。
i'm also concerned about the plastic in the refrigerator , and i'm concerned about the plastic and the toxins that leach from plastic into us and into our bodies .	我也擔心冰箱裡的塑膠 , 我擔心塑膠和塑膠從塑膠到我們身上的毒素 。
so i came together with a group of other people who were all looking at this issue , and we created the plastic pollution coalition .	所以我和一群人一起研究這個問題 , 我們創造了塑膠污染聯盟 。
we have many initiatives that we're working on , but some of them are very basic .	我們有許多我們正在努力的倡議 , 但有些是非常基本的 。
one is: if 80 to 90 percent of what we're finding in the ocean of the marine debris that we're finding in the ocean is plastic , then why don't we call it what it is .	第一:如果我們在海洋中發現的80% ~ 90%就是我們在海洋中發現的塑膠 , 那麼我們為什麼不把它稱為它 。
recycling everybody kind of ends their books about being sustainable and greening with the idea of recycling .	回收每個人的書 , 都是為了永續發展和綠化 , 用回收的想法來回收 。
you put something in a bin and you don't have to think about it again .	你把東西放在一個垃圾桶裡 , 你不用再想一想 。
what is the reality of that ?	這是什麼 ?
in the united states , less than seven percent of our plastics are recycled .	在美國 , 只有不到7%的塑膠被回收 。
and if you really look into it , particularly when it comes to plastic bottles , most of it is only downcycled , or incinerated , or shipped to china .	如果你仔細觀察 , 尤其是當談到塑膠瓶 , 大部分只會被降低 , 或是被運到中國 。
it is downcycled and turned into lesser things , while a glass bottle can be a glass bottle again or can be used again a plastic bottle can never be a plastic bottle again .	它被降級 , 轉換成較少的東西 , 而玻璃瓶可以再次變成玻璃瓶 , 或者可以再次使用 , 塑膠瓶也無法再次變成塑膠瓶 。
so this is a big issue for us .	所以這對我們來說是個大問題 。
another thing that we're looking at and asking people to think about is we've added a fourth r onto the front of the " reduce , reuse , recycle , " three r's , and that is refuse .	我們正在看另一件事 , 請大家思考 , 我們在 「 縮減、重覆使用、回收 」 前面加上第四圈 , 三圈 , 那就拒絕了 。
whenever possible , refuse singleuse and disposable plastics .	每當可能時 , 都拒絕使用單一和可用的塑膠 。
alternatives exist ; some of them are very oldschool .	替代方案存在 ; 有些則是很老的學齡 。
i myself am now collecting these cool pyrex containers and using those instead of glad and tupperware containers to store food in .	我現在正在收集這些很酷的pyrex容器 , 用這些 , 而不是glad和upperware的容器來儲存食物 。
and i know that i am doing a service to myself and my family .	我知道我對自己和我的家人做了一個服務 。
it's very easy to pick up a stainlesssteel bottle or a glass bottle , if you're traveling and you've forgotten to bring your stainlesssteel bottle and fill that up with water or filtered water , versus purchasing plastic bottled water .	很容易拿起一瓶不穩定的瓶子 , 或玻璃瓶 , 如果你去旅行 , 你忘了帶你的不確定的瓶子填滿水或過濾水 , 而不是購買塑膠瓶 。
i guess what i want to say to everybody here and i know that you guys know a lot about this issue is that this is a huge problem in the oceans , but this is a problem that we've created as consumers and we can solve .	我想我想要向大家說的是我知道你們對這個議題的了解是 , 這在海洋裡是個很大的問題 , 但這是我們身為消費者 , 我們能解決的一個問題 。
we can solve this by raising awareness of the issue and teaching people to choose alternatives .	我們能解決這個問題 , 藉由提升大家的意識 , 並教導人們選擇替代方案 。
so whenever possible , to choose alternatives to singleuse plastics .	所以 , 盡可能地選擇單一塑膠的替代方案 。
we can cut the stem tide the stem of this into our oceans and in doing so , save our oceans , save our planet , save ourselves .	我們可以把這些幹細胞切成海洋 , 這樣 , 拯救我們的海洋 , 拯救我們的地球 , 拯救我們自己 。
this demo from pattie maes' lab at mit , spearheaded by pranav mistry was the buzz of ted . it's a wearable device with a projector that paves the way for profound interaction with our environment . imagine " minority report " and then some .	這位來自麻省理工學院maes實驗室的示範 , 由帕拉福利所引發的 , 是ted的buzz 。 它是一個可穿戴式裝置 , 用來和環境深遠互動的專案 。 想像一下 , 「 少數族裔報告 」 , 然後有一些 。
demo , design , interface design , technology	demo , 設計 , 介面設計 , 科技 , 科技 。
pattie maes and pranav mistry demo sixthsense	派屈瑪斯和帕拉夫•密切利 , 第十六感 。
i've been intrigued by this question of whether we could evolve or develop a sixth sense a sense that would give us seamless access and easy access to metainformation or information that may exist somewhere that may be relevant to help us make the right decision about whatever it is that we're coming across .	我對這個問題很感興趣 , 關於我們能否演化或發展出第六種感官的感官 , 使我們能取得無縫且容易取得改造或存在的資訊 , 可能在某些地方 , 協助我們做出正確的決定 , 決定我們要面對的是什麼 。
and some of you may argue , well , don't today's cell phones do that already ?	在座有些人可能認為 , 現今的手機不是已經做到的嗎 ?
but i would say no .	但我會說 , 不 。
when you meet someone here at ted and this is the top networking place , of course , of the year you don't shake somebody's hand and then say , " can you hold on for a moment while i take out my phone and google you ? "	當你在ted認識某個人時 , 當然 , 這是最頂尖的網路網絡 , 在那一年你不會握某人的手 , 然後說: 「 你能拿出我的手機和google嗎 ? 」
or when you go to the supermarket and you're standing there in that huge aisle of different types of toilet papers , you don't take out your cell phone , and open a browser , and go to a website to try to decide which of these different toilet papers is the most ecologically responsible purchase to make .	或當你去超市 , 站在那裏巨大的廁所論文 , 你不會拿出你的手機 , 打開瀏覽器 , 到一個網站 , 試著決定這些不同的廁所論文中哪些是最環保的購物 。
so we don't really have easy access to all this relevant information that can just help us make optimal decisions about what to do next and what actions to take .	所以我們沒有很容易取得所有相關的資訊 , 來協助我們做出最佳的決策 , 來做下一步該做的事 , 以及要採取什麼行動 。
and so my research group at the media lab has been developing a series of inventions to give us access to this information in a sort of easy way , without requiring that the user changes any of their behavior .	所以我在媒體實驗室的研究小組正在開發一系列的發明 , 讓我們能以簡單的方式取得這些資訊 , 不需要使用者改變他們的行為 。
and i'm here to unveil our latest effort , and most successful effort so far , which is still very much a work in process .	我在這裡要揭開我們最新的努力 , 目前為止 , 最成功的努力仍然是過程中的工作 。
i'm actually wearing the device right now and we've sort of cobbled it together with components that are off the shelf and that , by the way , only cost 350 dollars at this point in time .	我現在正穿著這個裝置 , 把它和擺脫架上的零件混合在一起 , 順便說一下 , 當時只有350美金 。
i'm wearing a camera , just a simple webcam , a portable , batterypowered projection system with a little mirror .	我戴著攝影機 , 只是一個簡單的網路攝影機 , 一個可攜帶、電池充電的投影系統 , 裡面有一面鏡子 。
these components communicate to my cell phone in my pocket which acts as the communication and computation device .	這些元件對我口袋裡的手機進行溝通 , 作為溝通和計算裝置 。
and in the video here we see my student pranav mistry , who's really the genius who's been implementing and designing this whole system .	在這支影片中 , 我們看到我的學生帕納•密里 , 他真的是執行和設計這整個系統的天才 。
and we see how this system lets him walk up to any surface and start using his hands to interact with the information that is projected in front of him .	我們看到這個系統讓他走到任何表面 , 用他的手和投影在他面前的資訊互動 。
the system tracks the four significant fingers .	這個系統追蹤了四隻重要的手指 。
in this case , he's wearing simple marker caps that you may recognize .	在這個例子中 , 他戴著簡單的標記帽子 , 可以辨識出來 。
but if you want a more stylish version you could also paint your nails in different colors .	但如果你想要比較像風格的版本 , 你也可以用不同顏色畫出你的指甲 。
and the camera basically tracks these four fingers and recognizes any gestures that he's making so he can just go to , for example , a map of long beach , zoom in and out , etc .	攝影機基本上追蹤了這四隻手指 , 並辨識出他所做的任何動作 , 例如 , 他可以去看長海的地圖 , 放大 , 放大等等 。
the system also recognizes iconic gestures such as the " take a picture " gesture , and then takes a picture of whatever is in front of you .	系統也辨識出象徵性的手勢 , 例如 「 拍照 」 手勢 , 接著拍一張你面前的照片 。
and when he then walks back to the media lab , he can just go up to any wall and project all the pictures that he's taken , sort through them and organize them , and resize them , etc . , again using all natural gestures .	當他走回媒體實驗室時 , 他可以到任何牆上 , 投影他所拍攝的所有照片 , 透過照片 , 整理它們 , 再次重塑它們 , 再次使用所有的自然手勢 。
so , some of you most likely were here two years ago and saw the demo by jeff han or some of you may think , " well , doesn't this look like the microsoft surface table ? "	所以 , 有些人可能兩年前來到這裡 , 看到jeffhan的示威 , 有些人可能會想: 「 這不像微軟表面的表面嗎 ? 」
and yes , you also interact using natural gestures , both hands , etc .	沒錯 , 你也用天然手勢來互動 , 雙手等等 。
but the difference here is that you can use any surface , you can walk to up to any surface , including your hand if nothing else is available and interact with this projected data .	但這裡的差別是 , 你可以用任何表面 , 你可以走到任何表面 , 包括你的手 , 如果沒有其他東西可以使用 , 和這個投影資料互動 。
the device is completely portable , and can be . . .	這個裝置是完全可攜式的 , 也可以是......
so one important difference is that it's totally mobile .	其中一個很重要的差異是它完全是移動的 。
another even more important difference is that in mass production this would not cost more tomorrow than today's cell phones and would actually not sort of be a bigger packaging could look a lot more stylish than this version that i'm wearing around my neck .	另一個更重要的差別在於 , 在大量生產上 , 這不會比現今的手機貴得多 , 且不會比我在脖子上戴的更大的包裝看起來更像風格 。
but other than letting some of you live out your fantasy of looking as cool as tom cruise in " minority report , " the reason why we're really excited about this device is that it really can act as one of these sixthsense devices that gives you relevant information about whatever is in front of you .	但 , 除了讓你們之外 , 在《少數報告》中 , 湯姆•克魯斯 , 我們之所以對這個裝置感到很興奮的原因 , 是因為它真的可以作為這第六個感知裝置之一 , 讓你知道你面前的任何東西 。
so we see pranav here going into the supermarket and he's shopping for some paper towels .	這裡我們看到pranav進入超市 , 他正在購買一些紙巾 。
and , as he picks up a product the system can recognize the product that he's picking up , using either image recognition or marker technology , and give him the green light or an orange light .	當他拿起產品時 , 系統可以辨識出他拿到的產品 , 使用影像辨識或標記技術 , 給他綠光或橘色光 。
he can ask for additional information .	他可以要求額外的資訊 。
so this particular choice here is a particularly good choice , given his personal criteria .	所以 , 這個特定的選擇 , 尤其是他個人的標準 。
some of you may want the toilet paper with the most bleach in it rather than the most ecologicallyresponsible choice .	在座有些人可能想要有最毒的衛生紙 , 而不是最環保的選擇 。
if he picks up a book in the bookstore , he can get an amazon rating it gets projected right on the cover of the book .	如果他在書店裡拿起一本書 , 他就能拿到亞馬遜的評分 , 書的封面 。
this is juan's book , our previous speaker , which gets a great rating , by the way , at amazon .	這是朱安的書 , 我們之前的講者 , 順便說一下 , 亞馬遜的評分很棒 。
and so , pranav turns the page of the book and can then see additional information about the book reader comments , maybe sort of information by his favorite critic , etc .	所以 , 帕拉夫把書的頁面翻過來 , 還能看到書讀者留言的額外資訊 , 可能有點像是他最愛的批評 , 等等 。
if he turns to a particular page he finds an annotation by maybe an expert of a friend of ours that gives him a little bit of additional information about whatever is on that particular page .	如果他轉到某個特定的頁面 , 他會發現一個朋友的註冊 , 給他一點額外的資訊 , 關於那個頁面上的任何東西 。
reading the newspaper it never has to be outdated .	閱讀報紙 , 它永遠不會過時 。
you can get video annotations of the event that you're reading about you can get the latest sports scores etc .	你可以取得你閱讀的事件的影片註冊 , 你可以得到最新的運動分數等等 。
this is a more controversial one .	這更具爭議性 。
as you interact with someone at ted , maybe you can see a word cloud of the tags , the words that are associated with that person in their blog and personal web pages .	當你和ted的某人互動 , 也許你可以看見標籤的雲 , 和他在部落格和個人網頁中的那個人所說的話 。
in this case , the student is interested in cameras , etc .	在這個例子中 , 學生對攝影機感興趣 , 等等 。
on your way to the airport , if you pick up your boarding pass , it can tell you that your flight is delayed , that the gate has changed , etc .	在你的機場上 , 如果你拿起你的登機證 , 它可以告訴你你的飛行延遲了 , 門已經改變了 。
and , if you need to know what the current time is it's as simple as drawing a watch on your arm .	如果你需要知道目前的時光是什麼樣子 , 就如同你手臂上的手錶一樣簡單 。
so that's where we're at so far in developing this sixth sense that would give us seamless access to all this relevant information about the things that we may come across .	這就是我們目前正在發展的第六感 , 讓我們能無縫地取得我們可能遇到的所有相關資訊 。
my student pranav , who's really , like i said , the genius behind this .	我的學生panav , 正如我所說 , 這背後的天才 。
he does deserve a lot of applause because i don't think he's slept much in the last three months , actually .	他的確值得很多掌聲 , 因為我不認為他在過去三個月就睡太多了 。
and his girlfriend is probably not very happy about him either .	他的女友也可能對他也不滿意 。
but it's not perfect yet , it's very much a work in progress .	但它還不夠完美 , 它在進步上是很大的 。
and who knows , maybe in another 10 years we'll be here with the ultimate sixth sense brain implant .	誰知道 , 也許在接下來的十年內 , 我們會在這裡 , 最後的第六感大腦植入 。
phyllis rodriguez and aicha elwafi have a powerful friendship born of unthinkable loss . rodriguez' son was killed in the world trade center attacks on september 11 , 2001 ; elwafi's son zacarias moussaoui was convicted of a role in those attacks and is serving a life sentence . in hoping to find peace , these two moms have come to understand and respect one another .	菲利斯•羅德里格茲和亞歷山大•埃瓦菲有強大的友誼 , 出生於不可思議的損失 。 羅德里克斯的兒子在2001年九月十一日被殺害 ; 艾瓦菲的兒子薩科尼被指定在這些攻擊中 , 被定罪 , 同時也被判定為一生 。 希望找到和平 , 這兩個媽媽媽媽必須彼此了解並尊重 。
culture , global issues , politics	文化、全球議題、政治、政治、
9/11 healing: the mothers who found forgiveness , friendship	9/11療癒:找到寬恕的母親、友誼的母親 。
phyllis rodriguez: we are here today because of the fact that we have what most people consider an unusual friendship .	菲利斯•羅德里格斯:我們今天在這裡 , 是因為我們有大部分人認為的非比尋常的友誼 。
and yet , it feels natural to us now .	然而 , 我們現在感覺很自然 。
i first learned that my son had been in the world trade center on the morning of september 11th , 2001 .	我第一次發現我兒子在世界貿易中心在2001年9月11日的早上 。
we didn't know if he had perished yet until 36 hours later .	我們不知道他是否死亡 , 直到36小時後 。
at the time , we knew that it was political .	當時 , 我們知道它是政治的 。
we were afraid of what our country was going to do in the name of our son my husband , orlando , and i and our family .	我們害怕我們的國家會以我們的兒子名字來命名 , 我的丈夫 , 奧蘭多和我的家人 。
and when i saw it and yet , through the shock , the terrible shock , and the terrible explosion in our lives , literally , we were not vengeful .	當我看到它 , 但 , 透過震驚 , 恐怖的衝擊 , 以及人生中很糟糕的爆炸 , 真的 , 我們並沒有被毒殺 。
and a couple of weeks later when zacarias moussaoui was indicted on six counts of conspiracy to commit terrorism , and the u . s . government called for a death penalty for him , if convicted , my husband and i spoke out in opposition to that , publicly .	幾個禮拜後 , zacariasmoussaui指出六個陰謀致力於犯下恐怖主義 , 而美國政府要求他為死刑 , 如果定罪 , 我的丈夫和我在公開場合的對立 。
through that and through human rights groups , we were brought together with several other victims' families .	透過這點 , 透過人權團體 , 我們和其他受害者家人聚集在一起 。
when i saw aicha in the media , coming over when her son was indicted , and i thought , " what a brave woman .	當我在媒體上看到阿icha時 , 她兒子被指控 , 我心想: 「 什麼是勇敢的女人 。
someday i want to meet that woman when i'm stronger . "	有一天 , 我想要在我強壯的時候見那個女人 。 」
i was still in deep grief ; i knew i didn't have the strength .	我還在深刻的悲慟中 , 我知道我沒有力量 。
i knew i would find her someday , or we would find each other .	我知道有一天我會找到她 , 或者我們會找到彼此 。
because , when people heard that my son was a victim , i got immediate sympathy .	因為 , 當人們聽到我兒子是受害者時 , 我立即得到同情 。
but when people learned what her son was accused of , she didn't get that sympathy .	但當人們知道她的兒子被指控 , 她並沒有得到同情 。
but her suffering is equal to mine .	但她的苦難等於我 。
so we met in november 2002 , and aicha will now tell you how that came about .	我們在2002年11月見面 , 艾卡哈現在會告訴你那是怎麼來的 。
aicha elwafi: good afternoon , ladies and gentlemen .	阿ichaelfi:午安 , 各位先生女士 。
i am the mother of zacarias moussaoui .	我是祖魯人的母親 。
and i asked the organization of human rights to put me in touch with the parents of the victims .	我請人權組織讓我聯絡受害者的父母 。
so they introduced me to five families .	所以他們介紹我到五個家庭 。
and i saw phyllis , and i watched her .	我看到phyllis , 我看著她 。
she was the only mother in the group .	她是團體裡唯一的母親 。
the others were brothers , sisters .	其他人則是兄弟姐妹 。
and i saw in her eyes that she was a mother , just like me .	我在她的眼中看到她是母親 , 就像我一樣 。
i suffered a lot as a mother .	身為母親 , 我常受苦 。
i was married when i was 14 .	我十四歲時結婚 。
i lost a child when i was 15 , a second child when i was 16 .	我十五歲時失去了一個孩子 , 一個十六歲的第二個孩子 。
so the story with zacarias was too much really .	zacarias的故事實在太多了 。
and i still suffer , because my son is like he's buried alive .	我仍然受苦 , 因為我的兒子就像是他活著 。
i know she really cried for her son .	我知道她真的為她的兒子哭了 。
but she knows where he is .	但她知道他在哪裡 。
my son , i don't know where he is .	我兒子 , 我不知道他在哪裡 。
i don't know if he's alive . i don't know if he's tortured .	我不知道他是否活著 , 我不知道他有沒有折磨 。
i don't know what happened to him .	我不知道他發生了什麼事 。
so that's why i decided to tell my story , so that my suffering is something positive for other women .	這就是為什麼我決定說我的故事 , 所以我的苦難對其他女性來說是正面的 。
for all the women , all the mothers that give life , you can give back , you can change .	所有女性 , 所有給予生命的母親 , 你可以回饋 , 你可以改變 。
it's up to us women , because we are women , because we love our children .	取決於我們女性 , 因為我們是女性 , 因為我們愛我們的孩子 。
we must be handinhand and do something together .	我們必須攜手合作 。
it's not against women , it's for us , for us women , for our children .	不是反對女人 , 而是為了我們 , 為我們女人 , 為我們的孩子 。
i talk against violence , against terrorism .	我對抗暴力 , 反對恐怖主義 。
i go to schools to talk to young , muslim girls so they don't accept to be married against their will very young .	我去學校和年輕的穆斯林女孩談 , 讓他們不接受婚姻會很年輕 。
so if i can save one of the young girls , and avoid that they get married and suffer as much as i did , well this is something good .	所以 , 如果我能拯救其中一個年輕女孩 , 避免她們結婚和受苦 , 嗯 , 這是好事 。
this is why i'm here in front of you .	這就是為什麼我站在你們面前 。
pr: i would like to say that i have learned so much from aicha , starting with that day we had our very first meeting with other family members which was a very private meeting with security , because it was november 2002 , and , frankly , we were afraid of the superpatriotism of that time in the country those of us family members .	pr:我想說 , 我從阿icha學到很多 , 從那天開始 , 我們第一次和其他家庭成員會面 , 那是2002年11月的私人會議 , 坦白說 , 我們害怕那個國家的超級病患 。
but we were all so nervous .	但我們都很緊張 。
" why does she want to meet us ? "	「 為什麼她要和我們見面 ? 」
and then she was nervous .	然後她緊張了 。
" why did we want to meet her ? "	「 為什麼我們想要見到她 ? 」
what did we want from each other ?	我們彼此想要什麼 ?
before we knew each others' names , or anything , we had embraced and wept .	在我們知道彼此的名字之前 , 或任何事之前 , 我們都擁抱和哭泣 。
then we sat in a circle with support , with help , from people experienced in this kind of reconciliation .	接著 , 我們和支持、協助 , 坐在一個圈子裡 , 人們經歷到這種和解 。
and aicha started , and she said , " i don't know if my son is guilty or innocent , but i want to tell you how sorry i am for what happened to your families .	aicha開始說: 「 我不知道我的兒子是否有罪或無辜 , 但我想告訴各位 , 我對你的家庭的影響有多抱歉 。
i know what it is to suffer , and i feel that if there is a crime , a person should be tried fairly and punished . "	我知道受苦是什麼 , 我覺得如果有犯罪 , 一個人應該被公平審判 , 被懲罰 。 」
but she reached out to us in that way , and it was , i'd like to say , it was an icebreaker .	但她用那樣的方式向我們伸出援手 , 我會說 , 那是個冰架 。
and what happened then is we all told our stories , and we all connected as human beings .	接下來發生的是 , 我們都訴說了我們的故事 , 我們都以人類的身分連結 。
by the end of the afternoon it was about three hours after lunch we'd felt as if we'd known each other forever .	下午的結尾大約是午餐後的三小時 , 我們會覺得我們永遠都知道彼此 。
now what i learned from her , is a woman , not only who could be so generous under these present circumstances and what it was then , and what was being done to her son , but the life she's had .	我從她身上學到的是 , 一個女人 , 不僅可以在現有的環境下慷慨 , 以及當時的狀況 , 以及她兒子所做的事 , 還有她兒子的生活 。
i never had met someone with such a hard life , from such a totally different culture and environment from my own .	我從來沒有遇過這麼艱難的人生 , 來自完全不同的文化和環境 。
and i feel that we have a special connection , which i value very much .	我覺得我們有一種特別的連結 , 我很珍惜 。
and i think it's all about being afraid of the other , but making that step and then realizing , " hey , this wasn't so hard .	我認為這一切都是為了害怕對方 , 但要踏出這一步 , 然後意識到: 「 嘿 , 這並不難 。
who else can i meet that i don't know , or that i'm so different from ? "	我還能和誰見面 , 我不知道 , 或和我的不同 ? 」
so , aicha , do you have a couple of words for conclusion ?	所以 , 阿icha , 你有幾個字可以得到結論嗎 ?
because our time is up .	因為我們的時間到了 。
aw: i wanted to say that we have to try to know other people , the other .	艾美:我想說 , 我們得要試著認識別人 , 另一位 。
you have to be generous , and your hearts must be generous , your mind must be generous .	你必須是慷慨的 , 你的心必須是慷慨的 , 你的心智必須是慷慨的 。
you must be tolerant .	你必須忍受 。
you have to fight against violence .	你必須對抗暴力 。
and i hope that someday we'll all live together in peace and respecting each other .	我希望有一天我們會一起生活在和平中 , 並尊重彼此 。
this is what i wanted to say .	這是我想要說的 。
too much of the world lacks access to clean drinking water . engineer michael pritchard did something about it inventing the portable lifesaver filter , which can make the most revolting water drinkable in seconds . an amazing demo from tedglobal 2009 .	世上太多人缺乏乾淨的飲用水 。 工程師麥可•普萊特 , 做了一些事情 , 發明了可攜帶的生命過濾器 , 可以在幾秒鐘內做出最具反轉性的飲用水 。 這是2009年tedglobal的一個很棒的演變 。
business , demo , design , global issues , invention , technology , water	商業、mo、設計、全球議題、發明、科技、水、水、水 , 等等 。
michael pritchard's water filter turns filthy water drinkable	michaelprichard的水過濾會讓骯髒的水變乾淨 , 飲用水會變乾淨 。
i'd like to talk about a couple of things today .	今天我想談談幾件事 。
the first thing is water .	第一件事是水 。
now i see you've all been enjoying the water that's been provided for you here at the conference , over the past couple of days .	現在我看到你們都很享受在會議上為你們提供的水 , 在過去的幾天裡 。
and i'm sure you'll feel that it's from a safe source .	我相信你們會覺得這是來自安全的來源 。
but what if it wasn't ?	但如果不是這樣呢 ?
what if it was from a source like this ?	如果它是來自像這樣的來源呢 ?
then statistics would actually say that half of you would now be suffering with diarrhea .	接著 , 統計數字會說你們當中有一半的人會受腹瀉所苦 。
i talked a lot in the past about statistics , and the provision of safe drinking water for all .	我在過去談過很多關於統計的議題 , 以及所有人的安全飲用水 。
but they just don't seem to get through .	但他們似乎沒有經歷過 。
and i think i've worked out why .	我想我已經找出原因了 。
it's because , using current thinking , the scale of the problem just seems too huge to contemplate solving .	那是因為 , 使用目前的思考 , 問題的規模似乎太大了 , 無法思索解決 。
so we just switch off: us , governments and aid agencies .	所以我們關掉:我們 , 政府和援助機構 。
well , today , i'd like to show you that through thinking differently , the problem has been solved .	今天 , 我想用不同的角度來看 , 問題已經解決了 。
by the way , since i've been speaking , another 13 , 000 people around the world are suffering now with diarrhea .	順帶一提 , 自從我開始說話之後 , 世界各地又有一萬三千人受苦 。
and four children have just died .	四個孩子就死了 。
i invented lifesaver bottle because i got angry .	我發明了生命安全瓶 , 因為我生氣了 。
i , like most of you , was sitting down , the day after christmas in 2004 , when i was watching the devastating news of the asian tsunami as it rolled in , playing out on tv .	我和大部分人一樣 , 在2004年聖誕節過後的那天 , 我看著亞洲海嘯爆發的消息 , 在電視上播放 。
the days and weeks that followed , people fleeing to the hills , being forced to drink contaminated water or face death .	接下來的幾週 , 人們逃到山丘上 , 被迫喝污染的水或死亡 。
that really stuck with me .	這真的讓我印象深刻 。
then , a few months later , hurricane katrina slammed into the side of america .	接著 , 幾個月後 , 卡崔娜颶風衝向美國 。
" okay , " i thought , " here's a first world country , let's see what they can do . "	「 好吧 , 」 我想: 「 這裡是第一個世界國家 , 讓我們看看他們能做什麼 。 」
do you know it took five days to get water to the superdome ?	你知道花了五天才能把水送到超級迷嗎 ?
people were shooting each other on the streets for tv sets and water .	人們在街上互相槍擊電視機和水 。
that's when i decided i had to do something .	那是我決定要做點什麼的時候 。
now i spent a lot of time in my garage , over the next weeks and months , and also in my kitchen much to the dismay of my wife .	現在 , 我在車庫待了很多時間 , 在接下來的幾個禮拜和幾個月 , 在我的廚房裡 , 我太太太太太太太很不安 。
however , after a few failed prototypes , i finally came up with this , the lifesaver bottle .	然而 , 經過幾次失敗的原型之後 , 我終於想出了這個 , 救命瓶子 。
okay , now for the science bit .	好吧 , 現在來談談科學 。
before lifesaver , the best hand filters were only capable of filtering down to about 200 nanometers .	在救生員之前 , 最好的手過濾器只能過濾大約200奈米 。
the smallest bacteria is about 200 nanometers .	最小的細菌大約是200奈米 。
so a 200nanometer bacteria is going to get through a 200nanometer hole .	所以 , 一個200奈米的細菌會通過一個200奈米的洞 。
the smallest virus , on the other hand , is about 25 nanometers .	另一方面 , 最小的病毒大約是25奈米 。
so that's definitely going to get through those 200 nanometer holes .	這絕對會穿過那兩百奈米的洞 。
lifesaver pores are 15 nanometers .	生命體內水孔有15奈米 。
so nothing is getting through .	所以 , 沒有任何東西能穿過 。
okay , i'm going to give you a bit of a demonstration .	好 , 我來示範一下 。
would you like to see that ?	你想要看到嗎 ?
i spent all the time setting this up , so i guess i should .	我花了很多時間設定這件事 , 所以我想我應該這麼做 。
we're in the fine city of oxford .	我們正處於最好的牛津城市 。
so someone's done that up .	所以 , 有人這麼做了 。
fine city of oxford , so what i've done is i've gone and got some water from the river cherwell , and the river thames , that flow through here . and this is the water .	牛津的精華城市 , 我所做的是從河邊的水取得一些水 , 還有河流 , 流過這裡 。 這就是水 。
but i got to thinking , you know , if we were in the middle of a flood zone in bangladesh , the water wouldn't look like this .	但我想 , 如果我們在孟加拉的洪水區中央 , 水就不會像這樣 。
so i've gone and got some stuff to add into it .	所以 , 我做了一些東西來加入它 。
and this is from my pond .	這是來自我的池塘 。
have a smell of that , mister cameraman .	聞到一味 , 攝影師 。
we're just going to pour that in there .	我們就直接把它倒進去 。
michael pritchard: okay . we've got some runoff from a sewage plant farm .	michaelprichard:好的 , 我們有一些從污水廠跑過來的 。
so i'm just going to put that in there .	所以 , 我要把它放進去 。
put that in there . there we go .	把它放進去 , 就這樣 。
and some other bits and pieces , chuck that in there .	還有其他的部分和碎片 , 把它浸在裡面 。
and i've got a gift here from a friend of mine's rabbit .	我有一個來自我朋友的兔子的禮物 。
so we're just going to put that in there as well .	我們也要把它放進去 。
the lifesaver bottle works really simply .	救命瓶子很簡單 。
you just scoop the water up .	你只要把水分開來 。
today i'm going to use a jug just to show you all . let's get a bit of that poo in there .	今天我要用一個斷層給你們看 , 讓你們看一下吧 。
that's not dirty enough . let's just stir that up a little bit .	這還不夠髒 。 讓我們再稍微攪拌一下 。
okay , so i'm going to take this really filthy water , and put it in here . do you want a drink yet ?	好吧 , 我現在要用這個非常骯髒的水 , 把它放進去 。 你還想要飲料嗎 ?
okay . there we go .	好 , 開始了 。
give it a few pumps . okay ?	給一些幫浦 。 好嗎 ?
that's all that's necessary .	這就是必要的 。
now as soon as i pop the teat , sterile drinking water is going to come out .	一旦我把茶倒下 , 無菌的飲用水就會出現 。
i've got to be quick . okay , ready ?	我得快點 。 好 , 準備好了嗎 ?
there we go . mind the electrics .	就這樣 。 注意電 。
that is safe , sterile drinking water .	那是安全、無菌飲用水 。
there you go chris .	去克里斯 。
what's it taste of ?	它嚐到什麼 ?
let's see chris's program throughout the rest of the show . okay ?	我們來看看克里斯的節目在其餘的節目 。 好嗎 ?
okay . lifesaver bottle is used by thousands of people around the world .	好吧 , 世界各地有數以千計的人在使用生命安全瓶 。
it'll last for 6 , 000 liters .	它會維持六千公升 。
and when it's expired , using failsafe technology , the system will shut off , protecting the user .	儘管如此 , 使用失敗的技術 , 系統會關閉 , 保護使用者 。
pop the cartridge out . pop a new one in .	把貨車送出去 , 把一個新裝置進去 。
it's good for another 6 , 000 liters .	另外六千個公升是好的 。
so let's look at the applications .	咱們來看看應用 。
traditionally , in a crisis , what do we do ?	傳統上 , 在危機中 , 我們該怎麼做 ?
then , after a few weeks , we set up camps .	接著 , 幾個星期後 , 我們設立營地 。
and people are forced to come into the camps to get their safe drinking water .	人們被迫進入營地 , 取得安全的飲用水 。
what happens when 20 , 000 people congregate in a camp ?	當20萬人聚集在難民營時會發生什麼事 ?
diseases spread . more resources are required .	疾病散播 , 需要更多資源 。
the problem just becomes selfperpetuating .	問題就變成自我表達 。
but by thinking differently , and shipping these , people can stay put .	但透過不同的思考方式 , 運送這些東西 , 人們就可以保持下去 。
they can make their own sterile drinking water , and start to get on with rebuilding their homes and their lives .	他們可以自己製造無菌飲用水 , 開始重建家園和生活 。
now , it doesn't require a natural disaster for this to work .	現在 , 這並不需要自然災害才能成功 。
using the old thinking , of national infrastructure and pipe work , is too expensive .	用舊的想法 , 國家基礎建設和管道工作 , 實在太貴了 。
when you run the numbers on a calculator , you run out of noughts .	當你在計算器上運行數字時 , 你就跑出來了 。
so here is the " thinking different " bit .	這裡是 「 思考不同 」 的部分 。
instead of shipping water , and using manmade processes to do it , let's use mother nature . she's got a fantastic system .	不要運送水 , 用人造的過程來做 , 讓我們用大自然 。 她有一個很棒的系統 。
she picks the water up from there , desalinates it , for free , transports it over there , and dumps it onto the mountains , rivers , and streams .	她從那裡取得水 , 免費地將水淡化 , 運送到那裡 , 把它丟到山上、河流 , 和河流上 。
and where do people live ? near water .	人們住在哪裡 ? 靠近水 。
all we've go to do is make it sterile . how do we do that ?	我們要做的就是讓它變得無菌 , 我們要怎麼做 ?
well , we could use the lifesaver bottle .	嗯 , 我們可以用救命瓶子 。
or we could use one of these .	或者 , 我們可以用其中一種 。
the same technology , in a jerry can .	同樣的技術 , 在jerry的罐子裡 。
this will process 25 , 000 liters of water ; that's good enough for a family of four , for three years .	這會處理2萬5千公升的水 ; 這對四個家庭來說已經夠好了 , 三年了 。
and how much does it cost ?	要花多少錢 ?
about half a cent a day to run .	每天花費約半美分 。
so , by thinking differently , and processing water at the point of use , mothers and children no longer have to walk four hours a day to collect their water .	所以 , 透過不同的思考方式 , 在使用水的時候 , 母親和孩子們不再需要每天走四個小時來收集他們的水 。
they can get it from a source nearby .	他們可以從附近的來源取得 。
so with just eight billion dollars , we can hit the millennium goal's target of halving the number of people without access to safe drinking water .	只要花八十億美金 , 我們就能達到千禧目標 , 目標是要把沒有安全飲用水的人數減少 。
to put that into context , the u . k . government spends about 12 billion pounds a year on foreign aid .	將其放入情境中 , 英國政府每年花費大約一百二十億英鎊給外援 。
but why stop there ?	但為什麼要停止 ?
with 20 billion dollars , everyone can have access to safe drinking water .	有了20億美元 , 每個人都能取得安全的飲用水 。
so the threeandahalf billion people that suffer every year as a result , and the two million kids that die every year , will live .	結果每年有三十五億人受苦 , 每年死亡的兩百萬名孩子 , 會活下去 。
paddy ashdown claims that we are living in a moment in history where power is changing in ways it never has before . in a spellbinding talk at tedxbrussels he outlines the three major global shifts that he sees coming .	paddyashdown聲稱我們生活在歷史上 , 權力正在改變的方式 , 從來沒有改變過 。 在tedxbrussel的拼字演說中 , 他排除了他所見的三大全球變遷 。
foreign policy , global issues , politics , world cultures	外交政策 , 全球議題 , 政治 , 世界文化 , 文化 。
paddy ashdown: the global power shift	paddyashdown:全球的權力轉變 。
there's a poem written by a very famous english poet at the end of the 19th century .	十九世紀末 , 有一首非常有名的英文詩人寫的詩 。
it was said to echo in churchill's brain in the 1930s .	在三十年代 , 有人說要在教堂的腦袋裡回音 。
and the poem goes: " on the idle hill of summer , lazy with the flow of streams , hark i hear a distant drummer , drumming like a sound in dreams , far and near and low and louder on the roads of earth go by , dear to friend and food to powder , soldiers marching , soon to die . "	然後這首詩說: 「 在夏天的冰山 , 和河流的流動下 , 我聽到一個遙遠的鼓聲 , 像在夢裡的聲響 , 距離很低 , 越來越大聲的道路上 , 親愛的朋友和食物到粉末 , 士兵們遊行 , 很快就死了 。 」
those who are interested in poetry , the poem is " a shropshire lad " written by a . e . housman .	那些對詩歌感興趣的人 , 這首詩是 " 蝦子女士 " 由a.e.休斯曼所寫 。
but what housman understood , and you hear it in the symphonies of nielsen too , was that the long , hot , silvan summers of stability of the 19th century were coming to a close , and that we were about to move into one of those terrifying periods of history when power changes .	但 , 休士人了解的 , 你也在尼爾森的交響樂中聽到了 , 就是十九世紀的漫長、熱、西爾文的夏天 , 即將接近 , 而我們即將進入歷史上最可怕的時期之一 。
and these are always periods , ladies and gentlemen , accompanied by turbulence , and all too often by blood .	這些都是時期 , 各位先生女士 , 伴隨著亂流 , 經常是血液 。
and my message for you is that i believe we are condemned , if you like , to live at just one of those moments in history when the gimbals upon which the established order of power is beginning to change and the new look of the world , the new powers that exist in the world , are beginning to take form .	我對你們的訊息是 , 我相信我們已經被確認了 , 只活在歷史上的那些時刻 , 那些被建立的秩序開始改變世界的新看法 , 新的勢力 , 世界存在的新勢力開始形成 。
and these are and we see it very clearly today nearly always highly turbulent times , highly difficult times , and all too often very bloody times .	今天我們很清楚地看到它幾乎每次都非常混亂 , 極度困難 , 且經常是血腥時期 。
by the way , it happens about once every century .	順便一提 , 它發生在每世紀一次 。
you might argue that the last time it happened and that's what housman felt coming and what churchill felt too was that when power passed from the old nations , the old powers of europe , across the atlantic to the new emerging power of the united states of america the beginning of the american century .	你也許會主張 , 最後一次發生了 , 休士人也感受到了 , 教會也感受到 , 當權力從舊國家、歐洲的老勢力 , 跨越大西洋到美國新興的新興國家 , 美國本世紀初期 。
and of course , into the vacuum where the tooold european powers used to be were played the two bloody catastrophes of the last century the one in the first part and the one in the second part: the two great world wars .	當然 , 在真空中 , 以前歐洲人的力量 , 都是在上個世紀的兩個血腥災難 , 第一部分 , 第二部分是:兩次世界大戰 。
mao zedong used to refer to them as the european civil wars , and it's probably a more accurate way of describing them .	maozedong以前稱呼他們為歐洲內戰 , 這可能是更準確的描述他們的方式 。
well , ladies and gentlemen , we live at one of those times .	各位先生女士 , 我們生活在其中之一 。
but for us , i want to talk about three factors today .	但對我們來說 , 我今天要談的三個因素 。
and the first of these , the first two of these , is about a shift in power .	第一種 , 第一種是權力的轉變 。
and the second is about some new dimension which i want to refer to , which has never quite happened in the way it's happening now .	第二 , 關於一些新的維度我想說的是 , 這種維度從來沒有發生過 。
but let's talk about the shifts of power that are occurring to the world .	但讓我們來談談權力的轉變 , 發生在世界上 。
and what is happening today is , in one sense , frightening because it's never happened before .	今天發生的是 , 在某種意義上 , 害怕 , 因為它從來沒有發生過 。
we have seen lateral shifts of power the power of greece passed to rome and the power shifts that occurred during the european civilizations but we are seeing something slightly different .	我們已經見識過希臘的力量轉移到羅馬的力量和在歐洲文明發生的權力轉移但我們卻看到一些稍微不同的東西
for power is not just moving laterally from nation to nation .	權力不只從國家轉移到國家 。
it's also moving vertically .	它也垂直移動 。
what's happening today is that the power that was encased , held to accountability , held to the rule of law , within the institution of the nation state has now migrated in very large measure onto the global stage .	現今正在發生的力量是 , 被監禁的權力 , 被控訴法律規則 , 在國家的制度中 , 現在已經遷移到極大的全球舞台上 。
the globalization of power we talk about the globalization of markets , but actually it's the globalization of real power .	全球化的權力我們談的是全球化市場 , 但實際上它是全球化的權力 。
and where , at the nation state level that power is held to accountability subject to the rule of law , on the international stage it is not .	在國家的層級上 , 權力被控訴法律的規則 , 在國際舞台上 , 它不是 。
the international stage and the global stage where power now resides: the power of the internet , the power of the satellite broadcasters , the power of the money changers this vast moneygoround that circulates now 32 times the amount of money necessary for the trade it's supposed to be there to finance the money changers , if you like , the financial speculators that have brought us all to our knees quite recently , the power of the multinational corporations now developing budgets often bigger than mediumsized countries .	國際舞台和全球各地的權力 , 網際網路的力量 , 衛星廣播者的力量 , 金錢改變了這個廣大的金錢改革者的力量 , 交通的金額現在是貿易所必要的三十二倍 , 該有金錢去補助金錢的改變者 , 如果你喜歡的話 , 金融的推動者將我們全都帶到我們的膝蓋上 , 最近 , 大量的跨國企業的力量 , 大幅發展 , 大幅增加了大幅發展中國家 。
these live in a global space which is largely unregulated , not subject to the rule of law , and in which people may act free of constraint .	這些生活在一個完全沒有規範的全球空間 , 而非法律規則 , 而在其中 , 人們可能不受限制 。
now that suits the powerful up to a moment .	這跟強而有力的時刻有關 。
it's always suitable for those who have the most power to operate in spaces without constraint , but the lesson of history is that , sooner or later , unregulated space space not subject to the rule of law becomes populated , not just by the things you wanted international trade , the internet , etc . but also by the things you don't want international criminality , international terrorism .	那些在沒有限制的情況下 , 最有權力的人 , 總是適當的 , 但歷史的教訓是:很快 , 或很快地 , 沒有受到法律規範的影響 , 不只是你想要的國際貿易 , 網路等等 。 還有你不想要的國際犯罪 , 國際恐怖主義 。
the revelation of 9/11 is that even if you are the most powerful nation on earth , nevertheless , those who inhabit that space can attack you even in your most iconic of cities one bright september morning .	911事件的揭示是 , 即使你是地球上最強大的國家 , 儘管如此 , 那些住在那空間的人 , 甚至可以攻擊你最具代表性的城市 , 一個九月早晨 。
it's said that something like 60 percent of the four million dollars that was taken to fund 9/11 actually passed through the institutions of the twin towers which 9/11 destroyed .	據說 , 佔了四百萬美金的百分之六十 , 被送到911恐怖攻擊的金額 , 實際上通過了雙胞胎塔的機構 , 911摧毀了 。
you see , our enemies also use this space the space of mass travel , the internet , satellite broadcasters to be able to get around their poison , which is about destroying our systems and our ways .	我們的敵人也用這個空間 , 大眾旅行、網路、衛星廣播 , 來抵達它們的毒物 , 也就是破壞我們的系統和方法 。
sooner or later , sooner or later , the rule of history is that where power goes governance must follow .	不久後 , 不久後 , 歷史的規則就是權力的治理必須跟隨 。
and if it is therefore the case , as i believe it is , that one of the phenomenon of our time is the globalization of power , then it follows that one of the challenges of our time is to bring governance to the global space .	正如我所說的 , 假如我相信 , 我們這個時代的一個現象就是全球化的權力 , 那麼我們這個時代的挑戰就是把統治力帶到全球 。
and i believe that the decades ahead of us now will be to a greater or lesser extent turbulent the more or less we are able to achieve that aim: to bring governance to the global space .	我相信 , 未來的幾十年 , 將會是更大或更少的亂流 , 我們能夠達成這個目標:把治理帶到全球 。
now notice , i'm not talking about government .	請注意 , 我不是在說政府 。
i'm not talking about setting up some global democratic institution .	我不是在說要設立一些全球性的民主機構 。
my own view , by the way , ladies and gentlemen , is that this is unlikely to be done by spawning more u . n . institutions .	順帶一提 , 我自己的觀點是 , 女士們先生們 , 這種觀點不太可能是出發更多聯合國的機構 。
if we didn't have the u . n . , we'd have to invent it .	如果我們沒有聯合國 , 我們就得要發明它 。
the world needs an international forum .	世界需要一個國際論壇 。
it needs a means by which you can legitimize international action .	它需要一種方法 , 你可以合法化國際行動 。
but when it comes to governance of the global space , my guess is this won't happen through the creation of more u . n . institutions .	但當談到管理全球空間時 , 我的猜測是 , 這不會發生在聯合國制度的創建中 。
it will actually happen by the powerful coming together and making treatybased systems , treatybased agreements , to govern that global space .	它會由強大的力量團結起來 , 建立以條約為基礎的系統、以條約為基礎的協議 , 來管理全球空間 。
and if you look , you can see them happening , already beginning to emerge .	如果你看 , 你可以看到它們正在發生 , 已經開始出現了 。
the world trade organization: treatybased organization , entirely treatybased , and yet , powerful enough to hold even the most powerful , the united states , to account if necessary .	世界貿易組織:以條約為基礎的組織 , 完全以條約為基礎 , 但 , 強大到能夠容納最強大的國家 , 美國是必要的 。
kyoto: the beginnings of struggling to create a treatybased organization .	kyoto:努力創建一個以條約為基礎的組織 。
the g20: we know now that we have to put together an institution which is capable of bringing governance to that financial space for financial speculation .	二十國:我們現在知道 , 我們得要組合一個機構 , 讓治理可以帶到金融空間 , 來做金融推測 。
and that's what the g20 is , a treatybased institution .	這就是g20的主要原因 , 一個以條約為基礎的機構 。
now there's a problem there , and we'll come back to it in a minute , which is that if you bring the most powerful together to make the rules in treatybased institutions , to fill that governance space , then what happens to the weak who are left out ?	現在有個問題 , 我們等一下再回來談談 , 如果你把最強大的力量結合起來 , 以條約為基礎的機構 , 來填補治理的空間 , 那麼弱者會發生什麼事 ?
and that's a big problem , and we'll return to it in just a second .	這是個大問題 , 我們等一下就會回到問題上 。
so there's my first message , that if you are to pass through these turbulent times more or less turbulently , then our success in doing that will in large measure depend on our capacity to bring sensible governance to the global space .	所以這是我第一個要傳遞的訊息 , 如果你要越過這些亂流的時間越多 , 那麼我們的成功會大大地取決於我們的能力 , 將合理的治理帶到全球 。
and watch that beginning to happen .	看著它開始發生 。
my second point is , and i know i don't have to talk to an audience like this about such a thing , but power is not just shifting vertically , it's also shifting horizontally .	我的第二點是 , 我知道我不需要和像這樣的觀眾談談 , 但權力不只是垂直轉變 , 也在轉變 。
you might argue that the story , the history of civilizations , has been civilizations gathered around seas with the first ones around the mediterranean , the more recent ones in the ascendents of western power around the atlantic .	你可能會認為 , 文明的歷史 , 已經在海裡聚集在地中海最初的文明 , 越是近期的文明 , 出現在大西方勢力的衝突中 。
well it seems to me that we're now seeing a fundamental shift of power , broadly speaking , away from nations gathered around the atlantic [seaboard] to the nations gathered around the pacific rim .	我看來 , 我們現在看到的是權力的轉變 , 廣泛地說 , 遠離大西洋公園周圍的國家聚集在太平洋岸邊緣的國家 。
now that begins with economic power , but that's the way it always begins .	這從經濟力量開始 , 但這一直是這樣開始的 。
you already begin to see the development of foreign policies , the augmentation of military budgets occurring in the other growing powers in the world .	你已經開始看到外國政策的發展 , 軍事預算的擴增 , 發生在世界上其他增長的力量 。
i think actually this is not so much a shift from the west to the east ; something different is happening .	我認為這並不是西方移民的轉變 , 而是有不同的事情發生了 。
my guess is , for what it's worth , is that the united states will remain the most powerful nation on earth for the next 10 years , 15 , but the context in which she holds her power has now radically altered ; it has radically changed .	我的猜測是 , 值得的是 , 美國會留住地球上最強大的國家 , 未來十年、十五年 , 但她持有的權力已經徹底改變了 ; 它徹底改變了 。
we are coming out of 50 years , most unusual years , of history in which we have had a totally monopolar world , in which every compass needle for or against has to be referenced by its position to washington a world bestrode by a single colossus .	我們正從50年來 , 史上最不尋常的年份 , 歷史中 , 我們有一個完全獨一無二的世界 , 每一個羅盤都必須被它的位置給華盛頓 , 一個單一的大科索斯所指出的世界 。
but that's not a usual case in history .	但這不是歷史上常見的案例 。
in fact , what's now emerging is the much more normal case of history .	事實上 , 現在出現的是更正常的歷史 。
you're beginning to see the emergence of a multipolar world .	你開始看到一個多向世界的出現 。
up until now , the united states has been the dominant feature of our world .	到目前為止 , 美國一直是世界的主導特徵 。
they will remain the most powerful nation , but they will be the most powerful nation in an increasingly multipolar world .	他們會維持最強大的國家 , 但他們會是世界上越來越強大的國家 。
and you begin to see the alternative centers of power building up in china , of course , though my own guess is that china's ascent to greatness is not smooth .	你開始看到中國的替代權力中心當然 , 我的猜測是中國的優勢不是平滑的 。
it's going to be quite grumpy as china begins to democratize her society after liberalizing her economy .	隨著中國在自由化經濟後 , 開始將她的社會民主化 。
but that's a subject of a different discussion .	但這是個不同的討論 。
you see india , you see brazil .	你看到印度 , 巴西 。
you see increasingly that the world now looks actually , for us europeans , much more like europe in the 19th century .	你可以看到 , 越來越多的歐洲人看起來 , 更像十九世紀的歐洲人 。
europe in the 19th century: a great british foreign secretary , lord canning , used to describe it as the " european concert of powers . "	十九世紀的歐洲:一個英國外交部長 , 倫敦罐頭 , 用來形容它是 「 歐洲的權力協會 」 。
there was a balance , a fivesided balance .	有一個平衡 , 一個五邊的平衡 。
britain always played to the balance .	英國總是為了平衡而扮演 。
if paris got together with berlin , britain got together with vienna and rome to provide a counterbalance .	如果巴黎和柏林一起 , 英國和維也納和羅馬合作 , 來提供平衡 。
now notice , in a period which is dominated by a monopolar world , you have fixed alliances nato , the warsaw pact .	請注意 , 在這段期間 , 由單一世界主宰的期間 , 你有固定的聯盟 , nato , 戰爭的先驅 。
a fixed polarity of power means fixed alliances .	一個固定的權力 , 意味著聯盟 。
but a multiple polarity of power means shifting and changing alliances .	但多種權力的對立意味著轉變和改變聯盟 。
and that's the world we're coming into , in which we will increasingly see that our alliances are not fixed .	這就是我們要進入的世界 , 我們會漸漸看到我們的聯盟不是固定的 。
canning , the great british foreign secretary once said , " britain has a common interest , but no common allies . "	坎林 , 偉大的英國外交部長曾經說過: 「 英國有很大的利益 , 但沒有普遍的盟友 。 」
and we will see increasingly that even we in the west will reach out , have to reach out , beyond the cozy circle of the atlantic powers to make alliances with others if we want to get things done in the world .	我們會逐漸看到 , 即使我們西方國家會伸出援手 , 必須伸出援手 , 超越大西洋的力量圈 , 才能和其他人聯盟 , 如果我們想讓世界上的一切都做得更好 。
note , that when we went into libya , it was not good enough for the west to do it alone ; we had to bring others in .	注意 , 當我們進入利比亞時 , 西方國家並不夠好 , 我們得要把其他人帶進來 。
we had to bring , in this case , the arab league in .	在這個例子中 , 我們必須把阿拉伯聯盟帶進來 。
my guess is iraq and afghanistan are the last times when the west has tried to do it themselves , and we haven't succeeded .	我的猜測是伊拉克和阿富汗是西方試過的最後一次 , 我們還沒成功 。
my guess is that we're reaching the beginning of the end of 400 years i say 400 years because it's the end of the ottoman empire of the hegemony of western power , western institutions and western values .	我想 , 我們已經達到400年底了 , 我說400年了 , 因為那是西方國家權力的終結 , 西方的西方國家制度和西方價值觀的終結 。
you know , up until now , if the west got its act together , it could propose and dispose in every corner of the world .	你知道 , 到目前為止 , 如果西方國家團結起來 , 它可以在世界上的每一個角落提出並消除 。
but that's no longer true .	但這已經不再是事實了 。
take the last financial crisis after the second world war .	以第二次世界大戰後的金融危機為例 。
the west got together the bretton woods institution , world bank , international monetary fund the problem solved .	西方國家聚集了布雷頓森林機構 , 世界銀行 , 國際貨幣基金--這個問題解決了 。
now we have to call in others .	現在我們必須在別人身上打電話 。
now we have to create the g20 .	現在我們必須創造g20 。
now we have to reach beyond the cozy circle of our western friends .	現在我們必須超越西方朋友圈 。
let me make a prediction for you , which is probably even more startling .	讓我為你們做個預測 , 這可能更令人吃驚 。
i suspect we are now reaching the end of 400 years when western power was enough .	我懷疑我們現在已經達到400年底了 , 那時西方的權力已經足夠了 。
people say to me , " the chinese , of course , they'll never get themselves involved in peacemaking , multilateral peacemaking around the world . "	人們對我說: 「 中國 , 當然 , 他們永遠不會參與和平協會 , 全世界的多邊和平協會 。 」
oh yes ? why not ?	喔 ? 為什麼不呢 ?
how many chinese troops are serving under the blue beret , serving under the blue flag , serving under the u . n . command in the world today ?	有多少位中國軍隊在藍色的貝雷下服役 , 在藍色的旗子下服役 , 在聯合國指揮下服役 ?
how many americans ? 11 .	有多少美國人 ? 十一歲 。
what is the largest naval contingent tackling the issue of somali pirates ?	什麼是最大的海軍隊處理索馬利海盜的問題 ?
the chinese naval contingent .	中國的指導內容 。
of course they are , they are a mercantilist nation .	當然 , 他們是一名合併主義的國家 。
they want to keep the sea lanes open .	他們想要保持海道開放 。
increasingly , we are going to have to do business with people with whom we do not share values , but with whom , for the moment , we share common interests .	漸漸地 , 我們得要和那些不分享價值觀的人做生意 , 同時 , 我們有共同的利益 。
it's a whole new different way of looking at the world that is now emerging .	這是一個全新的角度來看現在正在興起的世界 。
and here's the third factor , which is totally different .	第三個因素是完全不同的 。
today in our modern world , because of the internet , because of the kinds of things people have been talking about here , everything is connected to everything .	現今 , 在我們的現代世界裡 , 由於網路 , 因為人們在這裡談論的東西 , 一切都和所有事物有關 。
we are now interdependent .	我們現在是相互依賴的 。
we are now interlocked , as nations , as individuals , in a way which has never been the case before , never been the case before .	我們現在被封鎖 , 作為國家 , 作為個體 , 在以前從來沒有這樣過 , 以前從來沒有這樣過 。
the interrelationship of nations , well it's always existed .	國家之間的關聯性 , 它總是存在的 。
diplomacy is about managing the interrelationship of nations .	外交是管理國家之間的關聯性 。
but now we are intimately locked together .	但現在我們被緊密鎖住了 。
you get swine flu in mexico , it's a problem for charles de gaulle airport 24 hours later .	你在墨西哥有豬流感 , 查爾斯•高爾的機場在24小時後就有問題了 。
lehman brothers goes down , the whole lot collapses .	雷曼兄弟下降了 , 整個崩潰了 。
there are fires in the steppes of russia , food riots in africa .	俄羅斯的大草原、非洲的食物暴動 。
we are all now deeply , deeply , deeply interconnected .	我們現在都深深、深切的相互連結 。
and what that means is the idea of a nation state acting alone , not connected with others , not working with others , is no longer a viable proposition .	這意味著 , 一個國家獨立行動的理念 , 和他人連結 , 而非和他人合作 , 不再是個可行的建議 。
because the actions of a nation state are neither confined to itself , nor is it sufficient for the nation state itself to control its own territory , because the effects outside the nation state are now beginning to affect what happens inside them .	因為一個國家的行動本身也不被限制 , 也不足以讓國家自己控制自己的領土 , 因為國家的影響已經開始影響他們內在的狀況 。
i was a young soldier in the last of the small empire wars of britain .	我是英國最後一個小型帝國戰爭的年輕士兵 。
at that time , the defense of my country was about one thing and one thing only: how strong was our army , how strong was our air force , how strong was our navy and how strong were our allies .	那時 , 我國家的防禦 , 只有一件事:我們的軍隊有多強壯 , 我們的空軍有多強壯 , 我們的海軍有多強壯 , 我們的盟友有多強壯 。
that was when the enemy was outside the walls .	那是敵人在牆外的時候 。
now the enemy is inside the walls .	敵人在牆壁裡 。
now if i want to talk about the defense of my country , i have to speak to the minister of health because pandemic disease is a threat to my security , i have to speak to the minister of agriculture because food security is a threat to my security , i have to speak to the minister of industry because the fragility of our hitech infrastructure is now a point of attack for our enemies as we see from cyber warfare i have to speak to the minister of home affairs because who has entered my country , who lives in that terraced house in that inner city has a direct effect on what happens in my country as we in london saw in the 7/7 bombings .	現在 , 如果我想要談談我國家的防禦 , 我得要和健康部長談談 , 因為流行疾病對我的安全是威脅 , 我得要和農業部長談談 , 因為糧食保障對我的保安 , 我得要和工業部談談談 , 因為我們的希臘基礎建設的脆弱 , 現在我們看到敵人對我們的敵人來說 , 在網路戰場上 , 我得要談談談談談我們國家的影響 , 因為在77個國家裡 , 在我的家裡 , 貧民窟裡 , 貧民窟裡 , 貧民窟裡 , 貧民區的家裡 , 貧民窟裡 , 貧民窟裡 , 貧民窟裡 , 貧民區的家裡 , 貧民區已經發生了 。
it's no longer the case that the security of a country is simply a matter for its soldiers and its ministry of defense .	一個國家的安全性不再只是對士兵及國防的重要性 。
it's its capacity to lock together its institutions .	它是將其制度結合的能力 。
and this tells you something very important .	這告訴你們一件很重要的事 。
it tells you that , in fact , our governments , vertically constructed , constructed on the economic model of the industrial revolution vertical hierarchy , specialization of tasks , command structures have got the wrong structures completely .	它告訴你 , 事實上 , 我們的政府 , 垂直建構 , 建立在工業革命的經濟模式上 , 垂直的階級制度 , 任務的專業化 , 指令結構完全錯了 。
you in business know that the paradigm structure of our time , ladies and gentlemen , is the network .	在商業界 , 各位先生女士 , 這種模式就是網路 。
it's your capacity to network that matters , both within your governments and externally .	網絡的能力很重要 , 不論是你的政府或外部 。
so here is ashdown's third law .	這裡是shdown的第三定律 。
by the way , don't ask me about ashdown's first law and second law because i haven't invented those yet ; it always sounds better if there's a third law , doesn't it ?	順帶一提 , 不要問我阿什登第一定律和第二定律 , 因為我還沒發明過這些 ; 如果有第三定律 , 聽起來就會比較好 , 對吧 ?
ashdown's third law is that in the modern age , where everything is connected to everything , the most important thing about what you can do is what you can do with others .	ashdown第三定律是 , 在現代 , 每件事都和每件事連結在一起 , 最重要的事就是你能做的事 , 就是你能做的事 。
the most important bit about your structure whether you're a government , whether you're an army regiment , whether you're a business is your docking points , your interconnectors , your capacity to network with others .	不管你是政府 , 不管你是軍隊註冊 , 不管你是企業 , 是你的支票點 , 你的連結點 , 和他人建立網路的能力 。
you understand that in industry ; governments don't .	你明白這一點 , 在產業裡 , 政府不懂 。
but now one final thing .	但最後一件事 。
if it is the case , ladies and gentlemen and it is that we are now locked together in a way that has never been quite the same before , then it's also the case that we share a destiny with each other .	如果是這樣的 , 各位先生女士 , 女士們 , 我們現在被關在以前從來沒有完全相同的情況下 , 那也是我們彼此命運的案例 。
suddenly and for the very first time , collective defense , the thing that has dominated us as the concept of securing our nations , is no longer enough .	突然間 , 集體防禦 , 主導我們作為保護國家安全的概念 , 已經不夠了 。
it used to be the case that if my tribe was more powerful than their tribe , i was safe ; if my country was more powerful than their country , i was safe ; my alliance , like nato , was more powerful than their alliance , i was safe .	以前 , 如果我的部落比他們的部落更強大 , 我是安全的 ; 如果我的國家比他們的國家更強大 , 我是安全的 ; 我的盟友 , 像是nato , 比他們的盟友更強大 , 我很安全 。
it is no longer the case .	它不再是案例了 。
the advent of the interconnectedness and of the weapons of mass destruction means that , increasingly , i share a destiny with my enemy .	大規模毀滅性武器的出現意味著 , 我和敵人有越來越多的命運 。
when i was a diplomat negotiating the disarmament treaties with the soviet union in geneva in the 1970s , we succeeded because we understood we shared a destiny with them .	1970年代 , 我曾和日內瓦的蘇聯協商協商 , 我們成功 , 因為我們知道我們和他們分享了命運 。
collective security is not enough .	集體安全不夠 。
peace has come to northern ireland because both sides realized that the zerosum game couldn't work .	和平來到北愛爾蘭 , 因為雙方意識到零和遊戲無法運作 。
they shared a destiny with their enemies .	他們和敵人分享了命運 。
one of the great barriers to peace in the middle east is that both sides , both israel and , i think , the palestinians , do not understand that they share a collective destiny .	在中東和平的一個大障礙是以色列和巴勒斯坦人的兩邊 , 他們並不知道他們有共同的命運 。
and so suddenly , ladies and gentlemen , what has been the proposition of visionaries and poets down the ages becomes something we have to take seriously as a matter of public policy .	所以 , 女士們先生們 , 先生們 , 遠見者和詩人的主張 , 我們必須認真看待公共政策 。
i started with a poem , i'll end with one .	我從一首詩開始 , 我會用一首 。
the great poem of john donne's .	約翰•唐諾的偉大詩 。
" send not for whom the bell tolls . "	「 不要送誰去花錢 。 」
the poem is called " no man is an island . "	這首詩叫做 「 沒有人是一座島嶼 。 」
and it goes: " every man's death affected me , for i am involved in mankind , send not to ask for whom the bell tolls , it tolls for thee . "	答案是: 「 每個男人的死亡都會影響我 , 因為我涉及人類 , 不要去尋求誰的鈴聲 , 要去找誰 。 」
for john donne , a recommendation of morality .	對於約翰唐諾 , 一種道德的建議 。
for us , i think , part of the equation for our survival .	對我們來說 , 我認為 , 是我們生存的一部分 。
to find the path to long life and health , dan buettner and team study the world's " blue zones , " communities whose elders live with vim and vigor to recordsetting age . at tedxtc , he shares the 9 common diet and lifestyle habits that keep them spry past age 100 .	為了找到長壽和健康的路 , 丹•布特納和團隊研究世界的 「 藍色區域 」 , 他們的長輩和維京人住在一起 , 在tedxtc記錄年齡 。 他分享了9種常見的飲食習慣 , 讓他們能在一百歲之前流行 。
biology , culture , exploration , food , health , life , science	生物學、文化、探索、食物、健康、生命、科學、科學、科學 。
dan buettner: how to live to be 100+	丹•布伊特納:如何活到一百倍+
something called the danish twin study established that only about 10 percent of how long the average person lives , within certain biological limits , is dictated by our genes .	丹麥雙胞胎研究發現 , 一般人的平均壽命只有百分之十 , 在某些生物限制下 , 是由我們的基因決定 。
the other 90 percent is dictated by our lifestyle .	另外百分之九十是由生活方式主宰 。
so the premise of blue zones: if we can find the optimal lifestyle of longevity we can come up with a de facto formula for longevity .	所以 , 藍色區域的前提是:如果我們能找到長壽的最佳生活方式 , 我們就能找到長壽的事實公式 。
but if you ask the average american what the optimal formula of longevity is , they probably couldn't tell you .	但如果你問美國人長壽的最佳公式 , 他們可能不會告訴你 。
they've probably heard of the south beach diet , or the atkins diet .	他們可能聽說過南海灘的飲食 , 或墨水的飲食 。
you have the usda food pyramid .	你有美國食品金字塔 。
there is what oprah tells us .	歐普拉告訴我們 ,
there is what doctor oz tells us .	奧茲醫生告訴我們什麼 。
the fact of the matter is there is a lot of confusion around what really helps us live longer better .	事實是 , 對於真正幫助我們活得更好的事物 , 有很多困惑 。
should you be running marathons or doing yoga ?	你應該跑馬拉松還是做瑜伽 ?
should you eat organic meats or should you be eating tofu ?	你應該吃有機肉還是應該吃豆腐 ?
when it comes to supplements , should you be taking them ?	談到供應時 , 你應該要拿它們嗎 ?
how about these hormones or resveratrol ?	荷爾蒙或復育運動呢 ?
and does purpose play into it ?	是否有目的呢 ?
spirituality ? and how about how we socialize ?	精神 ? 我們如何社交呢 ?
well , our approach to finding longevity was to team up with national geographic , and the national institute on aging , to find the four demographically confirmed areas that are geographically defined .	我們尋找長壽的方法是和國家地理雜誌合作 , 國家老化研究所 , 找出四個人口統計的地區 , 地理上定義的區域 。
and then bring a team of experts in there to methodically go through exactly what these people do , to distill down the crosscultural distillation .	接著 , 帶一組專家來研究這些人所做的事 , 將跨文化的干擾逐漸減少 。
and at the end of this i'm going to tell you what that distillation is .	最後我要告訴各位那是什麼 。
but first i'd like to debunk some common myths when it comes to longevity .	但 , 首先 , 我想在長壽的過程中破除一些常見的迷思 。
and the first myth is if you try really hard you can live to be 100 .	第一個迷思是 , 如果你真的很努力 , 你可以活到100歲 。
the problem is , only about one out of 5 , 000 people in america live to be 100 .	問題是 , 美國的50000人中只有1人活到100歲 。
your chances are very low .	你的機會非常低 。
even though it's the fastest growing demographic in america , it's hard to reach 100 .	儘管它是美國成長最快的人口統計 , 但它很難達到100歲 。
the problem is that we're not programmed for longevity .	問題是 , 我們沒有為長壽設計 。
we are programmed for something called procreative success .	我們被編寫成所謂的繁榮成功 。
i love that word .	我愛這個詞 。
it reminds me of my college days .	它讓我想起我大學的日子 。
biologists term procreative success to mean the age where you have children and then another generation , the age when your children have children .	生物學家術語是成功的年齡 , 意思是你有孩子的年齡 , 接著是另一個世代 , 當你的孩子有小孩的年齡 。
after that the effect of evolution completely dissipates .	在那次演化的效應完全消失了 。
if you're a mammal , if you're a rat or an elephant , or a human , in between , it's the same story .	如果你是哺乳類動物 , 如果你是一隻老鼠 , 或一隻大象 , 或人類 , 在兩者之間 , 則是相同的故事 。
so to make it to age 100 , you not only have to have had a very good lifestyle , you also have to have won the genetic lottery .	為了讓它達到一百歲 , 你不只需要有很好的生活方式 , 你還得贏得基因彩票 。
the second myth is , there are treatments that can help slow , reverse , or even stop aging .	第二個迷思是 , 有些治療可以減緩、逆轉 , 甚至阻止老化 。
when you think of it , there is 99 things that can age us .	想想看 , 有99件事情可以讓我們老化 。
deprive your brain of oxygen for just a few minutes , those brain cells die , they never come back .	剝奪了你的腦部氧 , 短短幾分鐘 , 這些腦細胞就會死亡 , 它們永遠不會回來 。
play tennis too hard , on your knees , ruin your cartilage , the cartilage never comes back .	玩網球太硬 , 在你的膝蓋 , 毀壞你的軟骨 , 軟骨永遠不會回來 。
our arteries can clog . our brains can gunk up with plaque , and we can get alzheimer's .	我們的動脈會堵塞 。 我們的大腦可以用白斑來引導 , 我們可以得到阿茲海默症 。
there is just too many things to go wrong .	有太多事情會出錯 。
our bodies have 35 trillion cells , trillion with a " t . " we're talking national debt numbers here .	我們的身體有35兆個細胞 , 有一兆個 「 t 」 。 我們在這裡談的是國家債務數字 。
those cells turn themselves over once every eight years .	這些細胞每8年就一次自轉一次 。
and every time they turn themselves over there is some damage . and that damage builds up .	每當他們轉過來時 , 就會造成損害 。
and it builds up exponentially .	它以指數的方式建造 。
it's a little bit like the days when we all had beatles albums or eagles albums and we'd make a copy of that on a cassette tape , and let our friends copy that cassette tape , and pretty soon , with successive generations that tape sounds like garbage .	有點像當我們有披頭四或老鷹專輯的日子 , 我們會在錄音帶上複製 , 讓朋友們複製錄錄錄錄錄音帶 , 很快地 , 錄音帶聽起來就像垃圾一樣 。
well , the same things happen to our cells .	同樣的事發生在我們的細胞上 。
that's why a 65yearold person is aging at a rate of about 125 times faster than a 12yearold person .	這就是為什麼一個65歲的人老化的速度比一個125歲的人快125倍 。
so , if there is nothing you can do to slow your aging or stop your aging , what am i doing here ?	所以 , 如果沒有任何東西可以減緩老化或阻止老化 , 我在這裡做什麼 ?
well , the fact of the matter is the best science tells us that the capacity of the human body , my body , your body , is about 90 years , a little bit more for women .	事實上 , 最好的科學告訴我們 , 人體的能力 , 我的身體 , 你的身體大約是90年 , 對女人來說 , 稍微多一點 。
but life expectancy in this country is only 78 .	但在美國的預期壽命只有78歲 。
so somewhere along the line , we're leaving about 12 good years on the table .	所以 , 在這條路上 , 我們留下了大約12年的好年 。
these are years that we could get .	這些是我們可以得到的 。
and research shows that they would be years largely free of chronic disease , heart disease , cancer and diabetes .	研究顯示 , 它們會大多不再是慢性疾病、心臟疾病、癌症、糖尿病 。
we think the best way to get these missing years is to look at the cultures around the world that are actually experiencing them , areas where people are living to age 100 at rates up to 10 times greater than we are , areas where the life expectancy is an extra dozen years , the rate of middle age mortality is a fraction of what it is in this country .	我們認為 , 讓這些缺失的最佳方式就是看看全世界的文化 , 真正體驗到它們的文化 , 人們生活的年齡比我們現在的百歲還要高十倍 , 預期壽命多了十多年 , 中年死亡率的比例是這個國家的一部分 。
we found our first blue zone about 125 miles off the coast of italy , on the island of sardinia .	我們在義大利海岸的海岸找到了我們的第一個藍色區域 , 在薩丁尼亞島上 。
and not the entire island , the island is about 1 . 4 million people , but only up in the highlands , an area called the nuoro province .	不是整個島嶼 , 島嶼大約有140萬人 , 但只有在高地 , 一個叫做努羅省的區域 。
and here we have this area where men live the longest , about 10 times more centenarians than we have here in america .	這裡我們有男人最長壽的地區 , 比美國這裡的百歲人多了十倍 。
and this is a place where people not only reach age 100 , they do so with extraordinary vigor .	這個地方 , 人們不只到達100歲 , 還在做非凡的訪客 。
places where 102 year olds still ride their bike to work , chop wood , and can beat a guy 60 years younger than them .	在那裡 , 十二歲的人仍然騎腳踏車去工作 , 木頭 , 還能打敗比他們年輕六十歲的人 。
their history actually goes back to about the time of christ .	他們的歷史回到基督的時代 。
it's actually a bronze age culture that's been isolated .	它其實是種孤立的青銅文化 。
because the land is so infertile , they largely are shepherds , which occasions regular , lowintensity physical activity .	因為土地太不生育了 , 大多是牧羊人 , 偶爾會有規律、低強度的實體活動 。
their diet is mostly plantbased , accentuated with foods that they can carry into the fields .	他們的飲食大部分是以植物為基礎的 , 主要是以食物為中心 , 他們可以帶到田野中 。
they came up with an unleavened whole wheat bread called carta musica made out of durum wheat , a type of cheese made from grassfed animals so the cheese is high in omega3 fatty acids instead of omega6 fatty acids from cornfed animals , and a type of wine that has three times the level of polyphenols than any known wine in the world .	他們想出了一個未發酵的全麥麵包 , 叫做carta音樂 , 由笨蛋製成的一種乳酪 , 一種來自草食動物的乳酪 , 乳酪是omega-3脂肪酸 , 而不是omega-6脂肪酸 , 一種葡萄糖含有三倍於世界上所知的葡萄酒量 。
but the real secret i think lies more in the way that they organize their society .	但我認為真正的秘密是他們組織社會的方式 。
and one of the most salient elements of the sardinian society is how they treat older people .	薩丁尼亞社會中最常見的元素之一就是他們對待老年人的方式 。
you ever notice here in america , social equity seems to peak at about age 24 ?	你有沒有注意到 , 在美國 , 社會平等似乎是在24歲時達到高峰 ?
just look at the advertisements .	看看廣告 。
here in sardinia , the older you get the more equity you have , the more wisdom you're celebrated for .	在薩丁尼亞 , 年紀越長 , 你得到越多的平等 , 你所得到的智慧越多 。
you go into the bars in sardinia , instead of seeing the sports illustrated swimsuit calendar , you see the centenarian of the month calendar .	你走進薩丁尼亞的酒吧 , 而不是看到運動畫出的游泳日曆 , 你看到的是月曆的百歲人 。
this , as it turns out , is not only good for your aging parents to keep them close to the family it imparts about four to six years of extra life expectancy research shows it's also good for the children of those families , who have lower rates of mortality and lower rates of disease .	事實證明 , 這不僅對你的老年人父母來說是有益的 , 讓他們靠近家庭 , 還能維持大約四到六年的額外壽命研究顯示 , 對那些家庭的孩子來說也是有益的 , 他們的死亡率比較低 , 疾病的比例也比較低 。
that's called the grandmother effect .	這叫做祖母效應 。
we found our second blue zone on the other side of the planet , about 800 miles south of tokyo , on the archipelago of okinawa .	我們發現地球另一邊的第二個藍色區域 , 東京的南方約800英哩 , 位在奧地加哥的阿基地 。
okinawa is actually 161 small islands .	okinawa實際上是161個小島
and in the northern part of the main island , this is ground zero for world longevity .	在主島的北部 , 這是世界長壽的零地 。
this is a place where the oldest living female population is found .	這個地方是最古老的女性族群被發現的地方 。
it's a place where people have the longest disabilityfree life expectancy in the world .	這個地方 , 人們有世界上最長的身心障礙壽命 。
they have what we want .	他們有我們想要的 。
they live a long time , and tend to die in their sleep , very quickly , and often , i can tell you , after sex .	牠們活很久 , 通常會在牠們的睡眠中死亡 , 很快 , 通常 , 我會告訴你 , 性之後 。
they live about seven good years longer than the average american .	他們的壽命比美國人的平均壽命長七年 。
five times as many centenarians as we have in america .	美國和百歲人一樣 , 有五倍之多 。
one fifth the rate of colon and breast cancer , big killers here in america .	五分之一的蟻群和乳癌的比例 , 在美國這裡的大型殺手 。
and one sixth the rate of cardiovascular disease .	心血管疾病的第六分之一 。
and the fact that this culture has yielded these numbers suggests strongly they have something to teach us .	事實是 , 這種文化讓這些數字很強烈地表示他們有東西可以教我們 。
what do they do ?	他們會怎麼做 ?
once again , a plantbased diet , full of vegetables with lots of color in them .	再一次 , 以植物為基礎的飲食 , 裡面有很多顏色的蔬菜 。
and they eat about eight times as much tofu as americans do .	他們和美國人一樣吃大約八倍的豆腐 。
more significant than what they eat is how they eat it .	比他們吃的東西更重要 。
they have all kinds of little strategies to keep from overeating , which , as you know , is a big problem here in america .	他們有各式各樣的小策略可以避免過度使用 , 如你所知 , 這在美國是個大問題 。
a few of the strategies we observed: they eat off of smaller plates , so they tend to eat fewer calories at every sitting .	我們觀察到的一些策略:它們會從較小的盤子裡吃掉 , 所以它們會在每位坐著時吃比較少的卡路里 。
instead of serving family style , where you can sort of mindlessly eat as you're talking , they serve at the counter , put the food away , and then bring it to the table .	與其服用家人風格 , 在談話時 , 你可以輕鬆地吃 , 不用在櫃子上 , 把食物拿走 , 然後把它帶到桌子上 。
they also have a 3 , 000yearold adage , which i think is the greatest sort of diet suggestion ever invented .	他們還有3000年的廣告 , 我認為這是有史以來最偉大的飲食建議 。
it was invented by confucius .	它是由混亂所發明的 。
and that diet is known as the hara , hatchi , bu diet .	這種飲食被稱為 「 哈拉 , hatchi , htchi , butifttantt 。 」
it's simply a little saying these people say before their meal to remind them to stop eating when their stomach is [80] percent full .	簡單來說 , 這些人在吃飯之前說 , 要提醒他們不要再吃80%的肚子 。
it takes about a half hour for that full feeling to travel from your belly to your brain .	要花大約半小時 , 才能從你的肚子到你的大腦 。
and by remembering to stop at 80 percent it helps keep you from doing that very thing .	記住 , 80%的停止 , 它會幫助你不做這事 。
but , like sardinia , okinawa has a few social constructs that we can associate with longevity .	但 , 像薩丁尼亞 , okinwa有一些社會結構 , 可以讓我們和長壽有關 。
we know that isolation kills .	我們知道孤立會致死 。
fifteen years ago , the average american had three good friends .	15年前 , 美國人平均有三個好朋友 。
we're down to one and half right now .	我們現在只剩一半 。
if you were lucky enough to be born in okinawa , you were born into a system where you automatically have a half a dozen friends with whom you travel through life .	如果你夠幸運 , 在okinawa出生 , 你就生在一個系統裡 , 自動有半個朋友 , 和你在人生中旅行 。
they call it a moai . and if you're in a moai you're expected to share the bounty if you encounter luck , and if things go bad , child gets sick , parent dies , you always have somebody who has your back .	他們稱之為moai 。 如果你是moai , 你預期會遇上運氣 , 如果你遇到運氣 , 孩子會生病 , 父母會死 , 總是會有人背 。
this particular moai , these five ladies have been together for 97 years .	這五個女士聚集了九十七年 。
their average age is 102 .	他們的平均年齡是102歲 。
typically in america we've divided our adult life up into two sections .	一般來說 , 在美國 , 我們把成人的生命分成兩部分 。
there is our work life , where we're productive .	這是我們的工作生活 , 我們有生產力 。
and then one day , boom , we retire .	然後有一天 , 我們退休了 。
and typically that has meant retiring to the easy chair , or going down to arizona to play golf .	通常這就意味著退休椅子 , 或是去亞利桑那州玩高爾夫球 。
in the okinawan language there is not even a word for retirement .	在俄克納瓦語中 , 甚至沒有退休的詞彙 。
instead there is one word that imbues your entire life , and that word is " ikigai . "	取而代之 , 一生中有一個詞是 「 ikigai 」 。
and , roughly translated , it means " the reason for which you wake up in the morning . "	大約是翻譯了 , 意思是 「 早上醒來的原因 。 」
for this 102yearold karate master , his ikigai was carrying forth this martial art .	對於這位102歲的凱爾特大師 , 他的吉加尼帶著這件火星藝術 。
for this hundredyearold fisherman it was continuing to catch fish for his family three times a week .	對於這一百歲的漁夫而言 , 每週捕魚量持續三倍 。
and this is a question . the national institute on aging actually gave us a questionnaire to give these centenarians .	這是個問題 。 國家老化研究所給我們一份問卷 , 給我們一份問卷 , 給予百歲人 。
and one of the questions , they were very culturally astute , the people who put the questionnaire .	其中一個問題是 , 他們是非常文化的財富 , 那些提出問卷的人 。
one of the questions was , " what is your ikigai ? "	其中一個問題是: 「 你的ikigai是什麼 ? 」
they instantly knew why they woke up in the morning .	他們馬上就知道為什麼早上起床 。
for this 102 year old woman , her ikigai was simply her greatgreatgreatgranddaughter .	對於這102歲的老婦人 , 她的吉加西只是她的曾曾曾曾曾曾孫女 。
two girls separated in age by 101 and a half years .	兩個女孩在101歲就分開了 。
and i asked her what it felt like to hold a greatgreatgreatgranddaughter .	我問她是什麼感覺 , 拿著曾曾曾曾曾曾孫女的感覺 。
and she put her head back and she said , " it feels like leaping into heaven . "	她回頭說: 「 感覺就像跳上天堂 。 」
i thought that was a wonderful thought .	我覺得這是個很棒的想法 。
my editor at geographic wanted me to find america's blue zone .	我在地理雜誌的編輯希望我能找到美國的藍色區域 。
and for a while we looked on the prairies of minnesota , where actually there is a very high proportion of centenarians .	有一陣子 , 我們看明尼蘇達的草原 , 那裡有非常高比例的百歲人 。
but that's because all the young people left .	但那是因為所有的年輕人都離開了 。
so , we turned to the data again .	所以 , 我們再次轉向資料 。
and we found america's longestlived population among the seventhday adventists concentrated in and around loma linda , california .	我們發現美國最長壽的人口是加州的第七天冒險家集中在加州的羅馬林達 。
adventists are conservative methodists .	先進者是保守的方法主義者 。
they celebrate their sabbath from sunset on friday till sunset on saturday .	他們在星期五日落的日落慶祝他們的安息日直到星期六日落
a " 24hour sanctuary in time , " they call it .	他們稱之為 「 24小時的庇護所 」 。
and they follow five little habits that conveys to them extraordinary longevity , comparatively speaking .	他們遵循五個小習慣 , 傳達給他們非凡的長壽 , 相對來說 。
in america here , life expectancy for the average woman is 80 .	在美國 , 平均女性平均壽命是80歲 。
but for an adventist woman , their life expectancy is 89 .	但對一位先進女士而言 , 他們的預期壽命是89 。
and the difference is even more pronounced among men , who are expected to live about 11 years longer than their american counterparts .	差別在於 , 比起他們的美國人多了11年 。
now , this is a study that followed about 70 , 000 people for 30 years .	這個研究追蹤了大約七萬人三十年 。
sterling study . and i think it supremely illustrates the premise of this blue zone project .	嚴格的研究 。 我認為這很明顯說明了這個藍色區域計畫的前提 。
this is a heterogeneous community .	這是個異性族群 。
it's white , black , hispanic , asian .	它是白人、黑人、西班牙語、亞洲人 。
the only thing that they have in common are a set of very small lifestyle habits that they follow ritualistically for most of their lives .	他們唯一的共通點是一組非常小的生活習慣 , 他們在人生中幾乎都是以儀式來追蹤 。
they take their diet directly from the bible .	他們直接從聖經中取得他們的飲食 。
genesis: chapter one , verse [29] , where god talks about legumes and seeds , and on one more stanza about green plants , ostensibly missing is meat .	遺傳:第一章 , 第二章 , 上帝談到傳單和種子 , 再談到綠色植物 , 很明顯地 , 遺漏了肉 。
they take this sanctuary in time very serious .	他們認真看待這個保護區 。
for 24 hours every week , no matter how busy they are , how stressed out they are at work , where the kids need to be driven , they stop everything and they focus on their god , their social network , and then , hardwired right in the religion , are nature walks .	每週有24小時 , 不論他們有多忙、工作壓力多大 , 孩子需要被驅動 , 他們會停止一切 , 專注於他們的上帝、他們的社交網路 , 然後 , 在宗教中 , 天生就走路了 。
and the power of this is not that it's done occasionally , the power is it's done every week for a lifetime .	這種力量的力量並不是偶爾會發生 , 權力是每週都在做一輩子 。
none of it's hard . none of it costs money .	沒有一個困難 。 沒有一個代價 。
adventists also tend to hang out with other adventists .	冒險家們也傾向和其他的冒險家混在一起 。
so , if you go to an adventist's party you don't see people swilling jim beam or rolling a joint .	所以 , 如果你去參加一位先進派對 , 你不會看到人們在游動吉姆姆姆 , 或是在開關 。
instead they're talking about their next nature walk , exchanging recipes , and yes , they pray .	取而代之的是 , 他們在談論下一個自然步行 , 交換食譜 , 沒錯 , 他們祈禱 。
but they influence each other in profound and measurable ways .	但它們互相影響 , 以深遠且可測量的方式 。
this is a culture that has yielded ellsworth whareham .	這是一種文化 , 讓埃爾斯•沃爾斯•萊姆得到了價值 。
ellsworth whareham is 97 years old .	埃爾斯•沃爾罕姆已經九十七歲了 。
he's a multimillionaire , yet when a contractor wanted 6 , 000 dollars to build a privacy fence , he said , " for that kind of money i'll do it myself . "	他是數百萬富翁 , 但當一個承包商想要6 , 000美元來建立隱私的柵欄 , 他說: 「 為了這樣的錢 , 我會自己去做 。 」
so for the next three days he was out shoveling cement , and hauling poles around .	所以接下來的三天 , 他出門了水泥 , 四處運送兩極 。
and predictably , perhaps , on the fourth day he ended up in the operating room .	也許 , 在第四天 , 他最後到了手術室 。
but not as the guy on the table ; the guy doing openheart surgery .	但不是這位在桌上的人 ; 做開心手術的人 。
at 97 he still does 20 openheart surgeries every month .	九十七歲時 , 他仍然每個月做二十次開心手術 。
ed rawlings , 103 years old now , an active cowboy , starts his morning with a swim .	艾德•格林斯 , 103歲 , 活躍的牛仔 , 早上開始游泳 。
and on weekends he likes to put on the boards , throw up rooster tails .	週末 , 他喜歡裝在板子上 , 丟下羅斯特的尾巴 。
her grandson actually lives in the twin cities here .	她的孫子其實住在雙胞胎城市 。
she starts her day with lifting weights .	她開始了她的日子 , 帶著升重 。
she rides her bicycle .	她騎腳踏車 。
and then she gets in her rootbeer colored 1994 cadillac seville , and tears down the san bernardino freeway , where she still volunteers for seven different organizations .	然後她走進rootbeer , 彩色了1994年卡迪拉克賽維爾 , 在聖bernardino高速公路上 , 她仍然自願為七個不同的組織自願 。
i've been on 19 hardcore expeditions .	我參加了19次硬幣探險 。
i'm probably the only person you'll ever meet who rode his bicycle across the sahara desert without sunscreen .	我可能是你遇過的唯一一個騎腳踏車橫跨撒哈拉沙漠 , 沒有防曬霜 。
but i'll tell you , there is no adventure more harrowing than riding shotgun with marge deton .	但我會告訴你 , 沒有冒險 , 比起馬克•德頓的騎腳踏車更痛苦 。
" a stranger is a friend i haven't met yet ! " she'd say to me .	「 陌生人是我尚未見面的朋友 ! 」 她會對我說 。
so , what are the common denominators in these three cultures ?	所以 , 在這三個文化中 , 有哪些共同點 ?
what are the things that they all do ?	他們所做的事是什麼 ?
and we managed to boil it down to nine .	我們成功歸結為九個 。
in fact we've done two more blue zone expeditions since this and these common denominators hold true .	事實上 , 自此以來 , 我們還做了兩次藍色區域探險 , 這些常見的探險員都堅持著真相 。
and the first one , and i'm about to utter a heresy here , none of them exercise , at least the way we think of exercise .	首先 , 我將要說的是 , 這裡沒有運動 , 至少我們認為運動的方式 。
instead , they set up their lives so that they are constantly nudged into physical activity .	相反地 , 他們建立了自己的生命 , 讓他們經常被剝奪到實體活動 。
these 100yearold okinawan women are getting up and down off the ground , they sit on the floor , 30 or 40 times a day .	這些100歲的俄羅瓦婦女正站在地面上 , 每天坐30到40次 。
sardinians live in vertical houses , up and down the stairs .	薩丁尼亞人住在垂直的房子裡 , 樓梯上下 。
every trip to the store , or to church or to a friend's house occasions a walk .	每次旅行到店裡 , 或去教堂 , 或去朋友家 , 都會有走路 。
they don't have any conveniences .	他們沒有任何方便 。
there is not a button to push to do yard work or house work .	沒有按下按鈕 , 做院子工作或房子工作 。
if they want to mix up a cake , they're doing it by hand .	如果他們想要混合蛋糕 , 他們會用手做 。
that burns calories just as much as going on the treadmill does .	跑步機的燃燒卡路里和跑步機一樣 。
