when they do do intentional physical activity , it's the things they enjoy . they tend to walk , the only proven way to stave off cognitive decline , and they all tend to have a garden .	當他們做刻意的身體活動時 , 他們很享受 , 他們傾向於走路 , 唯一能證明偷走認知衰退的途徑 , 他們都傾向有花園 。
they know how to set up their life in the right way so they have the right outlook .	他們知道如何以正確的方式生活 , 讓他們有正確的前景 。
each of these cultures take time to downshift .	每一種文化都需要時間下降 。
the sardinians pray . the seventhday adventists pray .	薩丁尼亞人祈禱 。 第七天的冒險家祈禱 。
the okinawans have this ancestor veneration .	okinawans有一位祖先探險家 。
but when you're in a hurry or stressed out , that triggers something called the inflammatory response , which is associated with everything from alzheimer's disease to cardiovascular disease .	但當你處在急救或壓力之中 , 會觸發一種叫 「 發炎反應 」 的反應 , 這種反應和阿茲海默症的一切有關 , 從阿茲海默症到心血管疾病 。
when you slow down for 15 minutes a day you turn that inflammatory state into a more antiinflammatory state .	當你一天放慢15分鐘 , 你就會把發炎狀態轉變成更抗炎的狀態 。
they have vocabulary for sense of purpose , ikigai , like the okinawans .	他們有詞彙 , 目的、ikigai , 像是okinawans 。
you know the two most dangerous years in your life are the year you're born , because of infant mortality , and the year you retire .	你知道你生命中最危險的兩年是你出生的那一年 , 因為嬰兒死亡率 , 而你退休的那一年 。
these people know their sense of purpose , and they activate in their life , that's worth about seven years of extra life expectancy .	這些人知道自己的目的 , 他們活躍在自己的人生中 , 值得七年的預期壽命 。
there's no longevity diet .	沒有長壽飲食 。
instead , these people drink a little bit every day , not a hard sell to the american population .	相反地 , 這些人每天喝一點點酒 , 而不是賣給美國人 。
they tend to eat a plantbased diet .	他們傾向吃植物的飲食 。
doesn't mean they don't eat meat , but lots of beans and nuts .	不是說牠們不吃肉 , 而是很多豆子和堅果 。
and they have strategies to keep from overeating , little things that nudge them away from the table at the right time .	他們有策略來避免過度的小事 , 讓他們遠離桌子 。
and then the foundation of all this is how they connect .	這一切的基礎就是它們如何連結 。
they put their families first , take care of their children and their aging parents .	他們先把家人放在第一點 , 照顧他們的孩子和他們的老年人 。
they all tend to belong to a faithbased community , which is worth between four and 14 extra years of life expectancy if you do it four times a month .	他們全都屬於信仰型的社區 , 值於每個月四到十四年的預期壽命 , 如果你每個月做四次 。
and the biggest thing here is they also belong to the right tribe .	最重要的是 , 它們也屬於對的部落 。
they were either born into or they proactively surrounded themselves with the right people .	他們不是出生 , 或主動把自己和對的人圍繞在一起 。
we know from the framingham studies , that if your three best friends are obese there is a 50 percent better chance that you'll be overweight .	我們從法蘭罕默研究得知 , 如果三個最好的朋友過胖 , 會有百分之五十的機率是過重的 。
so , if you hang out with unhealthy people , that's going to have a measurable impact over time .	所以 , 如果你和不健康的人聊天 , 隨時間就會產生可測量的影響 。
instead , if your friend's idea of recreation is physical activity , bowling , or playing hockey , biking or gardening , if your friends drink a little , but not too much , and they eat right , and they're engaged , and they're trusting and trustworthy , that is going to have the biggest impact over time .	相反地 , 如果你的朋友對於復育的概念是物理活動 , 弓箭 , 或彈奏曲棍 , 騎腳踏車或園藝 , 如果你的朋友喝點小酒 , 但不太太太好吃 , 他們很有吸引力 , 信任和值得信賴 , 這會隨著時間產生最大的影響 。
diets don't work . no diet in the history of the world has ever worked for more than two percent of the population .	飲食是行不通的 。 世界歷史上沒有飲食 , 超過百分之二的人口都沒有用 。
exercise programs usually start in january ; they're usually done by october .	運動程式通常是一月開始的 ; 通常是十月完成的 。
when it comes to longevity there is no short term fix in a pill or anything else .	當談到長壽時 , 藥丸或其它什麼都沒有短期修復 。
but when you think about it , your friends are longterm adventures , and therefore , perhaps the most significant thing you can do to add more years to your life , and life to your years . thank you very much .	但當你想到的時候 , 你的朋友是長期冒險 , 因此 , 也許你能做的最重要的事 , 多加年你的人生 , 及生活 , 非常謝謝你 。
ink that conducts electricity ; a window that turns from clear to opaque at the flip of a switch ; a jelly that makes music . all this stuff exists , and catarina mota says: it's time to play with it . mota leads us on a tour of surprising and cool new materials , and suggests that the way we'll figure out what they're good for is to experiment , tinker and have fun .	墨水指揮電力 ; 一扇窗戶 , 從清晰的轉換到開關 ; 製成音樂的水母 。 所有這些東西都存在 , 卡塔娜•莫塔說:是時候和它一起玩 。 mota帶領我們到驚喜且酷炫的新材料旅程 , 並建議我們要知道如何做實驗、做粉絲 , 並且有趣 。
creativity , design , technology	創造力 , 設計 , 科技 , 科技 , 創造力 , 設計 , 科技 , 科技 。
catarina mota: play with smart materials	catarinamota:用智慧材料玩樂 。
i have a friend in portugal whose grandfather built a vehicle out of a bicycle and a washing machine so he could transport his family .	我在葡萄牙有個朋友 , 他的祖父用腳踏車和洗衣機建造了一台車 , 讓他可以運送他的家人 。
he did it because he couldn't afford a car , but also because he knew how to build one .	他這麼做是因為他買不起一輛車 , 也因為他知道怎麼建造一個 。
there was a time when we understood how things worked and how they were made , so we could build and repair them , or at the very least make informed decisions about what to buy .	曾有一段時間 , 我們明白事情是如何運作的 , 以及它們是如何運作的 , 這樣我們才能建造、修復它們 , 或至少要知道如何購買什麼 。
many of these doityourself practices were lost in the second half of the 20th century .	許多這種做法在二十世紀後半葉消失了 。
but now , the maker community and the opensource model are bringing this kind of knowledge about how things work and what they're made of back into our lives , and i believe we need to take them to the next level , to the components things are made of .	但現在 , 製造商社區和開源模型將這種知識帶入我們生活中 , 我相信我們需要把它們帶到下一個層級 , 以零件組成的 。
for the most part , we still know what traditional materials like paper and textiles are made of and how they are produced .	大部分的情況下 , 我們仍然知道紙張和紡織品的傳統材料是怎麼組成的 , 以及它們是如何產生的 。
but now we have these amazing , futuristic composites plastics that change shape , paints that conduct electricity , pigments that change color , fabrics that light up .	但現在我們有了這些令人驚訝、美妙的複合材料 , 會改變形狀、油漆、導電、變色、顏料、發光 。
let me show you some examples .	讓我給你們看一些例子 。
so conductive ink allows us to paint circuits instead of using the traditional printed circuit boards or wires .	所以導電墨水能讓我們繪製電路而不是使用傳統印刷電路板或電線
in the case of this little example i'm holding , we used it to create a touch sensor that reacts to my skin by turning on this little light .	在我手上的這個小例子中 , 我們用它來製造觸摸感測器 , 用這個小小的光來啟動我的皮膚 。
conductive ink has been used by artists , but recent developments indicate that we will soon be able to use it in laser printers and pens .	由藝術家所使用的導電墨水 , 但最近的發展指出 , 我們很快就會用雷射印表機和筆來使用 。
and this is a sheet of acrylic infused with colorless lightdiffusing particles .	這張照片是用無顏色的光照射粒子注射出來的 。
what this means is that , while regular acrylic only diffuses light around the edges , this one illuminates across the entire surface when i turn on the lights around it .	這意味著 , 雖然一般的水晶只會在邊緣散射出光 , 這個光會在整個表面打開燈泡時 , 整個表面都會發光 。
two of the known applications for this material include interior design and multitouch systems .	這材料的兩種應用 , 包括室內設計和多點觸控系統 。
and thermochromic pigments change color at a given temperature .	溫度的溫度會改變顏色 。
so i'm going to place this on a hot plate that is set to a temperature only slightly higher than ambient and you can see what happens .	所以我要把這個放在一個熱盤上 , 讓溫度比環境稍高 , 你可以看到會發生什麼事 。
so one of the principle applications for this material is , amongst other things , in baby bottles , so it indicates when the contents are cool enough to drink .	所以 , 這種材料的原則之一就是 , 在嬰兒瓶中 , 嬰兒瓶中 , 它會指出 , 當內容物夠酷 , 可以喝的時候 。
so these are just a few of what are commonly known as smart materials .	這些只是一般所知的智慧材料 。
in a few years , they will be in many of the objects and technologies we use on a daily basis .	幾年後 , 它們會出現在我們每天使用的許多物品和技術中 。
we may not yet have the flying cars science fiction promised us , but we can have walls that change color depending on temperature , keyboards that roll up , and windows that become opaque at the flick of a switch .	我們可能還沒有飛車科幻小說給我們保證 , 但我們可以有改變顏色的牆 , 取決於溫度 , 鍵盤會滾起來 , 窗戶會變成開關的反光 。
so i'm a social scientist by training , so why am i here today talking about smart materials ?	所以 , 我是社會科學家 , 我今天要談的是智慧型材料 ?
well first of all , because i am a maker .	首先 , 因為我是製造家 。
i'm curious about how things work and how they are made , but also because i believe we should have a deeper understanding of the components that make up our world , and right now , we don't know enough about these hightech composites our future will be made of .	我很好奇事物是如何運作的 , 也是因為我相信我們應該更深入了解組成我們的世界的元件 , 而現在 , 我們對於這些高科技組成的組成 , 我們的未來還不夠了解 。
smart materials are hard to obtain in small quantities .	聰明的材料很難在小量中取得 。
there's barely any information available on how to use them , and very little is said about how they are produced .	幾乎沒有任何關於如何使用它們的資訊 , 幾乎沒有任何關於它們如何產生的資訊 。
so for now , they exist mostly in this realm of trade secrets and patents only universities and corporations have access to .	所以 , 目前 , 他們主要存在於貿易秘密的領域 , 只有大學和企業才能取得專利 。
so a little over three years ago , kirsty boyle and i started a project we called open materials .	三年前 , kirsty男孩和我成立了一個專案 , 我們稱之為開放式材料 。
it's a website where we , and anyone else who wants to join us , share experiments , publish information , encourage others to contribute whenever they can , and aggregate resources such as research papers and tutorials by other makers like ourselves .	這是一個網站 , 我們和任何想要加入我們的人 , 分享實驗、出版資訊 , 鼓勵大家隨時都能做出貢獻 , 以及聚集的資源 , 例如研究論文 , 以及其他像我們一樣的人 。
we would like it to become a large , collectively generated database of doityourself information on smart materials .	我們希望它成為一個大型、集體的資料庫 , 資料庫是關於智慧材料的資料庫 。
but why should we care how smart materials work and what they are made of ?	但我們為什麼要關心智慧材料是如何運作的 ? 以及它們的組成成是什麼 ?
first of all , because we can't shape what we don't understand , and what we don't understand and use ends up shaping us .	首先 , 因為我們無法改變我們不了解的東西 , 以及我們不了解的東西 , 最終會影響我們 。
the objects we use , the clothes we wear , the houses we live in , all have a profound impact on our behavior , health and quality of life .	我們使用的物品、穿著的衣服、住的房子 , 都對我們的行為、健康和生活品質有深遠的影響 。
so if we are to live in a world made of smart materials , we should know and understand them .	所以 , 如果我們要生活在一個由智慧材料組成的世界 , 我們應該要知道並了解它們 。
secondly , and just as important , innovation has always been fueled by tinkerers .	第二 , 同樣重要的是 , 創新總是由tinker推動的 。
so many times , amateurs , not experts , have been the inventors and improvers of things ranging from mountain bikes to semiconductors , personal computers , airplanes .	很多時候 , 業餘人士 , 不是專家 , 都是發明者和改進者 , 從山腳踏車到半導體、個人電腦、飛機 。
the biggest challenge is that material science is complex and requires expensive equipment .	最大的挑戰是材料科學很複雜 , 且需要昂貴的設備 。
but that's not always the case .	但這並不總是如此 。
two scientists at university of illinois understood this when they published a paper on a simpler method for making conductive ink .	伊利諾大學的兩位科學家在出版論文時 , 明白了一篇比較簡單的論文 , 用來製作導電墨水 。
jordan bunker , who had had no experience with chemistry until then , read this paper and reproduced the experiment at his maker space using only offtheshelf substances and tools .	約旦•布朗克 , 他沒有化學經驗 , 直到那時 , 讀到這篇論文 , 並在他的製造商空間中繁殖這個實驗 , 只用現成的物質和工具 。
he used a toaster oven , and he even made his own vortex mixer , based on a tutorial by another scientist/maker .	他用烤箱 , 甚至用他自己的蒸氣混合器 , 根據另一位科學家/maker的指導 。
jordan then published his results online , including all the things he had tried and didn't work , so others could study and reproduce it .	喬登後來在網路上發表了他的結果 , 包括他嘗試過的所有事情 , 並且沒有成功 , 其他人可以研究並複製它 。
so jordan's main form of innovation was to take an experiment created in a wellequipped lab at the university and recreate it in a garage in chicago using only cheap materials and tools he made himself .	約旦的主要創新形式是把一個實驗在大學裡的一個很好的設備實驗室裡 , 並在芝加哥的車庫裡重建 , 只用便宜的材料和工具 , 他自己製造了 。
and now that he published this work , others can pick up where he left and devise even simpler processes and improvements .	而現在他發表了這項研究 , 其他人可以取得他離開的地方 , 甚至可以設計更簡單的過程和改善 。
another example i'd like to mention her project's goal is to highlight the expressive qualities of materials while focusing on the creativity and skills of the builder .	另外一個例子我想提一下她的專案計畫的目的是要強調材料的表現特質 , 同時專注在建造者的創意和技能上 。
electronics kits are very powerful in that they teach us how things work , but the constraints inherent in their design influence the way we learn .	電子設備在他們教導我們事情是如何運作的 , 但在他們的設計中 , 限制影響了我們學習的方式 。
so hannah's approach , on the other hand , is to formulate a series of techniques for creating unusual objects that free us from predesigned constraints by teaching us about the materials themselves .	另一方面 , 漢娜的做法是建立一系列的技術來創造出非凡的物體 , 讓我們免於規劃限制 , 來教導我們關於物質本身的知識 。
so amongst hannah's many impressive experiments , this is one of my favorites .	在漢娜許多令人印象深刻的實驗中 , 這是我最喜歡的之一 。
[ " paper speakers " ] what we're seeing here is just a piece of paper with some copper tape on it connected to an mp3 player and a magnet .	我們現在看到的只是一張紙 , 上面有一些銅膠帶 , 連接mp3播放器和磁鐵 。
so based on the research by marcelo coelho from mit , hannah created a series of paper speakers out of a wide range of materials from simple copper tape to conductive fabric and ink .	所以 , 根據麻省理工學院marcelocollho的研究漢娜創造了一系列的紙喇叭 , 從簡單的銅膠帶到導電的布料和墨水 。
just like jordan and so many other makers , hannah published her recipes and allows anyone to copy and reproduce them .	就像約旦和許多其他製造家漢娜發表了她的食譜讓任何人複製並複製它們
but paper electronics is one of the most promising branches of material science in that it allows us to create cheaper and flexible electronics .	但紙本電子產品是材料科學中最有希望的分支之一 , 讓我們能創造出更便宜、更靈活的電子產品 。
so hannah's artisanal work , and the fact that she shared her findings , opens the doors to a series of new possibilities that are both aesthetically appealing and innovative .	所以漢娜的手工工藝作品 , 她分享她的發現 , 開啟了一系列新的可能性 , 這兩者都是美學和創新的 。
so the interesting thing about makers is that we create out of passion and curiosity , and we are not afraid to fail .	創作者有趣的地方是 , 我們用熱情和好奇心來創造 , 我們不害怕失敗 。
we often tackle problems from unconventional angles , and , in the process , end up discovering alternatives or even better ways to do things .	我們經常從非傳統的角度來處理問題 , 在過程中 , 我們最後會發現替代方案 , 或甚至更好的做事方式 。
so the more people experiment with materials , the more researchers are willing to share their research , and manufacturers their knowledge , the better chances we have to create technologies that truly serve us all .	所以 , 越多人實驗材料 , 研究人員願意分享他們的研究 , 製造他們的知識 , 我們就越有機會創造出真正服務我們所有人的科技 。
so i feel a bit as ted nelson must have when , in the early 1970s , he wrote , " you must understand computers now . "	我覺得tednelson在1970年代早期 , 他寫道: 「 你現在必須要了解電腦 。 」
back then , computers were these large mainframes only scientists cared about , and no one dreamed of even having one at home .	那時 , 電腦是這些巨大的主題 , 只有科學家在乎 , 甚至沒有人夢到家裡 。
so it's a little strange that i'm standing here and saying , " you must understand smart materials now . "	我站在這裡說有點奇怪 , 說: 「 你現在必須要了解智慧型材料 。 」
just keep in mind that acquiring preemptive knowledge about emerging technologies is the best way to ensure that we have a say in the making of our future .	請記住 , 取得新興科技的知識是確保我們未來有所說的最好方法 。
when we drive , we get into a glass bubble , lock the doors and press the accelerator , relying on our eyes to guide us even though we can only see the few cars ahead of and behind us . but what if cars could share data with each other about their position and velocity , and use predictive models to calculate the safest routes for everyone on the road ? jennifer healey imagines a world without accidents .	當我們開車時 , 我們會進入玻璃泡泡 , 鎖住門 , 壓住加速器 , 仰賴我們的眼睛 , 指引我們即使我們只能看到前面的幾輛車子後面的車子 。 但如果車子能彼此分享資料 , 關於他們的位置和速度 , 以及用預測模型 , 來計算路上每個人最安全的路線 , 珍妮佛瑞想像一個沒有意外的世界 。
jennifer healey: if cars could talk , accidents might be avoidable	珍妮:如果汽車可以說話 , 意外可能會被避免 。
let's face it: driving is dangerous .	讓我們面對現實:開車是危險的 。
it's one of the things that we don't like to think about , but the fact that religious icons and good luck charms show up on dashboards around the world betrays the fact that we know this to be true .	這是我們不喜歡思考的一件事 , 但宗教圖標和好運魅力卻出現在世界各地 , 背叛我們所知道的事實 。
car accidents are the leading cause of death in people ages 16 to 19 in the united states leading cause of death and 75 percent of these accidents have nothing to do with drugs or alcohol .	車禍是美國十六歲到十九歲的主要死因 , 導致死亡和百分之七十五的意外和毒品或酒精無關 。
no one can say for sure , but i remember my first accident .	沒人能肯定地說 , 但我記得我第一次意外 。
i was a young driver out on the highway , and the car in front of me , i saw the brake lights go on .	我當時是開高速公路的年輕駕駛 , 前面的車子 , 我看到了煞車燈 。
i'm like , " okay , all right , this guy is slowing down , i'll slow down too . "	我說: 「 好吧 , 好吧 , 這傢伙正在慢下來 , 我也會慢下來 。 」
i step on the brake .	我踏上煞車 。
but no , this guy isn't slowing down .	但不 , 這個人並沒有慢下來 。
this guy is stopping , dead stop , dead stop on the highway .	這傢伙正在停車 , 停車 , 停在高速公路上 。
it was just going 65 to zero ?	只剩65到零嗎 ?
i slammed on the brakes .	我踩煞車 。
i felt the abs kick in , and the car is still going , and it's not going to stop , and i know it's not going to stop , and the air bag deploys , the car is totaled , and fortunately , no one was hurt .	我感覺到abs被踢進去 , 車子還沒停下來 , 我知道它不會停下來 , 空氣袋被部署了 , 很幸運的是 , 沒有人受傷 。
but i had no idea that car was stopping , and i think we can do a lot better than that .	但我完全不知道那輛車正在停止 , 我認為我們可以做得更好 。
i think we can transform the driving experience by letting our cars talk to each other .	我想我們可以改變開車的體驗 , 讓車子彼此交談 。
i just want you to think a little bit about what the experience of driving is like now .	我只是想讓各位思考一下駕駛的體驗 。
get into your car . close the door . you're in a glass bubble .	走進你的車裡 , 關上門 。 你在玻璃泡裡 。
you can't really directly sense the world around you .	你無法直接感受周遭的世界 。
you're in this extended body .	你在這個延伸的身體裡 。
you're tasked with navigating it down partiallyseen roadways , in and amongst other metal giants , at superhuman speeds .	你的任務是將它導向一部分的路道 , 在另一條金屬巨人 , 以超人的速度來導航 。
okay ? and all you have to guide you are your two eyes .	好嗎 ? 你只要指引你兩隻眼睛 。
okay , so that's all you have , eyes that weren't really designed for this task , but then people ask you to do things like , you want to make a lane change , what's the first thing they ask you do ?	好吧 , 這就是你們所有的眼睛 , 不是為這個任務設計而設計的 , 但接著人們請你做這樣的事 , 你想要做出改變 , 他們問你的第一件事是什麼 ?
take your eyes off the road . that's right .	把你的眼睛從路上拿走 , 沒錯 。
stop looking where you're going , turn , check your blind spot , and drive down the road without looking where you're going .	別再去看你在哪裡 , 轉 , 看你的盲點 , 開車到路上 , 不看你在哪裡 。
you and everyone else . this is the safe way to drive .	你和其他人 。 這是安全的開車方式 。
why do we do this ? because we have to , we have to make a choice , do i look here or do i look here ?	為什麼我們要這樣做 ? 因為我們必須做出選擇 , 看看這裡 , 還是看這裡 ?
and usually we do a fantastic job picking and choosing what we attend to on the road .	通常我們會做一件很棒的工作 , 選擇我們在路上的目的 。
but occasionally we miss something .	但偶爾我們忽略了一些事情 。
occasionally we sense something wrong or too late .	偶爾我們會覺得錯了或太晚了 。
in countless accidents , the driver says , " i didn't see it coming . "	無數次的意外 , 司機說: 「 我沒看到它來了 。 」
and i believe that . i believe that .	我相信這一點 。 我相信這一點 。
we can only watch so much .	我們只能看得太多 。
but the technology exists now that can help us improve that .	但現有的科技 , 可以協助我們改善它 。
in the future , with cars exchanging data with each other , we will be able to see not just three cars ahead and three cars behind , to the right and left , all at the same time , bird's eye view , we will actually be able to see into those cars .	未來 , 隨著車子彼此交換資料 , 我們不僅能看到三輛車後面三輛 , 左右兩輛 , 同時 , 鳥的眼睛 , 我們還能看到這些車子 。
we will be able to see the velocity of the car in front of us , to see how fast that guy's going or stopping .	我們將能夠看見前方的車子的速度 , 看看那傢伙的車子的速率或停車 。
if that guy's going down to zero , i'll know .	如果那個人要降到零 , 我就會知道 。
and with computation and algorithms and predictive models , we will be able to see the future .	有了計算、演算法和預測模型 , 我們就能看見未來 。
you may think that's impossible .	你可能會認為這是不可能的 。
how can you predict the future ? that's really hard .	你要如何預測未來 ? 這真的很難 。
actually , no . with cars , it's not impossible .	實際上 , 沒有車子 , 不是不可能的 。
cars are threedimensional objects that have a fixed position and velocity .	汽車是三維的物體 , 擁有固定的位置和速度 。
they travel down roads .	他們沿著道路往下走 。
often they travel on prepublished routes .	他們經常旅行在預先發表的路上 。
it's really not that hard to make reasonable predictions about where a car's going to be in the near future .	要預測在不久的將來 , 車子會在哪裡做出合理的預測 。
even if , when you're in your car and some motorcyclist comes bshoom ! 85 miles an hour down , lanesplitting i know you've had this experience that guy didn't " just come out of nowhere . "	即使 , 當你在車裡 , 有些摩托車騎士來了 , 每小時85英哩 , 車道化 , 我知道你有過這樣的經驗 , 那個人沒有 「 出櫃 」 。
that guy's been on the road probably for the last half hour .	那個人在路上 , 可能已經有半小時了 。
right ? i mean , somebody's seen him .	對吧 ? 我的意思是 , 有人看過他 。
ten , 20 , 30 miles back , someone's seen that guy , and as soon as one car sees that guy and puts him on the map , he's on the map position , velocity , good estimate he'll continue going 85 miles an hour .	十、二十、三十英里後 , 有人看過那個人 , 只要一輛車看到那個人 , 把他放在地圖上 , 他在地圖上 , 速度 , 估計他會每小時八十五英哩 。
you'll know , because your car will know , because that other car will have whispered something in his ear , like , " by the way , five minutes , motorcyclist , watch out . "	你們會知道 , 因為你的車會知道 , 因為另一輛車會在他的耳朵上說: 「 順便一提 , 五分鐘 , 摩托車手 , 注意 。 」
you can make reasonable predictions about how cars behave .	你可以對汽車的行為做出合理的預測 。
i mean , they're newtonian objects .	我的意思是 , 它們是牛頓的物體 。
that's very nice about them .	這對他們來說很棒 。
so how do we get there ?	所以 , 我們要如何做到 ?
we can start with something as simple as sharing our position data between cars , just sharing gps .	我們可以從簡單的開始 , 如分享車子間的位置資料 , 分享gps 。
if i have a gps and a camera in my car , i have a pretty precise idea of where i am and how fast i'm going .	如果我的車子裡有gps和攝影機 , 我有一個很精確的概念 , 關於我在哪裡 , 以及我要走多快 。
with computer vision , i can estimate where the cars around me are , sort of , and where they're going .	有了電腦視覺 , 我可以估計我身邊的車子在哪裡 , 有點像是在哪裡 。
and same with the other cars .	其他車子也一樣 。
they can have a precise idea of where they are , and sort of a vague idea of where the other cars are .	他們可以精確地知道自己在哪裡 , 有點像是對其他車子的看法 。
what happens if two cars share that data , if they talk to each other ?	如果兩個車子共享這些資料 , 如果它們彼此交談 , 會發生什麼事 ?
i can tell you exactly what happens .	我可以告訴你會發生什麼事 。
professor bob wang and his team have done computer simulations of what happens when fuzzy estimates combine , even in light traffic , when cars just share gps data , and we've moved this research out of the computer simulation and into robot test beds that have the actual sensors that are in cars now on these robots: stereo cameras , gps , and the twodimensional laser range finders that are common in backup systems .	bobwang教授和他的團隊做了電腦模擬 , 模擬當模擬混合物時 , 甚至在電動車共享gps的資料 , 我們把這個研究從電腦模擬中移到機器人的模擬床上 , 這些感應器現在都在這些機器人身上:stereo攝影機、gps、gps , 和二維雷射測量器在後備系統中普遍存在 。
we also attach a discrete shortrange communication radio , and the robots talk to each other .	我們還附著一個短距離通訊的無線電機 , 機器人彼此交談 。
when these robots come at each other , they track each other's position precisely , and they can avoid each other .	當這些機器人彼此聚在一起時 , 它們會精確地追蹤彼此的位置 , 它們能避免彼此 。
we're now adding more and more robots into the mix , and we encountered some problems .	我們現在在混合中加入越來越多的機器人 , 我們遇到了一些問題 。
one of the problems , when you get too much chatter , it's hard to process all the packets , so you have to prioritize , and that's where the predictive model helps you .	其中一個問題是 , 當你太過量的聊天時 , 很難處理所有的包裝 , 所以你得要先順序 , 這就是預測模型協助你的地方 。
if your robot cars are all tracking the predicted trajectories , you don't pay as much attention to those packets .	如果你的機械車都在追蹤預測軌跡 , 你就不會注意到那些包裝 。
you prioritize the one guy who seems to be going a little off course .	你把一個看起來有點偏離軌道的人優先化了 。
that guy could be a problem .	那傢伙可能是個問題 。
and you can predict the new trajectory .	你可以預測新的軌跡 。
so you don't only know that he's going off course , you know how .	所以你不只知道他會去上課 , 你知道的 。
and you know which drivers you need to alert to get out of the way .	你知道你需要警告哪個駕駛才能離開 。
and we wanted to do how can we best alert everyone ?	我們想怎麼讓大家更警醒 ?
how can these cars whisper , " you need to get out of the way ? "	這些車子怎麼可能會竊竊竊竊竊私語: 「 你需要走出路嗎 ? 」
well , it depends on two things: one , the ability of the car , and second the ability of the driver .	嗯 , 它取決於兩件事:一 , 汽車的能力 , 第二 , 駕駛的能力 。
if one guy has a really great car , but they're on their phone or , you know , doing something , they're not probably in the best position to react in an emergency .	如果一個人有很棒的車子 , 但他們在手機上 , 或者 , 你知道 , 做點什麼 , 他們可能不是在緊急情況中做出最好的反應 。
so we started a separate line of research doing driver state modeling .	所以 , 我們開始了分開的研究 , 做司機狀態模型 。
and now , using a series of three cameras , we can detect if a driver is looking forward , looking away , looking down , on the phone , or having a cup of coffee .	現在 , 用了一系列的三台攝影機 , 我們可以偵測到駕駛的前方 , 向下看 , 向下看 , 或用一杯咖啡 。
we can predict the accident and we can predict who , which cars , are in the best position to move out of the way to calculate the safest route for everyone .	我們可以預測意外 , 且我們可以預測誰 , 哪一輛車最好的位置 , 不用去計算每個人最安全的路線 。
fundamentally , these technologies exist today .	基本上 , 這些技術今天就存在了 。
i think the biggest problem that we face is our own willingness to share our data .	我認為我們面臨的最大問題是我們自願分享我們的資料 。
i think it's a very disconcerting notion , this idea that our cars will be watching us , talking about us to other cars , that we'll be going down the road in a sea of gossip .	我認為這是個很讓人不安的概念 , 我們的車子會看著我們 , 談到其他車子 , 我們會走下路 , 走進八卦 。
but i believe it can be done in a way that protects our privacy , just like right now , when i look at your car from the outside , i don't really know about you .	但我相信 , 可以用一種方式來保護我們的隱私 , 就像現在一樣 , 當我從外面看你的車 , 我並不知道你 。
if i look at your license plate number , i don't really know who you are .	如果我看你的牌牌數 , 我並不知道你是誰 。
i believe our cars can talk about us behind our backs .	我相信我們的車子可以在我們的背後談論我們 。
and i think it's going to be a great thing .	我認為這將會是一件很棒的事 。
i want you to consider for a moment if you really don't want the distracted teenager behind you to know that you're braking , that you're coming to a dead stop .	我希望你們花點時間思考一下 , 如果你不想要你身後的那些分心的青少年 , 知道你在煞車 , 你即將停下來 。
by sharing our data willingly , we can do what's best for everyone .	透過意願分享我們的數據 , 我們就能為每個人做最好的事 。
so let your car gossip about you .	所以 , 讓你的車子向你走一遍 。
it's going to make the roads a lot safer .	它會讓道路更安全 。
x prize founder peter diamandis talks about how he helped stephen hawking fulfill his dream of going to space by flying together into the upper atmosphere and experiencing weightlessness at zero g .	xprize創辦人peterdamandis談到他如何協助史蒂芬霍金實現太空的夢想 , 透過一起飛進上層大氣層 , 體驗到零g的無重量 。
business , flight , science , short talk , space , technology , universe	商業、飛行、科學、簡短的談話、太空、科技、宇宙、宇宙 。
peter diamandis on stephen hawking in zero g	peterdamandis在stephenhenhawking在0guk工作中 , 採用stephenhenhawings
those of you who know me know how passionate i am about opening the space frontier .	認識我的人知道我對打開太空前線的熱情有多大 。
so when i had the chance to give the world's expert in gravity the experience of zero gravity , it was incredible .	所以當我有機會給世界地心引力專家-無重力的體驗 , 這實在是太了不起了 。
and i want to tell you that story .	我想告訴各位這個故事 。
i first met him through the archon x prize for genomics .	我第一次見到他是基因組學的原子獎 。
it's a competition we're holding , the second x prize , for the first team to sequence 100 human genomes in 10 days .	這是我們所舉辦的競賽 , 第二個xprize , 最早的團隊在十天內將100個人類基因組排列 。
we have something called the genome 100 100 individuals we're sequencing as part of that .	我們有所謂的基因組100個我們將其定序為其中之一 。
craig venter chairs that event .	克萊格•凡特的椅子 。
and i met professor hawking , and he said his dream was to travel into space .	我遇到了霍金教授 , 他說他的夢想是走進太空 。
and i said , " i can't take you there , but i can take you into weightlessness into zerog .	我說: 「 我不能帶你到那裡 , 但我可以帶你進入無重力的狀態 , 進入零 。
and he said , on the spot , " absolutely , yes . "	他說: 「 絕對 , 是的 。 」
well , the only way to experience zerog on earth is actually with parabolic flight , weightless flight .	地球上唯一能體驗到零的辦法就是飛行 , 沒有重量的飛行 。
you take an airplane , you fly over the top , you're weightless for 25 seconds .	你搭飛機 , 飛過頂部 , 沒重25秒 。
come back down , you weigh twice as much .	回來 , 重量是兩倍 。
you do it again and again .	你一而再再而三地做 。
you can get eight , 10 minutes of weightlessness how nasa's trained their astronauts for so long .	你可以得到8、10分鐘無重力的無重力 , 長久以來美國太空總署訓練他們的太空人 。
we set out to do this .	我們開始做這件事 。
it took us 11 years to become operational .	我們花了11年才開始營運 。
and we announced that we were going to fly stephen hawking .	我們宣佈我們要飛史蒂芬霍金 。
we had one government agency and one company aircraft operator say , you're crazy , don't do that , you're going kill the guy .	我們有一間政府機構和一間公司飛機操作員說 , 你瘋了 , 不要這樣做 , 你要殺了那個人 。
and he wanted to go .	他想要去 。
we worked hard to get all the permissions .	我們努力取得所有許可 。
and six months later , we sat down at kennedy space center .	六個月後 , 我們坐在甘迺迪太空中心 。
we had a press conference , we announced our intent to do one zerog parabola , give him 25 seconds of zerog .	我們有一場記者會議 , 我們宣佈我們打算做一個零和的拋物面 , 給他25秒的零 。
and if it went really well , we might do three parabolas .	如果一切順利的話 , 我們可能會做三個拋物面鏡 。
well , we asked him why he wanted to go up and do this .	我們問他為什麼要上去做這件事 。
and what he said , for me , was very moving .	他說 , 對我來說 , 是非常動人的 。
he said , " life on earth is at an everincreasing risk of being wiped out by disaster . . .	他說: 「 地球上的生命在不斷增加的危機上被災難所摧毀......
i think the human race doesn't have a future if it doesn't go into space .	我認為如果它沒有進入太空 , 人類就沒有未來 。
i therefore want to encourage public interest in space . "	所以我想鼓勵公眾對太空的興趣 。 」
we took him out to the kennedy space center , up inside the nasa vehicle , into the back of the zerog airplane .	我們把他帶到甘迺迪太空中心 , 在nasa的車子裡 , 帶到零號飛機後面 。
we had about 20 people who made donations we raised $150 , 000 in donations for children's charities who flew with us .	我們有20個人捐款 , 我們募到150 , 000美金給兒童慈善機構 。
a few tedsters here .	這裡有幾個tedster 。
we set up a whole er .	我們設立了一個全部的伺服器 。
we had four emergency room doctors and two nurses on board the airplane .	我們有四個急診室醫生和兩位護士登上飛機
we were monitoring his po2 of his blood , his heart rate , his blood pressure .	我們在監控他的血液、他的心跳、他的血壓 。
we had everything all set in case of an emergency ; god knows , you don't want to hurt this worldrenowned expert .	我們所有的事都發生在緊急情況下 , 上帝知道 , 你不想傷害這個世界知名的專家 。
we took off from the shuttle landing facility , where the shuttle takes off and lands .	我們從shutle登陸機構起飛 , 太空梭起飛 , 降落地 。
and my partner byron lichtenberg and i carefully suspended him into zerog .	我的另一半是lichtenberg , 我非常小心地把他暫停成零 。
once he was there , [we] let him go to experience what weightlessness was truly like .	一旦他去了 , 讓他體驗到無重力的真實性 。
and after that first parabola , you know , the doc said everything is great . he was smiling , and we said go .	在第一個拋物夾之後 , 你知道的 , 醫生說一切都很棒 。 他在微笑 , 我們說去了 。
so we did a second parabola .	所以我們做了第二個拋物線 。
we actually floated an apple in homage to sir isaac newton because professor hawking holds the same chair at cambridge that isaac newton did .	事實上 , 我們讓艾薩克•牛頓爵士擔任一個蘋果 , 因為霍金教授在艾薩克•牛頓的劍橋舉辦了同樣的椅子 。
and we did a fourth , and a fifth and a sixth .	我們做了第四個 , 第五個第六個 。
and a seventh and an eighth .	第七次和第八次 。
and this man does not look like a 65yearold wheelchairbound man .	這個人看起來不像一個65歲的輪椅人物 。
he was so happy .	他非常開心 。
we are living on a precious jewel , and it's during our lifetime that we're moving off this planet .	我們活在珍貴的珠寶寶上 , 在我們這星球的一生中 , 我們正在離開這個星球 。
please join us in this epic adventure .	請加入我們這次史詩般的冒險 。
medical animator david bolinsky presents 3 minutes of stunning animation that show the bustling life inside a cell .	醫療動畫大衛•布林斯基在3分鐘內展現出令人驚訝的動畫 , 讓細胞內部的破裂生命 。
design , entertainment , film , health , medicine , science , technology , visualizations	設計、娛樂、電影、健康、醫學、科技、視覺化、視覺化、視覺化、電影、健康、醫療、醫學、科學、技術、視覺化、視覺化的
david bolinsky animates a cell	大衛•布林斯基會動畫一個細胞 。
i'm a medical illustrator , and i come from a slightly different point of view .	我是醫學插圖師 , 我來自稍微不同的觀點 。
i've been watching , since i grew up , the expressions of truth and beauty in the arts and truth and beauty in the sciences .	自從我長大以來 , 我一直在注意到 , 在科學中 , 藝術和美麗的表情 。
and while these are both wonderful things in their own right they both have very wonderful things going for them truth and beauty as ideals that can be looked at by the sciences and by math are almost like the ideal conjoined twins that a scientist would want to date .	雖然他們自己的權利 , 這些都是美好的事物 , 他們都有很美好的事物 , 把他們看待真相和美 , 看得見科學和數學 , 幾乎就像是理想的雙胞胎 , 科學家會想要約會 。
these are expressions of truth as awefull things , by meaning they are things you can worship .	這些是真實的表達 , 作為令人敬畏的事物 , 意思是 , 這些是你可以崇拜的事物 。
they are ideals that are powerful . they are irreducible .	它們是強而有力的理想 。 它們是無法引導的 。
they are unique . they are useful sometimes , often a long time after the fact .	它們是獨一無二的 , 有時是有用的 , 通常在事實後很長一段時間 。
and you can actually roll some of the pictures now , because i don't want to look at me on the screen .	你現在可以翻一些照片 , 因為我不想在螢幕上看著我 。
truth and beauty are things that are often opaque to people who are not in the sciences .	真相和美經常對那些不在科學領域的人不太友善 。
they are things that describe beauty in a way that is often only accessible if you understand the language and the syntax of the person who studies the subject in which truth and beauty is expressed .	它們是用來形容美麗的方式 , 通常只能在你了解語言和研究主題的同義詞時 , 才會被表達出來的 。
if you look at the math , e=mc squared , if you look at the cosmological constant , where there's an anthropic ideal , where you see that life had to evolve from the numbers that describe the universe these are things that are really difficult to understand .	如果你看數學e=mc平方 , 如果你看宇宙學的常數 , 那裡有一個人類理想 , 在那裡你會發現生命必須從描述宇宙的數字演化出來 , 這些是很難理解的 。
and what i've tried to do since i had my training as a medical illustrator since i was taught animation by my father , who was a sculptor and my visual mentor i wanted to figure out a way to help people understand truth and beauty in the biological sciences by using animation , by using pictures , by telling stories so that the things that are not necessarily evident to people can be brought forth , and can be taught , and can be understood .	自從我受過醫學插畫的訓練 , 自從我被教導父親的動畫 , 他是雕塑家 , 我的視覺導師 , 我想找出方法來幫助人們了解生物科學的真相和美麗 , 藉由動畫 , 用圖片說故事 , 讓人們不見得會被引導 , 並且可以被教導 。
students today are often immersed in an environment where what they learn is subjects that have truth and beauty embedded in them , but the way they're taught is compartmentalized and it's drawn down to the point where the truth and beauty are not always evident .	現今 , 學生常被沉浸在一個環境中 , 他們學到的是真相和美麗的主題 , 但他們被教導的方式卻被比較了 , 被吸引到事實和美 , 並非總是顯而易見的 。
it's almost like that old recipe for chicken soup where you boil the chicken until the flavor is just gone .	就像是雞湯的老食譜 , 把雞煮沸 , 直到味道消失 。
we don't want to do that to our students .	我們不想讓學生這樣做 。
so we have an opportunity to really open up education .	所以我們有機會真正開放教育 。
and i had a telephone call from robert lue at harvard , in the molecular and cellular biology department , a couple of years ago . he asked me if my team and i would be interested and willing to really change how medical and scientific education is done at harvard .	我在哈佛大學的robertlue打來一通電話 , 在幾年前的分子和細胞生物系裡 。 他問我 , 我的團隊是否有興趣 , 我願意改變哈佛大學的醫學和科學教育方式 。
so we embarked on a project that would explore the cell that would explore the truth and beauty inherent in molecular and cellular biology so that students could understand a larger picture that they could hang all of these facts on .	所以我們開始進行一項計畫 , 來探索細胞 , 來探索分子和細胞生物學中的真相和美 , 讓學生能了解他們能記住的所有事實 。
they could have a mental image of the cell as a large , bustling , hugely complicated city that's occupied by micromachines .	他們可能有對細胞的心理影像作為一個大型、繁忙的城市 , 一個由微機組成的複雜城市 。
and these micromachines really are at the heart of life .	這些微機械的確是生命的核心 。
these micromachines , which are the envy of nanotechnologists the world over , are selfdirected , powerful , precise , accurate devices that are made out of strings of amino acids .	這些微機械 , 正是奈米科技專家世界各地的電視節目 , 自主、強而有力、精確、精確的裝置 , 由胺基酸組成 。
and these micromachines power how a cell moves .	這些微機械是如何移動的 。
they power how a cell replicates . they power our hearts .	它們驅動細胞如何複製 , 驅動我們的心臟 。
they power our minds .	它們驅動了我們的心智 。
and so what we wanted to do was to figure out how we could make this story into an animation that would be the centerpiece of biovisions at harvard , which is a website that harvard has for its molecular and cellular biology students that will in addition to all the textual information , in addition to all the didactic stuff put everything together visually , so that these students would have an internalized view of what a cell really is in all of its truth and beauty , and be able to study with this view in mind , so that their imaginations would be sparked , so that their passions would be sparked and so that they would be able to go on and use these visions in their head to make new discoveries and to be able to find out , really , how life works .	所以我們想要做的是找出我們如何把這個故事變成動畫 , 將是哈佛大學生物觀測中心的主題 , 這個網站是哈佛為它分子和細胞生物學的學生 , 加上所有的文字信息 , 再加上所有的視覺資料 , 讓這些學生們對它的真實和美有內在的視角 , 並且能夠研究它們的視角 , 這樣他們就能發現它們的生命 。
so we set out by looking at how these molecules are put together .	所以我們開始研究這些分子是如何組合在一起的 。
we worked with a theme , which is , you've got macrophages that are streaming down a capillary , and they're touching the surface of the capillary wall , and they're picking up information from cells that are on the capillary wall , and they are given this information that there's an inflammation somewhere outside , where they can't see and sense .	我們和一個主題合作 , 也就是說 , 你有巨噬細胞 , 它們在微血管壁上流下 , 它們碰觸到微血管壁的表面 , 它們在微血管壁上接收到來自細胞的資訊 , 它們得到的資訊是外面的發炎 , 它們看不見、感覺不到 。
but they get the information that causes them to stop , causes them to internalize that they need to make all of the various parts that will cause them to change their shape , and try to get out of this capillary and find out what's going on .	但他們得到的資訊 , 會讓他們停止 , 造成他們內化 , 讓他們需要製造出各種各樣的零件 , 來改變他們的形狀 , 試著離開這個微血管 , 找出發生了什麼事 。
so these molecular motors we had to work with the harvard scientists and databank models of the atomically accurate molecules and figure out how they moved , and figure out what they did .	所以這些分子馬達 , 我們必須和哈佛科學家和資料庫合作 , 研究原子正確分子的資料模型 , 找出它們如何移動 , 找出它們做了什麼 。
and figure out how to do this in a way that was truthful in that it imparted what was going on , but not so truthful that the compact crowding in a cell would prevent the vista from happening .	想辦法用真相的方式來做這件事 , 讓事情變得更真實 , 但事實並非如此 , 牢房裡的精密擁擠 , 會阻止病毒的發生 。
and so what i'm going to show you is a threeminute reader's digest version of the first aspect of this film that we produced . it's an ongoing project that's going to go another four or five years .	接下來我要給你們看的是一個三分鐘的讀者的消化版本 , 我們製作的這部電影的第一個面向 。 這是一個持續進行的專案計畫 , 將要花四到五年 。
and i want you to look at this and see the paths that the cell manufactures these little walking machines , they're called kinesins that take these huge loads that would challenge an ant in relative size .	我希望你們看看這張圖 , 看到細胞製造這些小機器的路徑 , 它們被稱為 「 松樹 」 , 將大量的螞蟻大小挑戰相對大小的螞蟻 。
run the movie , please .	請播放電影 。
but these machines that power the inside of the cells are really quite amazing , and they really are the basis of all life because all of these machines interact with each other .	但這些能驅動細胞內部的機器是相當驚人的 , 它們真的是所有生命的基礎 , 因為這些機器彼此互動 。
they pass information to each other .	他們互相傳遞資訊 。
they cause different things to happen inside the cell .	它們會導致細胞內發生不同的事 。
and the cell will actually manufacture the parts that it needs on the fly , from information that's brought from the nucleus by molecules that read the genes .	細胞會製造它需要在果蠅身上所需的部分 , 來自從細胞核中取出的分子 , 以閱讀基因的分子 。
no life , from the smallest life to everybody here , would be possible without these little micromachines .	沒有生命 , 從最小的生命到這裡的每個人 , 沒有這些微機械 。
in fact , it would really , in the absence of these machines , have made the attendance here , chris , really quite sparse .	事實上 , 在沒有這些機器的情況下 , 它會讓這裡的出席率 , 克里斯 , 真的很大 。
this is the fedex delivery guy of the cell .	這是細胞的fedex遞送者 。
this little guy is called the kinesin , and he pulls a sack that's full of brand new manufactured proteins to wherever it's needed in the cell whether it's to a membrane , whether it's to an organelle , whether it's to build something or repair something .	這個小傢伙被稱為 「 海底 」 , 他把一個包裝滿全新的製造蛋白質到細胞所需的任何地方 , 不論是用到細胞膜 , 不論是用來製造或修補東西 。
and each of us has about 100 , 000 of these things running around , right now , inside each one of your 100 trillion cells .	我們每一個人身上都有大約十萬個這種東西在四處奔跑 , 就在你一百兆個細胞中 。
so no matter how lazy you feel , you're not really intrinsically doing nothing .	所以 , 不論你有多懶惰 , 你本質上都沒有做任何事 。
so what i want you to do when you go home is think about this , and think about how powerful our cells are .	所以當你回家時 , 我希望你們想想這一點 , 想想我們的細胞有多強大 。
and think about some of the things that we're learning about cellular mechanics .	想想看我們所學到的細胞機械 。
once we figure out all that's going on and believe me , we know almost a percent of what's going on once we figure out what's going on , we're really going to be able to have a lot of control over what we do with our health , with what we do with future generations , and how long we're going to live .	一旦我們搞懂了一切 , 相信我 , 我們幾乎知道發生了什麼事 , 我們真的能夠對我們的健康有很大的控制權 , 和我們未來的世代做些什麼 , 以及我們能活多久 。
and hopefully we'll be able to use this to discover more truth , and more beauty .	希望我們能用它來發掘更多真相 , 更美麗 。
but it's really quite amazing that these cells , these micromachines , are aware enough of what the cell needs that they do their bidding .	令人驚訝的是 , 這些細胞 , 這些微機能 , 已經足以察覺到細胞所需的作用 。
they work together . they make the cell do what it needs to do .	他們一起工作 。 他們讓細胞做它需要做的事 。
and their working together helps our bodies huge entities that they will never see function properly .	他們一起工作 , 協助我們的身體龐大的實體 , 他們永遠不會看到適當的功能 。
enjoy the rest of the show . thank you .	享受這場演出的其他演出 。 謝謝 。
becky blanton planned to live in her van for a year and see the country , but when depression set in and her freelance job ended , her camping trip turned into homelessness . in this intimate talk , she describes her experience of becoming one of america's working homeless .	beckyb蘭頓計劃在她的車裡住了一年 , 看到這個國家 , 但當憂鬱症開始 , 她的難民工作結束時 , 她的營地變成無家可歸的無家可歸者 。 在這個親密的演講中 , 她描述了她成為美國無家可歸者的經驗 。
adventure , happiness , life , personal growth , poverty , social change , society , storytelling	冒險、快樂、人生、個人的成長、貧窮、社會變遷、故事故事、故事、故事、故事、故事、故事、故事、社會、社會、故事、故事、故事、故事、故事、
becky blanton: the year i was homeless	beckyb蘭頓:那一年我是無家可歸的那一年 , 我是無家可歸的 。
i'm a writer and a journalist , and i'm also an insanely curious person , so in 22 years as a journalist , i've learned how to do a lot of new things .	我是作家和記者 , 我也是一位好奇的人 , 所以身為記者 , 我學會了很多新事 。
and three years ago , one of the things i learned how to do was to become invisible .	三年前 , 我學到的其中一件事就是變成看不見的 。
i became one of the working homeless .	我成為工作無家可歸者之一 。
i quit my job as a newspaper editor after my father died in february of that same year , and decided to travel .	我辭掉我父親在同一年二月去世的報紙編輯工作 , 決定去旅行 。
his death hit me pretty hard .	他的死亡讓我非常難受 。
and there were a lot of things that i wanted to feel and deal with while i was doing that .	我在做這件事時 , 會想去感受和處理很多事情 。
i've camped my whole life . and i decided that living in a van for a year to do this would be like one long camping trip .	我終其一生都在營運 。 我決定住在車裡住了一年 , 去做這個會是一趟漫長的露營旅程 。
so i packed my cat , my rottweiler and my camping gear into a 1975 chevy van , and drove off into the sunset , having fully failed to realize three critical things .	我把貓、腐爛的推動器和營地裝備打包 , 送到1975年的雪佛利車上 , 開到日落 , 完全沒有意識到三件重要的事 。
one: that society equates living in a permanent structure , even a shack , with having value as a person .	第一:社會將生活在一個永久的結構中 , 甚至是一個回憶 , 作為一個人有價值 。
two: i failed to realize how quickly the negative perceptions of other people can impact our reality , if we let it .	第二:我沒有意識到 , 其他人的負面感知有多快 , 如果我們允許它來影響我們的現實 。
three: i failed to realize that homelessness is an attitude , not a lifestyle .	第三:我沒意識到 , 無家可歸是一種態度 , 而非生活方式 。
at first , living in the van was great .	一開始 , 住在車裡是很棒的 。
i showered in campgrounds . i ate out regularly .	我在營地裡洗澡 , 我常常吃東西 。
and i had time to relax and to grieve .	我有時間放鬆和悲傷 。
but then the anger and the depression about my father's death set in .	但接著 , 我父親的死亡集團 , 憤怒和憂鬱 。
my freelance job ended . and i had to get a fulltime job to pay the bills .	我的自由工作終止了 。 我必須得到全職的工作來支付帳單 。
what had been a really mild spring turned into a miserably hot summer .	當時很溫和的春天 , 變成了很糟糕的夏天 。
and it became impossible to park anywhere without being very obvious that i had a cat and a dog with me , and it was really hot .	在任何地方 , 公園都不可能 , 很明顯地 , 我有一隻貓 , 一隻狗 , 和我在一起 , 真的很熱 。
the cat came and went through an open window in the van .	貓來了 , 穿過車窗的窗戶 。
the doggy went into doggy day care .	狗狗進入了產婦照顧 。
whenever i could , i used employee showers in office buildings and truck stops .	每當我能做到時 , 我都會在辦公大樓裡使用員工洗澡 , 卡車停下來 。
or i washed up in public rest rooms .	或者我在公共房間洗澡 。
nighttime temperatures in the van rarely dropped below 80 degrees fahrenheit , making it difficult or impossible to sleep .	夜班的車溫度很少下降到華氏80度 , 使得睡覺困難或無法睡覺 。
food rotted in the heat .	食物在暖氣中轉動 。
ice in my ice chest melted within hours , and it was pretty miserable .	數小時之內 , 冰層會融化 , 很悲慘 。
i couldn't afford to find an apartment , or couldn't afford an apartment that would allow me to have the rottweiler and the cat .	我負擔不起去找公寓 , 或不負擔得起的公寓 , 讓我能有推特威爾和貓 。
and i refused to give them up , so i stayed in the van .	我拒絕放棄 , 所以我留在車上 。
and when the heat made me too sick to walk the 50 feet to the public restroom outside my van at night , i used a bucket and a trash bag as a toilet .	當暖氣讓我不舒服地走50英尺 , 走在我車外的公共廁所時 , 我用桶和垃圾袋當廁所 。
when winter weather set in , the temperatures dropped below freezing . and they stayed there .	當冬天的天氣出現時 , 溫度降到冰凍之下 , 它們留在那裡 。
and i faced a whole new set of challenges .	我面對了一系列新的挑戰 。
i parked a different place every night so i would avoid being noticed and hassled by the police .	我每天晚上停車 , 避免被警察察察察察察察察察察察察察察察察察察覺 。
i didn't always succeed .	我並不總是成功 。
but i felt out of control of my life .	但我覺得自己無法控制我的人生 。
and i don't know when or how it happened , but the speed at which i went from being a talented writer and journalist to being a homeless woman , living in a van , took my breath away .	我不知道何時或何時會發生 , 但我的速度從一個有才華的作家和記者變成一個無家可歸的女人 , 住在車裡 , 帶著我的呼吸 。
i hadn't changed . my i . q . hadn't dropped .	我還沒改變 , 我的智商還沒下降 。
my talent , my integrity , my values , everything about me remained the same .	我的才華、我的完整性、我的價值觀 , 所有關於我的事都一樣 。
but i had changed somehow .	但我已經改變了 。
i spiraled deeper and deeper into a depression .	我更深入憂鬱 。
and eventually someone referred me to a homeless health clinic .	最終有人把我稱為無家可歸的健康診所 。
and i went . i hadn't bathed in three days .	我去了 。 三天後我還沒洗澡 。
i was as smelly and as depressed as anyone in line .	我和排隊中的任何人一樣感到沮喪 。
i just wasn't drunk or high .	我只是不喝醉或喝醉 。
and when several of the homeless men realized that , including a former university professor , they said , " you aren't homeless . why are you really here ? "	當數個無家可歸的人意識到 , 包括以前的大學教授 , 他們說: 「 你不是無家可歸 。 你為什麼在這裡 ? 」
other homeless people didn't see me as homeless , but i did .	其他無家可歸的人沒把我視為無家可歸 , 但我做到了 。
then the professor listened to my story and he said , " you have a job . you have hope .	接著 , 教授傾聽我的故事 , 他說: 「 你有工作 , 你有希望 。
the real homeless don't have hope . "	真正的無家可歸沒有希望 。 」
a reaction to the medication the clinic gave me for my depression left me suicidal . and i remember thinking , " if i killed myself , no one would notice . "	診所給我憂鬱症的反應讓我有自殺傾向 。 我記得在想: 「 如果我殺了我自己 , 沒人注意到 。 」
a friend told me , shortly after that , that she had heard that tim russert , a nationally renowned journalist , had been talking about me on national t . v .	不久後 , 一位朋友告訴我 , 她聽說提姆•羅斯 , 全國知名的記者 , 一直在談論我國家電視 。
an essay i'd written about my father , the year before he died , was in tim's new book .	我寫的一篇文章是關於我父親的 , 在他死前一年 , 是在提姆的新書中 。
and he was doing the talk show circuit . and he was talking about my writing .	他在演說電路 。 他在談我的寫作 。
and when i realized that tim russert , former moderator of " meet the press , " was talking about my writing , while i was living in a van in a walmart parking lot , i started laughing .	當我意識到timrustt , 前主持 「 見面新聞 」 的陳述者 , 談到我的寫作 , 當我在walmart停車場 , 我開始笑 。
i started laughing because it got to the point where , was i a writer , or was i a homeless woman ?	我開始笑是因為我是作家 , 還是無家可歸的女人 ?
so i went in the bookstore . and i found tim's book .	所以我去了書店 。 我找到了提姆的書 。
and i stood there . and i reread my essay .	我站在那裡 , 重新讀我的短文 。
because i was a writer .	因為我是個作家 。
i was a writer .	我是作家 。
shortly after that i moved back to tennessee .	在那之後不久 , 我搬回田納西 。
i alternated between living in a van and couch surfing with friends .	我和朋友住在貨車和沙發衝浪之間的區別 。
and i started writing again .	我又開始寫作了 。
by the summer of the following year i was a working journalist .	隔年夏天 , 我是一名工作記者 。
i was winning awards . i was living in my own apartment .	我在贏得獎項 。 我住在自己的公寓裡 。
i was no longer homeless .	我不再無家可歸 。
and i was no longer invisible .	我不再被看不見了 。
thousands of people work full and parttime jobs , and live in their cars .	數以千計的人都在工作 , 有時工作 , 住在他們的車裡 。
but society continues to stigmatize and criminalize living in your vehicle or on the streets .	但社會持續汙名和犯罪化生活在你的車子或街道上 。
so the homeless , the working homeless , primarily remain invisible .	所以 , 無家可歸者 , 工作無家可歸者 , 主要是隱形的 。
but if you ever meet one , engage them , encourage them , and offer them hope .	但如果你曾經見過他們 , 讓他們參與 , 鼓勵他們 , 並提供他們希望 。
the human spirit can overcome anything if it has hope .	人類精神可以克服任何事情 , 如果它有希望的話 。
and i'm not here to be the poster girl for the homeless .	我不是來這裡為無家可歸的海報 。
i'm not here to encourage you to give money to the next panhandler you meet .	我不是來這裡鼓勵你們把錢給下一個乞討者 。
but i am here to tell you that , based on my experience , people are not where they live , where they sleep , or what their life situation is at any given time .	但我來這裡要告訴各位 , 根據我的經驗 , 人們不是住在他們居住的地方 , 他們在哪裡睡覺 , 或是任何時間生活的情況 。
three years ago i was living in a van in a walmart parking lot , and today i'm speaking at ted .	三年前 , 我住在一輛walmart停車場 , 今天我在ted演講 。
hope always , always finds a way . thank you .	希望總是找到方法 。 謝謝 。
at tedxchange , thailand's " mr . condom , " mechai viravaidya , walks us through the country's bold plan to raise its standard of living , starting in the 1970s . first step: population control . and that means a lot of frank , funny and very effective talk about condoms .	在tedxchange , 泰國的 「 保險套先生 」 、 「 墨拉威亞先生 」 , 帶著我們走過國家大膽的計劃 , 提升生活的標準 , 第一步:人口控制 。 這意味著很多富蘭克、好笑且非常有效的討論保險套 。
culture , global issues , health , population , science	文化、全球議題、健康、人口、科學、科學、
mechai viravaidya: how mr . condom made thailand a better place	墨西亞:保險套先生如何讓泰國成為更好的地方 。
now , when i was a young man 40 years ago , the country was very , very poor with lots and lots and lots of people living in poverty .	四十年前 , 當我還是個年輕人時 , 這個國家非常非常貧窮 , 生活在貧窮之中 。
we decided to do something about it , but we didn't begin with a welfare program or a poverty reduction program .	我們決定做點什麼 , 但我們不是從福利計畫開始 , 或減少貧窮計畫 。
but we began with a familyplanning program , following a very successful maternal child health activity , sets of activities .	但我們從一個家庭規劃計畫開始 , 遵循一個非常成功的孕育兒童健康活動 , 一組活動 。
so basically , no one would accept family planning if their children didn't survive .	基本上 , 沒有人會接受家庭規劃 , 如果他們的孩子沒有存活 ,
so the first step: get to the children , get to the mothers , and then follow up with family planning .	所以 , 第一步:帶到孩子們 , 去找母親 , 然後跟著家人規劃 。
not just child mortality alone , you need also family planning .	不只是兒童死亡率 , 你還需要家庭規劃 。
now let me take you back as to why we needed to do it .	現在 , 讓我帶各位回到我們為什麼需要這麼做 。
in my country , that was the case in 1974 .	在我的國家 , 那是1974年的案例 。
seven children per family tremendous growth at 3 . 3 percent .	家庭平均每人7個孩子的成長率是3.3% 。
there was just no future .	沒有未來 。
we needed to reduce the population growth rate .	我們需要減少人口成長率 。
so we said , " let's do it . "	所以我們說: 「 咱們來做吧 。 」
the women said , " we agree . we'll use pills , but we need a doctor to prescribe the pills , " and we had very , very few doctors .	女性說: 「 我們同意 , 我們會使用藥丸 , 但我們需要醫生來開藥 。 」 我們非常非常非常少的醫生 。
we didn't take no as an answer ; we took no as a question .	我們不把答案當作一個答案 , 我們不把問題當作一個問題 。
we went to the nurses and the midwives , who were also women , and did a fantastic job at explaining how to use the pill .	我們去了護士和助產士 , 他們也是女人 , 做了一個很棒的工作 , 解釋如何使用藥丸 。
that was wonderful , but it covered only 20 percent of the country .	那很棒 , 但它佔了全國的百分之二十 。
what do we do for the other 80 percent leave them alone and say , " well , they're not medical personnel . "	我們為其他80%的人做些什麼 , 讓他們獨自一人說: 「 嗯 , 他們不是醫療人員 。 」
no , we decided to do a bit more .	不 , 我們決定再做一點 。
so we went to the ordinary people that you saw .	所以我們去找一般人 。
actually , below that yellow sign i wish they hadn't wiped that , because there was " cocacola " there .	其實 , 在那黃色標誌下面我希望他們還沒聽過 , 因為那裡有 「 可口可樂 」 。
we were so much bigger than cocacola in those days .	當時我們比可口可樂還要大很多 。
and no difference , the people they chose were the people we chose .	沒有差別 , 他們選的人是我們選的人 。
they were wellknown in the community , they knew that customers were always right , and they were terrific , and they practiced their family planning themselves .	他們在社區中很熟悉 , 他們知道客戶總是對的 , 他們很棒 , 他們親自練習自己的家庭規劃 。
so they could supply pills and condoms throughout the country , in every village of the country .	所以他們可以在全國各地提供藥丸和保險套 。
so there we are . we went to the people who were seen as the cause of the problem to be the solution .	所以 , 我們就在那裡 。 我們去找被視為是解決問題的人們 。
wherever there were people and you can see boats with the women , selling things here's the floating market selling bananas and crabs and also contraceptives wherever you find people , you'll find contraceptives in thailand .	不論在哪裡 , 都有人和女人買船 , 賣東西是浮動的市場 , 賣香蕉和螃蟹 , 還有避孕用品 , 不論你在泰國找到人 , 你都會找到避孕品 。
and then we decided , why not get to religion because in the philippines , the catholic church was pretty strong , and thai people were buddhist .	然後我們決定 , 為什麼不去宗教 , 因為在菲律賓 , 天主教教會很強壯 , 泰國人是佛教徒 。
we went to them and they said , " look , could you help us ? "	我們去找他們 , 他們說: 「 看 , 你能幫我們嗎 ? 」
i'm there the one in blue , not the yellow holding a bowl of holy water for the monk to sprinkle holy water on pills and condoms for the sanctity of the family .	我是藍色的 , 不是黃色的 , 手上拿著一碗神聖的水 , 來灑水在藥丸上和保險套上 。
and this picture was sent throughout the country .	這張照片被送到全國各地 。
so some of the monks in the villages were doing the same thing themselves .	所以有些村落的僧侶也在做同樣的事 。
and the women were saying , " no wonder we have no sideeffects .	女人說: 「 難怪我們沒有副作用 。
it's been blessed . "	它被祝福了 。 」
that was their perception .	那是他們的感知 。
and then we went to teachers .	然後我們去找老師 。
you need everybody to be involved in trying to provide whatever it is that make humanity a better place .	你需要每個人試著提供任何讓人類變得更好的地方 。
so we went to the teachers .	所以我們去找老師 。
over a quarter of a million were taught about family planning with a new alphabet a , b for birth , c for condom , i for iud , v for vasectomy .	超過25萬人被教導要用新的字母a、b、c出生、保險套、大腸切除術 。
and then we had a snakes and ladders game , where you throw dice .	然後我們有了蛇和雷達比賽 , 你扔掉了 。
if you land on anything profamily planning , you move ahead .	如果你降落在熟悉的規劃上 , 你就先往前走 。
like , " mother takes the pill every night .	比如說: 「 媽媽每天要吃藥 。
very good , mother . move ahead .	非常好的 , 母親 , 向前走 。
uncle buys a condom . very good , uncle . move ahead .	叔叔買保險套 。 非常好 , 叔叔 。 搬到前面 。
uncle gets drunk , doesn't use condom . come back , start again . "	叔叔喝醉 , 不用保險套 , 回來 , 再來 。 」
again , education , class entertainment .	同樣的 , 教育 , 階級娛樂 。
and the kids were doing it in school too .	孩子們也在學校這麼做 。
we had relay races with condoms , we had children's condomblowing championship .	我們有保險套的競賽 , 我們有兒童保險套的冠軍 。
and before long , the condom was know as the girl's best friend .	不久後 , 保險套是女孩最好的朋友 。
in thailand , for poor people , diamonds don't make it so the condom is the girl's best friend .	在泰國 , 對窮人來說 , 鑽石不會變成這樣 , 所以保險套是女孩最好的朋友 。
we introduced our first microcredit program in 1975 , and the women who organized it said , " we only want to lend to women who practice family planning .	我們在1975年介紹了第一個微型貸款計畫 , 組織計畫的女性說: 「 我們只想借助實踐家庭規劃的女性 。
if you're pregnant , take care of your pregnancy .	如果你懷孕了 , 照顧懷孕 。
if you're not pregnant , you can take a loan out from us . "	如果你沒有懷孕 , 你可以從我們身上借貸 。 」
and that was run by them .	而他們就是這樣運作的 。
and after 35/36 years , it's still going on .	35/36年後 , 它還在進行中 。
it's a part of the village development bank ; it's not a real bank , but it's a fund microcredit .	它是村落發展銀行的一部分 ; 它不是真正的銀行 , 而是基金的小額貸款 。
and we didn't need a big organization to run it it was run by the villagers themselves .	我們不需要一個大型組織來經營它 , 由村民們自己經營 。
and you probably hardly see a thai man there , it's always women , women , women , women .	你可能很難看到一位泰國男士 , 總是女人、女人、女人、女人 。
and then we thought we'd help america , because america's been helping everyone , whether they want help or not .	然後我們以為我們會幫助美國 , 因為美國對所有人都很有幫助 , 不管他們是否想要幫助 。
and this is on the fourth of july .	這是七月四日的狀況 。
we decided to provide vasectomy to all men , but in particular , american men to the front of the queue , right up to the ambassador's residence during his [unclear] .	我們決定為所有人提供真空的切除術 , 尤其是 , 美國人在隊伍的前面 , 就在大使的前面 。
and the hotel gave us the ballroom for it very appropriate room .	飯店給了我們一間房間 , 給了我們非常適合的房間 。
and since it was near lunch time , they said , " all right , we'll give you some lunch .	他們說: 「 好吧 , 我們會給你一些午餐時間 。
of course , it must be american cola .	當然 , 它一定是美國的可樂 。
you get two brands , coke and pepsi .	有兩個品牌 , 可口可樂和百事可樂 。
and then the food is either hamburger or hotdog . "	然後食物不是漢堡或熱狗 。 」
and i thought a hotdog will be more symbolic .	我以為熱狗比較有象徵意義 。
and here is this , then , young man called willy bohm who worked for the usaid .	這裡是一位年輕人 , 叫做威利•博姆 , 他為美國援助工作 。
obviously , he's had his vasectomy because his hotdog is half eaten , and he was very happy .	很明顯 , 他有很大的選擇 , 因為他的熱狗半吃了一半 , 且他很開心 。
it made a lot of news in america , and it angered some people also .	它在美國製造了很多新聞 , 它也激怒了一些人 。
i said , " don't worry . come over and i'll do the whole lot of you . "	我說: 「 別擔心 , 過來 , 我會做你們很多人 。 」
in all this thing , from seven children to 1 . 5 children , population growth rate of 3 . 3 to 0 . 5 .	在這一切中 , 從七個孩童到一百五個孩童 , 人口增長率是3.3到0.5 。
you could call it the cocacola approach if you like it was exactly the same thing .	你可以稱它為可口可樂 , 如果你喜歡它是完全一樣的 。
i'm not sure whether cocacola followed us , or we followed cocacola , but we're good friends .	我不確定可口可樂是否跟隨我們 , 或跟隨可口可樂 , 但我們是好朋友 。
and so that's the case of everyone joining in .	這就是大家加入的案例 。
we didn't have a strong government . we didn't have lots of doctors .	我們沒有強大的政府 , 我們沒有很多醫生 。
but it's everybody's job who can change attitude and behavior .	但每個人都能改變態度和行為 。
then aids came along and hit thailand , and we had to stop doing a lot of good things to fight aids .	接著 , 愛滋病來到泰國 , 我們必須停止做很多好事來對抗愛滋病 。
but unfortunately , the government was in denial , denial , denial .	但不幸的是 , 政府被否認、否認、否認 。
so our work wasn't affected .	所以我們的作品沒有受到影響 。
so i thought , " well , if you can't go to the government , go to the military . "	所以我想: 「 嗯 , 如果你不能去政府 , 去軍隊 。 」
so i went to the military and asked to borrow 300 radio stations .	所以我去了軍隊 , 要求借300間無線電站 。
they have more than the government , and they've got more guns than the government .	他們有比政府更多的槍 , 比政府更多的槍 。
so i asked them , could they help us in our fight against hiv .	所以我問他們 , 他們能否協助我們對抗愛滋病毒 。
and after i gave them statistics , they said , " yes . okay . you can use all the radio stations , television stations . "	在我給他們統計之後 , 他們說: 「 好的 。 你可以用所有的電台、電視台 。 」
and that's when we went onto the airwaves .	這就是我們登上飛機的時候 。
and then we got a new prime minister soon after that .	然後我們很快就得到了新首相 。
and he said , " mechai , could you come and join ? "	他說: 「 梅西 , 你能來加入嗎 ? 」

so i said , " okay . "	所以我說: 「 好吧 。 」
he became the chairman of the national aids committee and increased the budget fiftyfold .	他成為國家愛滋病委員會的主席 , 並增加五十倍的預算 。
every ministry , even judges , had to be involved in aids education everyone and we said the public , institutions , religious institutions , schools everyone was involved .	每個部門、甚至法官 , 都必須參與愛滋病教育 , 每一個人 , 我們都說 , 公眾、機構、宗教機構、學校都參與其中 。
and here , every media person had to be trained for hiv .	這裡 , 每一個媒體人員都必須接受愛滋病的訓練 。
and we gave every station half a minute extra for advertising to earn more money .	我們提供每一間車站半分鐘的廣告 , 來賺更多的錢 。
so they were happy with that .	所以他們很開心 。
and then aids education in all schools , starting from university .	然後所有學校的愛滋病教育 , 從大學開始 。
and these are high school kids teaching high school kids .	這些是高中生在教導高中生 。
and the best teachers were the girls , not the boys , and they were terrific .	最好的老師是女生 , 不是男生 , 她們很棒 。
and these girls who go around teaching about safe sex and hiv were known as mother theresa .	這些環繞著教導安全性愛滋病毒的女孩 , 被稱為 「 阿雷莎媽媽 」 。
and then we went down one more step .	然後我們再走下一步 。
these are primary school kids third , fourth grade going to every household in the village , every household in the whole of thailand , giving aids information and a condom to every household , given by these young kids .	這些是第一所學校三年級的孩童 , 四年級 , 在村子裡的每個家庭 , 整個泰國的每個家庭 , 提供愛滋病資訊和保險套給每個家庭 , 給這些孩子 。
and no parents objected , because we were trying to save lives , and this was a lifesaver .	沒有父母反對 , 因為我們試著拯救生命 , 這是個救命 。
and we said , " everyone needs to be involved . "	我們說: 「 每個人都需要參與 。 」
so you have the companies also realizing that sick staff don't work , and dead customers don't buy .	所以你也有公司意識到生病的員工不行 , 而死去的客戶卻不買 。
so they all trained .	所以他們都受過訓練 。
and then we have this captain condom , with his harvard mba , going to schools and night spots .	然後我們就有了這位船長保險套 , 他的哈佛大學mba , 去上學和夜班 。
and they loved him . you need a symbol of something .	他們愛他 , 你需要一些東西的象徵 。
in every country , every program , you need a symbol , and this is probably the best thing he's ever done with his mba .	在每個國家 , 每個專案 , 你都需要一個符號 , 這可能是他對mba做過最好的事 。
and then we gave condoms out everywhere on the streets everywhere , everywhere .	接著 , 我們把保險套放在街上 , 到處都有 。
in taxis , you get condoms .	在計程車中 , 你會得到保險套 。
and also , in traffic , the policemen give you condoms our " cops and rubbers " programs .	此外 , 在交通中 , 警察會給你保險套 , 我們的 「 警察 」 計畫 。
so , can you imagine new york policemen giving out condoms ?	所以 , 你能想像紐約警察發放保險套嗎 ?

and then finally , in thailand we're buddhist , we don't have a god , so instead , we say , " in rubber we trust . "	最後 , 在泰國 , 我們是佛教徒 , 我們沒有神 , 所以我們會說: 「 在橡膠中 , 我們相信 。 」
so you can see that we added everything to our endeavor to make life better for the people .	所以你可以看到 , 我們把一切都加到我們的努力 , 讓人民的生活變得更好 。
we had condoms in all the refrigerators in the hotels and the schools , because alcohol impairs judgment .	我們在旅館和學校都有保險套 , 因為酒精障評斷 。

and then we decided to help people out of poverty , now that we got aids somewhat out of the way this time , not with government alone , but in cooperation with the business community .	接著 , 我們決定要幫助人們脫離貧窮 , 現在我們得到了愛滋病 , 這次不是單單靠政府 , 而是和商業社群合作 。
because poor people are business people who lack business skills and access to credit .	因為窮人是商人 , 他們缺乏商業技能 , 無法取得信用 。
those are the things to be provided by the business community .	這些是商業界提供的 。
we're trying to turn them into barefoot entrepreneurs , little business people .	我們試著把他們變成赤腳企業家 , 小商業人士 。
the only way out of poverty is through business enterprise .	逃離貧窮唯一的方法就是透過企業 。
so , that was done .	所以 , 就這樣完成了 。
the money goes from the company into the village via treeplanting .	這筆錢從公司變成了村落 , 變成了樹木 。
it's not a free gift .	這不是免費的禮物 。
they plant the trees , and the money goes into their microcredit fund , which we call the village development bank .	他們種植樹木 , 錢進入他們的小額貸款基金 , 我們稱之為鄉村發展銀行 。
everybody joins in , and they feel they own the bank , because they have brought the money in .	每個人都加入 , 他們覺得自己擁有銀行 , 因為他們把錢帶進來 。
and before you can borrow the money , you need to be trained .	在你借錢之前 , 你需要被訓練 。
and we believe if you want to help the poor , those who are living in poverty , access to credit must be a human right .	我們相信 , 如果你想要幫助窮人 , 住在貧窮中的人 , 能夠取得信用 , 就必須要是人權 。
access to credit must be a human right .	信用資本必須是人權 。
otherwise they'll never get out of poverty .	否則他們永遠不會脫離貧困 。
and then before getting a loan , you must be trained .	在取得貸款之前 , 你必須要受過訓練 。
here's what we call a " barefoot mba , " teaching people how to do business so that , when they borrow money , they'll succeed with the business .	我們稱之為 「 赤腳mba 」 , 教導人們如何做生意 , 這樣 , 當他們借錢時 , 他們就會成功 。
these are some of the businesses: mushrooms , crabs , vegetables , trees , fruits , and this is very interesting nike ice cream and nike biscuits ; this is a village sponsored by nike .	這些是一些生意:蘑菇、螃蟹、蔬菜、樹木、水果 , 這是非常有趣的nike冰淇淋和nike餅乾 ; 這是一個由nike贊助的村莊 。
they said , " they should stop making shoes and clothes .	他們說: 「 他們應該停止製作鞋子和衣服 。
make these better , because we can afford them . "	做得更好 , 因為我們負擔得起 。 」
and then we have silk , thai silk .	然後我們有絲、泰國絲 。
now we're making scottish tartans , as you can see on the left , to sell to all people of scottish ancestors .	現在我們正在做蘇格蘭紋身 , 左邊可以看到 , 賣給所有蘇格蘭祖先 。
so anyone sitting in and watching tv , get in touch with me .	所以 , 任何人坐著看電視 , 跟我聯絡 。
and then this is our answer to starbucks in thailand " coffee and condoms . "	這是我們在泰國的星巴克《咖啡和保險套》的答案 。

can you imagine , at every starbucks that you can also get condoms ?	你能想像嗎 , 在每個你能得到保險套的星巴克裡 ?
you can order your condoms with your with your cappuccino .	你可以用你的卡普奇諾來訂購保險套 。
and then now , finally in education , we want to change the school as being underutilized into a place where it's a lifelong learning center for everyone .	最後 , 在教育上 , 我們想要改變學校 , 把學校當作不被利用的地方 , 讓每個人成為終身學習中心 。
we call this our schoolbased integrated rural development .	我們稱之為學校基於整合的農村發展 。
and it's a center , a focal point for economic and social development .	它是一個經濟和社會發展的中心點 。
redo the school , make it serve the community needs .	重新設計學校 , 讓它能服務社區的需求 。

and we use vegetables around the school ground , so they raise their own vegetables .	我們在學校的地面上使用蔬菜 , 讓它們養活自己的蔬菜 。
and then , finally , i firmly believe , if we want the mdgs to work the millennium development goals we need to add family planning to it .	最後 , 我堅定相信 , 如果我們希望mdgs可以完成千禧年發展目標 , 我們需要加入家庭計畫 。
of course , child mortality first and then family planning everyone needs family planning service it's underutilized .	當然 , 孩童死亡率首先 , 接著是家庭規劃 , 每個人都需要家庭規劃服務 。
