your smartphone may feel like a friend but a true friend would give you a smile once in a while . at ted2013 , keller rinaudo demos romo , the smartphonepowered mini robot who can motor along with you on a walk , slide you a cup of coffee across the table , and react to you with programmable expressions .	你的智慧手機可能會感覺像個朋友 , 但一個真正的朋友 , 一陣子會給你一個微笑一陣子 。 在ted2013 , kellerrinaudoderomo , 和你一起散步的智能機器人 , 投影片給你一杯咖啡 , 橫跨桌子 , 和你互動 。
keller rinaudo: a mini robot powered by your phone	凱勒•里納多:一個迷你機器人是由你的手機供給你的 。
so just by a show of hands , how many of you all have a robot at home ?	舉個例子 , 在座有多少人家裡都有機器人 ?
not very many of you .	很多人都沒有 。
okay . and actually of those hands , if you don't include roomba how many of you have a robot at home ?	好的 。 實際上 , 如果你不包含室巴你們有多少人在家裡有機器人 ?
that's the problem that we're trying to solve at romotive that i and the other 20 nerds at romotive are obsessed with solving .	這就是我們在romotive努力解決的問題 , 我和其他20個在romotive迷戀的怪胎 , 都迷上了解決問題 。
so we really want to build a robot that anyone can use , whether you're eight or 80 .	所以我們真的想要製造一個任何人都可以使用的機器人 , 不管你是8或80歲 。
and as it turns out , that's a really hard problem , because you have to build a small , portable robot that's not only really affordable , but it has to be something that people actually want to take home and have around their kids .	結果發現 , 這是個非常困難的問題 , 因為你必須建造一個小型可攜式的機器人 , 不僅是可以負擔得起的 , 而且它必須是人們真正想要帶回家 , 帶著孩子去的地方 。
this robot can't be creepy or uncanny .	這個機器人不能很詭異或不可思議 。
he should be friendly and cute .	他應該是友善的、可愛的 。
romo's a robot that uses a device you already know and love your iphone as his brain .	romo是一個用你已經知道的裝置來愛你的iphone是他的大腦 。
and by leveraging the power of the iphone's processor , we can create a robot that is wifi enabled and computer visioncapable for 150 bucks , which is about one percent of what these kinds of robots have cost in the past .	透過透過iphone處理器的力量 , 我們就能創造一個可以在150美金上實現的機器人 , 機器人的視覺化成本大約是過去的150美金之一 。
when romo wakes up , he's in creature mode .	當romo醒來時 , 他在創造模式中 。
so he's actually using the video camera on the device to follow my face .	所以他實際上是用裝置上的攝影機來追蹤我的臉 。
if i duck down , he'll follow me .	如果我倒下 , 他會跟著我 。
he's wary , so he'll keep his eyes on me .	他很溫暖 , 所以他會盯著我看 。
if i come over here , he'll turn to follow me .	如果我來這裡 , 他會轉身跟著我 。
if i come over here he's smart .	如果我來這裡 , 他很聰明 。
and if i get too close to him , he gets scared just like any other creature .	如果我太靠近他 , 他就會嚇到和其他生物一樣 。
so in a lot of ways , romo is like a pet that has a mind of his own .	所以 , 在很多方面 , romo就像個寵物 , 擁有自己的想法 。
thanks , little guy .	謝謝 , 小傢伙 。
and if i want to explore the world uhoh , romo's tired if i want to explore the world with romo , i can actually connect him from any other ios device .	如果我想要探索世界──呃 , romo已經累了──如果我想要用romo來探索這個世界 , 我真的可以將他與任何其他ios設備連結 。
so here's the ipad .	這是ipad 。
and romo will actually stream video to this device .	羅摩會將影片串流到這個裝置上 。
so i can see everything that romo sees , and i get a robot'seyeview of the world .	所以我可以看到romo看到的一切 , 我得到了一個機器人的世界觀 。
now this is a free app on the app store , so if any of you guys had this app on your phones , we could literally right now share control of the robot and play games together .	這是應用程式的免費應用程式 , 所以 , 如果你們有人在手機上有這個應用程式 , 我們現在可以把機器人和玩遊戲一起分享 。
so i'll show you really quickly , romo actually he's streaming video , so you can see me and the entire ted audience .	我很快地給你們看romo , 他正在串流影片 , 所以你們可以看到我和整個ted觀眾 。
if i get in front of romo here .	如果我來到羅摩這裡 。
and if i want to control him , i can just drive .	如果我想要控制他 , 我就能開車 。
so i can drive him around , and i can take pictures of you .	所以 , 我可以隨意開車 , 拍下你們的照片 。
i've always wanted a picture of a 1 , 500person ted audience .	我總是想要一張1500名ted觀眾的照片 。
so i'll snap a picture .	我來拍一張照片 。
and in the same way that you scroll through content on an ipad , i can actually adjust the angle of the camera on the device .	和你在ipad上瀏覽內容的方式一樣 , 我可以調整裝置上的攝影機的角度 。
so there are all of you through romo's eyes .	所以在座所有人都透過romo的眼睛 。
and finally , because romo is an extension of me , i can express myself through his emotions .	最後 , 因為romo是我的延伸 , 我可以透過他的情緒來表達自己 。
so i can go in and i can say let's make romo excited .	所以 , 我可以進去 , 我可以說 , 讓我們來做romo興奮 。
but the most important thing about romo is that we wanted to create something that was literally completely intuitive .	但關於romo最重要的是 , 我們想要創造完全直覺的東西 。
you do not have to teach someone how to drive romo .	你不需要教別人如何駕駛romo 。
in fact , who would like to drive a robot ?	事實上 , 誰會想要開機器人 ?
thank you , scott .	謝謝 , 史考特 。
and even cooler , you actually don't have to be in the same geographic location as the robot to control him .	更酷的是 , 你不需要像機器人在同一個地理位置來控制他 。
so he actually streams twoway audio and video between any two smart devices .	所以他在任何兩個聰明的裝置中 , 實際上是雙向音頻和影像 。
so you can log in through the browser , and it's kind of like skype on wheels .	所以你可以在瀏覽器上登入 , 有點像是在輪子上的天空 。
so we were talking before about telepresence , and this is a really cool example .	所以 , 我們之前談到遠端監聽 , 這是個很酷的例子 。
you can imagine an eightyearold girl , for example , who has an iphone , and her mom buys her a robot .	你可以想像一個八歲的女孩 , 例如 , 她有iphone , 她媽媽買了一台機器人 。
that girl can take her iphone , put it on the robot , send an email to grandma , who lives on the other side of the country .	那個女孩可以拿她的iphone , 把它放在機器人上 , 寄送一封電子郵件給國內另一邊的祖母 。
grandma can log into that robot and play hideandgoseek with her granddaughter for fifteen minutes every single night , when otherwise she might only be able to get to see her granddaughter once or twice a year .	祖母可以登入那個機器人 , 和她的孫子一起玩隱藏糖果 , 每晚十五分鐘 , 否則她只能看到她的孫子一年一次或兩次 。
so those are a couple of the really cool things that romo can do today .	這些是romo今天能做的一些很酷的事 。
but i just want to finish by talking about something that we're working on in the future .	但我只想談談我們未來正在努力的事物 。
this is actually something that one of our engineers , dom , built in a weekend .	這其實是其中一個工程師 , 多姆 , 在一個週末建造的 。
it's built on top of a google open framework called blockly .	它是建立在谷歌開放的架構上 , 叫做 「 街區 」 。
this allows you to drag and drop these blocks of semantic code and create any behavior for this robot you want .	這讓你可以拖動這些海豹編碼的積木 , 為你想要的機器人創造任何行為 。
you do not have to know how to code to create a behavior for romo .	你不需要知道如何寫程式來為romo創造一個行為 。
and you can actually simulate that behavior in the browser , which is what you see romo doing on the left .	你可以模擬瀏覽器的行為 , 也就是左邊的romo在做的 。
and then if you have something you like , you can download it onto your robot and execute it in real life , run the program in real life .	如果你有你喜歡的東西 , 你可以把它下載到你的機器人上 , 在現實生活中執行 , 執行程式 。
and then if you have something you're proud of , you can share it with every other person who owns a robot in the world .	如果你感到自豪的是 , 你可以和世界上所有擁有機器人的人分享 。
so all of these wifi–enabled robots actually learn from each other .	所有這些wi-fi的機器人 , 都能互相學習 。
the reason we're so focused on building robots that everyone can train is that we think the most compelling use cases in personal robotics are personal .	我們之所以專注於建造一個人都能訓練的機器人 , 是因為我們認為在個人機器人中 , 最有吸引力的用途是個人的 。
they change from person to person .	他們從人變成人 。
so we think that if you're going to have a robot in your home , that robot ought to be a manifestation of your own imagination .	所以 , 我們認為 , 如果你在家裡有機器人 , 機器人應該是你自己的想像力的表現 。
so i wish that i could tell you what the future of personal robotics looks like .	所以我希望我能告訴你個人機器人的未來是什麼樣子 。
to be honest , i have no idea .	老實說 , 我不知道 。
but what we do know is that it isn't 10 years or 10 billion dollars or a large humanoid robot away .	但我們確實知道 , 它不是10年或100億美元 , 或一個大型的人類機器人 。
the future of personal robotics is happening today , and it's going to depend on small , agile robots like romo and the creativity of people like yourselves .	個人機器人的未來正在發生 , 它將會取決於小型、敏捷的機器人 , 像是romo , 以及像你們這樣的人的創造力 。
so we can't wait to get you all robots , and we can't wait to see what you build .	所以 , 我們等不及要讓你們所有機器人 , 我們等不及要看你建造什麼 。
author and activist isabel allende discusses women , creativity , the definition of feminism and , of course , passion in this talk .	作者和激進分子伊莎貝爾會討論女性、創意、女性主義的定義 , 當然 , 還有這場演說中的熱情 。
entertainment , global issues , love , parenting , storytelling , women , world cultures	娛樂、全球議題、愛、養育、說故事、女性、世界文化、文化、文化、
isabel allende tells tales of passion	伊莎貝爾•阿言德說出關於熱情的故事 。
thank you so much . it's really scary to be here among the smartest of the smart .	非常謝謝你們 。 非常可怕 , 在這裡是聰明最聰明的人之一 。
i'm here to tell you a few tales of passion .	我在這裡要告訴各位幾個關於熱情的故事 。
there's a jewish saying that i love .	有句猶太人說我很愛 。
what is truer than truth ? answer: the story .	什麼是真的 ? 答案是:故事 。
i'm a storyteller . i want to convey something that is truer than truth about our common humanity .	我是一個說故事的人 。 我想要傳達一個比我們共同的人性更真實的東西 。
all stories interest me , and some haunt me until i end up writing them .	所有故事都對我感興趣 , 有些令我不安 , 直到我最後寫下它們 。
certain themes keep coming up: justice , loyalty , violence , death , political and social issues , freedom .	某些主題不斷出現:正義、忠誠、暴力、死亡、政治、社會議題、自由 。
i'm aware of the mystery around us , so i write about coincidences , premonitions , emotions , dreams , the power of nature , magic .	我注意到周遭的神秘 , 所以我寫了有關巧合、正義、情緒、夢想、大自然的力量、魔法的力量 。
in the last 20 years i have published a few books , but i have lived in anonymity until february of 2006 , when i carried the olympic flag in the winter olympics in italy .	在過去20年 , 我發表了幾本書 , 但直到2006年二月 , 當我在義大利的冬季奧運會帶著奧運國旗 。
that made me a celebrity . now people recognize me in macy's , and my grandchildren think that i'm cool .	這讓我成為了名人 。 現在人們在macy的作品中認識我 , 而我的孫子認為我很酷 。
allow me to tell you about my four minutes of fame .	讓我來告訴你們我四分鐘的名聲 。
one of the organizers of the olympic ceremony , of the opening ceremony , called me and said that i had been selected to be one of the flagbearers .	奧林匹克典禮的一個組織者打電話給我 , 說我被選為旗幟之一 。
i replied that surely this was a case of mistaken identity because i'm as far as you can get from being an athlete .	我回答說 , 這絕對是錯誤的身分 , 因為我可以從運動員身上得到的 。
actually , i wasn't even sure that i could go around the stadium without a walker .	事實上 , 我甚至不確定自己可以到達體育場 , 不用走動器 。
i was told that this was no laughing matter .	我被告知這不是笑話 。
this would be the first time that only women would carry the olympic flag .	這是第一次 , 只有女性會帶著奧林匹克旗 。
five women , representing five continents , and three olympic gold medal winners .	五位女性 , 代表五大洲 , 三位奧運金牌贏家 。
my first question was , naturally , what was i going to wear ?	我的第一個問題是 , 很自然的 , 我要穿什麼衣服 ?
a uniform , she said , and asked for my measurements .	她說 , 一個制服 , 要求我的測量 。
i had a vision of myself in a fluffy anorak , looking like the michelin man .	我對自己有遠見的遠景 , 像是米開林人 。
by the middle of february , i found myself in turin , where enthusiastic crowds cheered when any of the 80 olympic teams was in the street .	到了二月的時候 , 我在土耳其找到自己 , 在那裡 , 熱切的群眾歡呼 , 當時任何80個奧運團隊都在街上 。
those athletes had sacrificed everything to compete in the games .	那些運動員犧牲了遊戲中的一切 。
they all deserved to win , but there's the element of luck .	他們都值得勝利 , 但幸運的元素 。
a speck of snow , an inch of ice , the force of the wind , can determine the result of a race or a game .	一片雪 , 一英吋的冰 , 風力 , 可以決定種族或遊戲的結果 。
however , what matters most more than training or luck is the heart .	然而 , 最重要的事 , 除了訓練或運氣 , 最重要的是心臟 。
only a fearless and determined heart will get the gold medal .	只有無懼且堅定的心會得到金牌 。
it is all about passion .	這全是關於熱情 。
the streets of turin were covered with red posters announcing the slogan of the olympics .	土耳其街道被紅色海報覆蓋 , 宣佈奧運的口號 。
passion lives here . isn't it always true ?	熱情存在這裡 , 不是嗎 ?
heart is what drives us and determines our fate .	心就是驅使我們決定我們的命運 。
that is what i need for my characters in my books: a passionate heart .	這就是我書中的角色所需要的:熱情的心 。
i need mavericks , dissidents , adventurers , outsiders and rebels , who ask questions , bend the rules and take risks .	我需要馬夫利克、異議人士、冒險家、外人和叛軍 , 他們會問問題、彎曲規則、冒險 。
people like all of you in this room .	像在座的各位一樣 。
nice people with common sense do not make interesting characters .	有常識的好人不會做出有趣的角色 。
they only make good former spouses .	他們只能做出好的前配偶 。
in the green room of the stadium , i met the other flag bearers: three athletes , and the actresses susan sarandon and sophia loren .	在體育場的綠色房間 , 我見到另一支旗熊:三名運動員 , 女演員蘇珊•薩蘭登和蘇菲雅•羅倫 。
also , two women with passionate hearts: wangari maathai , the nobel prizewinner from kenya who has planted 30 million trees . and by doing so , she has changed the soil , the weather , in some places in africa , and of course the economic conditions in many villages .	此外 , 有兩位充滿熱情的婦女:旺加里•馬塔伊 , 來自肯亞的諾貝爾獎得主 , 他種下了三千萬棵樹 。 藉此 , 她改變了土壤、氣候 , 在非洲某些地方 , 當然 , 在許多村莊裡 , 經濟狀況也改變了 。
and somaly mam , a cambodian activist who fights passionately against child prostitution .	柬埔寨的激進分子 , 會對抗兒童賣淫 。
when she was 14 years old , her grandfather sold her to a brothel .	當她十四歲時 , 她的祖父把她賣給兄弟 。
she told us of little girls raped by men who believe that having sex with a very young virgin will cure them from aids .	她告訴我們小女孩被男人強暴 , 他們相信和小小的處女做愛 , 會從愛滋病中治癒她們 。
and of brothels where children are forced to receive five , 15 clients per day , and if they rebel , they are tortured with electricity .	孩子們被迫接收5、15個客戶 , 如果他們反叛 , 他們就會被電給折磨 。
in the green room i received my uniform .	在綠色房間 , 我收到了制服 。
it was not the kind of outfit that i normally wear , but it was far from the michelin man suit that i had anticipated . not bad , really .	這不是我平常穿的那種衣服 , 但它離我所預期的米徹林化的服裝很遠 。 真的不錯 。
i looked like a refrigerator .	我看起來像是冰箱 。
but so did most of the flagbearers , except sophia loren , the universal symbol of beauty and passion .	除了蘇菲雅羅倫 , 大部份的旗幟都符合美和熱情的象徵 。
sophia is over 70 and she looks great .	蘇菲雅超過七十歲 , 她看起來很棒 。
she's sexy , slim and tall , with a deep tan .	她很迷人、很辛苦、很高 , 帶著很深的坦承 。
now , how can you have a deep tan and have no wrinkles ?	那麼 , 你要如何有深色的坦承 , 且沒有皺紋 ?
when asked in a tv interview , " how could she look so good ? "	電視訪問時 , 問道: 「 她要如何看起來這麼好 ? 」
she replied , " posture . my back is always straight , and i don't make old people's noises . "	她回答: 「 姿勢 , 我的背總是直的 , 我不會發出老人的聲音 。 」
so , there you have some free advice from one of the most beautiful women on earth .	這裡有一些免費的建議 , 來自地球上最美麗的女人之一 。
no grunting , no coughing , no wheezing , no talking to yourselves , no farting .	沒有發言 , 沒有咳嗽 , 沒有發臭 , 沒有跟自己說話 , 沒有遲到 。
well , she didn't say that exactly .	嗯 , 她並沒有完全這樣說 。
at some point around midnight , we were summoned to the wings of the stadium , and the loudspeakers announced the olympic flag , and the music started by the way , the same music that starts here , the aida march .	在午夜的時候 , 我們被召喚去體育場的翅膀 , 大聲說出奧運旗 , 順道一提 , 音樂的起始點是艾迪達大遊行 。
sophia loren was right in front of me she's a foot taller than i am , not counting the poofy hair .	蘇菲雅羅倫就在我面前 , 她比我高了一英尺 , 不算頭髮 。
she walked elegantly , like a giraffe on the african savannah , holding the flag on her shoulder . i jogged behind on my tiptoes holding the flag on my extended arm , so that my head was actually under the damn flag .	她很優雅地行走 , 像在非洲薩凡納的長頸鹿 , 肩膀握著旗子 。 我在我的尖端握著旗子 , 伸出我的手 , 這樣我的頭就在該死的旗子底下 。
all the cameras were , of course , on sophia .	當然 , 所有的攝影機在蘇菲雅 。
that was fortunate for me , because in most press photos i appear too , although often between sophia's legs .	這對我來說很幸運 , 因為在大部分的印刷照片中 , 雖然通常在蘇菲雅的腿之間 。
a place where most men would love to be .	一個大部分男人都喜歡的地方 。
the best four minutes of my entire life were those in the olympic stadium .	我一生中最棒的四分鐘是那些在奧運會場的人 。
my husband is offended when i say this although i have explained to him that what we do in private usually takes less than four minutes so he shouldn't take it personally .	我老公被冒犯了 , 我說這句話雖然我向他解釋 , 我們私下做的事通常會花不到四分鐘 , 所以他不應該把這件事個人化 。
i have all the press clippings of those four magnificent minutes , because i don't want to forget them when old age destroys my brain cells .	我有這四分鐘的記號 , 因為我不想忘記舊年紀摧毀我的腦細胞 。
i want to carry in my heart forever the key word of the olympics passion .	我想要永遠帶著奧運熱情的關鍵字眼 。
so here's a tale of passion .	這裡有個熱情的故事 。
the year is 1998 , the place is a prison camp for tutsi refugees in congo .	1998年 , 那個地方是剛果的監獄營 。
by the way , 80 percent of all refugees and displaced people in the world are women and girls .	順帶一提 , 世界上80%的難民和流離失所的是女性和女孩 。
we can call this place in congo a death camp , because those who are not killed will die of disease or starvation .	我們可以稱這個地方為剛果的死亡營 , 因為那些沒有被殺害的人 , 會死於疾病或飢餓 。
the protagonists of this story are a young woman , rose mapendo , and her children .	這個故事的主角是一位年輕女士 , 羅塞•馬多 , 她的孩子 。
she's pregnant and a widow .	她懷孕、寡婦 。
soldiers have forced her to watch as her husband was tortured and killed .	士兵迫使她看著她的丈夫被折磨並被殺害 。
somehow she manages to keep her seven children alive , and a few months later , she gives birth to premature twins .	不知怎麼的 , 她讓七個孩子活著 , 幾個月後 , 她生出了雙胞胎 。
two tiny little boys .	兩個小男孩 。
she cuts the umbilical cord with a stick , and ties it with her own hair .	她用一根棍子切下去 , 用自己的頭髮把它連結起來 。
she names the twins after the camp's commanders to gain their favor , and feeds them with black tea because her milk cannot sustain them .	她把營地指揮員工的雙胞胎命令命名 , 用黑茶餵食 , 因為她的牛奶無法維持它們 。
when the soldiers burst in her cell to rape her oldest daughter , she grabs hold of her and refuses to let go , even when they hold a gun to her head .	當士兵在她的牢房爆發強暴她最老的女兒時 , 她會抓住她並拒絕放手 , 即使他們拿著一把槍到她的頭上 。
somehow , the family survives for 16 months , and then , by extraordinary luck , and the passionate heart of a young american man , sasha chanoff , who manages to put her in a u . s . rescue plane , rose mapendo and her nine children end up in phoenix , arizona , where they're now living and thriving .	不知怎麼的 , 家人存活了16個月 , 然後 , 不凡的運氣 , 美國人的熱情 , 薩夏•查諾夫 , 他成功把她送進美國救援機 , 羅斯•圖多歐 , 她的九個孩子最後到亞利桑那州鳳凰城 , 他們現在居住和茁壯成長 。
mapendo , in swahili , means great love .	在斯瓦希里語 , 地圖是很棒的愛 。
the protagonists of my books are strong and passionate women like rose mapendo .	我書中的主角是強壯且有熱情的女性 , 如羅斯地圖 。
i don't make them up . there's no need for that .	我不放棄它們 , 不需要這樣做 。
i look around and i see them everywhere .	我環顧四周 , 到處都看到它們 。
i have worked with women and for women all my life .	我一生都和女性一起工作 。
i know them well .	我很熟悉他們 。
i was born in ancient times , at the end of the world , in a patriarchal catholic and conservative family .	我出生於古代 , 在世界末期 , 在父權天主教和保守的家庭中 。
no wonder that by age five i was a raging feminist although the term had not reached chile yet , so nobody knew what the heck was wrong with me .	難怪在我五歲的時候 , 我是個憤怒的女權主義者 , 雖然這個詞還沒有到智利 , 所以沒人知道我有什麼問題 。
i would soon find out that there was a high price to pay for my freedom , and for questioning the patriarchy .	我很快就會發現 , 為我的自由付出了很高的代價 , 並質疑父權 。
but i was happy to pay it , because for every blow that i received , i was able to deliver two .	但我很高興能支付這筆錢 , 因為每次我收到的炸彈 , 我都能送二次 。
once , when my daughter paula was in her twenties , she said to me that feminism was dated , that i should move on .	有一次 , 當我女兒保羅在她二十多歲時 , 她對我說 , 女權主義是約會的 , 我應該繼續前進 。
we had a memorable fight . feminism is dated ?	我們有一場難忘的戰鬥 , 女權主義是約會的 ?
yes , for privileged women like my daughter and all of us here today , but not for most of our sisters in the rest of the world who are still forced into premature marriage , prostitution , forced labor they have children that they don't want or they cannot feed .	沒錯 , 對於我女兒的特權女性來說 , 如今在座的各位 , 世界上大部分的姊妹們 , 她們仍然被迫要結婚、妓女 , 強迫她們有孩子不想要或無法餵飽 。
they have no control over their bodies or their lives .	他們無法控制自己的身體或生命 。
they have no education and no freedom .	他們沒有教育 , 也沒有自由 。
they are raped , beaten up and sometimes killed with impunity .	他們被強暴 , 被毆打 , 有時會被懲罰 。
for most western young women of today , being called a feminist is an insult .	現今大部分的西方年輕女性 , 被稱為女性主義者是侮辱 。
feminism has never been sexy , but let me assure you that it never stopped me from flirting , and i have seldom suffered from lack of men .	女性主義從來沒有過性感 , 但讓我保證 , 它從來沒有阻止我調情 , 且我很缺乏男性 。
feminism is not dead , by no means .	女性主義沒有死 , 絕對不會 。
it has evolved . if you don't like the term , change it , for goddess' sake .	它已經進化了 。 如果你不喜歡這個詞 , 改變它 , 為了女神的樣子 。
call it aphrodite , or venus , or bimbo , or whatever you want ; the name doesn't matter , as long as we understand what it is about , and we support it .	稱之為phrodite , 金星 , 或bimbo , 或任何你想要的東西 ; 這個名字並不重要 , 只要我們了解它是什麼 , 我們就支持它 。
so here's another tale of passion , and this is a sad one .	這裡還有另一個關於熱情的故事 , 這是個悲傷的故事 。
the place is a small women's clinic in a village in bangladesh .	這個地方是孟加拉村莊的小婦女診所 。
the year is 2005 .	2005年 。
jenny is a young american dental hygienist who has gone to the clinic as a volunteer during her threeweek vacation .	珍妮是一位年輕的美國牙醫衛生 , 她去了診所 , 在她的三週假期間當志願者 。
she's prepared to clean teeth , but when she gets there , she finds out that there are no doctors , no dentists , and the clinic is just a hut full of flies .	她準備好清潔牙齒 , 但當她走到那裡時 , 她發現沒有醫生 , 沒有牙醫 , 診所只滿是蒼蠅 。
outside , there is a line of women who have waited several hours to be treated .	在外面 , 有一系列的女性 , 等了好幾個小時才被治療 。
the first patient is in excruciating pain because she has several rotten molars .	第一位病人在極度痛苦 , 因為她有幾個腐爛的項目 。
jenny realizes that the only solution is to pull out the bad teeth .	珍妮知道 , 唯一的解決方案就是拉出壞牙齒 。
she's not licensed for that ; she has never done it .	她沒有執照 ; 她從來沒有做過 。
she risks a lot and she's terrified .	她的風險很大 , 她很害怕 。
she doesn't even have the proper instruments , but fortunately she has brought some novocaine .	她甚至沒有適當的樂器 , 但幸運的是 , 她帶來了一些諾維卡因 。
jenny has a brave and passionate heart .	珍妮有個勇敢且熱情的心 。
she murmurs a prayer and she goes ahead with the operation .	她謀殺了一名禱告 , 和手術一起前進 。
at the end , the relieved patient kisses her hands .	最終 , 釋放的病人親吻她的手 。
that day the hygienist pulls out many more teeth .	那天衛生學家抽出更多的牙齒 。
the next morning , when she comes again to the socalled clinic , her first patient is waiting for her with her husband .	第二天早上 , 當她再次回到所謂的診所時 , 她的第一個病人正等著她丈夫 。
the woman's face looks like a watermelon .	女人的臉看起來就像水月 。
it is so swollen that you can't even see the eyes .	腫到你看不到眼睛 。
the husband , furious , threatens to kill the american .	丈夫、憤怒、威脅要殺害美國人 。
jenny is horrified at what she has done , but then the translator explains that the patient's condition has nothing to do with the operation .	珍妮對她做過的事感到害怕 , 但翻譯者解釋了病人的狀況和手術沒有什麼關係 。
the day before , her husband beat her up because she was not home in time to prepare dinner for him .	前一天 , 她的丈夫打了她 , 因為她不在家 , 為他準備晚餐 。
millions of women live like this today .	現今有數百萬的女性像這樣生活 。
they are the poorest of the poor .	他們是窮人中最貧窮的人 。
although women do twothirds of the world's labor , they own less than one percent of the world's assets .	雖然世界上三分之二的女性勞工 , 她們擁有不到百分之一的全球資產 。
they are paid less than men for the same work if they're paid at all , and they remain vulnerable because they have no economic independence , and they are constantly threatened by exploitation , violence and abuse .	他們的薪水低於同一份工作的男性 , 如果他們付錢的話 , 他們的薪水完全低 , 因為他們沒有經濟獨立 , 他們經常受到剝削、暴力和虐待所威脅 。
it is a fact that giving women education , work , the ability to control their own income , inherit and own property , benefits the society .	事實是 , 給予女性教育、工作、控制自己收入、繼承和財產的能力 , 讓社會受益 。
if a woman is empowered , her children and her family will be better off .	如果一個女人被賦權 , 她的孩子和她的家人會更好 。
if families prosper , the village prospers , and eventually so does the whole country .	如果家人繁榮 , 村落的專家 , 最終整個國家也一樣 。
wangari maathai goes to a village in kenya .	wangarimaathai去肯亞的一個村莊
she talks with the women and explains that the land is barren because they have cut and sold the trees .	她和婦女談話 , 並解釋土地是荒謬的 , 因為他們砍掉了樹木 。
she gets the women to plant new trees and water them , drop by drop .	她讓婦女種植新的樹木 , 把它們澆水 , 掉下去 。
in a matter of five or six years , they have a forest , the soil is enriched , and the village is saved .	在五或六年之內 , 他們有森林 , 土壤被豐富 , 村落被拯救了 。
the poorest and most backward societies are always those that put women down .	最貧窮、最後退的社會總是那些把女性放下來的人 。
yet this obvious truth is ignored by governments and also by philanthropy .	然而 , 這種顯而易見的事實卻被政府和慈善機構忽略 。
for every dollar given to a women's program , 20 dollars are given to men's programs .	給女性專案的每一塊錢 , 有20塊錢給男性專案 。
women are 51 percent of humankind .	女性佔人類的51% 。
empowering them will change everything more than technology and design and entertainment .	給予他們力量 , 會改變一切 , 不只是科技、設計、娛樂 。
i can promise you that women working together linked , informed and educated can bring peace and prosperity to this forsaken planet .	我可以向你們保證 , 婦女們一起合作 , 連結、資訊、教育 , 能將和平和繁榮帶到這個被破壞的星球上 。
in any war today , most of the casualties are civilians , mainly women and children . they are collateral damage .	在今天的戰爭中 , 大部分的傷亡者都是平民百姓 , 主要是婦女和兒童 。 他們是冰封的傷害 。
men run the world , and look at the mess we have .	男人經營世界 , 看看我們所擁有的混亂 。
what kind of world do we want ?	我們想要什麼樣的世界 ?
this is a fundamental question that most of us are asking .	這是我們大多數人在問的一個基本問題 。
does it make sense to participate in the existing world order ?	參與現有的世界秩序是合理的嗎 ?
we want a world where life is preserved and the quality of life is enriched for everybody , not only for the privileged .	我們想要一個生活被保存、生活品質為每個人豐富的世界 , 不只是為了特權 。
in january i saw an exhibit of fernando botero's paintings at the uc berkeley library .	一月我看到佛南多•鮑特歐在加州大學柏克萊圖書館的畫作 。
no museum or gallery in the united states , except for the new york gallery that carries botero's work , has dared to show the paintings because the theme is the abu ghraib prison .	美國沒有博物館或畫廊 , 除了卡利波特奧的作品之外 , 還敢展現畫作 , 因為主題是阿布格拉伯監獄 。
they are huge paintings of torture and abuse of power , in the voluminous botero style .	它們是巨大的折磨和濫用權力的畫作 , 在大量的鮑特羅風格中 。
i have not been able to get those images out of my mind or my heart .	我無法把這些影像從我的心中或我的心中拿出來 。
what i fear most is power with impunity .	我最害怕的是不受懲罰的力量 。
i fear abuse of power , and the power to abuse .	我害怕濫用權力 , 以及濫用權力 。
in our species , the alpha males define reality , and force the rest of the pack to accept that reality and follow the rules .	在我們的物種中 , 雄性領袖定義現實 , 並強迫其他群體接受現實並遵守規則 。
the rules change all the time , but they always benefit them , and in this case , the trickledown effect , which does not work in economics , works perfectly .	規則隨時都改變 , 但他們總是受惠 , 在這個例子中 , 惡名昭彰的效應並不有效 。
abuse trickles down from the top of the ladder to the bottom .	虐待從梯子的頂部到底部 。
women and children , especially the poor , are at the bottom .	女人和孩子 , 特別是窮人 , 都在最底層 。
even the most destitute of men have someone they can abuse a woman or a child .	即便是最需要的人 , 也有可能會虐待女人或小孩的人 。
i'm fed up with the power that a few exert over the many through gender , income , race , and class .	我得到的力量是透過性別、收入、種族 , 和階級 。
i think that the time is ripe to make fundamental changes in our civilization .	我認為 , 該是我們文明的根本改變的時候了 。
but for real change , we need feminine energy in the management of the world .	但對於真正的改變 , 我們需要女性的能量來管理世界 。
we need a critical number of women in positions of power , and we need to nurture the feminine energy in men .	我們需要有權力的女性數量 , 我們需要培養男性的女性能源 。
i'm talking about men with young minds , of course .	我說的當然是年輕人 。
old guys are hopeless ; we have to wait for them to die off .	老年人是沒有希望的 , 我們必須等待他們死去 。
yes , i would love to have sophia loren's long legs and legendary breasts .	是的 , 我很樂意擁有索菲雅羅倫長的腿和傳奇的乳房 。
but given a choice , i would rather have the warrior hearts of wangari maathai , somaly mam , jenny and rose mapendo .	但 , 若有選擇 , 我寧願有勇氣的心臟 , 包括wangarimaathai , 瑪瑪瑪麗 , 珍妮 , 羅塞•地圖多 。
i want to make this world good .	我想讓這個世界變得更美好 。
not better , but to make it good .	不是更好 , 而是讓它變得更好 。
why not ? it is possible . look around in this room all this knowledge , energy , talent and technology .	為什麼不呢 ? 它是可能的 。 看看這個房間裡所有的知識 , 能源 , 天賦和科技 。
let's get off our fannies , roll up our sleeves and get to work , passionately , in creating an almost perfect world .	讓我們擺脫我們的空氣 , 捲起袖子 , 充滿熱情地工作 , 創造一個幾乎完美的世界 。
every day , in a city the size of london , 30 million meals are served . but where does all the food come from ? architect carolyn steel discusses the daily miracle of feeding a city , and shows how ancient food routes shaped the modern world .	每天 , 在倫敦大小的城市中 , 有三千萬餐是被服務的 。 但 , 所有的食物是從哪裡來的 ? 建築師卡羅爾討論了每天餵養城市的奇蹟 , 展示了古老的食物路線如何影響現代世界 。
cities , culture , food , global issues	城市、文化、食物、全球議題、全球議題、
carolyn steel: how food shapes our cities	卡羅琳•史提爾:食物如何影響我們的城市 。
how do you feed a city ?	你要如何餵飽一個城市 ?
it's one of the great questions of our time .	這是我們這個時代的一個大問題 。
yet it's one that's rarely asked .	但卻很少被問 。
we take it for granted that if we go into a shop or restaurant , or indeed into this theater's foyer in about an hour's time , there is going to be food there waiting for us , having magically come from somewhere .	我們視而為理所當然 , 如果我們去商店或餐廳 , 或在大約一小時內 , 就會有食物等待我們 , 神奇地從某處來 。
but when you think that every day for a city the size of london , enough food has to be produced , transported , bought and sold , cooked , eaten , disposed of , and that something similar has to happen every day for every city on earth , it's remarkable that cities get fed at all .	但當你認為 , 每一天在倫敦大小的城市裡 , 足夠的食物必須被生產、運輸、購買、煮飯、吃、丟棄 , 這樣的事每天都要發生在地球上的每個城市 , 都很了不起 。
we live in places like this as if they're the most natural things in the world , forgetting that because we're animals and that we need to eat , we're actually as dependent on the natural world as our ancient ancestors were .	我們生活在像這樣的地方 , 彷彿他們是世界上最自然的東西 , 因為我們是動物 , 我們需要吃 , 我們其實是依賴我們古老祖先的自然世界 。
and as more of us move into cities , more of that natural world is being transformed into extraordinary landscapes like the one behind me it's soybean fields in mato grosso in brazil in order to feed us .	越多人搬到城市裡 , 越多的自然世界被轉變為非凡的景觀 , 像在我身後的那個景觀 , 它是巴西的馬托格羅索的黃豆田 , 為了餵飽我們 。
these are extraordinary landscapes , but few of us ever get to see them .	這些都是非凡的風景 , 但我們當中有少數人能看到它們 。
and increasingly these landscapes are not just feeding us either .	越來越多的地景也不只是餵飽我們 。
as more of us move into cities , more of us are eating meat , so that a third of the annual grain crop globally now gets fed to animals rather than to us human animals .	當我們走進城市時 , 更多人在吃肉 , 所以現在全球每年有三分之一的穀物被餵食動物 , 而非我們人類 。
and given that it takes three times as much grain actually ten times as much grain to feed a human if it's passed through an animal first , that's not a very efficient way of feeding us .	由於需要三倍的穀物實際上是十倍的穀物來餵飽人類如果是先通過動物的話那就不太有效率地餵飽我們了
and it's an escalating problem too .	這也是一個危機的問題 。
by 2050 , it's estimated that twice the number of us are going to be living in cities .	到2050年 , 估計我們住在城市的兩倍 。
and it's also estimated that there is going to be twice as much meat and dairy consumed .	同時估計會有兩倍的肉類和乳酪消耗量 。
so meat and urbanism are rising hand in hand .	所以 , 肉類和都市主義正在舉手 。
and that's going to pose an enormous problem .	這將會帶來一個巨大的問題 。
six billion hungry carnivores to feed , by 2050 .	到2050年 , 六十億飢餓的屍體供應食物 。
that's a big problem . and actually if we carry on as we are , it's a problem we're very unlikely to be able to solve .	這是個大問題 。 實際上 , 如果我們繼續做下去 , 這個問題就不太可能解決 。
nineteen million hectares of rainforest are lost every year to create new arable land .	每年有9千萬公頃的雨林都消失了 , 創造出新的可耕地 。
although at the same time we're losing an equivalent amount of existing arables to salinization and erosion .	儘管同時我們失去了相當多的現有的耕地 , 來鹽化和侵蝕 。
we're very hungry for fossil fuels too .	我們也很渴望化石燃料 。
it takes about 10 calories to produce every calorie of food that we consume in the west .	西方每一卡路里大約需要十卡路里來生產我們所消耗的食物 。
and even though there is food that we are producing at great cost , we don't actually value it .	儘管我們所生產的食物成本很大 , 我們卻不珍視它 。
half the food produced in the usa is currently thrown away .	美國生產的一半食品已經被丟棄了 。
and to end all of this , at the end of this long process , we're not even managing to feed the planet properly .	最後 , 在這段漫長的過程結束時 , 我們甚至沒有適當的管理來餵飽地球 。
a billion of us are obese , while a further billion starve .	十億人肥胖 , 卻是十億人挨餓 。
none of it makes very much sense .	它沒有什麼合理的 。
and when you think that 80 percent of global trade in food now is controlled by just five multinational corporations , it's a grim picture .	當你認為 , 全球80%的貿易現在只能控制5個跨國企業 , 很嚴峻的照片 。
as we're moving into cities , the world is also embracing a western diet .	當我們進入城市時 , 世界也在擁抱西方飲食 。
and if we look to the future , it's an unsustainable diet .	如果我們看看未來 , 它是不永續的飲食 。
so how did we get here ?	我們是怎麼走到這一步的 ?
and more importantly , what are we going to do about it ?	更重要的是 , 我們要怎麼做 ?
well , to answer the slightly easier question first , about 10 , 000 years ago , i would say , is the beginning of this process in the ancient near east , known as the fertile crescent .	首先 , 先回答比較簡單的問題 , 大約一萬年前 , 我會說 , 這個過程在古老的東部 , 被稱為 「 肥沃的雪花 」 。
because , as you can see , it was crescent shaped .	因為 , 如你所見 , 它是近期的形狀 。
and it was also fertile .	這也是肥沃的 。
and it was here , about 10 , 000 years ago , that two extraordinary inventions , agriculture and urbanism , happened roughly in the same place and at the same time .	大約在一萬年前 , 這裡有兩項非凡的發明 , 農業和都市主義 , 大約在同一時間發生 。
this is no accident , because agriculture and cities are bound together . they need each other .	這不是意外 , 因為農業和城市團結在一起 , 他們需要彼此 。
because it was discovery of grain by our ancient ancestors for the first time that produced a food source that was large enough and stable enough to support permanent settlements .	因為我們古老的祖先第一次發現食物來源足夠大且穩定 , 足以支撐永久的定居地 。
and if we look at what those settlements were like , we see they were compact .	如果我們看看這些定居處的狀況 , 我們會看到它們是比較密集的 。
they were surrounded by productive farm land and dominated by large temple complexes like this one at ur , that were , in fact , effectively , spiritualized , central food distribution centers .	他們身邊圍繞著生產力的農場 , 由大型的神廟所主宰 , 例如烏爾的這一個 , 實際上是精神化、中央食物分配中心 。
because it was the temples that organized the harvest , gathered in the grain , offered it to the gods , and then offered the grain that the gods didn't eat back to the people .	因為是神殿組織收穫 , 聚集在穀物裡 , 將之送給神 , 然後提供了神不吃的穀物 。
so , if you like , the whole spiritual and physical life of these cities was dominated by the grain and the harvest that sustained them .	所以 , 如果你喜歡 , 這些城市的精神生活和實體生活 , 都是由穀物所支配的 , 以及維持它們的收穫所支配的 。
and in fact , that's true of every ancient city .	事實上 , 每座古城都是如此 。
but of course not all of them were that small .	但當然不是全部都這麼小 。
famously , rome had about a million citizens by the first century a . d .	著名的是 , 羅馬在第一世紀 , 有大約一百萬個公民 。
so how did a city like this feed itself ?	所以 , 像這樣的城市如何養活自己 ?
the answer is what i call " ancient food miles . "	答案是 , 我稱之為 「 古老的食物里程 」 。
basically , rome had access to the sea , which made it possible for it to import food from a very long way away .	基本上 , 羅馬可以接觸到海洋 , 讓它可以從很遠的地方進入進口食物 。
this is the only way it was possible to do this in the ancient world , because it was very difficult to transport food over roads , which were rough .	這是在古代世界 , 唯一可以做到的辦法 , 因為在路上運送食物是非常困難的 , 很粗糙 。
and the food obviously went off very quickly .	很顯然 , 食物很快就消失了 。
so rome effectively waged war on places like carthage and egypt just to get its paws on their grain reserves .	所以 , 羅馬有效地用戰爭來打仗 , 像是汽車和埃及 , 只為了取得他們的穀物保留地 。
and , in fact , you could say that the expansion of the empire was really sort of one long , drawn out militarized shopping spree , really .	事實上 , 你可以說 , 帝國擴張的確是相當長的 , 軍事化的購物圈 。
in fact i love the fact , i just have to mention this: rome in fact used to import oysters from london , at one stage . i think that's extraordinary .	事實上 , 我很愛這個事實:羅馬以前是從倫敦進口牡蠣的 , 在某個階段 , 我認為那是非凡的 。
so rome shaped its hinterland through its appetite .	所以羅馬用它的胃口塑造了它的印度地 。
but the interesting thing is that the other thing also happened in the preindustrial world .	但有趣的是 , 工業界也發生了另一件事 。
if we look at a map of london in the 17th century , we can see that its grain , which is coming in from the thames , along the bottom of this map .	如果我們看看十七世紀倫敦的地圖 , 我們可以看到它的穀物 , 它是從這張地圖的底部來的 。
so the grain markets were to the south of the city .	所以 , 穀物市場就在城市的南方 。
and the roads leading up from them to cheapside , which was the main market , were also grain markets .	引領他們走向廉價的道路 , 也就是主要的市場 , 也是穀物市場 。
and if you look at the name of one of those streets , bread street , you can tell what was going on there 300 years ago .	如果你看這些街道的名字 , 麵包街 , 你就能知道300年前發生了什麼事 。
and the same of course was true for fish .	當然 , 魚類也是如此 。
fish was , of course , coming in by river as well . same thing .	當然 , 魚也來到河裡 。 同樣的事 。
and of course billingsgate , famously , was london's fish market , operating onsite here until the mid1980s .	當然 , 比林肯很有名 , 是倫敦的魚市場 , 直到1980年代中期才開始運作 。
which is extraordinary , really , when you think about it .	這真是太不凡了 , 真的 , 想想看吧 。
everybody else was wandering around with mobile phones that looked like bricks and sort of smelly fish happening down on the port .	每個人都在用行動電話遊蕩 , 看起來像是磚頭 , 有點像是在港口的魚 。
this is another thing about food in cities: once its roots into the city are established , they very rarely move .	城市裡有另一件事是關於食物:一旦它的根部進入城市 , 它們就很少移動 。
meat is a very different story because , of course , animals could walk into the city .	肉是一種非常不同的故事 , 因為 , 當然 , 動物會走進城市 。
so much of london's meat was coming from the northwest , from scotland and wales .	倫敦大部分的肉都來自西北部 , 來自蘇格蘭和威爾斯 。
so it was coming in , and arriving at the city at the northwest , which is why smithfield , london's very famous meat market , was located up there .	所以它來了 , 抵達西北部的城市 , 這就是為什麼史密斯菲爾德 , 倫敦非常有名的肉市場 , 那裡就在那裡 。
poultry was coming in from east anglia and so on , to the northeast .	文化從東加利亞來到東北部 。
i feel a bit like a weather woman doing this . anyway , and so the birds were coming in with their feet protected with little canvas shoes .	我覺得有點像氣象女人這樣做 。 總之 , 鳥兒們會帶著腳來保護小畫布 。
and then when they hit the eastern end of cheapside , that's where they were sold , which is why it's called poultry .	接著 , 當它們抵達了廉價的東邊 , 也就是它們被賣掉的地方 , 這就是為什麼稱之為 「 文化 」 。
and , in fact , if you look at the map of any city built before the industrial age , you can trace food coming in to it .	事實上 , 如果你看看工業時代之前的任何一座城市地圖 , 你可以追蹤食物來到那裡 。
you can actually see how it was physically shaped by food , both by reading the names of the streets , which give you a lot of clues .	你可以看到它是如何被食物的形狀 , 不論是閱讀街道的名字 , 都會給你很多線索 。
friday street , in a previous life , is where you went to buy your fish on a friday .	星期五街 , 在以前的生活中 , 是你在星期五去買魚的地方 。
but also you have to imagine it full of food .	但同時 , 你也得要想像它充滿了食物 。
because the streets and the public spaces were the only places where food was bought and sold .	因為街道和公共空間是購買食物的地方 。
and if we look at an image of smithfield in 1830 you can see that it would have been very difficult to live in a city like this and be unaware of where your food came from .	如果我們看看1830年史密菲爾德的影像 , 你可以看到住在像這樣的城市 , 很難知道你的食物從何而來 。
in fact , if you were having sunday lunch , the chances were it was mooing or bleating outside your window about three days earlier .	事實上 , 如果你在星期日午餐的時候 , 可能是在三天前的窗戶外吹氣或吹氣 。
so this was obviously an organic city , part of an organic cycle .	這顯然是一個有機城市 , 一個有機循環的一部分 。
and then 10 years later everything changed .	十年後 , 一切都改變了 。
this is an image of the great western in 1840 .	這是1840年偉大西方國家的照片 。
and as you can see , some of the earliest train passengers were pigs and sheep .	如你所見 , 最早的乘客是豬和羊 。
so all of a sudden , these animals are no longer walking into market .	突然間 , 這些動物不再走進市場 。
they're being slaughtered out of sight and mind , somewhere in the countryside .	他們被趕出了視覺和心智 , 在鄉下某處 。
and they're coming into the city by rail .	他們會從鐵軌進入城市 。
and this changes everything .	這改變了一切 。
to start off with , it makes it possible for the first time to grow cities , really any size and shape , in any place .	首先 , 首先 , 它讓它可以第一次培養城市 , 任何大小和形狀 , 在任何地方 。
cities used to be constrained by geography ; they used to have to get their food through very difficult physical means .	城市以前被地理限制 ; 他們以前必須透過非常困難的實體來取得食物 。
all of a sudden they are effectively emancipated from geography .	突然間 , 它們從地理頻道中被有效地解放 。
and as you can see from these maps of london , in the 90 years after the trains came , it goes from being a little blob that was quite easy to feed by animals coming in on foot , and so on , to a large splurge , that would be very , very difficult to feed with anybody on foot , either animals or people .	如你所見 , 從倫敦的地圖 , 在火車出現的90年後 , 它從一塊很容易餵飽的小球 , 以此類推 , 到大型球體 , 很難餵飽任何人的腳 , 不論是動物或人 。
and of course that was just the beginning . after the trains came cars , and really this marks the end of this process .	當然 , 這只是開端 。 火車來了車之後 , 真的是這個過程的終點 。
it's the final emancipation of the city from any apparent relationship with nature at all .	它是城市最後的解放 , 完全是與大自然的關係 。
and this is the kind of city that's devoid of smell , devoid of mess , certainly devoid of people , because nobody would have dreamed of walking in such a landscape .	這是一種沒有聞到的城市 , 沒有混亂的城市 , 肯定沒有人會夢想走在這樣的地景上 。
in fact , what they did to get food was they got in their cars , drove to a box somewhere on the outskirts , came back with a week's worth of shopping , and wondered what on earth to do with it .	事實上 , 他們做的是 , 他們在他們的車子裡 , 開車到郊區的一個盒子裡 , 回來了一週的購物 , 想知道地球上有什麼用途 。
and this really is the moment when our relationship , both with food and cities , changes completely .	此時此刻 , 我們與食物和城市之間的關係 , 完全改變了 。
here we have food that used to be the center , the social core of the city at the periphery .	這裡我們有食物 , 以前是城市的中心 , 在周邊的城市的社會核心 。
it used to be a social event , buying and selling food .	它以前是社交活動 , 買賣和賣食物 。
we used to cook ; now we just add water , or a little bit of an egg if you're making a cake or something .	我們以前會煮飯 , 只要添加水 , 或添加一些蛋 , 只要你做蛋糕或其他東西 。
we don't smell food to see if it's okay to eat .	我們不會聞到食物 , 看看是否可以吃 。
we just read the back of a label on a packet .	我們只是讀包裝後面的標籤 。
and we don't value food . we don't trust it .	我們不重視食物 , 我們不相信它 。
so instead of trusting it , we fear it .	所以 , 我們不信任它 , 而是害怕它 。
and instead of valuing it , we throw it away .	而不是評價它 , 而是丟掉它 。
one of the great ironies of modern food systems is that they've made the very thing they promised to make easier much harder .	現代食品系統的諷刺之一是 , 他們讓自己承諾要更加困難 。
by making it possible to build cities anywhere and any place , they've actually distanced us from our most important relationship , which is that of us and nature .	若要在任何地方或任何地方建造城市 , 就能讓我們遠離我們最重要的關係 , 那就是我們和大自然 。
and also they've made us dependent on systems that only they can deliver , that , as we've seen , are unsustainable .	此外 , 他們也讓我們依賴系統 , 只依靠它們能傳遞的系統 , 如同我們所見 , 都是無法永續發展的 。
so what are we going to do about that ?	所以 , 我們要怎麼做 ?
it's not a new question .	這不是一個新的問題 。
500 years ago it's what thomas more was asking himself .	500年前 , 湯瑪士自己問了什麼 。
this is the frontispiece of his book " utopia . "	這是他的書《烏托邦》的前線 。
and it was a series of semiindependent citystates , if that sounds remotely familiar , a day's walk from one another where everyone was basically farmingmad , and grew vegetables in their back gardens , and ate communal meals together , and so on .	那是一系列的半獨立城市 , 如果這聽起來很熟悉 , 大家基本上都是農業 , 在後院種植蔬菜 , 一起吃共產餐 , 等等 。
and i think you could argue that food is a fundamental ordering principle of utopia , even though more never framed it that way .	我認為 , 食物是烏托邦的基本定律 , 雖然它從來沒有把它看成那樣 。
and here is another very famous " utopian " vision , that of ebenezer howard , " the garden city . "	這裡還有另一個非常著名的 「 烏托邦 」 願景 , 埃布尼茲霍華 , 《花園城》 。
same idea: series of semiindependent citystates , little blobs of metropolitan stuff with arable land around , joined to one another by railway .	同樣的想法:一系列的半獨立城市 , 一小塊大都市 , 附近的土地圍繞著鐵路 , 彼此連結 。
and again , food could be said to be the ordering principle of his vision .	同樣的 , 食物可以被說是他視覺的秩序原則 。
it even got built , but nothing to do with this vision that howard had .	它甚至被建造了 , 但和霍華的這個願景沒有關係 。
and that is the problem with these utopian ideas , that they are utopian .	這就是烏托邦的想法的問題 , 他們是烏托邦 。
utopia was actually a word that thomas moore used deliberately .	烏托邦是湯瑪斯•摩爾刻意使用的一個詞 。
it was a kind of joke , because it's got a double derivation from the greek .	這是個笑話 , 因為希臘有雙重衍生 。
it can either mean a good place , or no place .	它可能意味著一個好的地方 , 或沒有地方 。
because it's an ideal . it's an imaginary thing . we can't have it .	因為它是理想的 。 它是幻想的 。 我們不能擁有它 。
and i think , as a conceptual tool for thinking about the very deep problem of human dwelling , that makes it not much use .	我認為 , 作為一個概念性的工具 , 來思考人類在鑽研的深層問題 , 讓它不太使用 。
so i've come up with an alternative , which is sitopia , from the ancient greek , " sitos " for food , and " topos " for place .	所以我想出了一個替代方案 , 西托邦 , 來自古希臘文 , " 西托 " 為食物 , 和 " 湯波 " 定位 。
i believe we already live in sitopia .	我相信我們已經住在西托邦 。
we live in a world shaped by food , and if we realize that , we can use food as a really powerful tool a conceptual tool , design tool , to shape the world differently .	我們生活在一個由食物塑造的世界 , 如果我們了解到 , 我們可以把食物當作強大的工具 , 一個概念性的工具 , 設計工具 , 來改變世界 。
so if we were to do that , what might sitopia look like ?	所以如果我們這樣做 , 西托邦看起來會是什麼樣子 ?
well i think it looks a bit like this .	我覺得這看起來有點像這樣 。
i have to use this slide . it's just the look on the face of the dog .	我必須用這張投影片 , 只是狗的臉 。
but anyway , this is it's food at the center of life , at the center of family life , being celebrated , being enjoyed , people taking time for it .	無論如何 , 這是食物在生活的中心 , 在家庭生活的中心 , 被讚頌 , 被享受 , 人們花時間去做這件事 。
this is where food should be in our society .	食物應該在我們的社會裡 。
but you can't have scenes like this unless you have people like this .	除非你有這樣的人 , 否則你就不會有這樣的場景 。
by the way , these can be men as well .	順便一提 , 這些也可以是男人 。
it's people who think about food , who think ahead , who plan , who can stare at a pile of raw vegetables and actually recognize them .	人們會想到食物 , 誰會想 , 誰會想 , 誰可以盯著一堆蔬菜 , 並且真的會認得出來 。
we need these people . we're part of a network .	我們需要這些人 , 我們是網絡的一部分 。
because without these kinds of people we can't have places like this .	因為如果沒有這些人 , 我們就不能有這樣的地方 。
here , i deliberately chose this because it is a man buying a vegetable .	在這裡 , 我刻意選擇這個 , 因為這是一個人在買蔬菜 。
but networks , markets where food is being grown locally .	但網路、市場在當地成長 。
it's common . it's fresh .	它很常見 , 很新鮮 。
it's part of the social life of the city .	它是城市社會生活的一部分 。
because without that , you can't have this kind of place , food that is grown locally and also is part of the landscape , and is not just a zerosum commodity off in some unseen hellhole .	因為若沒有這些 , 你就不會有這種地方 , 當地種植的食物 , 同時也是地景的一部分 , 而不只是一個零和的商品 , 在一些未知的洞內 。
cows with a view .	用肉眼來看牛 。
steaming piles of humus .	蒸汽堆的 「 嗡 」 。
this is basically bringing the whole thing together .	這基本上是把整件事結合在一起 。
and this is a community project i visited recently in toronto .	這是我最近在多倫多拜訪過的一個社區計畫 。
it's a greenhouse , where kids get told all about food and growing their own food .	這是一間溫室 , 孩子們會被告知 , 關於食物和種植自己的食物 。
here is a plant called kevin , or maybe it's a plant belonging to a kid called kevin . i don't know .	這裡有一株叫凱文的植物 , 或者它屬於一個叫凱文的孩子 。 我不知道 。
but anyway , these kinds of projects that are trying to reconnect us with nature is extremely important .	總之 , 這些企圖將我們和大自然重新連結起來是非常重要的 。
so sitopia , for me , is really a way of seeing .	所以 , 對我來說 , 西托邦是種看法 。
it's basically recognizing that sitopia already exists in little pockets everywhere .	基本上 , 認為西托邦已經存在於各地的小口袋裡 。
the trick is to join them up , to use food as a way of seeing .	訣竅在於加入它們 , 用食物當作一種看待方式 。
and if we do that , we're going to stop seeing cities as big , metropolitan , unproductive blobs , like this .	如果我們這麼做 , 我們就不會把城市視為是大型、大都市、沒有生產力的斑點 , 像這樣 。
we're going to see them more like this , as part of the productive , organic framework of which they are inevitably a part , symbiotically connected .	我們將看到它們更像這樣 , 作為生產力、有機架構的一部分 , 它們是無可避免連接的部分 。
but of course , that's not a great image either , because we need not to be producing food like this anymore .	當然 , 這也不是很棒的影像 , 因為我們不再需要像這樣生產食物 。
we need to be thinking more about permaculture , which is why i think this image just sums up for me the kind of thinking we need to be doing .	我們需要考慮更多的永續培養 , 這就是為什麼我認為這張照片總結了我認為我們需要做的事 。
it's a reconceptualization of the way food shapes our lives .	它是一種重新概念化的食物如何影響我們的生活 。
the best image i know of this is from 650 years ago .	我所知道的最好的圖像是來自650年前 。
it's ambrogio lorenzetti's " allegory of good government . "	阿布羅吉歐•洛倫澤蒂的《好政府的寓言》 。
it's about the relationship between the city and the countryside .	重點是城市和鄉村之間的關係 。
and i think the message of this is very clear .	我認為這個訊息非常清楚 。
if the city looks after the country , the country will look after the city .	如果城市照顧這個國家 , 國家會照顧城市 。
and i want us to ask now , what would ambrogio lorenzetti paint if he painted this image today ?	我現在要我們問 , 如果他今天畫出這張圖 , 阿布羅吉歐•羅倫澤蒂畫了些什麼 ?
what would an allegory of good government look like today ?	今天的好政府會長什麼樣子 ?
because i think it's an urgent question .	因為我認為這是一個迫切的問題 。
it's one we have to ask , and we have to start answering .	這是我們必須問的問題 , 我們必須開始回答 。
we know we are what we eat .	我們知道我們吃的東西 。
we need to realize that the world is also what we eat .	我們需要了解到 , 世界也是我們吃的東西 。
but if we take that idea , we can use food as a really powerful tool to shape the world better .	但如果我們採用這個想法 , 我們就能把食物當作強大的工具來塑造世界變得更好 。
weeks from the charter for compassion launch , karen armstrong looks at religion's role in the 21st century: will its dogmas divide us ? or will it unite us for common good ? she reviews the catalysts that can drive the world's faiths to rediscover the golden rule .	二十一世紀以來 , 慈悲心發起的幾個禮拜 , 卡倫•阿姆斯壯看著宗教在二十一世紀扮演的角色:它會把我們分裂嗎 ? 或者它會讓我們共通嗎 ? 她會重新審視世界上的信仰 , 來重新發現黃金規則 。
god , ted prize , global issues , politics , religion , tedglobal2009 , violence	上帝、ted大獎、全球議題、政治、宗教、tedglobal2009、暴力、暴力 。
karen armstrong: let's revive the golden rule	karenarmstrong:咱們回顧黃金法則:咱們回顧黃金法則 。
for years i've been feeling frustrated , because as a religious historian , i've become acutely aware of the centrality of compassion in all the major world faiths .	多年來 , 我都感到沮喪 , 因為身為宗教歷史學家 , 我很敏銳地意識到同情心的核心 , 在全世界的所有信仰中 。
every single one of them has evolved their own version of what's been called the golden rule .	每一個人都演化出了他們自己的版本 , 稱為黃金法則 。
sometimes it comes in a positive version " always treat all others as you'd like to be treated yourself . "	有時 , 會出現一個正面的版本 , 「 永遠對待別人 , 只要你想要被治療 。 」
and equally important is the negative version " don't do to others what you would not like them to do to you . "	同樣重要的是 , 負面版本的 「 不要對別人做你不喜歡的事 。 」
look into your own heart , discover what it is that gives you pain and then refuse , under any circumstance whatsoever , to inflict that pain on anybody else .	看看你自己的心 , 發現讓你痛苦的是什麼 , 然後在任何情況下拒絕 , 把疼痛給任何人 。
and people have emphasized the importance of compassion , not just because it sounds good , but because it works .	人們強調同情心的重要性 , 不只是因為它聽起來很好 , 也因為它有用 。
people have found that when they have implemented the golden rule as confucius said , " all day and every day , " not just a question of doing your good deed for the day and then returning to a life of greed and egotism , but to do it all day and every day , you dethrone yourself from the center of your world , put another there , and you transcend yourself .	人們發現 , 當他們實施了金牌規則 , 如同混亂的說法: 「 一整天和每一天 , 」 不只是你做好的事 , 還會回到貪婪和自尊的人生裡 , 一整天 , 一整天 , 一整天 , 你就從世界的中心 , 丟下自己 , 然後你超越自己 。
and it brings you into the presence of what's been called god , nirvana , rama , tao .	它帶你進入了被稱為神的神、nirvana、rama、tao的存在 。
something that goes beyond what we know in our egobound existence .	在我們自負的存在之外 , 有些東西超越了我們所知道的 。
but you know you'd never know it a lot of the time , that this was so central to the religious life .	但你知道你從來不知道 , 這對宗教生活來說是很重要的 。
because with a few wonderful exceptions , very often when religious people come together , religious leaders come together , they're arguing about abstruse doctrines or uttering a council of hatred or inveighing against homosexuality or something of that sort .	因為有一些很棒的例外 , 通常當宗教人聚集在一起時 , 宗教領袖聚集在一起時 , 他們會爭論荒謬的教義 , 或是說出仇恨或意見對抗同性戀或類似的仇恨 。
often people don't really want to be compassionate .	通常人們不太想要有同情心 。
i sometimes see when i'm speaking to a congregation of religious people a sort of mutinous expression crossing their faces because people often want to be right instead .	我有時會看到 , 當我和宗教群體交談時 , 會有一種互相交流的表情 , 會跨越他們的臉孔 , 因為人們常常想做對的事 。
and that of course defeats the object of the exercise .	這當然打敗了運動的物體 。
now why was i so grateful to ted ?	為什麼我這麼感激ted ?
because they took me very gently from my booklined study and brought me into the 21st century , enabling me to speak to a much , much wider audience than i could have ever conceived .	因為他們很溫柔地從我的書籍研究帶我進入21世紀 , 讓我可以說出比我想像中還要更廣的觀眾 。
because i feel an urgency about this .	因為我對此感到很緊迫 。
if we don't manage to implement the golden rule globally , so that we treat all peoples , wherever and whoever they may be , as though they were as important as ourselves , i doubt that we'll have a viable world to hand on to the next generation .	如果我們沒有辦法實現全球的黃金法則 , 所以我們對待所有人 , 無論他們在哪裡 , 無論他們是誰 , 都跟我們一樣重要 , 我懷疑我們會有一個可行的世界 , 來交給下一代 。
the task of our time , one of the great tasks of our time , is to build a global society , as i said , where people can live together in peace .	我們這個時代的任務 , 我們這個時代最大的任務之一 , 就是建立一個全球社會 , 就像我所說的 , 在那裡 , 人們可以一起生活在和平中 。
and the religions that should be making a major contribution are instead seen as part of the problem .	該做出重大貢獻的宗教 , 被視為是問題的一部分 。
and of course it's not just religious people who believe in the golden rule .	當然 , 不只是宗教人士相信黃金法則 。
this is the source of all morality , this imaginative act of empathy , putting yourself in the place of another .	這是所有道德的來源 , 這種想像力的同理心 , 把自己放在另一個地方 。
and so we have a choice , it seems to me .	所以我們有選擇 , 似乎我有選擇 。
we can either go on bringing out or emphasizing the dogmatic and intolerant aspects of our faith , or we can go back to the rabbis . rabbi hillel , the older contemporary of jesus , who , when asked by a pagan to sum up the whole of jewish teaching while he stood on one leg , said , " that which is hateful to you , do not do to your neighbor .	我們可以說出話 , 或者強調我們的信仰的教義 , 或我們回到拉比希爾 , 老舊的耶穌會議 , 當他站在一條腿上時 , 要求他總結猶太教學 , 他說: 「 這對你不感興趣 , 不要對你的鄰居做事 。
that is the torah and everything else is only commentary . "	這就是托拉和其他一切都只是評論而已 。 」
and the rabbis and the early fathers of the church who said that any interpretation of scripture that bred hatred and disdain was illegitimate .	教會的早期教會和長老說任何仇恨和歧視都是非正當的 。
and we need to revive that spirit .	我們需要復興這精神 。
and it's not just going to happen because a spirit of love wafts us down .	這不會發生 , 因為愛的精神讓我們失望 。
we have to make this happen , and we can do it with the modern communications that ted has introduced .	我們必須實現這一點 , 並且我們可以利用ted介紹的現代通訊來實現 。
already i've been tremendously heartened at the response of all our partners .	我已經對所有伴侶的回應感到極大的鼓舞 。
in singapore , we have a group going to use the charter to heal divisions recently that have sprung up in singaporean society , and some members of the parliament want to implement it politically .	在新加坡 , 我們有一群人會用charter來治癒最近發生在新加坡的社會 , 有些議會的成員想要在政治上實施 。
in malaysia , there is going to be an art exhibition in which leading artists are going to be taking people , young people , and showing them that compassion also lies at the root of all art .	在馬來西亞 , 將會有一個藝術展覽 , 讓藝術家能帶領人們、年輕人 , 並讓他們知道 , 同情心也是所有藝術的根源 。
throughout europe , the muslim communities are holding events and discussions , are discussing the centrality of compassion in islam and in all faiths .	在整個歐洲 , 穆斯林社區正在舉辦活動和討論 , 正在討論伊斯蘭和所有信仰中的同情心的核心 。
but it can't stop there . it can't stop with the launch .	但它不能停在那 , 它不能停止發射 。
religious teaching , this is where we've gone so wrong , concentrating solely on believing abstruse doctrines .	宗教教學讓我們錯了 , 只專注於相信抽象的教義 。
religious teaching must always lead to action .	宗教教學一定會引起行動 。
and i intend to work on this till my dying day .	我打算在我死去的那一天工作 。
and i want to continue with our partners to do two things educate and stimulate compassionate thinking .	我希望我們的合作夥伴能做兩件事 , 教育和刺激同情心 。
education because we've so dropped out of compassion .	教育因為我們已經失去同情心 。
people often think it simply means feeling sorry for somebody .	人們常認為這意味著對某個人感到抱歉 。
but of course you don't understand compassion if you're just going to think about it .	當然 , 如果你想一想 , 你並不了解同情心 。
you also have to do it .	你也必須這麼做 。
i want them to get the media involved because the media are crucial in helping to dissolve some of the stereotypical views we have of other people , which are dividing us from one another .	我希望媒體參與其中 , 是因為媒體在協助解除一些我們對他人的刻板印象 , 將我們從彼此之間分開來 。
the same applies to educators .	教育工作者也一樣 。
i'd like youth to get a sense of the dynamism , the dynamic and challenge of a compassionate lifestyle .	我希望年輕人能感受到動態、動態 , 以及同情生活方式的挑戰 。
and also see that it demands acute intelligence , not just a gooey feeling .	同時也看到它需要急性智能 , 而非只有一種舒服的感覺 。
i'd like to call upon scholars to explore the compassionate theme in their own and in other people's traditions .	我想要打電話給學者 , 來探索他們自己的同情心主題 , 在其他人的傳統中 。
and perhaps above all , to encourage a sensitivity about uncompassionate speaking , so that because people have this charter , whatever their beliefs or lack of them , they feel empowered to challenge uncompassionate speech , disdainful remarks from their religious leaders , their political leaders , from the captains of industry .	最重要的是 , 鼓勵對於不親切的演講的敏感度 , 如此一來 , 是因為人們有這份文章 , 不論他們的信仰或缺乏信仰 , 他們都覺得賦權於挑戰不友善的言論 , 從他們的宗教領袖 , 他們的政治領袖 , 或工業領袖 。
because we can change the world , we have the ability .	因為我們可以改變世界 , 我們有能力 。
i would never have thought of putting the charter online .	我從來沒有想過把這張圖放上網 。
i was still stuck in the old world of a whole bunch of boffins sitting together in a room and issuing yet another arcane statement .	我仍然困在古老的世界裡 , 坐在房間裡的一堆棺材裡 , 再接著又一次的阿卡尼聲明 。
and ted introduced me to a whole new way of thinking and presenting ideas .	ted介紹了我一個全新的思考方式 , 和呈現想法 。
because that is what is so wonderful about ted .	因為這就是ted的美好之處 。
in this room , all this expertise , if we joined it all together , we could change the world .	在這個房間裡 , 所有的專業知識 , 如果我們一起合作 , 我們就能改變世界 。
and of course the problems sometimes seem insuperable .	當然 , 問題有時會更加惡化 。
but i'd just like to quote , finish at the end with a reference to a british author , an oxford author whom i don't quote very often , c . s . lewis .	但我想要引用一句話 , 結束後 , 說到英國作者 , 一位牛津作家 , 我不常引用c.s.lewis 。
but he wrote one thing that stuck in my mind ever since i read it when i was a schoolgirl .	但他寫了一件事 , 自從我讀書的時候 , 我就深深印印象深刻 。
it's in his book " the four loves . "	他的書《四個愛情》 。
he said that he distinguished between erotic love , when two people gaze , spellbound , into each other's eyes .	他說 , 他分辨出愛情 , 當兩個人凝視、拼字 , 分成對方的眼睛 。
and then he compared that to friendship , when two people stand side by side , as it were , shoulder to shoulder , with their eyes fixed on a common goal .	接著 , 他把這個和友誼做比較 , 當兩個人站在旁邊 , 就如同 , 肩膀 , 肩膀 , 眼睛固定在共同的目標上 。
we don't have to fall in love with each other , but we can become friends .	我們不需要愛上彼此 , 但我們能成為朋友 。
and i am convinced .	我深信不疑
i felt it very strongly during our little deliberations at vevey , that when people of all different persuasions come together , working side by side for a common goal , differences melt away .	我感到非常強烈 , 在我們在維維基的小小意志中 , 當所有不同的人聚集在一起時 , 一起努力努力 , 為了一個共同的目標努力 , 差異消失了 。
and we learn amity .	我們學到了野心 。
and we learn to live together and to get to know one another .	我們學會一起生活 , 去認識彼此 。
thank you very much .	非常謝謝各位 。
david macaulay relives the winding and sometimes surreal journey toward the completion of rome antics , his illustrated homage to the historic city .	大衛馬卡爾依依依靠風力 , 有時也不切實際的旅程 , 朝著羅馬帝國的綜合之旅 , 他對歷史城市的讚嘆 。

the text here is right side and upside down so that you are forced to turn the book around , and you can see it from ground point of view and from her point of view looking in the hole , getting a different kind of perspective , moving you around the space . particularly appropriate in a building that can contain perfectly a sphere dimensions of the diameter being the same as the distance from the center of the floor to the center of the oculus .	這裡的文字是對的 , 向下 , 所以你被迫要把書轉過來 , 從地面的角度看 , 從她的觀點看 , 從洞的角度看 , 到空間的角度 , 移動你 。 特別適當的是在一個建築中 , 裡面包含一個球體的寬度 , 和在直徑的距離 , 和地板的距離一樣 。
unfortunately for her , the anchor line gets tangled around the feet of some boy scouts who are visiting the pantheon , and they are immediately yanked out and given an extraordinary but terrifying tour of some of the domes of rome , which would , from their point of view , naturally be hanging upside down .	不幸的是 , 有些男孩偵查員到來參觀萬神廟 , 他們立刻被排擠 , 給出了不凡但可怕的旅程 , 從羅馬的角度來看 , 天然會被吊死 。
they bail out as soon as they get to the top of saint ivo , that little spiral structure you see there .	牠們一旦抵達聖艾佛的上方 , 就會保釋出來的螺旋結構 。
she continues on her way over piazza navona .	她繼續走下去 , 穿越潘薩拉納維娜的路 。
notices a lot of activity at the tre scalini restaurant , is reminded that it is lunchtime and she's hungry .	注意到很多在treskalini餐廳的活動 , 有人提醒說是午餐時間 , 她餓了 。
they keep on motoring towards the campo de' fiori , which they soon reach . ajax the dog is put in a basket and lowered with a list of food into the marketplace , which flourishes there until about one in the afternoon , and then is completely removed and doesn't appear again until six or seven the following morning .	他們持續向campodefiori進行動作 , 很快就有了 。 狗被放在籃子裡 , 上面放了一份食物到市場上 , 直到下午 , 牠完全被移除 , 直到六到七個早上才出現 。
anyway , the pooch gets back to the dirigible with the stuff .	總之 , 糞便會把這些東西挖回去 。
unfortunately , when she goes to unwrap the prosciutto , ajax makes a lunge for it .	不幸的是 , 當她去解開口號時 , ajax會為它做午餐 。
she's managed to save the prosciutto , but in the process she loses the tablecloth , which you can see flying away in the upper lefthand corner .	她成功地拯救了學科 , 但在她失去了桌布 , 你可以看到在左上角飛走 。
they continue without their tablecloth , looking for a place to land this thing so that they can actually have lunch .	他們沒有桌布 , 找一個地方降落這東西 , 這樣他們才能真的有午餐 。
they eventually discover a huge wall that's filled with small holes , ideal for docking a dirigible because you've got a place to tie up .	他們最終發現了一道巨大的牆 , 裡面充滿了小洞 , 理想的把一個負責的牆 , 因為你有地方可以綁起來 。
turns out to be the exterior wall that part of it that remains of the coliseum , so they park themselves there and have a terrific lunch and have a spectacular view .	原來是柱子剩下的外牆 , 所以他們自己停在那裡 , 吃了很棒的午餐 , 看了很壯觀的看法 。
at the end of lunch , they untie the anchor , they set off through the baths of caracalla and over the walls of the city and then an abandoned gatehouse and decide to take one more look at the pyramid of cestius , which has this lightning rod on top .	在午餐結束時 , 他們解開了主鎖 , 他們打開了卡卡拉的浴室 , 穿過城市的牆 , 接著是一間廢棄的房屋 , 決定再看一眼凱斯蒂斯的金字塔 , 上面有著閃電的捲 。
unfortunately , that's a problem: they get a little too close , and when you're in a dirigible you have to be very careful about spikes .	不幸的是 , 這是個問題:它們太靠近了 , 當你處在一個你必須非常小心尖峰的旅程中 。
so that sort of brings her little story to a conclusion .	所以 , 這就把她的小故事帶到一個結論上 。
marcello , on the other hand , is sort of a lazy guy , but he's not due at work until about noon .	另一方面 , marcello有點懶惰 , 但直到他開始工作 。
so , the alarm goes off and it's five to 12 or so .	所以 , 警報消失了 , 大約是五到十二歲 。
he gets up , leaps onto his scooter , races through the city past the church of santa maria della pace , down the alleys , through the streets that tourists may be wandering through , disturbing the quiet backstreet life of rome at every turn .	他站起來 , 跳上了他的螺旋槳 , 穿過城市的比賽 , 穿過聖塔馬利亞•德拉的教堂 , 沿著巷子 , 遊客可能穿過街道 , 每次轉動時 , 安靜的羅馬回饋生活 。
that speed with which he is moving , i hope i have suggested in this little image , which , again , can be turned around and read from both sides because there's text on the bottom and text on the top , one of which is upside down in this image .	他移動的速度 , 我希望我在這張圖片上建議 , 同樣的 , 可以從兩邊轉過來 , 從兩邊看 , 因為底部的文字和上面的文字 , 其中之一是反面的 。
so , he keeps on moving , approaching an unsuspecting waiter who is trying to deliver two plates of linguine in a delicate white wine clam sauce to diners who are sitting at a table just outside of a restaurant in the street .	所以 , 他繼續走下去 , 接近一名毫無疑問的服務生 , 他試圖在一間精緻的白酒杯醬料中 , 送兩張白酒杯醬給坐在一桌外的餐廳的餐廳 。
waiter catches on , but it's too late .	服務生抓住了 , 但太遲了 。
and marcello keeps moving in his scooter .	marcello一直搬進他的小屋裡 。
everything he sees from this point on is slightly affected by the linguine , but keeps on moving because this guy's got a job to do .	從這點 , 他看到的一切都有點受到語言學影響 , 但繼續前進 , 因為這個人有工作要做 。
removes some scaffolding . one of the reasons rome remains the extraordinary place it is that because of scaffolding and the determination to maintain the fabric , it is a city that continues to grow and adapt to the needs of the particular time in which it finds itself , or we find it .	移除一些支架 , 羅馬仍然是不平凡的地方之一 , 是因為支架和決心要維持布料 , 城市持續成長 , 適應特定時間需求的需求 , 或我們發現它 。
right through the piazza della rotonda , in front of the pantheon again wreaking havoc and finally getting to work .	穿過普利薩•德拉•羅頓達 , 在萬神殿前 , 又再次破壞了 , 終於到達了工作 。
marcello , as it turns out , is the driver of the number 64 bus , and if you've been on the number 64 bus , you know that it's driven with the same kind of exuberance as marcello demonstrated on his scooter .	結果發現 , marcello是64輛公車的司機 , 如果你參加了64輛公車 , 你知道它開車和marcello在他的分數上展示的一樣 。
and finally carletto . you see his apartment in the upper lefthand corner .	最後 , 卡萊托 。 你看到他的公寓在左上角 。
he's looking at his table ; he's planning to propose this evening to his girlfriend of 40 years , and he wants it to be perfect .	他在看他的桌子 ; 他打算要向他的女朋友提出這個計畫 , 要花四十年的時間 , 他希望它能完美 。
he's got candles out , he's got flowers in the middle and he's trying to figure out where to put the plates and the glasses .	他拿出蠟燭 , 中間有一朵花 , 他想辦法把盤子和玻璃放在哪裡 。
but he's not happy ; something's wrong .	但他不高興 , 有些事是錯的 。
the phone rings anyway , he's called to the palazzo .	總之 , 電話響了 , 他被叫到palazzo 。
he saunters he saunters at a good clip , but as compared to all the traveling we've just seen , he's sauntering .	他接觸了一段很棒的短片 , 但和我們剛剛看到的旅程相比 , 他在散步 。
everybody knows carletto , because he's in entertainment , actually ; he's in television .	大家都知道carleto , 因為他在娛樂 , 他在電視上 。
he's actually in television repair , which is why people know him .	他其實是在電視修復中 , 這就是為什麼人們認識他 。
so they all have his number .	所以他們都有他的數字 。
he arrives at the palazzo , arrives at the big front door .	他抵達了帕拉佐索 , 到達了大門 。
enters the courtyard and talks to the custodian , who tells him that there's been a disaster in the palazzo ; nobody's tvs are working and there's a big soccer game coming up , and the crowd is getting a little restless and a little nervous .	進入庭院 , 和顧客談話 , 他告訴他 , 在帕拉索有場災難 ; 沒有人在電視上工作 , 有一場很大的足球比賽來了 , 群眾變得有點不安靜 , 有點緊張 。
he goes down to the basement and starts to check the wiring , and then gradually works his way up to the top of the building , apartment by apartment , checking every television , checking every connection , hoping to find out what this problem is .	他走到地下室 , 開始檢查這些線路 , 然後漸漸地 , 走到建築頂端 , 公寓旁 , 檢查每個電視 , 檢查每一條連結 , 希望找出這個問題是什麼 。
he works his way up , finally , the grand staircase and then a smaller staircase until he reaches the attic .	他在路上工作 , 最後 , 大樓梯 , 接著是小樓梯 , 直到他抵達閣樓 。
he opens the window of the attic , of course , and there's a tablecloth wrapped around the building's television antenna .	他打開閣樓的窗戶 , 當然還有一張桌布包圍著建築物的電視天線 。
he removes it , the problems are solved , everybody in the palazzo is happy .	他移除它 , 問題解決了 , 帕拉zzo的每個人都很開心 。
and of course , he also solves his own problem .	當然 , 他也解決了他自己的問題 。
all he has to do now , with a perfect table , is wait for her to arrive .	他現在只需要用一張完美的桌子 , 等著她抵達 。
that was the first attempt , but it didn't seem substantial enough to convey whatever it was i wanted to convey about rome .	那是第一次嘗試 , 但似乎不夠大 , 可以傳達我想要傳達的關於羅馬的訊息 。
so i thought , well , i'll just do piazzas , and i'll get inside and underneath and i'll show these things growing and show why they're shaped the way they are and so on .	所以我想 , 好吧 , 我就來做piazzas , 然後我會進到裡面 , 然後我會展示這些東西的成長 , 展示它們為什麼會改變它們的形狀等等 。
and then i thought , that's too complicated . no , i'll just take my favorite bits and pieces and i'll put them inside the pantheon but keep the scale , so you can see the top of sant'ivo and the pyramid of cestius and the tempietto of bramante all side by side in this amazing space .	然後我想 , 這太複雜了 。 不 , 我會把我最喜歡的位元和碎片放進萬神廟裡 , 讓它保持尺度 , 這樣你就能看到西雅圖的頂端 , 西斯蒂烏斯的金字塔 , 以及巴曼特的溫度 , 全都排在這個美妙的空間中 。
now that's one drawing , so i thought maybe it's time for piranesi to meet escher .	這只是一張圖 , 所以我想也許是皮蘭西認識escher的時候了 。
you see that i'm beginning to really lose control here and also hope .	你看 , 我已經開始失去控制權了 , 也失去希望了 。
there's a very thin blue line of exhaust that sort of runs through this thing that would be kind of the trail that holds it all together .	有一條非常薄的藍色路線 , 有點像是穿過這條路 , 讓它整合在一起 。
then i thought , " wait a minute , what am i doing ? "	然後我想: 「 等等 , 我在做什麼 ? 」
a book is not only a neat way of collecting and storing information , it's a series of layers .	書不只是收集和儲存資訊的方式 , 它是一系列的層次 。
i mean , you always peel one layer off another ; we think of them as pages , doing it a certain way .	我的意思是 , 你總是把一層一層剝下來 ; 我們認為他們是網頁 , 用某種方式去做 。
but think of them as layers . i mean , rome is a place of layers horizontal layers , vertical layers and i thought , well just peeling off a page would allow me to if i got you thinking about it the right way would allow me to sort of show you the depth of layers .	但把它們想成層次 。 我的意思是 , 羅馬是層層層層的地層 , 垂直層 , 我想 , 只要把頁面撕下來 , 就會讓我用正確的方式來思考 , 讓我來展示層層的深度 。
the stucco on the walls of most of the buildings in rome covers the scars ; the scars of centuries of change as these structures have been adapted rather than being torn down .	羅馬大部份建築的牆壁都包含了疤痕 ; 數世紀以來 , 改變的疤痕已經被改造而不是被撕裂 。
if i do a foldout page on the lefthand side and let you just unfold it , you see behind it what i mean by scar tissue .	如果我在左手邊做一個摺疊頁 , 讓你剛剛展開 , 你可以看到我所說的傷疤組織背後的意義 。
you can see that in 1635 , it became essential to make smaller windows because the bad guys were coming or whatever .	你可以看到在1635年 , 讓小窗戶變得很重要 , 因為壞人來了 , 等等 。
adaptations all get buried under the stucco .	所有的適應都被埋在黏土下 。
i could peel out a page of this palazzo to show you what's going on inside of it .	我可以把這個帕拉佐索的一頁向你們展示裡面發生了什麼事 。
but more importantly , i could also show you what it looks like at the corner of one of those magnificent buildings with all the massive stone blocks , or the fake stone blocks done with brick and stucco , which is more often the case .	更重要的是 , 我也能向你們展示這些壯麗的建築 , 那些巨大的石頭積木 , 或用磚塊做成的假石塊 , 通常是這樣 。
so it becomes slightly threedimensional .	所以它變得有點三維 。
i could take you down one of those narrow little streets into one of those surprising piazzas by using a double gate fold double foldout page which , if you were like me reading a popup book as a child , you hopefully stick your head into .	我可以把其中一個狹窄的小街道帶到一個令人驚訝的廣場上 , 用雙層的摺疊紙 , 如果你和我一樣小時候讀了一本跳躍的書 , 你希望你能把頭伸進去 。
you wrap the pages around your head and are in that piazza for that brief period of time .	你把頭上的頁面纏繞在那短暫的時間裡 。
and i've really not done anything much more complicated than make foldout pages .	我真的沒有做任何比摺紙更複雜的東西 。
but then i thought , maybe i could be simpler here .	但接著我想 , 也許我可以簡單些 。
let's look at the pantheon and the piazza della rotonda in front of it .	咱們來看看萬神廟和前面的廣場廣場德拉•羅頓達 。
here's a book completely wide open .	這本書完全打開了 。
ok , if i don't open the book the whole way , if i just open it 90 degrees , we're looking down the front of the pantheon , and we're looking sort of at the top , more or less down on the square .	好 , 如果我不打開這本書 , 如果我打開它90度 , 我們就在萬神廟的前面 , 我們會看到有點像在上面 , 下方多或少 。
and if i turn the book the other way , we're looking across the square at the front of the pantheon .	如果我換個角度看這本書 , 我們在萬神廟的前方看了看 。
no foldouts , no tricks just a book that isn't open the whole way .	沒有摺紙 , 沒有把戲 , 只是一本完全沒有打開的書 。
that seemed promising . i thought , maybe i'll do it inside and i can even combine the foldouts with the only partially opened book .	這聽起來很有前景 。 我心想 , 也許我會在裡面做 , 我甚至可以把摺疊結合 , 再加上唯一的部分打開的書 。
so we get inside the pantheon and it grows and so on and so forth .	所以 , 我們進入萬神殿 , 它會不斷成長 , 諸如此類 。
and i thought , maybe i'm on the right track , but it sort of lost its human quality .	我想 , 也許我站在正確的軌道上 , 但這有點像是失去了人類的特質 。
so i went back to the notion of story , which is always a good thing to have if you're trying to get people to pay attention to a book and pick up information along the way .	所以 , 我回到故事的概念 , 如果你想要讓大家注意書 , 並在過程中取得信息 。
" pigeon's progress " struck me as a catchy title .	「 鴿子的進步 」 震驚了我是個抓住頭銜 。
if it was a homing pigeon , it would be called " homer's odyssey . "	如果牠是一隻蜂鳥 , 牠就會被稱為 「 荷馬的奇怪 」 。
but it was the journey of the . . .	但那是那趟旅程......
i mean , if a title works , use it . but it would be a journey that went through rome and showed all the things that i like about rome .	我的意思是 , 如果一個標題成功了 , 用它 。 但這會是一趟探訪羅馬的旅程 , 展示了我喜歡的羅馬 。
it's a pigeon sitting on top of a church .	它是坐在教堂的上方的鴿子 。
goes off during the day and does normal pigeon stuff . comes back , the whole place is covered with scaffolding and green netting and there's no way this pigeon can get home .	白天離開 , 做正常的鴿子 , 回來了 , 整個地方充滿了支架和綠色的網子 , 沒有辦法回家 。
so it's a homeless pigeon now and it's going to have to find another place to live , and that allows me to go through my catalog of favorite things , and we start with the tall ones and so on .	所以現在是無家可歸的鴿子 , 它必須找到另一個居住的地方 , 這讓我可以通過我最愛的目錄 , 我們從高高的鴿開始 。
maybe it has to go back and live with family members ; that's not always a good thing , but it does sort of bring pigeons together again .	也許它必須回去和家人住在一起 , 這不一定是件好事 , 但它確實能把鴿子帶回來 。
and i thought , that's sort of interesting , but maybe there's a person who should be involved in this in some way .	我心想 , 這有點有趣 , 但也許有一個人應該以某種方式參與其中 。
so i kind of came up with this old guy who spends his life looking after sick pigeons .	所以我想出了一個老傢伙 , 他在照顧生病的鴿子 。
he'll go anywhere to get them dangerous places and whatnot and they become really friends with this guy , and learn to do tricks for him and entertain him at lunchtime and stuff like that .	他會去任何地方 , 讓他們有危險的地方 , 什麼也沒有 , 他們會和這個傢伙成為真正的朋友 , 學會欺騙他 , 並在午餐時間娛樂他之類的 。
there's a real bond that develops between this old man and these pigeons .	在這老人和這些鴿子之間 , 有一個真實的連結 。
but unfortunately he gets sick . he gets really sick at the end of the story .	但不幸的是 , 他生病了 。 他在故事結束時就生病了 。
he's taught them to spell his name , which is aldo .	他被教導他們拼寫他的名字 , 也就是aldo 。
they show up one day after three or four days of not seeing him he lives in this little garret and they spell his name and fly around .	他們在三四天後出現 , 看不見他 , 他住在這個小車庫裡 , 拼了他的名字 , 四處飛來飛去 。
and he finally gets enough strength together to climb up the ladder onto the roof , and all the pigeons , a la red balloon , are there waiting for him and they carry him off over the walls of the city .	他終於得到了足夠的力量 , 把梯子爬到屋頂上 , 所有的鴿子、紅色氣球等著他 , 他們把他帶到城市的牆上 。
and i forgot to mention this: whenever he lost a pigeon , he would take that pigeon out beyond the walls of the city .	我忘了提一下:每當他失去一隻鴿子時 , 他就會把那隻鴿子帶到城市的牆外 。
in the old roman custom , the dead were never buried within the walls .	在古老的羅馬習俗中 , 死者從來沒有被埋在牆裡 。
and i thought that's a really cheery story .	我想這是個很歡迎的故事 。
. that's really going to go a long way .	這真的會很長一段時間 。
so anyway , i went through . . . and again , if packaging doesn't work and if the stories aren't going anywhere , i just come up with titles and hope that a title will sort of kick me off in the right direction .	所以 , 總之 , 我經歷了......再一次 , 如果包裝沒有用 , 如果故事沒去 , 我就想出了頭銜 , 希望頭銜會把我踢出正確的方向 。
and sometimes it does focus me enough and i'll even do a title page .	有時候它會讓我專注在上面 , 我甚至會做一個標題頁 。
so , these are all title pages that eventually led me to the solution i settled on , which is the story of a young woman who sends a message on a homing pigeon she lives outside the walls of the city of rome to someone in the city .	所以 , 這些都是標題頁面 , 最終引領我去解決方案 , 這也是一個年輕女子的故事 , 她把信息傳遞給她住在羅馬城外圍的人的故事 。
and the pigeon is flying down above the appian way here .	鴿子在飛行的上方飛越平行 。
you can see the tombs and pines and so on and so forth along the way .	你可以看到墳墓、松木等等 。
if you see the red line , you are seeing the trail of the pigeon ; if you don't see the red line , you are the pigeon .	如果你看到紅線 , 你就會看到鴿子的軌跡 ; 如果你看不見紅線 , 你就是鴿子 。
and it becomes necessary and possible , at this point , to try to convey what that sense would be like of flying over the city without actually moving .	在這個時點 , 它變得是必要且可能的 , 試著傳達出那種飛越城市的感覺 , 而不是真的在移動 。
past the pyramid of cestius these will seem very familiar to you , even if you haven't been to rome recently past the gatehouse .	越過了凱斯提烏斯的金字塔 , 這對你來說似乎很熟悉 , 即使你最近沒去過羅馬 。
this is something that's a little bit unusual .	這是有點不尋常的事 。
this pigeon does something that most homing pigeons do not do: it takes the scenic route , which was a device that i felt was necessary to actually extend this book beyond about four pages .	這種鴿子做一些最常謀殺的鴿子做不到的事:它要走上一路 , 那是我覺得需要的裝置 , 才能把這本書延伸到四頁以外 。
so , we circle around the coliseum , past the church of santa maria in cosmedin and the temple of hercules towards the river .	所以 , 我們圍繞著哥倫比亞的哥倫比亞教堂 , 穿越了聖瑪利亞的教堂 , 和海克力斯的神殿 , 朝向河邊 。
we almost collide with the cornice of the palazzo farnese designed by michelangelo , built of stone taken from the coliseum narrow escape .	我們幾乎和米開朗基羅的帕拉索法尼斯所設計的玉米花幾乎碰撞 , 建造的石頭是從哥倫比亞的逃離中拍下來的 。
we swoop down over the campo de' fiori .	我們沿著campodefiori下滑 。
this is one of those things i show to my students because it's a complete bastardization a denial of any rules of perspective .	這是我向學生展示的其中一件事 , 因為這是完全的禁止 , 否認任何觀點的規則 。
the only rule of perspective that i think matters is if it looks believable , you've succeeded .	我認為唯一重要的規則是 , 如果它看起來是可信的 , 你成功了 。
but you try and figure out where the vanishing points meet here ; a couple are on mars and a couple of others in cremona .	但你試著找出這裡消失的點在哪裡 ; 在火星上還有一些其他的火星 。
but into the piazza in front of santa maria della pace , where invariably a soccer game is going on , and we're hit by a soccer ball .	但在聖塔馬利亞的前面 , 在那裏 , 一場足球比賽正在進行 , 我們被足球擊中 。
now this is a terrible illustration of being hit by a soccer ball .	這是一個被足球撞擊的可怕插圖 。
i have all the pieces: there's santa maria della pace , there's a soccer ball , there's a little bit of a bird's wing nothing's happening , so i had to rethink it .	我有所有的碎片:有聖塔•德拉的速度 , 有一顆足球 , 有一小隻鳥的翅膀沒有發生 , 所以我得要重新思考 。
and if you do want to see santa maria della pace , these books are really flexible , incredibly interactive just turn it around and look at it the other way .	如果你想看到聖塔•德拉的速度 , 這些書是很靈活、非常互動的 , 只要把它轉過來 , 再看它 。
through the alley , we can see the impact is captured in the red line .	透過巷子 , 我們可以看到紅線被捕捉 。
and then bird manages to pull itself together past this medieval tower one of the few remaining medieval towers towards the church of sant'agnese and around the dome looking down into piazza navona which we've already mentioned and seen and flown over a couple of times ; there's the bernini statue of the four rivers and then past the wonderful borromini sant'ivo , stopping just long enough on the 26foot diameter oculus of the pantheon to catch our breath .	接著 , 鳥類會把自己拉過這棟中世紀的高塔 , 只有少數幾個中世紀的高塔 , 前往聖祖國教堂 , 繞著圓頂向下 , 向下看 , 看了幾次 , 我們已經看過了 , 經過了四條河流的伯尼 , 穿過了很棒的布羅米諾伊諾尼的聖誕節 , 停止在26英尺長的時間內 , 停止在我們呼吸的第十六英尺長 。
and then we can swoop inside and around ; and because we're flying , we don't really have to worry about gravity at this particular moment in time , so this drawing can be oriented in any way on the page .	接著 , 我們可以在裡面轉動 , 因為我們飛行 , 我們不用擔心在這個特定時刻的地心引力 , 所以這張圖可以在任何頁面上找到方向 。
we get a little exuberant as we pass gesu ; it's not surprising to sort of mimic the architecture in this way .	當我們經過gesu時 , 我們會有點生氣 ; 用這種方式模仿建築並不讓人意外 。
past the wonderful wall filled with the juxtaposition that i was talking about ; beautiful carvings set into the walls above the neon " ristorante " sign , and so on .	越過了美妙的牆 , 我剛剛提到的節奏 , 美麗的雕刻就在尼龍 「 崛起 」 標誌之上 , 諸如此類 。
and eventually , we arrive at the courtyard of the palazzo , which is our destination .	最終 , 我們抵達了帕拉索的庭院 , 那是我們的目的地 。
straight up through the courtyard into a little window into the attic , where somebody is working at the drawing board .	直接穿過庭院 , 進入一個小窗戶 , 進入閣樓 , 有人在畫板上工作 。
he removes the message from the leg of the bird ; this is what it says .	他從鳥的腿上移除訊息 , 這就是它所說的 。
as we look at the drawing board , we see what he's working on is , in fact , a map of the journey that the pigeon has just taken , and the red line extends through all the sights .	當我們看著畫板 , 我們看到他正在努力的實際上 , 是鴿子剛剛拍攝的地圖 , 紅線延伸到所有的視野 。
and if you want the information , so that we complete this cycle of understanding , all you have to do is read these paragraphs .	如果你想要這些資訊 , 所以我們完成了這個理解的循環 , 你只要讀一下這些段落 。
thank you very much .	非常謝謝各位 。
mit researcher skylar tibbits works on selfassembly the idea that instead of building something , we can create materials that build themselves , much the way a strand of dna zips itself together . it's a big concept at early stages ; tibbits shows us three inthelab projects that hint at what a selfassembling future might look like .	麻省理工學院研究員skylarbitits在自我組裝上運作 , 與其建造一些東西 , 我們能創造出能自己建構的材料 , 如同一股dnazips本身 。 這是在早期的階段 ; tibbit向我們展示了三項專案 , 暗示了自我組裝未來可能的樣子 。
skylar tibbits: can we make things that make themselves ?	天花斑斑斑斑海兔:我們能製造自己製造的東西嗎 ?
