today i'd like to show you the future of the way we make things .	今天我想向各位展示我們製造東西的方式的未來 。
i believe that soon our buildings and machines will be selfassembling , replicating and repairing themselves .	我相信 , 很快我們的建築物和機器就會自我組裝、複製、修復自己 。
so i'm going to show you what i believe is the current state of manufacturing , and then compare that to some natural systems .	所以 , 我要向你們展示我相信的 , 是目前製造業的狀態 , 然後將它和一些自然系統做比較 。
so in the current state of manufacturing , we have skyscrapers two and a half years [of assembly time] , 500 , 000 to a million parts , fairly complex , new , exciting technologies in steel , concrete , glass .	在目前的製造業狀態 , 我們有摩天大樓兩年半的時間組裝時間 , 五十萬到一百萬個零件 , 相當複雜、令人興奮的科技 , 鋼鐵、混凝土、玻璃 。
we have exciting machines that can take us into space five years [of assembly time] , 2 . 5 million parts .	我們有令人興奮的機器可以帶我們進入太空五年--[組裝時間]250萬個部分 。
but on the other side , if you look at the natural systems , we have proteins that have two million types , can fold in 10 , 000 nanoseconds , or dna with three billion base pairs we can replicate in roughly an hour .	但另一方面 , 如果你看一下自然系統 , 我們有兩百萬種類型的蛋白質 , 可以在一萬奈秒或dna中摺出三十億鹼基對 , 我們可以在大約一小時內複製 。
so there's all of this complexity in our natural systems , but they're extremely efficient , far more efficient than anything we can build , far more complex than anything we can build .	在我們的自然系統中 , 都有這種複雜性 , 但它們非常有效率 , 遠遠超過我們所能建造的任何東西 , 遠超過我們所能建造的任何複雜 。
they're far more efficient in terms of energy .	在能源方面 , 它們更有效率 。
they hardly ever make mistakes .	他們幾乎沒有犯錯 。
and they can repair themselves for longevity .	他們可以長壽地修復自己 。
so there's something super interesting about natural systems .	所以 , 天然系統有趣之處 。
and if we can translate that into our built environment , then there's some exciting potential for the way that we build things .	如果我們可以把它翻譯成我們的建築環境 , 那麼我們建造東西的方式有一些令人振奮的潛力 。
and i think the key to that is selfassembly .	我認為關鍵在於自我組裝 。
so if we want to utilize selfassembly in our physical environment , i think there's four key factors .	所以 , 如果我們想要在我們的物理環境中利用自我組裝 , 我認為有四個關鍵因素 。
the first is that we need to decode all of the complexity of what we want to build so our buildings and machines .	首先 , 我們需要解碼我們想要建造的東西的複雜性 , 以讓我們的建築和機器 。
and we need to decode that into simple sequences basically the dna of how our buildings work .	我們需要將它解碼成簡單的序列基本上就是我們的建築如何運作的dna 。
then we need programmable parts that can take that sequence and use that to fold up , or reconfigure .	接著 , 我們需要可編寫的零件 , 可以將這些序列拿來摺疊 , 或重新組裝 。
we need some energy that's going to allow that to activate , allow our parts to be able to fold up from the program .	我們需要一些能量來啟動它 , 讓我們的部件能夠從這個程式中折疊 。
and we need some type of error correction redundancy to guarantee that we have successfully built what we want .	我們需要一種錯誤的修正方式 , 來確保我們成功地建造我們想要的東西 。
so i'm going to show you a number of projects that my colleagues and i at mit are working on to achieve this selfassembling future .	所以 , 我要給你們看幾個項目 , 是我同事和我在麻省理工學院的同事 , 致力完成這個自我組裝的未來 。
the first two are the macrobot and decibot .	前兩種是macrobot和decibot 。
so these projects are largescale reconfigurable robots 8 ft . , 12 ft . long proteins .	這些專案是大規模的可重建機器人8英尺 , 12英尺長的蛋白質 。
they're embedded with mechanical electrical devices , sensors .	它們被機械電裝置 , 感應器嵌入 。
you decode what you want to fold up into , into a sequence of angles so negative 120 , negative 120 , 0 , 0 , 120 , negative 120 something like that ; so a sequence of angles , or turns , and you send that sequence through the string .	解碼你想要摺疊成一連串的角度 , 負120 , 負120 , 120 , 120 , 120 , 120 , 負120種類似的東西 ; 所以一連串的角度 , 或轉向 , 然後你將這個序列的序列發送給弦 。
each unit takes its message so negative 120 it rotates to that , checks if it got there and then passes it to its neighbor .	每個單位都收集它的訊息 , 如此負120次 , 它轉到那邊 , 檢查是否到那裡 , 然後把它傳給鄰居 。
so these are the brilliant scientists , engineers , designers that worked on this project .	這些是傑出的科學家 , 工程師 , 設計師 , 在這個專案上工作 。
and i think it really brings to light: is this really scalable ?	我認為它真的會帶來光明:這是真的可擴展的嗎 ?
i mean , thousands of dollars , lots of man hours made to make this eightfoot robot .	我的意思是 , 數千美元 , 許多人為了製作這八英尺的機器人 。
can we really scale this up ? can we really embed robotics into every part ?	我們真的能把這個規模擴大嗎 ? 我們能把機器人嵌入每一個部分嗎 ?
the next one questions that and looks at passive nature , or passively trying to have reconfiguration programmability .	下一個問題是 , 看著被動的自然 , 或被動地嘗試重新組裝程式性 。
but it goes a step further , and it tries to have actual computation .	但它進一步更進一步 , 它嘗試有實際的計算 。
it basically embeds the most fundamental building block of computing , the digital logic gate , directly into your parts .	基本上 , 它嵌入了電腦最基本的基礎組成元素 , 數位邏輯門 , 直接嵌入你的部分 。
so this is a nand gate .	這是一個nand門 。
you have one tetrahedron which is the gate that's going to do your computing , and you have two input tetrahedrons .	你有一個四面體 , 就是門用來計算 , 你有兩個四面體 。
one of them is the input from the user , as you're building your bricks .	其中之一是使用者的輸入 , 當你在建造你的磚塊時 。
the other one is from the previous brick that was placed .	另外一個是從前一塊被安置的磚塊 。
and then it gives you an output in 3d space .	接著 , 它會給你3d空間的輸出 。
so what this means is that the user can start plugging in what they want the bricks to do .	意思是 , 使用者可以開始把他們想要的磚塊黏起來 。
it computes on what it was doing before and what you said you wanted it to do .	它計算了它之前的做法 , 你說你想要它做什麼 。
and now it starts moving in threedimensional space so up or down .	現在它開始在三維空間中移動 , 以上或下 。
so on the lefthand side , [1 , 1] input equals 0 output , which goes down .	在左手邊 , [1 , 1]輸入等於0的輸出 , 下降了 。
on the righthand side , [0 , 0] input is a 1 output , which goes up .	在右手邊 , [0 , 0]輸入是1 , 上升 。
and so what that really means is that our structures now contain the blueprints of what we want to build .	這意味著我們的結構現在包含了我們想要建造的藍圖 。
so they have all of the information embedded in them of what was constructed .	所以他們所有的資訊都嵌入在他們身上 , 說明了什麼是建構出來的 。
so that means that we can have some form of selfreplication .	這意味著我們可以有某種形式的自我複製 。
in this case i call it selfguided replication , because your structure contains the exact blueprints .	在這個案例中 , 我稱之為自我複製 , 因為你的結構含有確切的藍圖 。
if you have errors , you can replace a part .	如果你有錯誤 , 你可以取代一部分 。
all the local information is embedded to tell you how to fix it .	所有當地的資訊都被嵌入來告訴你如何修復它 。
so you could have something that climbs along and reads it and can output at one to one .	所以你可以有爬上去讀到的東西 , 並且可以輸出一個到一個 。
it's directly embedded ; there's no external instructions .	它是直接嵌入的 , 沒有外部的指令 。
so the last project i'll show is called biased chains , and it's probably the most exciting example that we have right now of passive selfassembly systems .	我接下來要展示的最後一個專案叫做 「 偏見鏈 」 , 它可能是我們現在最令人興奮的例子 , 自動組裝系統 。
so it takes the reconfigurability and programmability and makes it a completely passive system .	所以 , 它需要可重組性和可編程性 , 讓它變成完全被動的系統 。
so basically you have a chain of elements .	基本上你有一連串的元素 。
each element is completely identical , and they're biased .	每個元素都是完全相同的 , 且它們是偏見的 。
so each chain , or each element , wants to turn right or left .	所以每一個鏈 , 或每個元素 , 都想要左轉或左轉 。
so as you assemble the chain , you're basically programming it .	所以當你組裝鏈 , 基本上你在編寫它 。
you're telling each unit if it should turn right or left .	你在告訴每個單位是否應該向右轉或向左轉 。
so when you shake the chain , it then folds up into any configuration that you've programmed in so in this case , a spiral , or in this case , two cubes next to each other .	所以當你搖動鏈 , 它會折疊成任何你編寫過的構造 , 在這個案例中 , 或在這個案例中 , 兩個立方體彼此相鄰 。
so you can basically program any threedimensional shape or onedimensional , twodimensional up into this chain completely passively .	基本上 , 你可以設計任何立體形狀或維度形狀 , 二維空間完全被動地進入這條鏈 。
so what does this tell us about the future ?	所以 , 這告訴我們什麼樣的未來 ?
i think that it's telling us that there's new possibilities for selfassembly , replication , repair in our physical structures , our buildings , machines .	我認為它告訴我們 , 自我組裝、複製、修復、修復我們的實體結構、建築、機器 。
there's new programmability in these parts .	這些部分有新的程式性 。
and from that you have new possibilities for computing .	從那之後你就有了新的計算能力 。
we'll have spatial computing .	我們會有空間計算 。
imagine if our buildings , our bridges , machines , all of our bricks could actually compute .	想像一下 , 如果我們的建築物、橋樑、機器 , 我們所有的磚塊都可以計算 。
that's amazing parallel and distributed computing power , new design possibilities .	那是很驚人的平行和分配運算能力 , 新的設計可能性 。
so it's exciting potential for this .	所以這很讓人興奮 。
so i think these projects i've showed here are just a tiny step towards this future , if we implement these new technologies for a new selfassembling world .	所以 , 我認為我在這裡展示的這些項目只是邁向這個未來的一小步 , 如果我們把這些新科技應用在一個新的自我組裝世界上 。
we've been to the moon , we've mapped the continents , we've even been to the deepest point in the ocean twice . what's left for the next generation to explore ? biologist and explorer nathan wolfe suggests this answer: almost everything . and we can start , he says , with the world of the unseeably small .	我們去過月球 , 我們繪製了非洲大陸 , 我們已經在海底深處了兩次 。 下一代去探索的是什麼 ? 生物學家和探險家納森•沃夫斯建議了這個答案:幾乎每一樣 。 我們都可以開始 , 他說 , 和不穩定的小世界 。
biodiversity , exploration , microbiology , science	生物多樣性 , 探索 , 微生物學 , 科學科學 ,
nathan wolfe: what's left to explore ?	nathanwolfe:還有什麼可以探索的 ?
recently i visited beloit , wisconsin .	最近我造訪了威斯康辛的地點 。
and i was there to honor a great 20th century explorer , roy chapman andrews .	我在那裡向一位偉大的二十世紀探險家羅伊•查普曼•安德魯斯致敬 。
during his time at the american museum of natural history , andrews led a range of expeditions to uncharted regions , like here in the gobi desert .	在他在美國自然歷史博物館的期間 , 安德魯斯帶領了一系列的探險 , 前往未知的區域 , 例如在戈比沙漠 。
he was quite a figure .	他是個很棒的人物 。
he was later , it's said , the basis of the indiana jones character .	他說 , 他後來是印第安納瓊斯的角色 。
and when i was in beloit , wisconsin , i gave a public lecture to a group of middle school students .	當我在威斯康辛的地下時 , 我給了一群中學學生一份公開演說 。
and i'm here to tell you , if there's anything more intimidating than talking here at ted , it'll be trying to hold the attention of a group of a thousand 12yearolds for a 45minute lecture .	我來這裡告訴各位 , 如果在ted演講中 , 有什麼事會比現在更嚇人 , 它會試著注意到一千十二歲的孩子 , 為了一個45分鐘的演講 ,
at the end of the lecture they asked a number of questions , but there was one that's really stuck with me since then .	在演講結束後 , 他們問了幾個問題 , 但在那之後 , 有個問題讓我很困擾 。
there was a young girl who stood up , and she asked the question: " where should we explore ? "	有位年輕女孩站起來 , 她問了這個問題: 「 我們該去哪裡探索 ? 」
i think there's a sense that many of us have that the great age of exploration on earth is over , that for the next generation they're going to have to go to outer space or the deepest oceans in order to find something significant to explore .	我想我們很多人有一種感覺 , 地球上探索的偉大時代已經結束了 , 在下一代 , 他們必須去外太空 , 或深海 , 才能找到重要的探索 。
but is that really the case ?	但真的是這樣嗎 ?
is there really nowhere significant for us to explore left here on earth ?	我們真的沒有什麼東西可以讓我們在地球上探索嗎 ?
it sort of made me think back to one of my favorite explorers in the history of biology .	這讓我回想到生物學史上我最喜歡的探險家之一 。
this is an explorer of the unseen world , martinus beijerinck .	這是個未知世界的探險家 , 馬丁.貝吉尼克 。
so beijerinck set out to discover the cause of tobacco mosaic disease .	所以 , beijerinck開始發現菸草病的原因 。
what he did is he took the infected juice from tobacco plants and he would filter it through smaller and smaller filters .	他的做法是從菸草植物中取出感染的果汁 , 他會用較小的濾嘴過濾過它 。
and he reached the point where he felt that there must be something out there that was smaller than the smallest forms of life that were ever known bacteria , at the time .	他直到他感覺到一定有比當時所知最小型的細菌還小的東西 。
he came up with a name for his mystery agent .	他為他的神秘經理取了名字 。
he called it the virus latin for " poison . "	他稱之為 「 毒藥 」 。
and in uncovering viruses , beijerinck really opened this entirely new world for us .	在發掘病毒的過程中 , beijerinck為我們開啟了這個全新的世界 。
we now know that viruses make up the majority of the genetic information on our planet , more than the genetic information of all other forms of life combined .	我們現在知道病毒組成了地球上大部分的基因信息 , 遠超過所有其他形式的生命形式 。
and obviously there's been tremendous practical applications associated with this world things like the eradication of smallpox , the advent of a vaccine against cervical cancer , which we now know is mostly caused by human papillomavirus .	很明顯地 , 已經有很大的實用應用 , 和這個世界有關 , 比如根除天花 , 疫苗的出現 , 與子宮頸癌的出現 , 我們現在知道大部分是由人類乳突病毒造成的 。
and beijerinck's discovery , this was not something that occurred 500 years ago .	beijerinck的發現 , 這不是500年前發生的事 。
it was a little over 100 years ago that beijerinck discovered viruses .	大約一百多年前 , beijerinck發現了病毒 。
so basically we had automobiles , but we were unaware of the forms of life that make up most of the genetic information on our planet .	基本上 , 我們有汽車 , 但我們不知道製造地球上大部分基因信息的生命形式 。
we now have these amazing tools to allow us to explore the unseen world things like deep sequencing , which allow us to do much more than just skim the surface and look at individual genomes from a particular species , but to look at entire metagenomes , the communities of teeming microorganisms in , on and around us and to document all of the genetic information in these species .	我們現在有很棒的工具可以讓我們探索未知的世界 , 像是深度定序 , 讓我們能做的不只是滑雪表面 , 還能從特定物種看出個別的基因組 , 看看整個微生物群落在我們身邊 , 記錄所有這些物種的基因資訊 。
we can apply these techniques to things from soil to skin and everything in between .	我們可以把這些技巧應用到土壤、皮膚、以及介於兩者之間的一切 。
in my organization we now do this on a regular basis to identify the causes of outbreaks that are unclear exactly what causes them .	在我的組織中 , 我們現在定期地做這件事 , 來找出造成它們的爆發原因 。
and just to give you a sense of how this works , imagine that we took a nasal swab from every single one of you .	為了讓各位了解這如何運作 , 想像一下 , 我們從你們每一個人身上取了一個鼻子的腫脹 。
and this is something we commonly do to look for respiratory viruses like influenza .	我們常常在尋找呼吸道病毒 , 如流感病毒 。
the first thing we would see is a tremendous amount of genetic information .	首先 , 我們會看到大量的基因信息 。
and if we started looking into that genetic information , we'd see a number of usual suspects out there of course , a lot of human genetic information , but also bacterial and viral information , mostly from things that are completely harmless within your nose .	如果我們開始研究這些遺傳信息 , 我們會看到許多普遍的嫌犯 , 當然 , 很多人類的基因信息 , 還有細菌和病毒信息 , 大多來自你鼻子內完全無害的事物 。
but we'd also see something very , very surprising .	但我們也會看到一些非常非常令人驚訝的事 。
as we started to look at this information , we would see that about 20 percent of the genetic information in your nose doesn't match anything that we've ever seen before no plant , animal , fungus , virus or bacteria .	當我們開始研究這些資訊時 , 我們會發現你的鼻子裡大約百分之二十的基因信息並不符合我們在沒有植物、動物、真菌、病毒或細菌之前所見到的任何東西 。
basically we have no clue what this is .	基本上 , 我們不知道這是什麼 。
and for the small group of us who actually study this kind of data , a few of us have actually begun to call this information biological dark matter .	對於我們這些實際研究這些資料的小組 , 我們當中有一些人開始稱之為生物暗物質 。
we know it's not anything that we've seen before ; it's sort of the equivalent of an uncharted continent right within our own genetic information .	我們知道這不是我們之前看到的任何東西 , 它有點像是我們自己的基因信息中未知的大陸 。
and there's a lot of it .	這裡有很多 。
if you think 20 percent of genetic information in your nose is a lot of biological dark matter , if we looked at your gut , up to 40 or 50 percent of that information is biological dark matter .	如果你認為你的鼻子裡有百分之二十的基因信息是許多生物暗物質如果我們看你的腸子 , 大約有百分之四十或五十的信息是生物暗物質
and even in the relatively sterile blood , around one to two percent of this information is dark matter can't be classified , can't be typed or matched with anything we've seen before .	即便在相對無菌的血液中 , 大約百分之二是暗物質無法被分類 , 無法被輸入或配對任何我們以前見過的 。
at first we thought that perhaps this was artifact .	一開始我們認為這可能是工藝品 。
these deep sequencing tools are relatively new .	這些深度定序的工具是相對新的 。
but as they become more and more accurate , we've determined that this information is a form of life , or at least some of it is a form of life .	但當它們變得越來越精確 , 我們決定了這些資訊是生命的一種形式 , 至少有些是生命的形式 。
and while the hypotheses for explaining the existence of biological dark matter are really only in their infancy , there's a very , very exciting possibility that exists: that buried in this life , in this genetic information , are signatures of as of yet unidentified life .	雖然解釋生物暗物質存在的假設僅僅是它們的初始 , 有一個非常非常令人興奮的可能存在:在生命中 , 埋藏在這些基因信息中 , 代表著尚未被辨識的生命的特徵 。
that as we explore these strings of a's , t's , c's and g's , we may uncover a completely new class of life that , like beijerinck , will fundamentally change the way that we think about the nature of biology .	當我們探索a、t、c、g的弦時 , 我們可能會發現一種全新的生命階級 , 像beijerinck , 會從根本上改變我們對生物學的本質的方式 。
that perhaps will allow us to identify the cause of a cancer that afflicts us or identify the source of an outbreak that we aren't familiar with or perhaps create a new tool in molecular biology .	或許可以讓我們辨識出癌症的成因 , 或辨識出我們不熟悉的疫情來源 , 或是製造分子生物學的新工具 。
i'm pleased to announce that , along with colleagues at stanford and caltech and ucsf , we're currently starting an initiative to explore biological dark matter for the existence of new forms of life .	我很高興地宣佈 , 和史丹佛、加州理工、加州大學和ucsf的同事一起 , 我們正在開始一項計畫 , 來探索生物暗物質 , 來探索新的生命形式的存在 。
a little over a hundred years ago , people were unaware of viruses , the forms of life that make up most of the genetic information on our planet .	大約一百多年前 , 人們不知道病毒是什麼樣的生命形式構成了地球上大部分的基因信息
a hundred years from now , people may marvel that we were perhaps completely unaware of a new class of life that literally was right under our noses .	一百年後 , 人們可能會驚嘆 , 我們可能完全沒有意識到一種全新的生活階級 , 幾乎就在我們的鼻子下 。
it's true , we may have charted all the continents on the planet and we may have discovered all the mammals that are out there , but that doesn't mean that there's nothing left to explore on earth .	沒錯 , 我們可能已經繪製了地球上所有的大陸 , 我們可能已經發現了所有的哺乳動物 , 但這並不意味著地球上沒有任何東西可以探索 。
beijerinck and his kind provide an important lesson for the next generation of explorers people like that young girl from beloit , wisconsin .	beijerinck和他的仁慈為下一代的探險家提供了很重要的一課 , 像是來自威斯康辛的年輕女孩 。
and i think if we phrase that lesson , it's something like this: don't assume that what we currently think is out there is the full story .	我認為 , 如果我們說出這一課 , 就會像這樣:不要假設我們目前所認為的 , 是全部的故事 。
go after the dark matter in whatever field you choose to explore .	不論你選擇去探索哪些領域的暗物質 。
there are unknowns all around us and they're just waiting to be discovered .	我們身邊都沒有人知道 , 他們只是等著被發現 。
legendary scientist david deutsch puts theoretical physics on the back burner to discuss a more urgent matter: the survival of our species . the first step toward solving global warming , he says , is to admit that we have a problem .	傳奇科學家大衛•狄斯奇把理論物理放在後方 , 來討論更迫切的問題:我們物種的生存 。 他說 , 解決全球暖化的第一步 , 就是承認我們有一個問題 。
climate change , cosmos , culture , environment , global issues , physics , science , technology , universe	氣候變遷、宇宙、文化、環境、全球議題、物理、科學、科技、宇宙、宇宙 。
david deutsch on our place in the cosmos	大衛破壞了我們在宇宙中的位置 。
we've been told to go out on a limb and say something surprising .	我們被告知去肢體 , 說些令人驚訝的事 。
so i'll try and do that , but i want to start with two things that everyone already knows .	我會試著這樣做 , 但我想要從大家都知道的兩件事開始 。
and the first one , in fact , is something that has been known for most of recorded history .	首先 , 事實上 , 大部分的記錄歷史都是已知的 。
and that is that the planet earth , or the solar system , or our environment or whatever , is uniquely suited to sustain our evolution or creation , as it used to be thought and our present existence , and most important , our future survival .	那就是地球、太陽系、環境 , 或其它地方 , 都是為了維持我們的演化或創造 , 如同以前所想到的、現在的存在 , 最重要的是 , 我們的未來生存 。
nowadays this idea has a dramatic name: spaceship earth .	現今這個想法有個戲劇性的名字:太空船地球 。
and the idea there is that outside the spaceship , the universe is implacably hostile , and inside is all we have , all we depend on .	理念就是 , 在太空船外 , 宇宙是不可避免的敵意 , 而在內部是我們所擁有的 , 我們所仰賴的一切 。
and we only get the one chance: if we mess up our spaceship , we've got nowhere else to go .	我們只有一個機會:如果我們搞砸了太空船 , 我們就沒有其他地方可以去 。
now , the second thing that everyone already knows is that contrary to what was believed for most of human history , human beings are not , in fact , the hub of existence .	大家早已知道的第二件事 , 與大部分人類歷史所相信的相反 , 事實上 , 人類並不是存在的中心 。
as stephen hawking famously said , we're just a chemical scum on the surface of a typical planet that's in orbit around a typical star , which is on the outskirts of a typical galaxy , and so on .	正如史蒂芬•霍金所說的 , 我們只是一個化學氣體在一個典型的星球上 , 繞著一個典型的恆星繞行軌道 , 在典型的銀河系的郊區 , 諸如此類 。
now the first of those two things that everyone knows is kind of saying that we're at a very untypical place , uniquely suited and so on , and the second one is saying that we're at a typical place .	大家所知道的這兩件事的第一件事就是說我們處在一個非常不典型的地方 , 特別適合等等 , 第二件事是說我們處在一個典型的地方 。
and especially if you regard these two as deep truths to live by and to inform your life decisions , then they seem a little bit to conflict with each other .	尤其是如果你把這兩者視為深層的真理 , 來告訴你們的人生決策 , 那麼它們似乎有點互相衝突 。
but that doesn't prevent them from both being completely false .	但這並不能讓他們完全錯誤 。
and they are . so let me start with the second one: typical . well is this a typical place ? well , let's look around , you know , and look in a random direction , and we see a wall , and chemical scum and that's not typical of the universe at all .	它們是 。 讓我從第二個例子開始 , 典型的這個地方 ? 嗯 , 咱們來看看四周 , 看看隨機的方向 , 我們看到一面牆 , 化學風景 , 這完全不是典型的宇宙 。
all you've got to do is go a few hundred miles in that same direction and look back , and you won't see any walls or chemical scum at all all you see is a blue planet . and if you go further than that , you'll see the sun , the solar system , and the stars and so on .	你只需要走幾百英哩 , 往同一個方向看 , 然後回頭看 , 你不會看到任何牆或化學風景 , 你看到的是藍色的星球 。 如果你進一步看 , 你會看到太陽 , 太陽系 , 太陽系等等 。
but that's still not typical of the universe , because stars come in galaxies .	但這還不是典型的宇宙 , 因為星星系是存在的 。
and most places in the universe , a typical place in the universe , is nowhere near any galaxies .	宇宙中的大部分地方 , 宇宙中的一個典型的地方 , 幾乎沒有任何一個星系 。
so let's go out further , till we're outside the galaxy , and look back , and yeah , there's the huge galaxy with spiral arms laid out in front of us .	讓我們再往外走 , 直到我們在銀河系之外 , 回頭看 , 是的 , 有一個巨大的銀河系 , 上面有螺旋槳在我們面前 。
and at this point we've come 100 , 000 light years from here .	在這個時點 , 我們已經從這裡來了十萬光年 。
but we're still nowhere near a typical place in the universe .	但我們仍然沒有在宇宙中一個典型的地方 。
to get to a typical place , you've got to go 1 , 000 times as far as that into intergalactic space .	要到一個典型的地方 , 你要走一千倍 , 到達星系間的空間 。
and so what does that look like ? typical .	那會是什麼樣子 ? 典型的 。
what does a typical place in the universe look like ?	宇宙中典型的地方長什麼樣子 ?
well , at enormous expense , ted has arranged a highresolution immersion virtual reality rendering of intergalactic space the view from intergalactic space .	嗯 , 在極大的花費之下 , ted已經安排了高解析度的現實 , 將星系間空間的視野從星系空間來呈現 。
so can we have the lights off , please , so we can see it ?	所以 , 我們能不能把燈關掉 , 拜託 , 看得到嗎 ?
well , not quite , not quite perfect you see , in intergalactic space intergalactic space is completely dark , pitch dark .	嗯 , 不是很完美 , 你看 , 在星系間空間中 , 空間是完全黑暗的 , 音高的黑暗 。
it's so dark that if you were to be looking at the nearest star to you , and that star were to explode as a supernova , and you were to be staring directly at it at the moment when its light reached you , you still wouldn't be able to see even a glimmer .	黑暗到如果你正盯著你最近的恆星 , 而那顆恆星被爆炸為超新星 , 你要直接盯著它看 , 當光照到你時 , 你仍然無法看見甚至是微生物 。
that's how big and how dark the universe is .	宇宙是如此的巨大和黑暗 。
and that's despite the fact that a supernova is so bright , so brilliant an event , that it would kill you stone dead at a range of several light years .	儘管事實超新星如此明亮 , 很棒的一個活動 , 它會讓你死於數光年 。
and yet from intergalactic space , it's so far away you wouldn't even see it .	然而 , 從星系間的空間 , 到目前為止 , 你根本看不到它 。
it's also very cold out there less than three degrees above absolute zero .	在絕對零度之上 , 它也非常冷 。
and it's very empty . the vacuum there is one million times less dense than the highest vacuum that our best technology on earth can currently create . so that's how different a typical place is from this place .	它是空無一物的 。 真空真空的密度比地球上最高的技術密度少了一百萬倍 。 所以 , 一般的科技是從這個地方產生的 。
and that is how untypical this place is .	這地方是如此的不典型 。
so can we have the lights back on please ? thank you .	所以 , 我們能把燈打回來嗎 ? 謝謝 。
now how do we know about an environment that's so far away , and so different , and so alien , from anything we're used to ?	我們要如何知道一個遙遠的環境 , 和我們以前所習慣的環境有所不同 ?
well , the earth our environment , in the form of us is creating knowledge .	地球我們的環境 , 以我們的形式 , 創造出知識 。
well , what does that mean ? well , look out even further than we've just been i mean from here , with a telescope and you'll see things that look like stars .	那代表什麼意思呢 ? 嗯 , 看看外面比我們剛剛提到的更遠 , 用望遠鏡來看 , 你會看到看起來像星星的東西 。
they're called " quasars . " quasars originally meant quasistellar object .	它們被稱為 「 正方 」 。 原本的意思是量子論 。
which means things that look a bit like stars . but they're not stars .	這意味著看起來有點像星星的東西 。 但它們不是星星 。
and we know what they are . billions of years ago , and billions of light years away , the material at the center of a galaxy collapsed towards a supermassive black hole .	我們知道它們是什麼 。 數十億年前 , 數十億光年之遙 , 銀河系中心的物質崩塌為超大質量的黑洞 。
and then intense magnetic fields directed some of the energy of that gravitational collapse . and some of the matter , back out in the form of tremendous jets which illuminated lobes with the brilliance of i think it's a trillion suns .	然後強烈的磁場引導了一些重力崩潰的能量 。 其中一些是以巨大的噴射機形式反映出來的 , 我認為它是一兆個太陽 。
now , the physics of the human brain could hardly be more unlike the physics of such a jet .	人類大腦的物理學幾乎不會跟噴射機的物理不一樣 。
we couldn't survive for an instant in it . language breaks down when trying to describe what it would be like in one of those jets .	我們無法立即存活下來 。 語言試圖描述其中一波噴射機的樣子 。
it would be a bit like experiencing a supernova explosion , but at pointblank range and for millions of years at a time .	這有點像在經歷超級新星爆炸 , 但在某個時間點 , 以及數百萬年 。
and yet , that jet happened in precisely such a way that billions of years later , on the other side of the universe , some bit of chemical scum could accurately describe , and model , and predict , and explain , above all there's your reference what was happening there , in reality .	然而 , 那個噴射機的確發生在數十億年後 , 在宇宙的另一邊 , 有些化學氣體可以準確地描述、模型 , 並預測 , 最重要的是你所參考的物質 , 在現實中發生了什麼事 。
the one physical system , the brain , contains an accurate working model of the other the quasar .	一個物理系統 , 一個大腦 , 有一個精確的運作模式 , 一個相對的夸薩 。
not just a superficial image of it , though it contains that as well , but an explanatory model , embodying the same mathematical relationships and the same causal structure .	不僅僅是它的膚淺形象 , 雖然它也包含了這個解釋模型 , 也包含了相同的數學關係 , 以及相同的因果結構 。
now that is knowledge . and if that weren't amazing enough , the faithfulness with which the one structure resembles the other is increasing with time . that is the growth of knowledge .	這就是知識 。 如果這還不夠精彩 , 另一種結構的信仰是隨著時間增加而增加 。 那就是知識的成長 。
so , the laws of physics have this special property .	所以 , 物理定律有特殊的特性 。
that physical objects , as unlike each other as they could possibly be , can nevertheless embody the same mathematical and causal structure and to do it more and more so over time .	這種實體物體 , 和它們可能的相對不一樣 , 不論如何體現相同的數學和因果結構 , 隨著時間不斷地進行 。
so we are a chemical scum that is different . this chemical scum has universality .	所以 , 我們是不同的化學氣體 。 這種化學氣體具有普遍性 。
its structure contains , with everincreasing precision , the structure of everything . this place , and not other places in the universe , is a hub which contains within itself the structural and causal essence of the whole of the rest of physical reality . and so , far from being insignificant , the fact that the laws of physics allow this , or even mandate that this can happen , is one of the most important things about the physical world .	它的結構包含著不斷增加的精準度 , 所有事物的結構 。 這個地方 , 而不是宇宙中的其他地方 , 一個中心本身包含了整個物理現實的結構和因果的本質 。 到目前為止 , 還忽略了物理定律 , 甚至這個定律能實現 , 是物理世界中最重要的事情之一 。
now how does the solar system and our environment , in the form of us acquire this special relationship with the rest of the universe ?	那麼 , 太陽系和環境的形式 , 在我們與宇宙其他地方的關係中 , 太陽系和我們的環境是什麼樣子 ?
well , one thing that's true about stephen hawking's remark i mean , it is true , but it's the wrong emphasis . one thing that's true about it is that it doesn't do it with any special physics . there's no special dispensation , no miracles involved . it does it simply with three things that we have here in abundance .	史蒂芬•霍金的remark是真的 , 但這是錯的 , 但它是錯誤的強調 。 一件事是 , 它沒有用任何特殊的物理 。 沒有特殊的干擾 , 沒有奇蹟涉及 。 它只用了我們在場的三件事情 。
one of them is matter , because the growth of knowledge is a form of information processing . information processing is computation , computation requires a computer there's no known way of making a computer without matter .	其中一個是重要的 , 因為知識的成長是一種資訊處理的形式 。 資訊處理是計算 , 計算需要一台電腦 , 不需要知道製造電腦的方式 。
we also need energy to make the computer , and most important , to make the media in effect onto which we record the knowledge that we discover .	我們也需要精力來製造電腦 , 最重要的是 , 讓媒體對我們發現的知識產生影響 。
and then thirdly , less tangible , but just as essential for the openended creation of knowledge , of explanations , is evidence .	第三點 , 比較不具體 , 但對開放式的知識、解釋而言 , 很重要的是證據 。
now , our environment is inundated with evidence .	現在 , 我們的環境受到證據的影響 。
we happen to get round to testing , let's say , newton's law of gravity about 300 years ago .	比方說 , 我們剛好接受測試 , 大約三百年前牛頓的重力定律 。
but the evidence that we used to do that was falling down on every square meter of the earth for billions of years before that , and will continue to fall on for billions of years afterwards . and the same is true for all the other sciences .	但我們過去所做的證據是 , 地球每平方米數十億年後 , 會持續下降數十億年 , 其他科學也是如此 。
as far as we know , evidence to discover the most fundamental truths of all the sciences is here just for the taking on our planet .	據我們所知 , 發現所有科學中最基本的真理 , 只是為了我們的地球而存在 。
our location is saturated with evidence , and also with matter and energy .	我們的地點充滿了證據 , 也充滿了物質和能量 。
out in intergalactic space , those three prerequisites for the openended creation of knowledge are at their lowest possible supply .	在星系間的空間中 , 這三個前提是為了開放式的知識創造 , 最低的可能供應量 。
as i said , it's empty ; it's cold ; and it's dark out there . or is it ?	正如我說的 , 它是空的 , 它是冷的 , 它是暗的 。 還是 ?
now actually , that's just another parochial misconception .	事實上 , 這只是另一個狹隘的誤解 。
because imagine a cube out there in intergalactic space , the same size as our home , the solar system . now that cube is very empty by human standards , but that still means that it contains over a million tons of matter .	想像一下 , 在星系間的空間中有一個立方體 , 和我們家一樣大 , 太陽系 。 現在這個立方體是以人類標準來看是空的 , 但仍然意味著它含有超過一百萬噸的物質 。
and a million tons is enough to make , say , a selfcontained space station , on which there's a colony of scientists that are devoted to creating an openended stream of knowledge , and so on .	例如 , 一百萬噸足以製造出一個自制的太空站 , 科學家們致力於創造一個開放式的知識流 , 諸如此類 。
now , it's way beyond present technology to even gather the hydrogen from intergalactic space and form it into other elements and so on .	除了現代科技之外 , 還能收集來自星系間空間的氫氣 , 將之形成其他元素等等 。
but the thing is , in a comprehensible universe , if something isn't forbidden by the laws of physics , then what could possibly prevent us from doing it , other than knowing how ?	但 , 重點是 , 在一個完全可理解的宇宙中 , 如果某樣東西不被物理定律禁止 , 那麼 , 除了知道怎麼辦 ?
in other words , it's a matter of knowledge , not resources .	換句話說 , 這是知識的問題 , 不是資源 。
and the same well , if we could do that we'd automatically have an energy supply , because the transmutation would be a fusion reactor and evidence ?	同樣的 , 如果我們能自動提供能源 , 因為交通是核融合反應器和證據呢 ?
well , again , it's dark out there to human senses . but all you've got to do is take a telescope , even one of presentday design , look out and you'll see the same galaxies as we do from here .	嗯 , 這跟人類的感官很暗 。 但你只需要用望遠鏡 , 即使是現今的設計之一 , 向外看 , 你會看到相同的銀河系 , 就像我們從這裡看到的一樣 。
and with a more powerful telescope , you'll be able to see stars , and planets .	有了更強大的望遠鏡 , 你可以看見恆星和行星 。
in those galaxies , you'll be able to do astrophysics , and learn the laws of physics .	在那些星系中 , 你可以做天體物理學 , 學習物理定律 。
and locally there you could build particle accelerators , and learn elementary particle physics , and chemistry , and so on .	當地可以製造粒子加速器 , 學習基本粒子物理 , 化學等等 。
probably the hardest science to do would be biology field trips because it would take several hundred million years to get to the nearest lifebearing planet and back .	可能是生物學領域之旅 , 最難的科學可能是生物學領域的旅程 , 因為要花數億年才能到達最近的生命星球 , 回到最近的地球上 。
but i have to tell you and sorry , richard but i never did like biology field trips much , and i think we can just about make do with one every few hundred million years .	但我必須告訴各位 , 抱歉 , 理查 , 但我從來不喜歡生物學實地旅程 , 我認為我們可以每隔幾億年就完成一次 。
so in fact , intergalactic space does contain all the prerequisites for the openended creation of knowledge . any such cube , anywhere in the universe , could become the same kind of hub that we are , if the knowledge of how to do so were present there .	所以事實上 , 星系間空間的確包含了開放式知識的所有前兆 。 任何這樣的立方體 , 都可以成為我們所處的同類空間 , 如果該怎麼做的話 。
so we're not in a uniquely hospitable place .	所以 , 我們不是在一個獨特的友善地方 。
if intergalactic space is capable of creating an openended stream of explanations , then so is almost every other environment . so is the earth . so is a polluted earth .	如果星系空間有能力創造出一個開放式的解釋 , 那麼幾乎是所有其他的環境 。 地球也是污染的地球 。
and the limiting factor , there and here , is not resources , because they're plentiful , but knowledge , which is scarce .	而限制因素 , 在這裡 , 不是資源 , 因為它們很豐富 , 但知識很稀少 。
now this cosmic knowledgebased view may and i think ought to make us feel very special . but it should also make us feel vulnerable , because it means that without the specific knowledge that's needed to survive the ongoing challenges of the universe , we won't survive them .	這種以宇宙為基礎的知識觀點 , 我認為應該讓我們感覺很特別 。 但這也讓我們感覺很脆弱 , 因為這意味著 , 若沒有必要的特定知識 , 我們就無法存活宇宙的挑戰 , 我們就不會存活下來 。
all it takes is for a supernova to go off a few light years away , and we'll all be dead !	超新星只需要幾年後才會消失 , 我們就會死掉 !
martin rees has recently written a book about our vulnerability to all sorts of things , from astrophysics , to scientific experiments gone wrong , and most importantly to terrorism with weapons of mass destruction .	馬丁•雷斯最近寫了一本關於我們對各種事物的脆弱性 , 從天體物理到科學實驗都出錯了 , 最重要的是用大規模毀滅性的武器來恐怖主義 。
and he thinks that civilization has only a 50 percent chance of surviving this century .	他認為 , 文明只有50%的存活率 。
i think he's going to talk about that later in the conference .	我想他稍後會談到這點 。
now i don't think that probability is the right category to discuss this issue in .	我不認為機率是正確的類別來討論這個問題 。
but i do agree with him about this . we can survive , and we can fail to survive .	但我同意他這件事 , 我們可以生存下來 , 我們也無法生存 。
but it depends not on chance , but on whether we create the relevant knowledge in time .	但它不取決於機率 , 而是我們是否在時間內創造出相關的知識 。
the danger is not at all unprecedented . species go extinct all the time .	危險不是史無前例的物種會隨時都滅絕
civilizations end . the overwhelming majority of all species and all civilizations that have ever existed are now history .	文明終止了 。 絕大多數的物種和所有現存的文明都是歷史 。
and if we want to be the exception to that , then logically our only hope is to make use of the one feature that distinguishes our species , and our civilization , from all the others namely , our special relationship with the laws of physics , our ability to create new explanations , new knowledge to be a hub of existence .	如果我們想成為例外 , 那麼邏輯上我們唯一的希望就是利用分辨人類和文明的特徵 , 和其他物種的特徵 , 我們和物理定律的特殊關係 , 我們創造新的解釋 , 新的知識是存在的樞紐 。
so let me now apply this to a current controversy , not because i want to advocate any particular solution , but just to illustrate the kind of thing i mean .	所以 , 讓我把這個應用到目前的爭議之上 , 不是因為我想要倡導任何特定的解決方案 , 只是說明我的意思 。
and the controversy is global warming .	爭議是全球暖化 。
now , i'm a physicist , but i'm not the right kind of physicist . in regard to global warming , i'm just a layman . and the rational thing for a layman to do is to take seriously the prevailing scientific theory . and according to that theory , it's already too late to avoid a disaster .	我是物理學家 , 但我不是正確的物理學家 。 在全球暖化方面 , 我只是個拉曼人 。 而一個拉曼人的理由是認真看待科學理論 。 根據這個理論 , 我已經太晚了 。
because if it's true that our best option at the moment is to prevent co2 emissions with something like the kyoto protocol , with its constraints on economic activity and its enormous cost of hundreds of billions of dollars or whatever it is , then that is already a disaster by any reasonable measure .	因為如果我們目前最好的選項就是阻止二氧化碳的排放 , 例如京都協定 , 它對於經濟活動的限制以及它的巨大成本 , 數百億美金或其它的代價 , 那就已經是某種合理的衡量了 。
and the actions that are advocated are not even purported to solve the problem , merely to postpone it by a little . so it's already too late to avoid it , and it probably has been too late to avoid it ever since before anyone realized the danger .	而那些被倡導的行動 , 甚至沒有被迫去解決這個問題 , 僅僅僅只是稍微退一步 。 所以它已經太遲了 , 無法避免它 , 可能已經太遲了 , 因為任何人都意識到危險之前 , 它可能已經太遲了 。
it was probably already too late in the 1970s , when the best available scientific theory was telling us that industrial emissions were about to precipitate a new ice age in which billions would die .	在1970年代 , 可能已經太遲了 , 當最好的科學理論告訴我們 , 工業排放即將降低數十億人死亡的新年齡 。
now the lesson of that seems clear to me , and i don't know why it isn't informing public debate .	這件事的教訓對我來說似乎很清楚 , 我不知道為何它沒有公眾辯論 。
it is that we can't always know . when we know of an impending disaster , and how to solve it at a cost less than the cost of the disaster itself , then there's not going to be much argument , really .	就是說 , 我們永遠不知道 。 當我們知道即將發生的災難 , 以及如何解決它的成本低於災難本身的成本 , 真的沒有太多的爭論 。
but no precautions , and no precautionary principle , can avoid problems that we do not yet foresee .	但沒有預防措施 , 也沒有預防措施 , 可以避免我們尚未預料到的問題 。
hence , we need a stance of problemfixing , not just problemavoidance .	因此 , 我們需要一步解決問題 , 而不只是有問題 。
and it's true that an ounce of prevention equals a pound of cure , but that's only if we know what to prevent .	沒錯 , 一盎司的預防等於一磅的療法 , 但只有在我們知道要預防什麼 。
if you've been punched on the nose , then the science of medicine does not consist of teaching you how to avoid punches .	如果你被打到鼻子上 , 那麼醫學的科學不會教導你如何避免打音 。
if medical science stopped seeking cures and concentrated on prevention only , then it would achieve very little of either .	如果醫學不再尋求解藥 , 只專注在預防上 , 那它也不會達到任何效果 。
the world is buzzing at the moment with plans to force reductions in gas emissions at all costs .	目前世界正在忙著打擊計劃 , 計畫要用所有成本來強制減少氣體排放 。
it ought to be buzzing with plans to reduce the temperature , and with plans to live at the higher temperature and not at all costs , but efficiently and cheaply . and some such plans exist , things like swarms of mirrors in space to deflect the sunlight away , and encouraging aquatic organisms to eat more carbon dioxide .	它應該要和規劃降低溫度 , 計畫要在更高的溫度下生存 , 不需花費 , 而是有效率地和廉價 。 有些計劃存在 , 像是在太空中的鏡子 , 將陽光反射 , 並且鼓勵水生菌去吃更多的二氧化碳 。
at the moment , these things are fringe research .	目前 , 這些東西是fringe研究 。
they're not central to the human effort to face this problem , or problems in general .	他們並不是人類努力解決這個問題的核心 , 或一般的問題 。
and with problems that we are not aware of yet , the ability to put right not the sheer good luck of avoiding indefinitely is our only hope , not just of solving problems , but of survival .	有了我們還沒意識到的問題 , 把正確的能力 , 不是無限避免的好運 , 就是我們唯一的希望 , 不只是解決問題 , 而是生存 。
so take two stone tablets , and carve on them .	拿兩塊石板 , 雕刻它們 。
on one of them , carve: " problems are soluble . "	其中之一是雕刻: 「 問題是 「 解決的 」 。
and on the other one carve: " problems are inevitable . "	另外一個雕刻: 「 問題是不可避免的 。 」
how can a struggling country break out of poverty if it's trapped in a system of bad rules ? economist paul romer unveils a bold idea: " charter cities , " cityscale administrative zones governed by a coalition of nations .	如果它被困在一個不好規則的系統中 , 一個掙扎的國家 , 要如何打破貧窮 ? 經濟學家保羅默提出一個大膽的想法: 「 特區城市 , 城市的管理區 , 由國家的聯盟統治 。
business , culture , economics , global issues , politics	商業、經濟、全球議題、政治、政治、
paul romer's radical idea: charter cities	保羅默的激進想法是:查爾斯都市的城市 ,
take a look at this picture .	看看這張照片 。
it poses a very fascinating puzzle for us .	它為我們帶來了一個令人著迷的謎題 。
these african students are doing their homework under streetlights at the airport in the capital city because they don't have any electricity at home .	這些非洲學生在首都市的機場街燈下做功課因為他們家裡沒有電
now , i haven't met these particular students , but i've met students like them .	我還沒見過這些特別的學生 , 但我也認識過像他們這樣的學生 。
let's just pick one for example , the one in the green shirt .	舉例來說 , 綠色襯衫中的一個 。
let's give him a name , too: nelson .	給他一個名字 , 尼爾森 。
i'll bet nelson has a cellphone .	我打賭nelson有手機 。
so here is the puzzle .	這就是謎題 。
why is it that nelson has access to a cuttingedge technology , like the cellphone , but doesn't have access to a 100yearold technology for generating electric light in the home ?	為什麼尼爾森可以使用尖端科技 , 像手機 , 但無法取得一百歲的科技 , 讓家裡產生電燈 ?
now , in a word , the answer is " rules . "	換言之 , 答案是 「 規則 」 。
bad rules can prevent the kind of winwin solution that's available when people can bring new technologies in and make them available to someone like nelson .	不好的規則可以預防雙贏的解決方案 , 當人們能把新技術帶到像尼爾森這樣的人身上 , 讓它們能被使用 。
what kinds of rules ?	什麼樣的規則 ?
the electric company in this nation operates under a rule , which says that it has to sell electricity at a very low , subsidized price in fact , a price that is so low it loses money on every unit that it sells .	這個國家的電力公司在一個規則下運作 , 據說它必須以非常低、補貼的價格 , 事實上 , 價格很低 , 價格低 , 價格低到每賣單位 。
so it has neither the resources , nor the incentives , to hook up many other users .	所以 , 它沒有資源 , 也沒有獎勵 , 來連結許多其他使用者 。
the president wanted to change this rule .	總統想要改變這個規則 。
he's seen that it's possible to have a different set of rules , rules where businesses earn a small profit , so they have an incentive to sign up more customers .	他看到 , 有不同的規則 , 有不同的規則 , 企業賺的小利潤是可能的 , 所以他們有動機去簽更多顧客 。
that's the kind of rules that the cellphone company that nelson purchases his telephony from operates under .	這類規則就是尼爾森購買的手機公司 。
the president has seen how those rules worked well .	總統看過這些規則如何運作 。
so he tried to change the rules for pricing on electricity , but ran into a firestorm of protest from businesses and consumers who wanted to preserve the existing subsidized rates .	所以他試著改變對電價價格的規則 , 但跑到商業和消費者的消防風暴中 , 他們想要保存現有的補貼率 。
so he was stuck with rules that prevented him from letting the winwin solution help his country .	所以他被困住的規則 , 阻止他讓雙贏解決方案來協助他的國家 。
and nelson is stuck studying under the streetlights .	尼爾森被困在街燈下學習 。
the real challenge then , is to try to figure out how we can change rules .	真正的挑戰是試著找出我們要如何改變規則 。
are there some rules we can develop for changing rules ?	是否有一些規則可以發展出改變規則 ?
i want to argue that there is a general abstract insight that we can make practical , which is that , if we can give more choices to people , and more choices to leaders who , in many countries , are also people .	我想主張 , 有一個普遍的抽象洞見 , 我們可以實踐 , 那就是 , 如果我們能給予人們更多選擇 , 在許多國家 , 領導者更多選擇 , 也是人 。
but , it's useful to present the opposition between these two .	但 , 這兩者之間的反對意見很有用 。
because the kind of choice you might want to give to a leader , a choice like giving the president the choice to raise prices on electricity , takes away a choice that people in the economy want .	因為你想要給予領導者的選擇 , 像給總統在電力上提高價格 , 拋棄人們想要的一個選擇 。
they want the choice to be able to continue consuming subsidized electric power .	他們想要選擇繼續消費補貼電力 。
so if you give just to one side or the other , you'll have tension or friction .	所以如果你只給一邊或另一邊 , 就會有張力或摩擦力 。
but if we can find ways to give more choices to both , that will give us a set of rules for changing rules that get us out of traps .	但如果我們能找到能給予更多選擇的方法 , 那就能給我們一套改變規則 , 讓我們擺脫陷阱的規則 。
now , nelson also has access to the internet .	尼爾森也能上網 。
and he says that if you want to see the damaging effects of rules , the ways that rules can keep people in the dark , look at the pictures from nasa of the earth at night .	他說 , 如果你想看到規則損壞的效應 , 規則可以讓人們留在黑暗中 , 看看美國太空總署的照片 。
in particular check out asia .	特別是亞洲 。
if you zoom in here , you can see north korea , in outline here , which is like a black hole compared to its neighbors .	如果你放大這裡 , 你可以看到北韓 , 在線上這裡 , 和鄰居相比 , 黑洞就像是黑洞 。
now , you won't be surprised to learn that the rules in north korea keep people there in the dark .	現在 , 你不會驚訝地發現北韓的規則會讓人們處在黑暗中 。
but it is important to recognize that north korea and south korea started out with identical sets of rules in both the sense of laws and regulations , but also in the deeper senses of understandings , norms , culture , values and beliefs .	但 , 很重要的是 , 要意識到北韓和南韓都起源於同一類的規則 , 以法律和法規的角度 , 同時 , 更深層的來說 , 了解、規範、文化、價值觀和信仰 。
when they separated , they made choices that led to very divergent paths for their sets of rules .	當他們分開時 , 他們會做出選擇 , 導致他們規則非常不同的路徑 。
so we can change we as humans can change the rules that we use to interact with each other , for better , or for worse .	我們人類可以改變我們人類可以改變我們使用的規則 , 讓彼此互動 , 更好 , 更糟糕 。
now let's look at another region , the caribbean .	咱們來看看另一個加勒比海地區 。
zoom in on haiti , in outline here .	放大在海地 , 這裡的線上 。
haiti is also dark , compared to its neighbor here , the dominican republic , which has about the same number of residents .	海地也是黑暗的 , 比起這裡的鄰居 , 多明尼加共和國 , 居民數量差不多 。
both of these countries are dark compared to puerto rico , which has half as many residents as either haiti or the dominican republic .	相較於波多黎各的兩個國家 , 兩國的居民比如海地或多明尼加共和國 。
what haiti warns us is that rules can be bad because governments are weak .	海地警告我們 , 規則可能會很糟 , 因為政府很弱 。
it's not just that the rules are bad because the government is too strong and oppressive , as in north korea .	不單是因為政府太強 , 壓迫 , 就像北韓一樣 。
so that if we want to create environments with good rules , we can't just tear down .	所以如果我們想要創造有好的規則的環境 , 我們就不能只撕下它 。
we've got to find ways to build up , as well .	我們也必須找到方法來建構 。
now , china dramatically demonstrates both the potential and the challenges of working with rules .	如今 , 中國戲劇性地展示了與規則相關的潛力和挑戰 。
back in the beginning of the data presented in this chart , china was the world's hightechnology leader .	回到這張圖的開端 , 中國是世界上的高科技領導者 。
chinese had pioneered technologies like steel , printing , gunpowder .	中國有先驅的技術 , 像是鋼、列印、槍枝 。
but the chinese never adopted , at least in that period , effective rules for encouraging the spread of those ideas a profit motive that could have encouraged the spread .	但中國人從未採用 , 至少在這段期間 , 有效的規則 , 鼓勵這些想法的傳播 , 一個利潤的動機 , 可以鼓勵傳播 。
and they soon adopted rules which slowed down innovation and cut china off from the rest of the world .	他們很快就採用了放慢創新的規則 , 把中國從世界其他地方砍掉 。
so as other countries in the world innovated , in the sense both of developing newer technologies , but also developing newer rules , the chinese were cut off from those advances .	所以 , 隨著世界上其他國家的創新 , 在發展新科技的意義上 , 也發展出新的規則 , 中國人從這些進步中被切斷 。
income there stayed stagnant , as it zoomed ahead in the rest of the world .	收入在那兒停滯不前 , 因為它放大到世界其他地方 。
this next chart looks at more recent data .	下一張圖表是比較近期的數據 。
it plots income , average income in china as a percentage of average income in the united states .	它描繪收入、中國的平均收入佔美國平均收入的比例
in the '50s and '60s you can see that it was hovering at about three percent .	在50年代和60年代 , 你可以看到大約佔了百分之三 。
but then in the late '70s something changed .	但在70年代末期 , 情況改變了 。
growth took off in china . the chinese started catching up very quickly with the united states .	經濟增長在中國起飛 , 中國開始迅速地趕上美國
if you go back to the map at night , you can get a clue to the process that lead to the dramatic change in rules in china .	如果你晚上回到地圖 , 就會得到一個線索 , 導致中國的規則大幅改變 。
the brightest spot in china , which you can see on the edge of the outline here , is hong kong .	中國最明亮的區域 , 各位可以看到 , 線上的邊緣 , 是香港 。
hong kong was a small bit of china that , for most of the 20th century , operated under a very different set of rules than the rest of mainland china rules that were copied from working market economies of the time , and administered by the british .	香港是中國的一小部分 , 在二十世紀大部分 , 採用的規則是非常不同的 , 比起當時工作市場經濟的其他國家 , 中國的主要規則 , 中國的管理者是英國的 。
in the 1950s , hong kong was a place where millions of people could go , from the mainland , to start in jobs like sewing shirts , making toys .	在1950年代 , 香港是一個讓數百萬人從大陸開始的工作 , 像是縫襯衫 , 玩具 。
but , to get on a process of increasing income , increasing skills led to very rapid growth there .	但 , 為了增加收入的過程 , 越來越多技能導致在那裡成長很快 。
hong kong was also the model which leaders like deng xiaoping could copy , when they decided to move all of the mainland towards the market model .	香港也是個典型 , 領導人喜歡香港的領導人可以複製 , 當他們決定把整個大陸都搬到市場模式上 。
but deng xiaoping instinctively understood the importance of offering choices to his people .	但蒙古直覺地了解到提供他選擇的重要性 。
so instead of forcing everyone in china to shift immediately to the market model , they proceeded by creating some special zones that could do , in a sense , what britain did: make the opportunity to go work with the market rules available to the people who wanted to opt in there .	所以 , 與其強迫所有中國人立即轉移到市場模式 , 他們採用的是創造一些特殊的區塊 , 可以做的事 , 也就是英國所做的:讓機會和市場規則合作 , 讓想要選擇的人可以使用 。
so they created four special economic zones around hong kong: zones where chinese could come and work , and cities grew up very rapidly there ; also zones where foreign firms could come in and make things .	所以 , 他們創造了四個特別的經濟區 , 包圍香港:中國可以來工作的地方 , 城市在很快地長大 ; 還有外國公司可以進來做點什麼 。
one of the zones next to hong kong has a city called shenzhen .	香港旁邊的一個區域有個叫做 「 深圳 」 的城市 。
in that city there is a taiwanese firm that made the iphone that many of you have , and they made it with labor from chinese who moved there to shenzhen .	在那個城市裡 , 有一個台灣公司 , 打造了座很多人的iphone , 他們把它做成了從中國人搬到深圳的勞工 。
so after the four special zones , there were 14 coastal cites that were open in the same sense , and eventually demonstrated successes in these places that people could opt in to , that they flocked to because of the advantages they offered .	所以在四個特別的區域之後 , 有十四個海岸公園在同一方面開放 , 最終在這些地方證明了成功 , 人們可以選擇的成功 , 因爲他們提供的好處 。
demonstrated successes there led to a consensus for a move toward the market model for the entire economy .	在那裡證明成功導致了一致的共識 , 朝向整個經濟的市場模式前進 。
now the chinese example shows us several points .	中國的例子讓我們看到幾個點 。
one is: preserve choices for people .	第一:保存人們的選擇 。
two: operate on the right scale .	第二:在正確的尺度上運作 。
if you try to change the rules in a village , you could do that , but a village would be too small to get the kinds of benefits you can get if you have millions of people all working under good rules .	如果你試著改變村落的規則 , 你就能做到 , 但村落太小 , 無法得到你所能得到的利益 , 如果你有數百萬人在好的規則下工作 。
on the other hand , the nation is too big .	另一方面 , 國家太大了 。
if you try to change the rules in the nation , you can't give some people a chance to hold back , see how things turn out , and let others zoom ahead and try the new rules .	如果你試著改變這個國家的規則 , 你就不能給一些人回報 , 看看結果如何 , 讓其他人放大 , 嘗試新的規則 。
but cities give you this opportunity to create new places , with new rules that people can opt in to .	但城市給你機會 , 創造出新的地方 , 讓人們可以選擇的新規則 。
and they're large enough to get all of the benefits that we can have when millions of us work together under good rules .	它們夠大 , 足以取得我們所能有的所有利益 , 只要有數百萬人在良好的規則下合作 。
so the proposal is that we conceive of something called a charter city .	所以 , 提議是我們構想了一種叫做 「 特區城市 」 的東西 。
we start with a charter that specifies all the rules required to attract the people who we'll need to build the city .	我們先從一個特定規則開始 , 來吸引我們需要建造城市的人 。
we'll need to attract the investors who will build out the infrastructure the power system , the roads , the port , the airport , the buildings .	我們需要吸引投資者來吸引建立基礎設施的投資者──系統、道路、港口、機場、大樓 。
you'll need to attract firms , who will come hire the people who move there first .	你需要吸引公司 , 先僱用搬到那裡的人 。
and you'll need to attract families , the residents who will come and live there permanently , raise their children , get an education for their children , and get their first job .	你需要吸引家庭 , 在那裡住在那裡 , 在那裡 , 養育孩子 , 為他們的孩子接受教育 , 並得到他們的第一份工作 。
with that charter , people will move there .	有了那篇文章 , 人們會搬到那裡 。
the city can be built .	城市可以被建造出來 。
and we can scale this model .	我們可以擴大這個模型 。
we can go do it over and over again .	我們可以一而再再而三地完成它 。
to make it work , we need good rules . we've already discussed that .	要成功 , 我們需要好的規則 。 我們已經討論過了 。
those are captured in the charter .	那些在章節中被捕捉 。
we also need the choices for people .	我們也需要人們的選擇 。
that's really built into the model if we allow for the possibility of building cities on uninhabited land .	這真的是建立在模型中 , 如果我們能在無人居住的土地上建造城市的可能性 。
you start from uninhabited territory .	你從未居住的領域開始 。
people can come live under the new charter , but no one is forced to live under it .	人們可以在新的章節下生存 , 但沒有人被迫活在其中 。
the final thing we need are choices for leaders .	最後我們需要的是領導者的選擇 。
and , to achieve the kind of choices we want for leaders we need to allow for the potential for partnerships between nations: cases where nations work together , in effect , de facto , the way china and britain worked together to build , first a little enclave of the market model , and then scale it throughout china .	為了達成我們想要的領導者的選擇 , 我們需要讓國家之間合作的可能性:實情 , 德魯 , 中國和英國一起合作 , 首先建立一個小型的市場模式 , 然後擴展到整個中國 。
in a sense , britain , inadvertently , through its actions in hong kong , did more to reduce world poverty than all the aid programs that we've undertaken in the last century .	在某種意義上 , 英國 , 無意間 , 透過香港的行動 , 減少了世界的貧窮 , 比上個世紀我們所經歷的所有援助計畫還要多 。
so if we allow for these kind of partnerships to replicate this again , we can get those kinds of benefits scaled throughout the world .	所以如果我們允許這種合作關係再次複製這個現象 , 我們就能讓這種好處遍及世界各地 。
in some cases this will involve a delegation of responsibility , a delegation of control from one country to another to take over certain kinds of administrative responsibilities .	在某些情況下 , 這會涉及到負責任的程度 , 從一個國家到另一個國家的授權 , 來克服某些類型的行政責任 。
now , when i say that , some of you are starting to think , " well , is this just bringing back colonialism ? "	當我這麼說的時候 , 有些人開始想: 「 嗯 , 這只是帶回殖民主義嗎 ? 」
it's not . but it's important to recognize that the kind of emotions that come up when we start to think about these things , can get in the way , can make us pull back , can shut down our ability , and our interest in trying to explore new ideas .	這不是 。 但重要的是要意識到當我們開始思考這些事情時 , 會出現的那種情緒 , 可以讓我們退一步 , 可以關閉我們的能力 , 以及我們想要探索新點子的興趣 。
why is this not like colonialism ?	為什麼不像殖民主義 ?
the thing that was bad about colonialism , and the thing which is residually bad in some of our aid programs , is that it involved elements of coercion and condescension .	殖民主義是不好的 , 而在我們的援助計畫中 , 則是它涉及了強制和保險的元素 。
this model is all about choices , both for leaders and for the people who will live in these new places .	這個模式是關於選擇 , 無論是領導者 , 還是對住在這些新地方的人 。
and , choice is the antidote to coercion and condescension .	選擇是對合作和保險的解藥 。
so let's talk about how this could play out in practice .	咱們來談談這如何實踐 。
let's take a particular leader , raul castro , who is the leader of cuba .	咱們來看看一位特別的領導人 , raulcastro , 他是古巴的領導人 。
it must have occurred to castro that he has the chance to do for cuba what deng xiaoping did for china , but he doesn't have a hong kong there on the island in cuba .	它一定會發生在卡斯楚 , 他有機會為古巴做些什麼 , 但他沒有古巴島的香港 。
he does , though , have a little bit of light down in the south that has a very special status .	不過 , 他的確在南方有一點點光線 , 上面有很特別的地位 。
there is a zone there , around guantanamo bay , where a treaty gives the united states administrative responsibility for a piece of land that's about twice the size of manhattan .	那裡有一塊區域 , 位在古曼納摩灣附近 , 在那裡 , 條約讓美國負責一塊土地的責任 , 大約是曼哈頓的兩倍 。
castro goes to the prime minister of canada and says , " look , the yankees have a terrible pr problem .	卡斯楚去加拿大總理說: 「 看 , 伊恩克有個可怕的pr問題 。
they want to get out .	他們想要出去 。
why don't you , canada , take over ?	為什麼不 , 加拿大 , 接管呢 ?
build run a special administrative zone .	建造一座特別的行政區 。
allow a new city to be built up there .	允許新城市在上面建造 。
allow many people to come in .	讓許多人進來 。
let us have a hong kong nearby .	讓我們附近有個香港 。
some of my citizens will move into that city as well .	我的公民也會搬到那個城市 。
others will hold back . but this will be the gateway that will connect the modern economy and the modern world to my country . "	其他人會支持 。 但這將會是通往我國家現代經濟和現代世界的通道 。 」
now , where else might this model be tried ?	現在 , 其他的模型還在哪裡試過 ?
well , africa . i've talked with leaders in africa .	非洲 。 我和非洲的領導人談過 。
many of them totally get the notion of a special zone that people can opt into as a rule .	許多人完全得到一個特殊區塊的概念 , 讓人們可以當作規則 。
it's a rule for changing rules .	它是改變規則的規則 。
it's a way to create new rules , and let people optin without coercion , and the opposition that coercion can force .	它是一種創造新規則的方式 , 讓人們不需要強迫 , 而合作的反對 。
they also totally get the idea that in some instances they can make more credible promises to longterm investors the kind of investors who will come build the port , build the roads , in a new city they can make more credible promises if they do it along with a partner nation .	他們也完全了解到 , 在某些情況下 , 他們可以對長期投資者做出更有信心的承諾 , 來建立港口的投資者 , 建立道路 , 在一個新的城市 , 他們可以做出更有信心的承諾 , 如果他們和一個夥伴國家合作的話 。
perhaps even in some arrangement that's a little bit like an escrow account , where you put land in the escrow account and the partner nation takes responsibility for it .	甚至在一些安排中 , 有點像escrow帳戶 , 把土地放在escrow帳戶中 , 合作夥伴們負責為此負責 。
there is also lots of land in africa where new cities could be built .	非洲有很多土地 , 在那裡 , 新的城市可以建造 。
this is a picture i took when i was flying along the coast .	這是我在海岸飛行時拍的照片 。
there are immense stretches of land like this land where hundreds of millions of people could live .	有很大的土地 , 像這樣的土地 , 有數億人可以住在那裡 。
now , if we generalize this and think about not just one or two charter cites , but dozens cities that will help create places for the many hundreds of millions , perhaps billions of people who will move to cities in the coming century is there enough land for them ?	現在 , 如果我們把這個概念整合起來 , 想想看 , 不僅僅是一兩間慈善團體 , 還有數十個城市 , 能協助為數億人創造出地方 , 也許數十億人在未來世紀會搬到城市 , 為他們帶來足夠的土地 ?
well , throughout the world , if we look at the lights at night , the one thing that's misleading is that , visually , it looks like most of the world is already built out .	嗯 , 在世界各地 , 如果我們晚上看燈光 , 誤導的一件事是 , 視覺上 , 它似乎是世界上大部分人已經建構出來了 。
so let me show you why that's wrong .	所以 , 讓我告訴各位 , 為什麼這才是錯的 。
take this representation of all of the land .	以這所有土地的代表為例 。
turn it into a square that stands for all the arable land on earth .	把它轉化成一個正方形 , 代表著地球上所有可耕地 。
and let these dots represent the land that's already taken up by the cities that three billion people now live in .	讓這些點代表已被三十億人口居住的城市所佔的土地 。
if you move the dots down to the bottom of the rectangle you can see that the cities for the existing three billion urban residents take up only three percent of the arable land on earth .	如果你把點移到長方形底部 , 你可以看到 , 現有的都市居民佔地球上可耕地的百分之三 。
so if we wanted to build cities for another billion people , they would be dots like this .	所以如果我們想為數十億人建造城市 , 他們會像這樣做 。
we'd go from three percent of the arable land , to four percent .	我們會從百分之三的可耕地 , 到百分之四 。
we'd dramatically reduce the human footprint on earth by building more cities that people can move to .	我們會大大減少地球上人類的足跡 , 藉由建造更多人能搬到的城市 。
and if these are cities governed by good rules , they can be cities where people are safe from crime , safe from disease and bad sanitation , where people have a chance to get a job .	如果這些城市被良好的規則管理 , 他們可以是城市 , 在那裡 , 人民是安全的 , 不受犯罪、疾病和不良的公共衛生 , 在那裡 , 人們有機會找到工作 。
they can get basic utilities like electricity .	他們可以取得基本的電力 。
their kids can get an education .	他們的孩子可以接受教育 。
so what will it take to get started building the first charter cities , scaling this so we build many more ?	所以 , 要開始建造第一座charter城市 , 擴展它 , 才能建造更多 ?
it would help to have a manual .	要有手冊是有幫助的 。
what university professors could do is write some details that might go into this manual .	大學教授可以做的是寫一些細節 , 可以進入這本手冊 。
you wouldn't want to let us run the cities , go out and design them .	你不會想讓我們跑出城市 , 走出去設計它們 。
you wouldn't let academics out in the wild .	你不會讓學術界出現在野外 。
but , you could set us to work thinking about questions like , suppose it isn't just canada that does the deal with raul castro .	但 , 你可以讓我們去思考一些問題 , 例如 , 假設它不只是加拿大 , 處理拉爾卡斯楚的問題 。
perhaps brazil comes in as a participant , and spain as well . and perhaps cuba wants to be one of the partners in a fourway joint venture .	也許巴西是受試者 , 西班牙也是 。 也許古巴想要成為四個關節冒險的夥伴之一 。
how would we write the treaty to do that ?	我們要如何寫條約 ?
there is less precedent for that , but that could easily be worked out .	沒有那麼多的先例 , 但這很容易被解決 。
how would we finance this ?	我們要如何資助這點 ?
turns out singapore and hong kong are cities that made huge gains on the value of the land that they owned when they got started .	結果發現 , 新加坡和香港是城市 , 在他們開始時所擁有的土地價值非常大 。
you could use the gains on the value of the land to pay for things like the police , the courts , but the school system and the health care system too , which make this a more attractive place to live , makes this a place where people have higher incomes which , incidentally , makes the land more valuable .	你可以利用土地的價值來支付警察、法院等 , 但學校系統和醫療系統 , 讓這個地方更吸引人居住 , 讓人們有更高的收入 , 順帶一提 , 讓土地更有價值 。
so the incentives for the people helping to construct this zone and build it , and set up the basic rules , go very much in the right direction .	所以 , 那些幫忙建構這個區域的人的動機 , 建立了基本的規則 , 走向正確的方向 。
so there are many other details like this .	所以 , 有很多像這樣的細節 。
how could we have buildings that are low cost and affordable for people who work in a first job , assembling something like an iphone , but make those buildings energy efficient , and make sure that they are safe , so they don't fall down in an earthquake or a hurricane .	我們要如何讓低成本、負擔得起的建築 , 讓第一份工作的人能夠組裝出像iphone一樣的東西 , 但要讓這些建築能有效率 , 確保它們是安全的 , 所以它們不會落在地震或颶風中 。
many technical details to be worked out , but those of us who are already starting to pursue these things can already tell that there is no roadblock , there's no impediment , other than a failure of imagination , that will keep us from delivering on a truly global winwin solution .	許多技術上的細節要被找出來 , 但那些已經開始追求這些事情的人 , 已經可以知道沒有障礙 , 沒有障礙 , 除了想像的失敗之外 , 這會讓我們無法實現真正的全球性的雙贏解決方案 。
let me conclude with this picture .	讓我用這張照片來總結 。
the reason we can be so well off , even though there is so many people on earth , is because of the power of ideas .	我們之所以能如此順利 , 即使地球上有這麼多人 , 是因為想法的力量 。
we can share ideas with other people , and when they discover them , they share with us .	我們可以和他人分享想法 , 當他們發現他們 , 他們和我們分享 。
it's not like scarce objects , where sharing means we each get less .	它不像稀有物品 , 分享的意義減少 。
when we share ideas we all get more .	當我們分享想法時 , 我們都會得到更多 。
when we think about ideas in that way , we usually think about technologies .	當我們用那樣的方式思考想法時 , 我們通常會想到科技 。
but there is another class of ideas: the rules that govern how we interact with each other ; rules like , let's have a tax system that supports a research university that gives away certain kinds of knowledge for free .	但還有另一類想法:管理我們如何互動的規則 ; 例如 , 咱們用稅收系統來支援一項研究大學 , 免費提供某些知識 。
let's have a system where we have ownership of land that is registered in a government office , that people can pledge as collateral .	咱們來個體制 , 在政府辦公室裡 , 我們有擁有土地的權力 , 人民可以承諾是冰封 。
if we can keep innovating on our space of rules , and particularly innovate in the sense of coming up with rules for changing rules , so we don't get stuck with bad rules , then we can keep moving progress forward and truly make the world a better place , so that people like nelson and his friends don't have to study any longer under the streetlights . thank you .	如果我們能持續創新我們的規則 , 尤其是創新在於改變規則的概念 , 所以我們不會陷入不好的規則 , 那麼我們可以繼續進步 , 讓世界變得更美好 , 像尼爾森和他的朋友不再需要在路燈下學習 。 謝謝 。
genomics pioneer craig venter takes a break from his epic roundtheworld expedition to talk about the millions of genes his team has discovered so far in its quest to map the ocean’s biodiversity .	基因學家克萊格•凡特在他史詩般的探險探險中休息了一段時間 , 來談談他的團隊發現的數百萬個基因 , 到目前為止 , 以繪製海洋生物多樣性 。
dna , biosphere , biotech , entrepreneur , genetics , invention , oceans , science , technology	dna、生物圈、生物科技、企業家、基因發明、海洋、科學、科技、科技、科技、科技、
craig venter on dna and the sea	克雷格•凡特在dna和海洋上 , 和海平面上都是 。
at the break , i was asked by several people about my comments about the aging debate .	休息時 , 幾個人問我有關老化的辯論的意見 。
and this will be my only comment on it .	這將會是我唯一的評論 。
and that is , i understand that optimists greatly outlive pessimists .	那就是 , 我了解樂觀主義者遠超過悲觀主義者 。
what i'm going to tell you about in my 18 minutes is how we're about to switch from reading the genetic code to the first stages of beginning to write the code ourselves .	在我18分鐘內 , 我要告訴各位的是 , 我們要如何轉換基因密碼 , 轉換到開始寫程式的第一階段 。
it's only 10 years ago this month when we published the first sequence of a freeliving organism , that of haemophilus influenzae .	僅僅在十年前 , 我們在這個月刊登了第一序列 , 一種自由生存的有機體 , 流感 。
that took a genome project from 13 years down to four months .	這個計畫從13年到4個月後進行了基因組計畫 。
we can now do that same genome project in the order of two to eight hours .	我們現在可以在兩到八個小時內完成同樣的基因組計畫 。
so in the last decade , a large number of genomes have been added: most human pathogens , a couple of plants , several insects and several mammals , including the human genome .	所以在過去十年 , 大量的基因組被加上了:大部分的人類病原體、幾種植物、幾種昆蟲和幾種哺乳動物 , 包括人類基因組 。
genomics at this stage of the thinking from a little over 10 years ago was , by the end of this year , we might have between three and five genomes sequenced ; it's on the order of several hundred .	在這一階段的基因組學在十年前是 , 今年底 , 我們可能有三到五個基因序列 ; 數百個基因組的序列 。
we just got a grant from the gordon and betty moore foundation to sequence 130 genomes this year , as a side project from environmental organisms .	我們剛從戈登和貝蒂摩爾基金會得到補助 , 今年我們將一百三十個基因組定序為環保有機體的副計畫 。
so the rate of reading the genetic code has changed .	所以閱讀遺傳密碼的速度已經改變了 。
but as we look , what's out there , we've barely scratched the surface on what is available on this planet .	但 , 正如我們所見 , 我們幾乎沒有抓到這個星球上可得的表面 。
most people don't realize it , because they're invisible , but microbes make up about a half of the earth's biomass , whereas all animals only make up about one onethousandth of all the biomass .	大部份人不明白 , 因為它們是看不見的 , 但微生物大約是地球一半的生物量 , 而所有的動物只佔所有生物量的一分之一 。
and maybe it's something that people in oxford don't do very often , but if you ever make it to the sea , and you swallow a mouthful of seawater , keep in mind that each milliliter has about a million bacteria and on the order of 10 million viruses .	也許是牛津人經常不會做的事 , 但如果你把它送到海裡 , 吞下一口海水 , 請記住每一毫升的海水都有大約一百萬隻細菌 , 以一千萬病毒的命令 。
less than 5 , 000 microbial species have been characterized as of two years ago , and so we decided to do something about it .	兩年前 , 只有不到5000種微生物被特徵化 , 所以我們決定做點什麼 。
and we started the sorcerer ii expedition , where we were , as with great oceanographic expeditions , trying to sample the ocean every 200 miles .	我們開始了sercer第二次探險 , 在那裡 , 我們和大型海洋探險一樣 , 試圖每200英哩的海洋樣本 。
we started in bermuda for our test project , then moved up to halifax , working down the u . s . east coast , the caribbean sea , the panama canal , through to the galapagos , then across the pacific , and we're in the process now of working our way across the indian ocean .	我們開始在百慕達做測試 , 然後搬到哈利法克斯 , 在美國東岸 , 加勒比海 , 巴拿馬峽谷 , 穿過太平洋 , 我們現在正在橫跨印度洋的路上 。
it's very tough duty ; we're doing this on a sailing vessel , in part to help excite young people about going into science .	這是非常困難的責任 , 我們在船艙上做這件事 , 有部分協助刺激年輕人進入科學領域 。
the experiments are incredibly simple .	實驗非常簡單 。
we just take seawater and we filter it , and we collect different size organisms on different filters , and then take their dna back to our lab in rockville , where we can sequence a hundred million letters of the genetic code every 24 hours .	我們只是過濾海水 , 收集不同的過濾器 , 然後把它們的dna帶回我們在洛克維爾的實驗室 , 在那裡 , 我們每24小時就能將一億個基因編碼的基因序列定序 。
and with doing this , we've made some amazing discoveries .	藉由這麼做 , 我們做出了一些驚人的發現 。
for example , it was thought that the visual pigments that are in our eyes there was only one or two organisms in the environment that had these same pigments .	舉例來說 , 人們認為我們眼中的視覺色素在環境中只有一到兩種有機體有相同的色素 。
it turns out , almost every species in the upper parts of the ocean in warm parts of the world have these same photoreceptors , and use sunlight as the source of their energy and communication .	結果發現 , 地球上所有海洋上層的物種 , 都有相同的攝影器 , 用陽光作為它們能量和溝通的來源 。
from one site , from one barrel of seawater , we discovered 1 . 3 million new genes and as many as 50 , 000 new species .	從一個網站 , 從一桶海水中 , 我們發現了130萬個新基因 , 和50000個新物種 。
we've extended this to the air now with a grant from the sloan foundation .	我們現在把這張照片延伸到空氣中 , 帶著來自斯蘭基金會的補助金 。
we're measuring how many viruses and bacteria all of us are breathing in and out every day , particularly on airplanes or closed auditoriums .	我們測量有多少病毒和細菌 , 我們每天都在呼吸中 , 特別是在飛機上 , 或關閉聽覺 。
we filter through some simple apparatuses ; we collect on the order of a billion microbes from just a day filtering on top of a building in new york city .	我們通過一些簡單的裝置過濾 ; 我們收集了十億微生物 , 來自紐約市的一棟大樓 。
and we're in the process of sequencing all that at the present time .	我們正處於定序的過程中 , 在當下 。
just on the data collection side , just where we are through the galapagos , we're finding that almost every 200 miles , we see tremendous diversity in the samples in the ocean .	僅僅在資料集中 , 透過加拉帕戈斯 , 我們發現幾乎每兩百英哩 , 我們在海洋中的樣本就看到了巨大的多樣性 。
some of these make logical sense , in terms of different temperature gradients .	有些邏輯上是合理的 , 以不同的溫度來說 。
so this is a satellite photograph based on temperatures red being warm , blue being cold and we found there's a tremendous difference between the warm water samples and the cold water samples , in terms of abundant species .	這是一張衛星照片 , 根據溫度的紅色 , 藍色的溫度 , 我們發現溫暖的水樣本和冷水樣本之間有很大的差異 。
the other thing that surprised us quite a bit is these photoreceptors detect different wavelengths of light , and we can predict that based on their amino acid sequence .	另一件讓我們吃驚的事是這些光感應器會偵測不同波長的光 , 我們可以根據它們的胺基酸序列來預測 。
and these vary tremendously from region to region .	而這些區域的區塊大幅增加 。
maybe not surprisingly , in the deep ocean , where it's mostly blue , the photoreceptors tend to see blue light .	或許不意外 , 在深海 , 那裡大部分是藍色的 , 光受器通常會看到藍光 。
when there's a lot of chlorophyll around , they see a lot of green light .	當周圍有很多葉綠素時 , 他們會看到很多綠光 。
but they vary even more , possibly moving towards infrared and ultraviolet in the extremes .	但它們可能更不同 , 在極端的紅外線和紫外線移動 。
just to try and get an assessment of what our gene repertoire was , we assembled all the data including all of ours thus far from the expedition , which represents more than half of all the gene data on the planet and it totaled around 29 million genes .	只為了評估我們的基因複製品的評估 , 我們把所有的資料組合起來 , 包括我們所有的資料 , 包括我們目前的探險 , 這代表地球上所有基因資料的一半 , 總共有2900萬個基因 。
and we tried to put these into gene families to see what these discoveries are: are we just discovering new members of known families , or are we discovering new families ?	我們試著把這些基因家庭放進基因中 , 看看這些發現是什麼:我們只是發現已知家庭的新成員 , 還是發現新的家庭 ?
and it turns out we have about 50 , 000 major gene families , but every new sample we take in the environment adds in a linear fashion to these new families .	結果發現 , 我們有大約五萬個主要的基因家庭 , 但我們所採集的每一個新樣本 , 加上線性時尚 , 給這些新家庭 。
so we're at the earliest stages of discovery about basic genes , components and life on this planet .	所以 , 我們正處於地球上最早期的發現 , 關於基本基因、元素和生命的階段 。
when we look at the socalled evolutionary tree , we're up on the upper righthand corner with the animals .	當我們看所謂的演化樹 , 我們在右上角和動物的右上角 。
of those roughly 29 million genes , we only have around 24 , 000 in our genome .	在大約兩千九百萬個基因中 , 我們的基因組只有兩萬四千個 。
and if you take all animals together , we probably share less than 30 , 000 and probably maybe a dozen or more thousand different gene families .	如果你把所有的動物集合在一起 , 我們大概有不到三萬個 , 可能有十幾個不同的基因家庭 。
i view that these genes are now not only the design components of evolution .	我覺得這些基因不僅僅是進化的設計組成 。
and we think in a genecentric view maybe going back to richard dawkins' ideas than in a genomecentric view , which are different constructs of these gene components .	我們認為在一個基因中心的觀點也許回到理查•達文斯的觀點 , 遠遠比基因組件的不同 。
synthetic dna , the ability to synthesize dna , has changed at sort of the same pace that dna sequencing has over the last decade or two , and is getting very rapid and very cheap .	合成dna , 合成dna的能力 , 在過去十年或二十年間 , dna定序的速度改變了 , 且變得非常快速、非常便宜 。
our first thought about synthetic genomics came when we sequenced the second genome back in 1995 , and that from mycoplasma genitalium .	我們首先想到合成基因組學 , 是在1995年我們定序第二組基因組時 , 這從我的生殖器中 。
and we have really nice tshirts that say , you know , " i heart my genitalium . "	我們有很棒的t恤 , 上面寫著: 「 我愛我的生殖器 。 」
this is actually just a microorganism .	這其實只是微生物 。
but it has roughly 500 genes .	但它有大約500個基因 。
haemophilus had 1 , 800 genes .	莫菲斯有1800個基因 。
and we simply asked the question , if one species needs 800 , another 500 , is there a smaller set of genes that might comprise a minimal operating system ?	我們只是問一個問題 , 如果一個物種需要800 , 另一個500種 , 是否有一組小型的基因組組成一個小型的作業系統 ?
so we started doing transposon mutagenesis .	所以 , 我們開始做交通突變 。
transposons are just small pieces of dna that randomly insert in the genetic code .	轉帳只不過是基因編碼中隨機插入的小dna 。
and if they insert in the middle of the gene , they disrupt its function .	如果它們在基因的中間插入 , 它們就會破壞它的功能 。
so we made a map of all the genes that could take transposon insertions and we called those " nonessential genes . "	所以我們做了一張圖 , 所有可以服用交通插射的基因 , 我們稱之為 「 不必要的基因 」 。
but it turns out the environment is very critical for this , and you can only define an essential or nonessential gene based on exactly what's in the environment .	但事實證明 , 環境是非常關鍵的 , 你只能根據環境的本質或不必要的基因來定義 。
we also tried to take a more directly intellectual approach with the genomes of 13 related organisms , and we tried to compare all of those , to see what they had in common .	我們也試著用比較直接的智力方法和13個相關有機體的基因組做比較 , 我們試著比較這些 , 看看它們有什麼共通點 。
and we got these overlapping circles . and we found only 173 genes common to all 13 organisms .	我們得到了這些重疊的圓圈 。 我們發現了173個基因 , 共有13種生物 。
the pool expanded a little bit if we ignored one intracellular parasite ; it expanded even more when we looked at core sets of genes of around 310 or so .	如果我們忽略一個細胞寄生蟲 , 池塘就會擴大一點 ; 當我們觀察核心基因大約是310左右 。
so we think that we can expand or contract genomes , depending on your point of view here , to maybe 300 to 400 genes from the minimal of 500 .	所以我們認為我們可以擴展或收縮基因 , 取決於你的觀點 , 到500到400個基因 。
the only way to prove these ideas was to construct an artificial chromosome with those genes in them , and we had to do this in a cassettebased fashion .	證明這些想法的唯一方法是用人造染色體組成 , 用這些基因組成 , 我們必須在基礎的時尚下進行 。
we found that synthesizing accurate dna in large pieces was extremely difficult .	我們發現在大片碎片中 , 合成的dna是非常困難的 。
ham smith and clyde hutchison , my colleagues on this , developed an exciting new method that allowed us to synthesize a 5 , 000base pair virus in only a twoweek period that was 100 percent accurate , in terms of its sequence and its biology .	漢姆•史密斯和克萊德•hutchison , 我在這方面的同事開發了一種令人振奮的新方法 , 讓我們能在兩週之內合成一組50000個鹼基對的病毒 , 大約是百分之百精確的基因序列和生物學 。
it was a quite exciting experiment when we just took the synthetic piece of dna , injected it in the bacteria and all of a sudden , that dna started driving the production of the virus particles that turned around and then killed the bacteria .	這是個相當令人振奮的實驗 , 當我們把合成的dna注射到細菌中 , 突然間 , dna開始驅動病毒粒子的生產 , 然後殺死細菌 。
this was not the first synthetic virus a polio virus had been made a year before but it was only one tenthousandth as active and it took three years to do .	這不是第一個合成病毒 , 一個小兒麻痺症病毒在一年前被製造出來的 , 但它只有一個十分之一活躍 , 且花了三年的時間 。
this is a cartoon of the structure of phi x 174 .	這是phix174的一幅卡通結構 。
this is a case where the software now builds its own hardware , and that's the notions that we have with biology .	這個軟體現在建立了自己的硬體 , 這就是我們對生物學的概念 。
people immediately jump to concerns about biological warfare , and i had recent testimony before a senate committee , and a special committee the u . s . government has set up to review this area .	人們馬上跳到關心生物戰事 , 我在參議會委員會前有了近期的證詞 , 還有一個特殊的委員會 , 美國政府開始重新審視這個領域 。
and i think it's important to keep reality in mind , versus what happens with people's imaginations .	我認為 , 保持現實是很重要的 , 和大家的想像力是怎麼回事 。
basically , any virus that's been sequenced today that genome can be made .	基本上 , 現今所有被基因組排序的病毒 。
and people immediately freak out about things about ebola or smallpox , but the dna from this organism is not infective .	人們馬上就對伊波拉或天花的事物感到怪異 , 但從這個生物體中產生的dna並不是有毒的 。
so even if somebody made the smallpox genome , that dna itself would not cause infections .	所以即使有人做了天花基因 , dna本身就不會造成感染 。
the real concern that security departments have is designer viruses .	安全部門真正擔心的是設計師病毒 。
and there's only two countries , the u . s . and the former soviet union , that had major efforts on trying to create biological warfare agents .	只有兩個國家 , 美國和前蘇聯 , 他們努力創造生物武器代理 。
if that research is truly discontinued , there should be very little activity on the knowhow to make designer viruses in the future .	如果這項研究真的被剝奪了 , 未來就應該要有非常少的活動來製造設計病毒 。
i think singlecell organisms are possible within two years .	我認為在兩年內 , 單細胞有機體是可能的 。
and possibly eukaryotic cells , those that we have , are possible within a decade .	可能在十年內 , 我們所擁有的真皮細胞 。
so we're now making several dozen different constructs , because we can vary the cassettes and the genes that go into this artificial chromosome .	我們現在正在製造數十個不同的構造 , 因為我們能改變貓咪和基因進入人造染色體的基因 。
the key is , how do you put all of the others ?	關鍵是 , 你要如何把他人都放在一起 ?
we start with these fragments , and then we have a homologous recombination system that reassembles those into a chromosome .	我們從這些碎片開始 , 然後我們有一套相同的重新組合系統 , 將它們重新組合成染色體 。
this is derived from an organism , deinococcus radiodurans , that can take three million rads of radiation and not be killed .	這是從一個有機體中衍生出來的 , 明確的輻射 , 可以吸收三百萬種輻射 , 而不是被殺害 。
it reassembles its genome after this radiation burst in about 12 to 24 hours , after its chromosomes are literally blown apart .	在輻射爆發12至24小時後 , 它的染色體會被爆炸 。
this organism is ubiquitous on the planet , and exists perhaps now in outer space due to all our travel there .	這種生物在地球上無所不在 , 可能就在外太空中 , 因為我們所有的旅程都在外太空中存在 。
this is a glass beaker after about half a million rads of radiation .	這是一架玻璃桶 , 經過了五十萬個輻射 。
the glass started to burn and crack , while the microbes sitting in the bottom just got happier and happier .	玻璃開始燃燒和裂縫 , 微生物坐在海底 , 變得更快樂 。
here's an actual picture of what happens: the top of this shows the genome after 1 . 7 million rads of radiation .	這是一張真實的照片上面顯示了一百七十萬個輻射的基因組 。
the chromosome is literally blown apart .	染色體真的分崩離析了 。
and here's that same dna automatically reassembled 24 hours later .	同樣的dna自動重組了24小時 。
it's truly stunning that these organisms can do that , and we probably have thousands , if not tens of thousands , of different species on this planet that are capable of doing that .	令人驚訝的是 , 這些生物能做到這一點 , 我們可能有數千種 , 如果不是數萬種 , 在這個星球上 , 可以做到這一點 。
after these genomes are synthesized , the first step is just transplanting them into a cell without a genome .	在這些基因組合成後 , 第一步便是將它們移植到一個沒有基因組的細胞中 。
so we think synthetic cells are going to have tremendous potential , not only for understanding the basis of biology but for hopefully environmental and society issues .	所以我們認為合成細胞將會有很大的潛力 , 不僅是為了了解生物學的基礎 , 更希望的是環境和社會議題 。
for example , from the third organism we sequenced , methanococcus jannaschii it lives in boiling water temperatures ; its energy source is hydrogen and all its carbon comes from co2 it captures back from the environment .	舉例來說 , 從我們排序的第三個有機體 , 甲烷 , 詹納西是沸水的溫度 ; 它的能量來源是氫 , 所有的碳來自於環境的二氧化碳 。
so we know lots of different pathways , thousands of different organisms now that live off of co2 , and can capture that back .	所以我們知道許多不同的途徑 , 數以千計的不同的生物住在二氧化碳上 , 可以捕捉到它 。
so instead of using carbon from oil for synthetic processes , we have the chance of using carbon and capturing it back from the atmosphere , converting that into biopolymers or other products .	所以 , 與其從石油上取代合成過程 , 我們有機會使用碳 , 從大氣中捕捉回來 , 將其轉換成生物聚合物或其他產品 。
we have one organism that lives off of carbon monoxide , and we use as a reducing power to split water to produce hydrogen and oxygen .	我們有一個生物存在於二氧化碳中 , 我們用它來降低水份 , 來產生氫和氧 。
also , there's numerous pathways that can be engineered metabolizing methane .	此外 , 有許多途徑可以被改造代謝甲烷 。
and dupont has a major program with statoil in norway to capture and convert the methane from the gas fields there into useful products .	杜邦有一項重大的計畫 , 用挪威的雕像來捕捉和從那裡轉換甲烷 , 變成有用的產品 。
within a short while , i think there's going to be a new field called " combinatorial genomics , " because with these new synthesis capabilities , these vast gene array repertoires and the homologous recombination , we think we can design a robot to make maybe a million different chromosomes a day .	不久之內 , 我認為會有一個叫做 「 組合基因體 」 的新領域 , 因為有了這些新的合成能力 , 這些大量的基因庫和同源的組合 , 我們認為我們可以設計一個機器人 , 一天可能製造出百萬種不同的染色體 。
and therefore , as with all biology , you get selection through screening , whether you're screening for hydrogen production , or chemical production , or just viability .	因此 , 如同生物學 , 你通過螢幕進行篩選 , 不論你在檢視氫生產 , 或化學生產 , 或僅僅是可行性 。
