to understand the role of these genes is going to be well within reach .	若要了解這些基因的角色 , 就會很好 。
we're trying to modify photosynthesis to produce hydrogen directly from sunlight .	我們試著修改光合作用 , 直接從陽光中直接產生氫 。
photosynthesis is modulated by oxygen , and we have an oxygeninsensitive hydrogenase that we think will totally change this process .	光合作用被氧氣調節 , 我們認為會完全改變這個過程 。
we're also combining cellulases , the enzymes that break down complex sugars into simple sugars and fermentation in the same cell for producing ethanol .	我們還在結合細胞分解複雜糖成簡單糖和發酵的酵素在同一個細胞中產生乙醇
pharmaceutical production is already under way in major laboratories using microbes .	製藥生產已經在主要實驗室中進行了 。
the chemistry from compounds in the environment is orders of magnitude more complex than our best chemists can produce .	環境中的化合物的化學性質比我們最好的化合物所能製造出來的大量化合物要複雜 。
i think future engineered species could be the source of food , hopefully a source of energy , environmental remediation and perhaps replacing the petrochemical industry .	我認為未來的工程物種可以是食物的來源 , 希望是能源、環境復原的來源 , 也許可以取代石化產業 。
let me just close with ethical and policy studies .	讓我用倫理和政策研究來結束 。
we delayed the start of our experiments in 1999 until we completed a yearandahalf bioethical review as to whether we should try and make an artificial species .	在1999年 , 我們延遲實驗的開端 , 直到我們完成了一年半的生物倫理評論 , 來評論我們是否該嘗試做人工物種 。
every major religion participated in this .	每個主要的宗教都參與其中 。
it was actually a very strange study , because the various religious leaders were using their scriptures as law books , and they couldn't find anything in them prohibiting making life , so it must be ok . the only ultimate concerns were biological warfare aspects of this , but gave us the go ahead to start these experiments for the reasons we were doing them .	這其實是個很奇怪的研究 , 因為各式各樣的宗教領袖把他們的文字當作法律書 , 他們無法在他們禁止製造生命的過程中找到任何東西 , 所以 , 唯一的關注是生物戰略的面向 , 但給了我們前一步的實驗 , 為我們做這些實驗的理由 。
right now the sloan foundation has just funded a multiinstitutional study on this , to work out what the risk and benefits to society are , and the rules that scientific teams such as my own should be using in this area , and we're trying to set good examples as we go forward .	現在 , sloan基金會剛剛資助了一份多個機構的研究 , 為社會帶來的風險和利益 , 以及像我這樣的團隊應該在這個領域中使用的規則 , 我們正試著設立一些好的例子 。
these are complex issues .	這些都是複雜的問題 。
except for the threat of bioterrorism , they're very simple issues in terms of , can we design things to produce clean energy , perhaps revolutionizing what developing countries can do and provide through various simple processes .	除了生物恐怖主義的威脅之外 , 它們是非常簡單的議題 , 我們能否設計東西來產生乾淨的能源 , 或許革命發展中國家能做些什麼 , 並提供各種簡單的過程 。
psychologist philip zimbardo says happiness and success are rooted in a trait most of us disregard: the way we orient toward the past , present and future . he suggests we calibrate our outlook on time as a first step to improving our lives .	心理學家菲利普津巴多說幸福和成功是根深蒂固的特質:我們朝向過去、現在和未來的方向前進 。 他建議我們以一步改善生活的第一步 。
brain , business , happiness , mind , psychology , science	大腦、商業、快樂、思維、心理學、科學、科學、
philip zimbardo prescribes a healthy take on time	菲利普津巴多開了健康照護時間 ,
i want to share with you some ideas about the secret power of time , in a very short time .	我想和大家分享一些關於時間的秘密力量的概念 , 在很短的時間內 。
video: all right , start the clock please . 30 seconds studio .	影片:好的 , 開始時鐘拜託 , 30秒工作室
keep it quiet please . settle down .	保持安靜 , 安定下來 。
it's about time . end sequence . take one .	大約是時間 。 結束序列 。 拿一個 。
10 , nine , eight , seven , six , five , four , three , two . . .	10、9、8、6、5、4、3、2......
philip zimbardo: let's tune into the conversation of the principals in adam's temptation .	菲利普津巴多:咱們來談談亞當的誘惑 。
" come on adam , don't be so wishywashy . take a bite . " " i did . "	「 來上亞當 , 不要太討喜 , 吃一點 。 」 「 我做過 。 」
" one bite , adam . don't abandon eve . "	「 一口 , 亞當 , 不要放棄 。 」
" i don't know , guys .	「 我不知道 , 各位 。
i don't want to get in trouble . "	我不想惹上麻煩 。 」
" okay . one bite . what the hell ? "	「 好 , 一口 。 到底是什麼 ? 」
life is temptation . it's all about yielding , resisting , yes , no , now , later , impulsive , reflective , present focus and future focus .	生命是誘惑 。 一切都是為了生存、抗拒 , 是的 , 不 , 後來 , 衝動、反思、焦點 , 以及未來的焦點 。
promised virtues fall prey to the passions of the moment .	被保證的美德落入了當下的熱情 。
of teenage girls who pledged sexual abstinence and virginity until marriage thank you george bush the majority , 60 percent , yielded to sexual temptations within one year .	十幾歲的女孩 , 她們主張性別缺陷和處女 , 直到婚姻 , 感謝妳的喬治布希──多數 , 60% , 她們在一年內得到性誘惑 。
and most of them did so without using birth control .	大部分的人都沒有使用生育控制 。
so much for promises .	承諾是如此 。
now lets tempt fouryearolds , giving them a treat .	現在讓我們誘惑四歲的孩子 , 給他們一份治療 。
they can have one marshmallow now . but if they wait until the experimenter comes back , they can have two .	他們現在可以有一顆棉花糖 。 但如果他們等到實驗員回來 , 他們就可以有兩顆 。
of course it pays , if you like marshmallows , to wait .	當然 , 如果你喜歡棉花糖 , 它會付錢 。
what happens is twothirds of the kids give in to temptation .	會發生的是三分之二的孩子 , 給他們誘惑 。
they cannot wait . the others , of course , wait .	當然 , 他們不能等 。 其他人 , 當然 , 等等 。
they resist the temptation . they delay the now for later .	他們抗拒誘惑 。 他們現在延遲了 。
walter mischel , my colleague at stanford , went back 14 years later , to try to discover what was different about those kids .	華特•密歇爾 , 我在史丹佛的同事 , 14年後回去 , 試著去了解這些孩子有什麼不同 。
there were enormous differences between kids who resisted and kids who yielded , in many ways .	在許多方面 , 抗拒和受害者的孩子之間有很大的差異 。
the kids who resisted scored 250 points higher on the sat .	那些拒絕分配250分的孩子 , 高出250分 。
that's enormous . that's like a whole set of different iq points .	這很龐大 。 這就像一整套不同的智商點 。
they didn't get in as much trouble . they were better students .	他們沒有陷入任何麻煩 , 他們是更好的學生 。
they were selfconfident and determined . and the key for me today , the key for you , is , they were futurefocused rather than presentfocused .	他們是自信且堅定的 。 今天對我來說 , 關鍵是 , 他們是未來的焦點 , 而不是現在的焦點 。
so what is time perspective ? that's what i'm going to talk about today .	所以 , 時間觀點是什麼 ? 這就是我今天要談的 。
time perspective is the study of how individuals , all of us , divide the flow of your human experience into time zones or time categories .	時間觀念是研究個體 , 我們所有人的研究 , 將你的人類經歷分為時間區 , 或時間分類 。
and you do it automatically and nonconsciously .	而你會自動做 , 無意識地做 。
they vary between cultures , between nations , between individuals , between social classes , between education levels .	文化、國家、個人、社會階級之間、教育水平之間的差異 。
and the problem is that they can become biased , because you learn to overuse some of them and underuse the others .	問題是 , 他們可以變得偏見 , 因為你學會過度使用一些偏見 , 並且低估其它部分 。
what determines any decision you make ?	你做了什麼決定 ?
you make a decision on which you're going to base an action .	你決定你要採取行動 。
for some people it's only about what is in the immediate situation , what other people are doing and what you're feeling .	對一些人而言 , 只有在即時情況下 , 其他人在做什麼 , 以及你在做什麼 。
and those people , when they make their decisions in that format we're going to call them " presentoriented , " because their focus is what is now .	那些人 , 當他們做出決定時 , 我們會稱他們為 「 簡報 」 , 因為他們專注在現在 。
for others , the present is irrelevant .	對其他人來說 , 現在的確是不相關的 。
it's always about " what is this situation like that i've experienced in the past ? "	總是關於 「 我過去經歷過的這種情況是什麼樣子 ? 」
so that their decisions are based on past memories .	所以他們的決策是基於過去的記憶 。
and we're going to call those people " pastoriented , " because they focus on what was .	我們會稱這些人為 「 過時 」 , 因為他們專注於什麼 。
for others it's not the past , it's not the present , it's only about the future .	對其他人來說 , 這不是過去 , 也不是現在 , 而是關於未來 。
their focus is always about anticipated consequences .	他們的焦點總是在乎預期的後果 。
we're going to call them " futureoriented . " their focus is on what will be .	我們稱他們為 「 未來 」 , 他們的焦點在於未來 。
so , time paradox , i want to argue , the paradox of time perspective , is something that influences every decision you make , you're totally unaware of .	所以 , 時間悖論 , 我想爭論 , 時間觀點的悖論 , 是影響你做出的每一個決定 , 你完全不知道的 。
namely , the extent to which you have one of these biased time perspectives .	換句話說 , 你對這些偏見的時間觀點的程度 。
well there is actually six of them . there are two ways to be presentoriented .	其實有六個 , 有兩種方式可以做簡報 。
there is two ways to be pastoriented , two ways to be future .	有兩種方式可以被貼上去 , 成為未來的兩種方式 。
you can focus on pastpositive , or pastnegative .	你可以把焦點放在過時或負面 。
you can be presenthedonistic , namely you focus on the joys of life , or presentfatalist it doesn't matter , your life is controlled .	你可以被關注生命的喜悅 , 或說是虛擬主義者不重要 , 你的人生被控制了 。
you can be futureoriented , setting goals .	你可以是未來的 , 設定目標 。
or you can be transcendental future: namely , life begins after death .	或者 , 你可以是超自然的未來:命名 , 生命起源於死亡 。
developing the mental flexibility to shift time perspectives fluidly depending on the demands of the situation , that's what you've got to learn to do .	發展出靈活性 , 來改變時間觀點 , 取決於情境的需求 , 這就是你學會做的 。
so , very quickly , what is the optimal time profile ?	所以 , 很快地 , 什麼是最佳的時間資料 ?
high on pastpositive . moderately high on future .	處於輕鬆的狀態 。 在未來 , 溫度高 。
and moderate on presenthedonism .	而現代主義的現代主義 。
and always low on pastnegative and presentfatalism .	總是低於負面和現代主義 。
so the optimal temporal mix is what you get from the past pastpositive gives you roots . you connect your family , identity and your self .	所以 , 最佳的暫時混合就是你從過去的過時混合物給你的根源 。 你將你的家人、身份和自我連結在一起 。
what you get from the future is wings to soar to new destinations , new challenges .	從未來你得到的是翅膀 , 到新的目的地 , 新的挑戰 。
what you get from the present hedonism is the energy , the energy to explore yourself , places , people , sensuality .	你從現在的喜悅主義中得到的就是能量 , 去探索你自己、地方、人、感覺 。
any time perspective in excess has more negatives than positives .	任何多餘時間的觀點都比正面的還要多 。
what do futures sacrifice for success ?	什麼樣的未來犧牲成功 ?
they sacrifice family time . they sacrifice friend time .	他們犧牲家庭時間 , 犧牲朋友時間 。
they sacrifice fun time . they sacrifice personal indulgence .	他們犧牲有趣的時光 。 他們犧牲個人的誘惑 。
they sacrifice hobbies . and they sacrifice sleep . so it affects their health .	他們犧牲嗜好 , 犧牲睡眠 。 所以這會影響他們的健康 。
and they live for work , achievement and control .	他們為工作、成就和控制而生活 。
i'm sure that resonates with some of the tedsters .	我敢肯定這和一些ted大會有關 。
and it resonated for me . i grew up as a poor kid in the south bronx ghetto , a sicilian family everyone lived in the past and present .	這對我來說很有共鳴 。 我在南布朗克斯ghet托長大 , 一個醫師家庭 , 每個人都住在過去和現在 。
i'm here as a futureoriented person who went over the top , who did all these sacrifices because teachers intervened , and made me future oriented .	我來這裡是一位有希望的人 , 走過頂端 , 犧牲了這些人 , 因為老師介入了 , 讓我有了未來的傾向 。
told me don't eat that marshmallow , because if you wait you're going to get two of them , until i learned to balance out .	告訴我不要吃那顆棉花糖 , 因為如果你等著你會拿到兩顆 , 直到我學會平衡 。
i've added presenthedonism , i've added a focus on the pastpositive , so , at 76 years old , i am more energetic than ever , more productive , and i'm happier than i have ever been .	我加上現代主義 , 我把焦點放在過時性 , 所以 , 七十六歲時 , 我比以往更有生產力 , 我比以前更快樂 。
i just want to say that we are applying this to many world problems: changing the dropout rates of school kids , combating addictions , enhancing teen health , curing vets' ptsd with time metaphors getting miracle cures promoting sustainability and conservation , reducing physical rehabilitation where there is a 50percent drop out rate , altering appeals to suicidal terrorists , and modifying family conflicts as timezone clashes .	我只是想說 , 我們把這個應用到許多世界問題上:改變學校孩子的輟學率、結合成癮、增強青少年健康、用時間隱喻來治療創傷創傷後壓力症候群 , 提高永續性和保育性 , 減少身體復健率 , 減少50% , 改變自殺恐怖份子 , 轉換為自殺傾向 , 轉換為家庭時間的衝突 。
so i want to end by saying: many of life's puzzles can be solved by understanding your time perspective and that of others .	我想以最後的結尾說:許多生命的謎題 , 都能透過了解你的時間觀點和他人的觀點來解決 。
and the idea is so simple , so obvious , but i think the consequences are really profound .	想法很簡單 , 很明顯 , 但我認為後果非常深刻 。
how many of today's headlines will matter in 100 years ? 1000 ? kirk citron's " long news " project collects stories that not only matter today , but will resonate for decades even centuries to come . at ted2010 , he highlights recent headlines with the potential to shape our future .	在一百年內 , 現今的頭條新聞會很重要 ? 1000年 ? kirkcron的 「 長新聞 」 計畫 , 不僅僅是現今 , 還會產生數十年的關注 , 甚至2010年 , 他會強調未來的頭條 , 可能塑造我們的未來 。
future , global issues , media , news , science	未來、全球議題、媒體、新聞、科學、科學、
kirk citron: and now , the real news	kirkcitron:現在 , 真正的新聞是真實的消息 。
we are drowning in news .	我們在新聞裡淹沒 。
reuters alone puts out three and a half million news stories a year .	光是檢查員一年就發佈了350萬個新聞故事 。
that's just one source .	這只是一個源頭 。
my question is: how many of those stories are actually going to matter in the long run ?	我的問題是:長期來說 , 到底有多少會影響到這些故事 ?
that's the idea behind the long news .	這是長期新聞背後的想法 。
it's a project by the long now foundation , which was founded by tedsters including kevin kelly and stewart brand .	這是一個長時間基金會的專案 , 由tedsters所創立的 , 包括凱文凱利和史都華特品牌 。
and what we're looking for is news stories that might still matter 50 or 100 or 10 , 000 years from now .	我們在尋找的新聞故事 , 可能在50到10萬年後還會影響到50到10000年 。
and when you look at the news through that filter , a lot falls by the wayside .	當你透過這個過濾器看新聞時 , 很多的情況下都會落下 。
to take the top stories from the a . p . this last year , is this going to matter in a decade ?	去年 , 從a.p.故事中 , 去年 , 這會在十年內發生嗎 ?
is this going to matter in 50 or 100 years ?	這會在50或100年內產生影響嗎 ?
okay , that was kind of cool .	好吧 , 這有點酷 。
but the top story of this past year was the economy , and i'm just betting that , sooner or later , this particular recession is going to be old news .	但過去一年的頭一次故事是經濟 , 我很快就會打賭 , 不久後 , 這個衰退將會是舊消息 。
so , what kind of stories might make a difference for the future ?	所以 , 什麼樣的故事能為未來帶來改變 ?
well , let's take science .	咱們來談談科學 。
someday , little robots will go through our bloodstreams fixing things .	有一天 , 小機器人會穿過我們的血液來修復東西 。
that someday is already here if you're a mouse .	如果你是一隻老鼠 , 那天就已經出現了 。
some recent stories: nanobees zap tumors with real bee venom ; they're sending genes into the brain ; a robot they built that can crawl through the human body .	有些最近的故事:奈米蟲和真蜜蜂毒液結合 ; 它們把基因送到大腦中 ; 一個可以透過人體爬行的機器人 。
what about resources ? how are we going to feed nine billion people ?	資源呢 ? 我們要如何餵飽90億人 ?
we're having trouble feeding six billion today .	我們現在正在餵飽六十億人 。
as we heard yesterday , there's over a billion people hungry .	如同我們昨天聽到的 , 有超過十億人挨餓 。
britain will starve without genetically modified crops .	英國沒有基因改造的作物 , 會餓死 。
bill gates , fortunately , has bet a billion on [agricultural] research .	幸運的是 , 比爾蓋茲在農業研究上有十億人 。
what about global politics ?	那麼全球政治呢 ?
the world's going to be very different when and if china sets the agenda , and they may .	世界將會非常不一樣 , 如果中國訂定了議程 , 他們也可能 。
they've overtaken the u . s . as the world's biggest car market , they've overtaken germany as the largest exporter , and they've started doing dna tests on kids to choose their careers .	他們已經超越美國 , 作為世界上最大的汽車市場 , 他們已經超越德國成為最大的出口者 , 他們開始做dna測試 , 讓孩子選擇他們的職業 。
we're finding all kinds of ways to push back the limits of what we know .	我們在尋找各種方法來推動我們所知的極限 。
some recent discoveries: there's an ant colony from argentina that has now spread to every continent but antarctica ; there's a selfdirected robot scientist that's made a discovery soon , science may no longer need us , and life may no longer need us either ; a microbe wakes up after 120 , 000 years .	有些近期的發現:阿根廷有一個蟻群 , 已經散播到每一塊大陸 , 但南極洲都有自主導的機器人科學家 , 很快地 , 科學就不再需要我們了 , 生命可能也不再需要我們了 ; 一個經過120萬年的微生物醒來 。
it seems that with or without us , life will go on .	似乎 , 不論我們 , 生命都會持續下去 。
but my pick for the top long news story of this past year was this one: water found on the moon .	但過去一年 , 我選的最新新聞是這個:在月球上發現的水 。
makes it a lot easier to put a colony up there .	要把蟻群放在那裡就更容易了 。
and if nasa doesn't do it , china might , or somebody in this room might write a big check .	如果美國太空總署不這麼做 , 中國可能 , 或在座的某個人可能會寫一份大支票 。
my point is this: in the long run , some news stories are more important than others .	我的重點是:在長期來說 , 有些新聞故事比其他新聞更重要 。
planetary scientist carolyn porco shows images from the cassini voyage to saturn , focusing on its largest moon , titan , and on frozen enceladus , which seems to shoot jets of ice .	地球科學家carolynpordco從卡斯尼航海到土星 , 專注於它最大的衛星、泰坦 , 以及凍結的土衛 , 這似乎是冰的噴射機 。
nasa , design , exploration , science , space , technology , universe , visualizations	美國太空總署、設計、探索、探索、太空、太空、科技、宇宙、視覺化、視覺化、視覺化 。
carolyn porco flies us to saturn	卡羅琳潘科讓我們飛向土星 , 飛向土星 。
in the next 18 minutes , i'm going to take you on a journey .	在接下來的18分鐘 , 我要帶各位踏上一段旅程 。
and it's a journey that you and i have been on for many years now , and it began some 50 years ago , when humans first stepped off our planet .	這趟旅程 , 你和我已經經歷過很多年了 , 50年前 , 當人類踏出地球時 , 它開始了 。
and in those 50 years , not only did we literally , physically set foot on the moon , but we have dispatched robotic spacecraft to all the planets all eight of them and we have landed on asteroids , we have rendezvoused with comets , and , at this point in time , we have a spacecraft on its way to pluto , the body formerly known as a planet .	在那50年裡 , 我們不僅真的在月球上設置了腳 , 我們還把機械太空船分散到所有行星的八個行星上 , 我們登陸了小行星 , 在這個時點 , 我們有一艘太空船 , 運行到冥王星 , 以前所知的星球 。
and all of these robotic missions are part of a bigger human journey: a voyage to understand something , to get a sense of our cosmic place , to understand something of our origins , and how earth , our planet , and we , living on it , came to be .	所有這些機械任務都是人類旅程的一部分:航海來了解事物 , 去了解宇宙的起源 , 去了解我們的起源 , 地球 , 和我們生活的 , 漸漸成真 。
and of all the places in the solar system that we might go to and search for answers to questions like this , there's saturn . and we have been to saturn before we visited saturn in the early 1980s but our investigations of saturn have become far more indepth in detail since the cassini spacecraft , traveling across interplanetary space for seven years , glided into orbit around saturn in the summer of 2004 , and became at that point the farthest robotic outpost that humanity had ever established around the sun .	在太陽系裡的所有地方 , 我們可能會去尋找像這樣的問題的答案 , 土星就存在 。 我們在1980年代造訪了土星 , 但我們的土星調查之後 , 土星的調查已經變得更加詳細 , 自從卡西尼號太空船飛行 , 穿越了星際太空七年 , 讓土星飛行到土星的軌道上 , 在2004年的那個時期 , 我們成為了地球上人類最遠景的機器人 。
now , the saturn system is a rich planetary system .	土星系統是個很豐富的星球系統 。
it offers mystery , scientific insight and obviously splendor beyond compare , and the investigation of this system has enormous cosmic reach .	它提供了神秘、科學的洞察 , 顯然超出了比較之外的資金 , 而這個系統的調查顯示了巨大的宇宙 。
in fact , just studying the rings alone , we stand to learn a lot about the discs of stars and gas that we call the spiral galaxies .	事實上 , 光靠研究環 , 我們就能學到很多關於星體和氣體的圓盤 , 我們稱之為螺旋星系 。
and here's a beautiful picture of the andromeda nebula , which is our closest , largest spiral galaxy to the milky way .	這是andromedanebula的美麗照片 , 這是我們最接近的 , 最大型的螺旋星系到銀河系 。
and then , here's a beautiful composite of the whirlpool galaxy , taken by the hubble space telescope .	這裡有個美麗的旋風星系是由哈伯太空望遠鏡所拍攝的
so the journey back to saturn is really part of and is also a metaphor for a much larger human voyage to understand the interconnectedness of everything around us , and also how humans fit into that picture .	所以 , 回到土星的旅程是其中的一部分 , 也是為了更大的人類旅程 , 來了解我們周遭的所有事物之間的關聯性 , 以及人類如何融入這張照片 。
and it pains me that i can't tell you all that we have learned with cassini .	這讓我無法告訴你們我們在卡西尼學到的一切 。
i can't show you all the beautiful pictures that we've taken in the last two and a half years , because i simply don't have the time .	我無法給你們看我們過去兩年半所拍攝的美麗照片 , 因為我沒有時間 。
so i'm going to concentrate on two of the most exciting stories that have emerged out of this major exploratory expedition that we are conducting around saturn , and have been for the past two and a half years .	所以 , 我要專注在兩個最令人振奮的故事中 , 在這個重大的探險探險探險旅程中 , 我們正進行土星四周進行 , 過去兩年半以來一直都是如此 。
saturn is accompanied by a very large and diverse collection of moons .	土星伴隨著大型多樣化的月球 。
they range in size from a few kilometers across to as big across as the u . s .	它們排列在幾公里寬的大小 , 大到和美國一樣大 。
most of the beautiful pictures we've taken of saturn , in fact , show saturn in accompaniment with some of its moons . here's saturn with dione , and then , here's saturn showing the rings edgeon , showing you just how vertically thin they are , with the moon enceladus .	我們拍攝了土星的大部分美麗照片 , 事實上 , 土星與衛星有一些月球 。 這是土星和鑽石 , 然後 , 土星展示了ringgeon , 向你展示了它們的垂直薄度 , 用土衛二 。
now , two of the 47 moons that saturn has are standouts .	土星的47個衛星中有兩個是站著 。
and those are titan and enceladus . titan is saturn's largest moon , and , until cassini had arrived there , was the largest single expanse of unexplored terrain that we had remaining in our solar system .	那些是土衛六和土衛二 。 泰坦是土星最大的衛星 , 直到卡西尼到達之前 , 是太陽系中最大的未探索地帶 。
and it is a body that has long intrigued people who've watched the planets .	它是一種長久以來很感興趣的人 , 觀看了行星 。
it has a very large , thick atmosphere , and in fact , its surface environment was believed to be more like the environment we have here on the earth , or at least had in the past , than any other body in the solar system .	它有非常大的厚厚的大氣層 , 事實上 , 它的表面環境被認為更像我們在地球上所生存的環境 , 或者至少在過去 , 比太陽系中任何其他的身體都要大 。
its atmosphere is largely molecular nitrogen , like you are breathing here in this room , except that its atmosphere is suffused with simple organic materials like methane and propane and ethane .	它的大氣層主要是分子氮 , 就像你在這裡呼吸一樣 , 除了它的大氣層充滿了簡單的有機物質 , 比如甲烷、丙烷和乙烷 。
and these molecules high up in the atmosphere of titan get broken down , and their products join together to make haze particles .	這些分子位於泰坦大氣層的大氣層中 , 分解破了 , 而它們的產品結合在一起 , 形成了 「 駭客粒子 」 。
this haze is ubiquitous . it's completely global and enveloping titan .	這種霧氣是無所不在的 , 完全是全球性的 , 包含土衛六 。
and that's why you cannot see down to the surface with our eyes in the visible region of the spectrum .	這也是為什麼你不能用眼睛在可見光譜中看到表面 。
but these haze particles , it was surmised , before we got there with cassini , over billions and billions of years , gently drifted down to the surface and coated the surface in a thick organic sludge .	但這些霧狀的粒子 , 在我們和卡西尼到那裡之前 , 已經有數十億年了 , 溫柔地移到表面 , 將表面覆蓋在厚厚的有機黏液中 。
so like the equivalent , the titan equivalent , of tar , or oil , or what we didn't know what .	如同泰坦 , 泰坦等同於油、油 , 或我們不知道什麼 。
but this is what we suspected . and these molecules , especially methane and ethane , can be liquids at the surface temperatures of titan .	但這就是我們所懷疑的 。 這些分子 , 特別是甲烷和乙烷 , 在土衛六的地表溫度上可以是液態 。
and so it turns out that methane is to titan what water is to the earth .	結果發現甲烷對地球來說是甚麼水 。
it's a condensable in the atmosphere , and so recognizing this circumstance brought to the fore a whole world of bizarre possibilities . you can have methane clouds , ok , and above those clouds , you have this hundreds of kilometers of haze , which prevent any sunlight from getting to the surface .	它在大氣層中是可以容納的 , 所以認知了這個環境 , 帶來了整個世界的奇特的可能性 。 你可以有甲烷雲 , 好 , 在這些雲層之上 , 你有數百公里的霧氣 , 防止任何陽光從表面照射到表面 。
the temperature at the surface is some 350 degrees below zero fahrenheit .	表面的溫度在華氏零度以下約350度 。
but despite that cold , you could have rain falling down on the surface of titan .	但儘管冷了 , 泰坦的表面下有雨 。
and doing on titan what rain does on the earth: it carves gullies ; it forms rivers and cataracts ; it can create canyons ; it can pool in large basins and craters .	在泰坦 , 下雨在地球上會做的事:它會雕刻 , 形成河流和領土 ; 它能創造峽谷 ; 它能聚集在大盆地和坑裡 。
it can wash the sludge off high mountain peaks and hills , down into the lowlands . so stop and think for a minute .	它可以洗掉高山峰和山丘 , 到低地 , 停下來 , 想一想 。
try to imagine what the surface of titan might look like .	試著想像土衛六表面是什麼樣子 。
it's dark . high noon on titan is as dark as deep earth twilight on the earth .	它是黑暗的 。 鐵達尼號的高點就像是地球深處的地球照明一樣黑暗 。
it's cold , it's eerie , it's misty , it might be raining , and you might be standing on the shores of lake michigan brimming with paint thinner .	它很冷 , 很小 , 很糟糕 , 可能是下雨 , 你可能站在密西根湖邊 , 用油漆粉刷來模仿 。
that is the view that we had of the surface of titan before we got there with cassini , and i can tell you that what we have found on titan , though it is not the same in detail , is every bit as fascinating as that story is .	這是我們在卡西尼號到達之前的土衛六表面 , 我可以告訴你們 , 我們在土衛六上所發現的 , 雖然它的細節不一樣 , 都和故事一樣迷人 。
and for us , it has been like the cassini people it has been like a jules verne adventure come true .	對我們來說 , 它就像是卡西尼人 , 它就像是一場青春期冒險一樣 。
as i said , it has a thick , extensive atmosphere .	如我所說 , 它有厚厚的大氣層 。
this is a picture of titan , backlit by the sun , with the rings as a beautiful backdrop .	這張照片是土衛六的背景 , 太陽的背景 , 背景是美麗的背景 。
and yet another moon there i don't even know which one it is . it's a very extensive atmosphere .	另外一個月球 , 我甚至不知道它是哪一個 。 它是一個非常廣闊的大氣層 。
we have instruments on cassini which can see down to the surface through this atmosphere , and my camera system is one of them .	我們在卡西尼號的儀器可以透過這個大氣層看到表面 , 我的相機系統就是其中之一 。
and we have taken pictures like this .	我們拍了這樣的照片 。
and what you see is bright and dark regions , and that's about as far as it got for us .	你看到的是明亮且黑暗的區域 , 差不多跟我們差不多 。
it was so mystifying: we couldn't make out what we were seeing on titan .	這太神奇了:我們無法在泰坦看到什麼 。
when you look closer at this region , you start to see things like sinuous channels we didn't know . you see a few round things .	當你靠近這個區域 , 你就會開始看到我們不知道的無數頻道 。 你看到一些圓形的東西 。
this , we later found out , is , in fact , a crater , but there are very few craters on the surface of titan , meaning it's a very young surface .	我們後來發現 , 其實是隕石坑 , 但土衛六表面上有非常少的隕石坑 , 意思是 , 它是非常年輕的表面 。
and there are features that look tectonic .	有些特徵看起來很像地形 。
they look like they've been pulled apart .	他們看起來好像被拉開了 。
whenever you see anything linear on a planet , it means there's been a fracture , like a fault .	每當你在一個星球上看到線條時 , 它就意味著有裂痕 , 像斷層一樣 。
and so it's been tectonically altered .	所以它已經被轉變了 。
but we couldn't make sense of our images , until , six months after we got into orbit , an event occurred that many have regarded as the highlight of cassini's investigation of titan .	但我們無法理解我們的影像 , 直到我們進入軌道六個月後 , 發生了一件事件 , 許多人都認為卡西尼的調查很明顯 。
and that was the deployment of the huygens probe , the europeanbuilt huygens probe that cassini had carried for seven years across the solar system . we deployed it to the atmosphere of titan , it took two and a half hours to descend , and it landed on the surface .	這就是huygens探測器的部署 , 歐洲的builthuygenshuygens探測器已經運載了七年的太陽系 。 我們將它部署到titan的大氣層 , 花了兩半小時的時間來下降 , 它落在地表上 。
and i just want to emphasize how significant an event this is .	我想要強調這個事件有多重要 。
this is a device of human making , and it landed in the outer solar system for the first time in human history .	這是人類製造的裝置 , 它在人類史上第一次登入外太陽系 。
it is so significant that , in my mind , this was an event that should have been celebrated with ticker tape parades in every city across the u . s . and europe , and sadly , that wasn't the case .	顯而易見的是 , 在我心目中 , 這個事件應該被讚頌 , 在美國和歐洲的每一個城市中 , 都應該被教導 , 這並非如此 。
it was significant for another reason . this is an international mission , and this event was celebrated in europe , in germany , and the celebratory presentations were given in english accents , and american accents , and german accents , and french and italian and dutch accents .	這很重要 , 因為另一個原因 。 這是國際的使命 , 這事件在歐洲、德國被讚頌 , 而慶祝的英文口音 , 美國口音 , 德國口音 , 法國口音 , 義大利和荷蘭口音 。
it was a moving demonstration of what the words " united nations " are supposed to mean: a true union of nations joined together in a colossal effort for good .	它是關於 「 聯合國 」 的主流示威 , 應該是意義:一個真正的民族團結合在一起 , 為了好而努力 。
and , in this case , it was a massive undertaking to explore a planet , and to come to understand a planetary system that , for all of human history , had been unreachable , and now humans had actually touched it .	在這個例子中 , 它是很大的目的是要探索一個星球 , 為了了解一個星球系統 , 在所有人類歷史上 , 都無法做到 , 現在 , 人類已經觸碰了它 。
so it was i mean , i'm getting goose bumps just talking about it .	所以 , 我的意思是 , 我會去做雞皮疙瘩 。
it was a tremendously emotional event , and it's something that i will personally never forget , and you shouldn't either .	那是個極大的情感事件 , 我個人永遠不會忘記 , 而你也不應該 。
but anyway , the probe took measurements of the atmosphere on the way down , and it also took panoramic pictures .	無論如何 , 探測器在下面的大氣層進行測量 , 它也拍了全景照片 。
and i can't tell you what it was like to see the first pictures of titan's surface from the probe . and this is what we saw .	我沒辦法告訴你們看第一張來自探測器的圖片 , 這是我們看到的 。
and it was a shocker , because it was everything we wanted those other pictures taken from orbit to be .	這是很震驚的 , 因為我們希望其他的照片都能從軌道上拍到 。
it was an unambiguous pattern , a geological pattern .	那是一種不明確的模式 , 一種地質模式 。
it's a dendritic drainage pattern that can be formed only by the flow of liquids .	它是一種只靠液體流動而形成的趨勢 。
and you can follow these channels and you can see how they all converge .	你可以追蹤這些頻道 , 看看它們如何聚集在一起 。
and they converge into this channel here , which drains into this region .	它們匯集到這條通道 , 流入這個區域 。
you are looking at a shoreline .	你們現在看到的是海岸線 。
was this a shoreline of fluids ? we didn't know .	這是液體的海岸線嗎 ? 我們不知道 。
but this is somewhat of a shoreline .	但這是海岸線 。
this picture is taken at 16 kilometers .	這張照片是在16公里拍攝的 。
this is the picture taken at eight kilometers , ok ? again , the shoreline .	這張照片是在8公里的地方拍的 , 好嗎 ? 再一次 , 海岸線 。
okay , now , 16 kilometers , eight kilometers this is roughly an airline altitude .	好吧 , 現在 , 16公里 , 8公里 , 這大約是航空高度 。
if you were going to take an airplane trip across the u . s . , you would be flying at these altitudes .	如果你要搭飛機橫跨美國 , 你就要飛越高度 。
so , this is the picture you would have at the window of titanian airlines as you fly across the surface of titan .	這張照片是你在泰坦航空的窗口 , 飛越了泰坦的表面 。
and then finally , the probe came to rest on the surface , and i'm going to show you , ladies and gentlemen , the first picture ever taken from the surface of a moon in the outer solar system .	最後 , 探測器出現在表面上 , 我要給各位看 , 各位先生女士 , 第一張從外太陽系表面拍攝的照片 。
and here is the horizon , ok ?	這裡是地平線 , 好嗎 ?
these are probably water ice pebbles , yes ?	這些可能是冰塊 , 是嗎 ?
and obviously , it landed in one of these flat , dark regions and it didn't sink out of sight . so it wasn't fluid that we landed in .	很明顯地 , 它降落在其中一個平坦、深色的區域 , 卻沒有掉落 。 所以 , 我們降落的並不是液體 。
what the probe came down in was basically the titan equivalent of a mud flat .	探測器的內部基本上等同於泥土平面 。
this is an unconsolidated ground that is suffused with liquid methane .	這是一個不穩定的地面 , 充滿了液態甲烷 。
and it's probably the case that this material has washed off the highlands of titan through these channels that we saw , and has drained over billions of years to fill in lowlying basins .	可能是這樣 , 這種材料在我們看到的這些通道上被沖洗掉了數十億年 , 來填滿低水池 。
and that is what the huygens probe landed in .	這就是huygens探測器降落的樣子 。
but still , there was no sign in our images , or even in the huygens' images , of any large , open bodies of fluids .	但 , 儘管如此 , 我們的影像仍然沒有標誌 , 甚至在幽默的影像中 , 沒有任何大型的液體 。
where were they ? it got even more puzzling when we found dunes .	他們在哪裡 ? 當我們找到沙丘時 , 會變得更加困惑 。
ok , so this is our movie of the equatorial region of titan , showing these dunes . these are dunes that are 100 meters tall , separated by a few kilometers , and they go on for miles and miles and miles .	好的 , 這是我們土衛六赤道的電影 , 顯示這些沙丘 。 這些沙丘是100公尺高 , 分開了幾公里 , 它們延伸了幾英里 , 甚至幾英哩 。
there's hundreds , up to a 1 , 000 or 1 , 200 miles of dunes .	高達一千到一千兩百英里的沙丘 。
this is the saharan desert of titan .	這是撒哈拉沙漠 。
it's obviously a place which is very dry , or you wouldn't get dunes .	這顯然是一個非常乾燥的地方 , 或者你不會得到沙丘 。
so again , it got puzzling that there were no bodies of fluid , until finally , we saw lakes in the polar regions .	又一次地 , 沒有液體 , 直到最後 , 我們看到了北極區的湖泊 。
and there is a lake scene in the south polar region of titan .	土衛六南極的湖泊有一景 。
it's about the size of lake ontario .	大約是安大略湖的大小 。
and then , only a week and a half ago , we flew over the north pole of titan and found , again , we found a feature here the size of the caspian sea .	然後 , 一週半前 , 我們飛越了土衛六北極 , 再次發現 , 我們發現了像木星海一樣大的特徵 。
so it seems that the liquids , for some reason we don't understand , or during at least this season , are apparently at the poles of titan .	所以看似液體 , 基於某些我們不了解的原因 , 或至少在這個季節 , 很明顯地是泰坦的極地 。
and i think you would agree that we have found titan is a remarkable , mystical place . it's exotic , it's alien , but yet strangely earthlike , and having earthlike geological formations and a tremendous geographical diversity , and is a fascinating world whose only rival in the solar system for complexity and richness is the earth itself .	我想你們會認同 , 我們發現泰坦是個很了不起、很神奇的地方 。 它是外星人 , 但卻是外星人 , 擁有像地球一樣的地質形成 , 以及極大的地理多樣性 , 而這個令人著迷的世界 , 它只對太陽系的複雜性和豐富 。
and so now we go onto enceladus . enceladus is a small moon , it's about a tenth the size of titan . and you can see it here next to england , just to show you the size . this is not meant to be a threat .	現在我們去土衛二 , 土衛二是個小月球 , 土衛六的大小大約是土衛六的十分之一 。 你可以看到它在英格蘭旁邊 , 展示它的大小 。 這不是威脅 。
and enceladus is very white , it's very bright , and its surface is obviously wrecked with fractures .	土衛二非常白 , 非常明亮 , 它的表面顯然破裂了 。
it is a very geologically active body .	它是一個非常地質活躍的身體 。
but the mother lode of discoveries on enceladus was found at the south pole and we're looking at the south pole here where we found this system of fractures .	但土衛二的發現地懶的媽媽在南極找到 , 我們現在看到的是南極 , 我們發現了這個破裂的系統 。
and they're a different color because they're a different composition .	它們是不同的顏色 , 因為它們是不同的組合 。
they are coated . these fractures are coated with organic materials .	它們是編碼的 。 這些碎片是用有機物質編碼的 。
moreover , this whole , entire region , the south polar region , has elevated temperatures . it's the hottest place on the planet , on the body .	此外 , 這整體 , 整個南極區域 , 有高度溫度 。 它是地球上最熱的地方 。
that's as bizarre as finding that the antarctic on the earth is hotter than the tropics .	這相當奇怪 , 發現地球上的南極比熱帶地區更熱 。
and then , when we took additional pictures , we discovered that from these fractures are issuing jets of fine , icy particles extending hundreds of miles into space .	接著 , 當我們拍攝更多的照片 , 我們發現從這些裂縫的噴射 , 好的 , 冰粒粒擴展了數百英哩的空間 。
and when we colorcode this image , to bring out the faint light levels , we see that these jets feed a plume that , in fact , we see , in other images , goes thousands of miles into the space above enceladus .	當我們繪製這張圖時 , 為了帶來微弱的光量 , 我們看到這些噴射機在其他的圖像中 , 我們看到在土衛二上方數千英哩的空間 。
my team and i have examined images like this , and like this one , and have thought about the other results from cassini .	我和我的團隊已經檢查了像這樣的圖片 , 像這張圖片 , 並考慮了卡西尼的其他結果 。
and we have arrived at the conclusion that these jets may be erupting from pockets of liquid water under the surface of enceladus .	我們得到的結論是 , 這些噴射機可能在土衛二表面下噴發出液態水 。
so we have , possibly , liquid water , organic materials and excess heat .	所以 , 我們可能有液態水、有機物質 , 以及過多的熱量 。
in other words , we have possibly stumbled upon the holy grail of modern day planetary exploration , or in other words , an environment that is potentially suitable for living organisms .	換句話說 , 我們可能偶然發現了現代行星探索的聖杯 , 換句話說 , 一個適合生存有機體的環境 。
and i don't think i need to tell you that the discovery of life elsewhere in our solar system , whether it be on enceladus or elsewhere , would have enormous cultural and scientific implications .	我不認為我需要告訴你們 , 太陽系中其他地方的生命 , 不論是在土衛二或其它地方 , 都會有很大的文化和科學上的影響 。
because if we could demonstrate that genesis had occurred not once , but twice , independently , in our solar system , then that means , by inference , it has occurred a staggering number of times throughout the universe and its 13 . 7 billion year history .	因為如果我們能證明遺傳的發生率不是一次 , 而是獨立的 , 在我們的太陽系中 , 那就意味著 , 根據推論 , 它在宇宙中發生了相當驚人的次數 , 且它有137億年的歷史 。
right now , earth is the only planet still that we know is teeming with life .	目前 , 地球仍然是我們所知的唯一一個星球 , 就是充滿生命 。
it is precious , it is unique , it is still , so far , the only home we've ever known .	它是珍貴的 , 它是獨一無二的 , 目前為止 , 我們所知的唯一家 。
and if any of you were alert and coherent during the 1960s and we'd forgive you , if you weren't , ok you would remember this very famous picture taken by the apollo 8 astronauts in 1968 .	如果你們當中有人在1960年代被警告和同心協力我們會原諒你 , 如果你不是 , 好吧你會記得1968年由阿波羅太空人拍的這張非常著名的照片
it was the first time that earth was imaged from space , and it had an enormous impact on our sense of place in the universe , and our sense of responsibility for the protection of our own planet .	那是第一次地球是來自太空的 , 它對我們所處的宇宙有很大的影響 , 我們對地球的保護有責任 。
well , we on cassini have taken an equivalent first , a picture that no human eye has ever seen before .	嗯 , 我們在卡西尼拍了一張相當於人類前所未見的照片 。
it is a total eclipse of the sun , seen from the other side of saturn .	這是太陽的全食 , 從土星的另一邊看過 。
and in this impossibly beautiful picture , you see the main rings backlit by the sun , you see the refracted image of the sun and you see this ring created , in fact , by the exhalations of enceladus .	在這不美麗的圖片中 , 你可以看到太陽的主要環 , 你可以看到太陽的反射形象 , 實際上 , 由土衛二的延伸而產生 。
but as if that weren't brilliant enough , we can spot , in this beautiful image , sight of our own planet , cradled in the arms of saturn's rings .	但就好像那還不夠聰明 , 我們可以在這個美麗的圖像中看到我們自己的星球 , 在土星光環的手臂上破裂 。
now , there is something deeply moving about seeing ourselves from afar , and capturing the sight of our little , blueocean planet in the skies of other worlds .	現在 , 有一個深切的動力 , 就是從遠處看我們自己 , 捕捉到我們在其它世界的小藍綠色星球 。
and that , and the perspective of ourselves that we gain from that , may be , in the end , the finest reward that we earn from this journey of discovery that started half a century ago .	我們從中得到的這個觀點 , 可能是 , 最終 , 我們從這個發現的旅程中得到最好的獎賞 。
as of 2005 , only 15 percent of the world was mapped . this slows the delivery of aid after a disaster and hides the economic potential of unused lands and unknown roads . in this short talk , google's lalitesh katragadda demos map maker , a group mapmaking tool that people around the globe are using to map their world .	至於2005年 , 全世界只有百分之十五的人口被繪製 。 這緩慢地在災難後提供援助 , 隱瞞未知的土地和未知的道路的經濟潛力 。 在這短篇短篇的演講中 , 谷歌的拉特•卡特•摩托製造器 , 一個團體地圖 , 讓全世界的人使用地圖來繪製他們的世界 。
collaboration , design , map , technology	合作 , 設計 , 地圖 , 技術 , 技術 ,
lalitesh katragadda: making maps to fight disaster , build economies	最近的katratradda:製作地圖來對抗災難 , 建立經濟體 。
in 2008 , cyclone nargis devastated myanmar .	2008年 , cyclonenargis摧毀了緬甸 。
millions of people were in severe need of help .	數百萬人需要協助 。
the u . n . wanted to rush people and supplies to the area .	聯合國想要把人和供應趕到這個區域 。
but there were no maps , no maps of roads , no maps showing hospitals , no way for help to reach the cyclone victims .	但沒有地圖 , 沒有道路的地圖 , 沒有地圖顯示醫院 , 沒有辦法協助到達自行車受害者 。
when we look at a map of los angeles or london , it is hard to believe that as of 2005 , only 15 percent of the world was mapped to a geocodable level of detail .	當我們看到洛杉磯或倫敦的地圖時 , 很難相信2005年 , 世界上只有百分之十五的人被描繪成可編碼的細節 。
the u . n . ran headfirst into a problem that the majority of the world's populous faces: not having detailed maps .	聯合國向世界大部分的民粹面臨的問題是:沒有細節的地圖 。
but help was coming .	但 , 協助來了 。
at google , 40 volunteers used a new software to map 120 , 000 kilometers of roads , 3 , 000 hospitals , logistics and relief points .	在google , 40個志願者用一個新軟體來繪製十二萬公里的道路 , 3 , 000間醫院 , 物流和救援點 。
and it took them four days .	他們花了四天的時間 。
the new software they used ? google mapmaker .	他們使用的新軟體 ? google地圖製造商 。
google mapmaker is a technology that empowers each of us to map what we know locally .	谷歌地圖製造者是一項科技 , 讓我們能繪製我們所知的地圖 。
people have used this software to map everything from roads to rivers , from schools to local businesses , and video stores to the corner store .	人們用這套軟體來繪製每樣東西 , 從道路到河流 , 從學校到當地的企業 , 及錄影商店到角落 。
nobel prize nominee hernando de soto recognized that the key to economic liftoff for most developing countries is to tap the vast amounts of uncapitalized land .	諾貝爾獎提名赫南多德索托發現大部分開發中國家的經濟起源的關鍵在於克服無數的土地 。
for example , a trillion dollars of real estate remains uncapitalized in india alone .	舉例來說 , 光在印度 , 就有一兆美金的房地產 , 仍然是不尋常的 。
in the last year alone , thousands of users in 170 countries have mapped millions of pieces of information , and created a map of a level of detail never thought viable .	光是在去年 , 170個國家就有數以千計的使用者繪製了數百萬個資訊 , 並創造出一張地圖 , 不可思議的地圖 。
and this was made possible by the power of passionate users everywhere .	這使得熱情使用者的力量無所不在 。
let's look at some of the maps being created by users right now .	咱們來看看一些用戶所創造出來的地圖 。
so , as we speak , people are mapping the world in these 170 countries .	所以 , 當我們說話時 , 在這170個國家 , 人們在繪製世界 。
you can see bridget in africa who just mapped a road in senegal .	你可以看到非洲的橋 , 剛在塞內加爾繪製了一條道路 。
and , closer to home , chalua , an n . g . road in bangalore .	離家很近 , 查爾 , 班加羅爾的一個n.g.路 。
this is the result of computational geometry , gesture recognition , and machine learning .	這是計算幾何學、姿勢認可和機器學習的結果 。
this is a victory of thousands of users , in hundreds of cities , one user , one edit at a time .	這是數以千計的使用者 , 在數百個城市裡 , 一個用戶 , 一次編輯 。
this is an invitation to the 70 percent of our unmapped planet .	這是對70%未開發的星球的邀請 。
welcome to the new world .	歡迎來到新世界 。
in 2003 , the palestinian village of budrus mounted a 10monthlong nonviolent protest to stop a barrier being built across their olive groves . did you hear about it ? didn't think so . brazilian filmmaker julia bacha asks why we only pay attention to violence in the israelpalestine conflict and not to the nonviolent leaders who may one day bring peace .	在2003年 , 布德魯斯村落登上了十個月的非暴力抗議 , 阻止了一道障礙 , 橫跨他們的橄欖樹林 。 你聽說過嗎 ? 巴西電影家朱利亞巴哈拉問為什麼我們只關心以色列衝突的暴力 , 而非暴力領導人 , 而非暴力的非暴力領袖 , 而非暴力的領導人 , 他們可能有一天會帶來和平 。
arts , communication , compassion , entertainment , film , peace , violence , war	藝術、溝通、同情、娛樂、電影、和平、暴力、戰爭、戰爭 。
julia bacha: pay attention to nonviolence	朱利亞巴哈:注意到非暴力行為 , 非暴力行為 。
for the last 8 years , i have dedicated my life to documenting the work of israelis and palestinians who are trying to end the conflict using peaceful means .	過去八年來 , 我致力於記錄以色列人和巴勒斯坦人的作品 , 他們試圖用和平的手段結束衝突 。
when i travel with my work across europe and the united states , one question always comes up: where is the palestinian gandhi ?	當我在歐洲和美國旅行時 , 總有一個問題出現了:巴勒斯坦甘地在哪裡 ?
why aren't palestinians using nonviolent resistance ?	為什麼巴勒斯坦人不用非暴力抗爭 ?
the challenge i face when i hear this question is that often i have just returned from the middle east where i spent my time filming dozens of palestinians who are using nonviolence to defend their lands and water resources from israeli soldiers and settlers .	當我聽到這個問題時 , 我面臨的挑戰是 , 我常常從中東回來 , 在那裡 , 我花了數十個時間拍攝無暴力的巴勒斯坦人 , 他們使用非暴力來保護他們的土地和水資源 , 來自以色列士兵和定居者 。
these leaders are trying to forge a massive national nonviolent movement to end the occupation and build peace in the region .	這些領導者試圖忘記一項巨大的全國非暴力運動 , 來終止該地區的職業和平 。
yet , most of you have probably never heard about them .	但 , 你們大部分人可能從來沒有聽過它們 。
this divide between what's happening on the ground and perceptions abroad is one of the key reasons why we don't have yet a palestinian peaceful resistance movement that has been successful .	在國外發生的事情和感知之間的分歧 , 是我們尚未擁有巴勒斯坦和平抗爭運動的關鍵原因之一 。
so i'm here today to talk about the power of attention , the power of your attention , and the emergence and development of nonviolent movements in the west bank , gaza and elsewhere but today , my case study is going to be palestine .	所以 , 我今天在這裡要談的是注意力的力量 , 關注的力量 , 以及在西岸、加薩、以及其他地方的非暴力運動的興起和發展 , 但現今 , 我的案例研究將會是巴勒斯坦 。
i believe that what's mostly missing for nonviolence to grow is not for palestinians to start adopting nonviolence , but for us to start paying attention to those who already are .	我相信 , 非暴力成長最少的不是巴勒斯坦人開始採用非暴力行為 , 而是讓我們開始注意那些已經有的人們 。
allow me to illustrate this point by taking you to this village called budrus .	讓我來說明一下這個點 , 讓我帶你們到這個叫做布德魯斯的村落 。
about seven years ago , they faced extinction , because israel announced it would build a separation barrier , and part of this barrier would be built on top of the village .	大約七年前 , 他們面臨滅絕 , 因為以色列宣佈要建造一個隔離障礙 , 其中一部分的障礙是建在村落的 。
they would lose 40 percent of their land and be surrounded , so they would lose free access to the rest of the west bank .	他們會失去百分之四十的土地 , 被包圍 , 所以他們會失去西岸的權利 。
through inspired local leadership , they launched a peaceful resistance campaign to stop that from happening .	透過當地的領導力 , 他們發起了和平的抗爭活動 , 來阻止這一切發生 。
let me show you some brief clips , so you have a sense for what that actually looked like on the ground .	讓我給你們看一些短片 , 所以你們可以理解在地面上看起來是什麼樣子 。
palestinian woman: we were told the wall would separate palestine from israel .	巴勒斯坦女人:我們被告知牆將巴勒斯坦和以色列分開 。
here in budrus , we realized the wall would steal our land .	在布德魯斯 , 我們發現牆會偷走我們的土地 。
israeli man: the fence has , in fact , created a solution to terror .	以色列男人:柵欄事實上 , 創造了恐怖的解決方案 。
man: today you're invited to a peaceful march .	男子:今天你被邀請去和平遊行 。
you are joined by dozens of your israeli brothers and sisters .	你被數十位以色列兄弟姐妹加入 。
israeli activist: nothing scares the army more than nonviolent opposition .	以色列的行動主義者:軍隊比非暴力的反對者更害怕 。
woman: we saw the men trying to push the soldiers , but none of them could do that .	女人:我們看到男人試著推動士兵 , 但沒有人能這麼做 。
but i think the girls could do it .	但我認為女孩們可以做到 。
fatah party member: we must empty our minds of traditional thinking .	法塔赫派對會員:我們必須清空傳統思維的思維 。
hamas party member: we were in complete harmony , and we wanted to spread it to all of palestine .	哈馬斯黨員:我們完全和諧 , 我們想要把它散播給所有的巴勒斯坦 。
chanting: one united nation .	聊天:一個聯合國 。
fatah , hamas and the popular front !	法塔、哈馬斯和流行的前線 !
news anchor: the clashes over the fence continue .	新聞主持:圍欄持續 。
reporter: israeli border police were sent to disperse the crowd .	記者:以色列邊界警察被送去散播群眾 。
they were allowed to use any force necessary .	他們被允許使用任何必要的力量 。
man: these are live bullets .	男人:這些是活的子彈 。
it's like fallujah . shooting everywhere .	這就好像失敗了 。 到處開槍 。
israeli activist: i was sure we were all going to die .	以色列的行動主義者:我相信我們都會死 。
but there were others around me who weren't even cowering .	但在我身邊 , 甚至沒有牛 。
israeli soldier: a nonviolent protest is not going to stop the [unclear] .	以色列士兵:非暴力抗議不會阻止它 。
protester: this is a peaceful march .	普林斯特:這是和平的遊行 。
there is no need to use violence .	沒有需要使用暴力 。
chanting: we can do it ! we can do it !	聊天:我們能做到 ! 我們可以做到 !
julia bacha: when i first heard about the story of budrus , i was surprised that the international media had failed to cover the extraordinary set of events that happened seven years ago , in 2003 .	朱利亞巴哈:當我第一次聽說布德魯斯的故事時 , 我很驚訝國際媒體並沒有報導七年前發生的非凡事件發生 。
what was even more surprising was the fact that budrus was successful .	更令人驚訝的是布德魯斯成功了 。
the residents , after 10 months of peaceful resistance , convinced the israeli government to move the route of the barrier off their lands and to the green line , which is the internationally recognized boundary between israel and the palestinian territories .	居民們 , 經過10個月的和平抗爭 , 說服以色列政府把障礙從他們的土地上移除 , 移到綠線上 , 也就是國際認可以色列和巴勒斯坦領土之間的界線 。
the resistance in budrus has since spread to villages across the west bank and to palestinian neighborhoods in jerusalem .	布德魯斯的抵抗力已經散播到整個西岸村落 , 到耶路撒冷的巴勒斯坦社區 。
yet the media remains mostly silent on these stories .	然而 , 媒體仍然沉默於這些故事 。
this silence carries profound consequences for the likelihood that nonviolence can grow , or even survive , in palestine .	這種沉默會帶來深遠的後果 , 造成非暴力的可能性 , 甚至在巴勒斯坦存活 。
violent resistance and nonviolent resistance share one very important thing in common ; they are both a form of theater seeking an audience to their cause .	暴力抗拒和非暴力抗拒有著一個非常重要的共通點 , 它們都是戲院尋求觀眾的形式 。
if violent actors are the only ones constantly getting frontpage covers and attracting international attention to the palestinian issue , it becomes very hard for nonviolent leaders to make the case to their communities that civil disobedience is a viable option in addressing their plight .	如果暴力演員是唯一經常被封鎖的報導 , 吸引國際關注巴勒斯坦議題的議題 , 對他們的社區來說 , 非暴力領袖來說 , 民間不服從是解決他們的困境的可行選項 。
the power of attention is probably going to come as no surprise to the parents in the room .	注意力的力量可能對房間的父母也不會感到驚訝 。
the surest way to make your child throw increasingly louder tantrums is by giving him attention the first time he throws a fit .	讓孩子變得越來越大聲的螞蟻 , 最確定的方式就是第一次讓他注意到他丟掉一個適合的時刻 。
the tantrum will become what childhood psychologists call a functional behavior , since the child has learned that he can get parental attention out of it .	幻肢會變成兒時心理學家所謂的功能性行為 , 因為孩子已經知道他能從中得到父母的注意力 。
parents can incentivize or disincentivize behavior simply by giving or withdrawing attention to their children .	父母可以鼓勵或不獎勵行為 , 僅僅僅是給予孩子們注意或忽略他們的孩子 。
but that's true for adults too .	但對成人來說也是如此 。
in fact , the behavior of entire communities and countries can be influenced , depending on where the international community chooses to focus its attention .	事實上 , 整個社區和國家的行為會受到影響 , 取決於國際社會選擇要把注意力聚焦的地方 。
i believe that at the core of ending the conflict in the middle east and bringing peace is for us to transform nonviolence into a functional behavior by giving a lot more attention to the nonviolent leaders on the ground today .	我相信 , 終結中東衝突的核心 , 帶來和平 , 是我們把非暴力行為轉化為一個功能性行為 , 做法是讓現今非暴力領袖更加關注非暴力領袖 。
in the course of taking my film to villages in the west bank , in gaza and in east jerusalem , i have seen the impact that even one documentary film can have in influencing the transformation .	在拍攝我拍攝的影片 , 到西岸、加薩 , 以及東耶路撒冷的村莊 , 我看到即使是一部紀錄片也能影響轉變 。
in a village called wallajeh , which sits very close to jerusalem , the community was facing a very similar plight to budrus .	在一個叫瓦拉je的村子裡 , 位在耶路撒冷附近 , 社區正面臨類似的困境 。
they were going to be surrounded , lose a lot of their lands and not have freedom of access , either to the west bank or jerusalem .	他們會被包圍 , 失去許多土地 , 沒有任何自由 , 不論是西岸或耶路撒冷 。
they had been using nonviolence for about two years but had grown disenchanted since nobody was paying attention .	兩年來 , 他們一直在使用非暴力行為 , 但從沒人注意到他們成長的過程中 , 他們已經被剝奪 。
so we organized a screening .	所以我們組織了一個螢幕 。
a week later , they held the most wellattended and disciplined demonstration to date .	一個禮拜後 , 他們舉辦了最好的示威 , 展現到目前為止 。
the organizers say that the villagers , upon seeing the story of budrus documented in a film , felt that there were indeed people following what they were doing , that people cared .	組織者說 , 村民們 , 看到布德魯士的故事 , 在電影中 , 感覺到確實有人在追蹤他們在做的事 , 人們在乎 。
so they kept on going .	所以他們繼續走下去 。
on the israeli side , there is a new peace movement called solidariot , which means solidarity in hebrew .	在以色列 , 有一個新的和平運動 , 叫做索利達里 , 意思是希伯來語的團結 。
the leaders of this movement have been using budrus as one of their primary recruiting tools .	這個運動的領導者一直用布德魯斯作為他們主要的招募工具之一 。
they report that israelis who had never been active before , upon seeing the film , understand the power of nonviolence and start joining their activities .	他們說 , 以色列人從來沒有活躍過 , 看電影 , 了解非暴力的力量 , 開始加入他們的活動 。
the examples of wallajeh and the solidariot movement show that even a smallbudget independent film can play a role in transforming nonviolence into a functional behavior .	華拉jeh和slidariot運動顯示即使是小型的獨立製片也能扮演一個角色 , 將非暴力轉變成一個功能行為 。
now imagine the power that big media players could have if they started covering the weekly nonviolent demonstrations happening in villages like bil'in , ni'lin , wallajeh , in jerusalem neighborhoods like sheikh jarrah and silwan the nonviolent leaders would become more visible , valued and effective in their work .	想像一下 , 大型媒體玩家能夠擁有的力量 , 如果他們開始報導每週的非暴力演示 , 在村落裡發生 , 比如比利利、尼林、瓦拉、瓦約、耶路撒冷的社區 , 如夏克•賈拉和絲瓦 , 非暴力領導人在工作中會變得更明顯、更有價值、更有效率 。
i believe that the most important thing is to understand that if we don't pay attention to these efforts , they are invisible , and it's as if they never happened .	我相信最重要的是要了解 , 如果我們不注意這些努力 , 它們是看不見的 , 就好像他們從來沒有發生過 。
but i have seen first hand that if we do , they will multiply .	但 , 我先看過如果我們這麼做 , 他們會乘以乘法 。
if they multiply , their influence will grow in the overall israelipalestinian conflict .	假如他們相乘 , 他們的影響會在以色列的衝突中成長 。
and theirs is the kind of influence that can finally unblock the situation .	他們的影響力就是那種最終能解開情況的影響力 。
these leaders have proven that nonviolence works in places like budrus .	這些領袖證明了非暴力行為在布德魯斯之類的地方 。
let's give them attention so they can prove it works everywhere .	讓我們把注意力給他們 , 讓他們可以隨時證明它是有效的 。
simon sinek has a simple but powerful model for inspirational leadership all starting with a golden circle and the question " why ? " his examples include apple , martin luther king , and the wright brothers . . .	西蒙辛克有個簡單但有力的領導模式 , 都是來自金圈 , 問題是:為什麼 ? 他的例子包括蘋果、馬丁路德金恩 , 以及萊特兄弟 。
bullseye , business , entrepreneur , leadership , sales , selling , success	牛兒、企業、企業家、領導力、銷售、銷售、成功、企業 。
simon sinek: how great leaders inspire action	西蒙.桑克:偉大的領導人如何啟發行動 ?
how do you explain when things don't go as we assume ?	你要如何解釋當事情不如我們所想的那樣 ?
or better , how do you explain when others are able to achieve things that seem to defy all of the assumptions ?	或更好的是 , 你要如何解釋 , 當其他人能夠達成那些看似違反所有假設的事物 ?
for example: why is apple so innovative ?	例如:為什麼蘋果如此創新 ?
year after year , after year , after year , they're more innovative than all their competition .	年復一年 , 年復一年 , 他們比所有的競爭都更有創意 。
and yet , they're just a computer company .	然而 , 他們只是一家電腦公司 。
they're just like everyone else .	他們就像其他人一樣 。
they have the same access to the same talent , the same agencies , the same consultants , the same media .	他們有相同的才能 , 同樣的機構 , 同樣的顧問 , 同樣的媒體 。
then why is it that they seem to have something different ?	那麼 , 為什麼他們似乎有不同的東西 ?
why is it that martin luther king led the civil rights movement ?	為什麼馬丁路德金恩帶領民權運動 ?
he wasn't the only man who suffered in a precivil rights america , and he certainly wasn't the only great orator of the day .	他不是唯一一個在美國受苦的人 , 他肯定不是那天唯一的偉大的演說者 。
and why is it that the wright brothers were able to figure out controlled , powered man flight when there were certainly other teams who were better qualified , better funded . . .	為什麼萊特兄弟能夠想出控制權力的飛行 , 尤其是其他更有資格、更有資金的團隊......
and they didn't achieve powered man flight , and the wright brothers beat them to it .	他們沒有實現人類飛行 , 萊特兄弟打敗了飛機 。
there's something else at play here .	這裡還有別的東西在演奏 。
about three and a half years ago i made a discovery .	大約三年半前 , 我做了一項發現 。
and this discovery profoundly changed my view on how i thought the world worked , and it even profoundly changed the way in which i operate in it .	這項發現深深地改變了我對世界運作的看法 , 甚至深深改變了我對世界的運作方式 。
as it turns out , there's a pattern .	結果發現 , 有一種模式 。
as it turns out , all the great and inspiring leaders and organizations in the world whether it's apple or martin luther king or the wright brothers they all think , act and communicate the exact same way .	事實證明 , 世界上所有的偉大、鼓舞人心的領導人和組織 , 不論是蘋果、馬丁路德金 , 或是他們都認為的萊特兄弟 , 都採取相同的方式來溝通 。
and it's the complete opposite to everyone else .	這完全相反 。
all i did was codify it , and it's probably the world's simplest idea .	我所做的就是編寫它 , 它可能是世界上最簡單的點子 。
i call it the golden circle .	我稱之為黃金圈 。
why ? how ? what ?	為什麼 ? 怎麼做 ? 什麼 ?
this little idea explains why some organizations and some leaders are able to inspire where others aren't .	這個小點子解釋了為什麼有些組織和一些領袖能夠啟發其他人不在哪裡 。
let me define the terms really quickly .	讓我很快的定義一下這個詞 。
every single person , every single organization on the planet knows what they do , 100 percent .	地球上每一個人 , 每一個組織都知道自己在做什麼 , 百分之百 。
some know how they do it , whether you call it your differentiated value proposition or your proprietary process or your usp .	有些人知道他們怎麼做 , 不管你稱它為你不同的價值提議 , 或你的屬性過程 , 或你的usp 。
but very , very few people or organizations know why they do what they do .	但很少人或組織知道他們為什麼要做事 。
and by " why " i don't mean " to make a profit . "	根據 「 為什麼 」 我不是要 「 賺錢 」 的意思 。
that's a result . it's always a result .	這是結果 。 結果總是是結果 。
by " why , " i mean: what's your purpose ?	根據 「 為什麼 」 我的意思是:你的目的是什麼 ?
what's your cause ? what's your belief ?	你的原因是什麼 ? 你的信念是什麼 ?
why does your organization exist ?	你的組織為什麼存在 ?
why do you get out of bed in the morning ?	為什麼早上要離開床 ?
and why should anyone care ?	為什麼有人要在乎 ?
well , as a result , the way we think , the way we act , the way we communicate is from the outside in .	結果就是 , 我們思考的方式 , 我們行動的方式 , 我們溝通的方式是從外部傳遞出來的 。
it's obvious . we go from the clearest thing to the fuzziest thing .	很明顯 , 我們從最清晰的東西到最瘋狂的東西 。
but the inspired leaders and the inspired organizations regardless of their size , regardless of their industry all think , act and communicate from the inside out .	但激發人心的領導人和激勵人心的組織 , 不論他們大小 , 不論他們的產業都認為、行動 , 以及從內部溝通 。
let me give you an example .	讓我舉個例子 。
i use apple because they're easy to understand and everybody gets it .	我用蘋果是因為它們很容易理解 , 每個人都懂 。
if apple were like everyone else , a marketing message from them might sound like this: " we make great computers .	如果蘋果跟其他人一樣 , 行銷訊息也許聽起來會像這樣: 「 我們製造出很棒的電腦 。
they're beautifully designed , simple to use and user friendly .	它們設計得很漂亮 , 很簡單 , 很容易使用和使用者 。
want to buy one ? " " meh . "	想要買一台嗎 ? 」 「 啊 。 」
and that's how most of us communicate .	這就是我們大多數人溝通的方式 。
that's how most marketing is done , that's how most sales is done and that's how most of us communicate interpersonally .	大部分的行銷是這樣做的 , 大部分的銷售是這樣做的 , 這就是我們大多數人之間的溝通方式 。
we say what we do , we say how we're different or how we're better and we expect some sort of a behavior , a purchase , a vote , something like that .	我們說我們所做的事 , 我們說我們是不同的 , 或我們如何更好 , 期待某種行為 , 購買、投票 , 諸如此類 。
here's our new law firm: we have the best lawyers with the biggest clients , we always perform for our clients who do business with us .	這是我們的新法律公司:我們有最好的律師 , 有最大的客戶 , 我們總是為我們的客戶和我們做生意 。
here's our new car: it gets great gas mileage , it has leather seats , buy our car .	這是我們的新車:它有很大的氣體 , 它有皮革座位 , 買我們的車 。
here's how apple actually communicates .	蘋果是如何溝通的 。
" everything we do , we believe in challenging the status quo .	「 我們所做的每件事 , 我們都相信挑戰現狀 。
we believe in thinking differently .	我們相信用不同的方式思考 。
the way we challenge the status quo is by making our products beautifully designed , simple to use and user friendly .	我們挑戰現狀的方式是讓我們的產品設計漂亮 , 簡單地使用和使用友善 。
we just happen to make great computers .	我們剛好能製造出很棒的電腦 。
want to buy one ? "	想要買一台嗎 ? 」
totally different right ? you're ready to buy a computer from me .	完全不一樣了嗎 ? 你準備好跟我買一台電腦了 。
all i did was reverse the order of the information .	我所做的只是逆轉資訊的順序 。
what it proves to us is that people don't buy what you do ; people buy why you do it .	它向我們證明 , 人們不買你做什麼 ; 人們買你為何這麼做 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼要這麼做 。
this explains why every single person in this room is perfectly comfortable buying a computer from apple .	這解釋了為什麼在座的每個人都很舒服從蘋果購買一台電腦 。
but we're also perfectly comfortable buying an mp3 player from apple , or a phone from apple , or a dvr from apple .	但我們也非常自在地購買蘋果的mp3播放器 , 或蘋果的手機 , 或蘋果的dvr 。
but , as i said before , apple's just a computer company .	但 , 就像我之前說的 , 蘋果只是一家電腦公司 。
there's nothing that distinguishes them structurally from any of their competitors .	沒有任何與他們競爭者的結構分辨出來的 。
their competitors are all equally qualified to make all of these products .	他們的競爭者都同等資格做出這些產品 。
in fact , they tried .	事實上 , 他們試過 。
a few years ago , gateway came out with flat screen tvs .	幾年前 , gateway出版了平面螢幕電視 。
they're eminently qualified to make flat screen tvs .	他們很明顯地申請製作平面螢幕 。
they've been making flat screen monitors for years .	他們多年來都在做平面螢幕監視器 。
dell came out with mp3 players and pdas , and they make great quality products , and they can make perfectly welldesigned products and nobody bought one .	dell和mp3玩家和pdas一起出發 , 他們製造了很棒的產品 , 他們可以做出完美的設計 , 沒有人買的 。
in fact , talking about it now , we can't even imagine buying an mp3 player from dell .	事實上 , 談到現在 , 我們甚至無法想像購買一名mp3球員 。
why would you buy an mp3 player from a computer company ?	為什麼要從電腦公司買mp3球員 ?
but we do it every day .	但我們每天都這樣做 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼要這麼做 。
the goal is not to do business with everybody who needs what you have .	目標並不是要跟任何需要的東西做生意 。
the goal is to do business with people who believe what you believe .	目標是和相信你所相信的人做生意 。
here's the best part: none of what i'm telling you is my opinion .	最棒的部分是:我告訴你們的不是我的意見 。
it's all grounded in the tenets of biology .	全都在生物學的網絡中生存 。
not psychology , biology .	不是心理學、生物學 。
if you look at a crosssection of the human brain , looking from the top down , what you see is the human brain is actually broken into three major components that correlate perfectly with the golden circle .	如果你觀察人類大腦的十字路口 , 從下面往下看 , 你會發現人類的大腦其實是分成三個主要元件 , 和黃金圈完全相關 。
our newest brain , our homo sapien brain , our neocortex , corresponds with the " what " level .	我們最新的大腦 , 我們的智人大腦 , 我們的新皮層 , 和 「 什麼 」 等級相對應 。
the neocortex is responsible for all of our rational and analytical thought and language .	新皮層負責所有的理性、分析的想法和語言 。
the middle two sections make up our limbic brains , and our limbic brains are responsible for all of our feelings , like trust and loyalty .	中間兩個部分組成了我們的邊緣大腦 , 我們的邊緣大腦負責所有的感受 , 比如信任和忠誠 。
it's also responsible for all human behavior , all decisionmaking , and it has no capacity for language .	它也負責所有人類的行為 , 所有的決策 , 且它沒有語言的能力 。
in other words , when we communicate from the outside in , yes , people can understand vast amounts of complicated information like features and benefits and facts and figures .	換句話說 , 當我們從外部溝通時 , 是的 , 人們能了解大量複雜的資訊 , 如特徵、好處、事實和數字 。
it just doesn't drive behavior .	它不會驅動行為 。
when we can communicate from the inside out , we're talking directly to the part of the brain that controls behavior , and then we allow people to rationalize it with the tangible things we say and do .	當我們從內部溝通時 , 我們直接和控制行為的部分談話 , 然後我們讓人們以我們所說及做的事情將它合理化 。
this is where gut decisions come from .	這就是腸道決策的來源 。
you know , sometimes you can give somebody all the facts and figures , and they say , " i know what all the facts and details say , but it just doesn't feel right . "	你知道 , 有時候你可以給別人所有事實和數字 , 他們會說: 「 我知道所有事實和細節都說了什麼 , 但這感覺不對 。 」
why would we use that verb , it doesn't " feel " right ?	為什麼我們要用這個動詞 , 感覺不對 ?
because the part of the brain that controls decisionmaking doesn't control language .	因為控制決策的大腦區域無法控制語言 。
and the best we can muster up is , " i don't know . it just doesn't feel right . "	最好的一點就是: 「 我不知道 , 感覺不對 。 」
or sometimes you say you're leading with your heart , or you're leading with your soul .	或者有時候你說你是帶著你的心 , 或者你是帶著你的靈魂領導 。
well , i hate to break it to you , those aren't other body parts controlling your behavior .	我討厭打破你 , 那些不是身體的部位控制你的行為 。
it's all happening here in your limbic brain , the part of the brain that controls decisionmaking and not language .	這一切都發生在你的邊緣腦中 , 大腦控制決策 , 而非語言的部分 。
but if you don't know why you do what you do , and people respond to why you do what you do , then how will you ever get people to vote for you , or buy something from you , or , more importantly , be loyal and want to be a part of what it is that you do .	但如果你不知道你為什麼做事 , 人們會回應你為什麼做事 , 那麼你會如何讓人們投票給你 , 或從你身上買東西 , 或更重要的是 , 忠誠 , 想要成為你做的事的一部分 。
again , the goal is not just to sell to people who need what you have ; the goal is to sell to people who believe what you believe .	同樣的 , 目標不只是賣給需要的人 ; 目標是賣給那些相信你所相信的人 。
the goal is not just to hire people who need a job ; it's to hire people who believe what you believe .	目標不只是僱用需要工作的人 ; 而是僱用那些相信你所相信的人 。
i always say that , you know , if you hire people just because they can do a job , they'll work for your money , but if you hire people who believe what you believe , they'll work for you with blood and sweat and tears .	我總是說 , 如果你雇用人們因為他們能做事 , 他們會為你的錢工作 , 但如果你雇用你相信你所相信的人 , 他們會用血、流汗和淚來工作 。
and nowhere else is there a better example of this than with the wright brothers .	沒有其他地方比萊特兄弟更好的例子 。
most people don't know about samuel pierpont langley .	大部分的人不知道samuelpierpontlangley 。
and back in the early 20th century , the pursuit of powered man flight was like the dot com of the day .	回到二十世紀初 , 追求權力飛行的追求就像白天的網路com一樣 。
everybody was trying it .	每個人都在嘗試 。
and samuel pierpont langley had , what we assume , to be the recipe for success .	而samuelpierpontlangley認為成功的配方
i mean , even now , you ask people , " why did your product or why did your company fail ? "	我是說 , 即使是現在 , 你問人們: 「 你的產品為什麼會失敗 ? 為什麼公司會失敗 ? 」
and people always give you the same permutation of the same three things: undercapitalized , the wrong people , bad market conditions .	人們總是給予你相同的三件事:被低估、錯誤的人、糟糕的市場條件 。
it's always the same three things , so let's explore that .	永遠都是相同的三件事 , 讓我們來探索它 。
samuel pierpont langley was given 50 , 000 dollars by the war department to figure out this flying machine .	samuelpierpontlangley得到了五萬美金的戰爭部門 , 想出這台飛行機器 。
money was no problem .	錢沒有問題 。
he held a seat at harvard and worked at the smithsonian and was extremely wellconnected ; he knew all the big minds of the day .	他在哈佛舉辦一席 , 在史密森尼工作 , 非常有連結 , 他很清楚白天所有的心智 。
he hired the best minds money could find and the market conditions were fantastic .	他雇用最好的心靈金錢 , 可以找到 , 市場條件很棒 。
the new york times followed him around everywhere , and everyone was rooting for langley .	紐約時報到處都跟著他 , 每個人都根深蒂固 。
then how come we've never heard of samuel pierpont langley ?	那我們怎麼從來沒有聽過samuelpierpontlangley ?
a few hundred miles away in dayton ohio , orville and wilbur wright , they had none of what we consider to be the recipe for success .	幾百英哩遠在俄亥俄州 , 奧維爾和威爾布萊特 , 他們沒有我們認為成功的配方 。
they had no money ; they paid for their dream with the proceeds from their bicycle shop ; not a single person on the wright brothers' team had a college education , not even orville or wilbur ; and the new york times followed them around nowhere .	他們沒有錢 , 他們付錢給他們的夢想 , 用自行車店裡的收入 ; 萊特兄弟的團隊沒有任何一個人有大學教育 , 甚至沒有威爾或威爾伯 ; 紐約時報也跟著他們走 。
the difference was , orville and wilbur were driven by a cause , by a purpose , by a belief .	差別在於 , 奧維爾和威爾布爾被一個目標所驅動 , 被一個信念所驅動 。
they believed that if they could figure out this flying machine , it'll change the course of the world .	他們相信 , 如果他們能搞清楚飛行機器 , 它就會改變世界的軌道 。
samuel pierpont langley was different .	samuelpierpontlangley不一樣 。
he wanted to be rich , and he wanted to be famous .	他想要變富有 , 他想要成為有名的 。
he was in pursuit of the result .	他在追求結果 。
he was in pursuit of the riches .	他在追求富裕 。
and lo and behold , look what happened .	你看 , 發生了什麼事 。
the people who believed in the wright brothers' dream worked with them with blood and sweat and tears .	相信萊特兄弟的夢想和血汗、淚水合作的人 。
the others just worked for the paycheck .	另外一些人才剛為付錢工作 。
and they tell stories of how every time the wright brothers went out , they would have to take five sets of parts , because that's how many times they would crash before they came in for supper .	他們說的故事是每當萊特兄弟出去的時候 , 他們就要服用五組零件 , 因為這是他們進入供應器之前會發生多少次 。
and , eventually , on december 17th , 1903 , the wright brothers took flight , and no one was there to even experience it .	到了1903年12月17日 , 萊特兄弟一起飛 , 甚至沒有人去體驗它 。
we found out about it a few days later .	幾天後我們就發現了 。
and further proof that langley was motivated by the wrong thing: the day the wright brothers took flight , he quit .	更進一步的證明 , 蘭利的動機是錯誤的:萊特兄弟搭飛機的那天 , 他辭職了 。
he could have said , " that's an amazing discovery , guys , and i will improve upon your technology , " but he didn't .	他可能會說: 「 那真是個驚人的發現 , 各位 , 我會改善你的科技 。 」 但他沒有 。
he wasn't first , he didn't get rich , he didn't get famous so he quit .	他不是第一個 , 他沒有變有錢 , 他沒有變有名 , 所以他放棄了 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼要這麼做 。
and if you talk about what you believe , you will attract those who believe what you believe .	如果你談到你所相信的事物 , 你會吸引那些相信你所相信的人 。
but why is it important to attract those who believe what you believe ?	但為什麼要吸引那些相信你所相信的人呢 ?
something called the law of diffusion of innovation , and if you don't know the law , you definitely know the terminology .	所謂的創新定律 , 如果你不知道法律 , 你絕對知道術語 。
the first two and a half percent of our population are our innovators .	我們人口的前2.5%是我們的創新者 。
the next 13 and a half percent of our population are our early adopters .	接下來的13.5%是我們早期使用者 。
the next 34 percent are your early majority , your late majority and your laggards .	下一個百分之三十四是你早期的多數人 , 你的多數人 , 和你的大眾 。
the only reason these people buy touch tone phones is because you can't buy rotary phones anymore .	這些人購買觸覺電話的唯一理由 , 就是因為你已經買不起了壞電話了 。
we all sit at various places at various times on this scale , but what the law of diffusion of innovation tells us is that if you want massmarket success or massmarket acceptance of an idea , you cannot have it until you achieve this tipping point between 15 and 18 percent market penetration , and then the system tips .	我們都坐在不同時間點 , 但創新的傳播法則告訴我們 , 如果你想要大眾市場成功或大眾市場接受這個想法 , 直到你達到15%到18%之間的趨勢 , 再來是系統 。
and i love asking businesses , " what's your conversion on new business ? "	我喜歡問企業: 「 你對新事業的轉變是什麼 ? 」
and they love to tell you , " oh , it's about 10 percent , " proudly .	他們很喜歡跟你說: 「 喔 , 大約是10% 。 」
well , you can trip over 10 percent of the customers .	嗯 , 你可以超過百分之十的客戶 。
we all have about 10 percent who just " get it . "	我們都有大約百分之十的 「 了解它 」 。
that's how we describe them , right ?	這就是我們描述它們的方式 , 對吧 ?
that's like that gut feeling , " oh , they just get it . "	這就像是那種直覺的感覺: 「 喔 , 他們就懂了 。 」
the problem is: how do you find the ones that get it before you're doing business with them versus the ones who don't get it ?	問題是:你要如何找到那些在和他們做生意前做的事 , 而不是那些不懂的人 ?
so it's this here , this little gap that you have to close , as jeffrey moore calls it , " crossing the chasm " because , you see , the early majority will not try something until someone else has tried it first .	所以這就是這個 , 你必須關閉的小差距 , 如同jefreymoore所說的 , " 交叉迷人 " 因為 , 你看 , 早期大部分的人不會嘗試一些東西 , 直到有人先試過 。
and these guys , the innovators and the early adopters , they're comfortable making those gut decisions .	這些人 , 創新者和早期採用者 , 他們很自在地做出這些腸道決策 。
they're more comfortable making those intuitive decisions that are driven by what they believe about the world and not just what product is available .	他們更自在地做出那些由他們所相信世界所驅動的直覺決策 , 而不只是產品的可用性 。
these are the people who stood in line for six hours to buy an iphone when they first came out , when you could have just walked into the store the next week and bought one off the shelf .	他們是排隊排隊六個小時買iphone的人 , 當他們第一次出來時 , 當你下週走進商店 , 買了一台手機 。
these are the people who spent 40 , 000 dollars on flat screen tvs when they first came out , even though the technology was substandard .	這些人花了四萬美金在平面電視上 , 剛剛出現的時候 , 花了四萬美金 , 儘管這項技術是訂閱的 。
and , by the way , they didn't do it because the technology was so great ; they did it for themselves .	順帶一提 , 他們沒有這麼做 , 因為這項技術太棒了 , 他們自己做到了 。
it's because they wanted to be first .	那是因為他們想要成為第一人 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it and what you do simply proves what you believe .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼做這件事 , 以及你做的事 , 只要證明你所相信的事 。
in fact , people will do the things that prove what they believe .	事實上 , 人們會做些證明他們所相信的事 。
the reason that person bought the iphone in the first six hours , stood in line for six hours , was because of what they believed about the world , and how they wanted everybody to see them: they were first .	前六個小時買下iphone的原因 , 排隊六個小時 , 是因為他們對這個世界的信念 , 以及他們希望大家見到的樣子:他們是第一個 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼要這麼做 。
so let me give you a famous example , a famous failure and a famous success of the law of diffusion of innovation .	讓我舉個有名的例子 , 一個有名的失敗和一個著名的創新定律 。
first , the famous failure .	首先 , 著名的失敗 。
it's a commercial example .	這是一個商業的例子 。
as we said before , a second ago , the recipe for success is money and the right people and the right market conditions , right ? you should have success then .	如同我們先前所說的 , 成功的食譜是金錢、對的人、對的市場狀況 , 對吧 ? 你應該有成功 。
from the time tivo came out about eight or nine years ago to this current day , they are the single highestquality product on the market , hands down , there is no dispute .	從八、九年前 , tivo出來到現今 , 他們是市場上最高品質的產品 , 手向下 , 沒有爭議 。
they were extremely wellfunded .	他們非常有資格 。
market conditions were fantastic .	市場條件很棒 。
i mean , we use tivo as verb .	我的意思是 , 我們用tivo作為動詞 。
i tivo stuff on my piece of junk time warner dvr all the time .	我經常在垃圾時間華納dvr身上提煉東西 。
but tivo's a commercial failure .	但tivo是個商業失敗 。
they've never made money .	他們從來沒有賺到錢 。
and when they went ipo , their stock was at about 30 or 40 dollars and then plummeted , and it's never traded above 10 .	當他們去ipo , 他們的股票價大約是三十到四十美金然後從來沒有超過十美金的交易
in fact , i don't think it's even traded above six , except for a couple of little spikes .	事實上 , 我不認為它在六號以上的交易 , 除了幾個小點 。
because you see , when tivo launched their product they told us all what they had .	因為你知道 , 當tivo發表他們的產品他們告訴我們他們所有的產品 。
they said , " we have a product that pauses live tv , skips commercials , rewinds live tv and memorizes your viewing habits without you even asking . "	他們說: 「 我們的產品會暫停現場電視、跳過廣告、rewinds現場電視 , 並記住你甚至沒有問過的視覺習慣 。 」
and the cynical majority said , " we don't believe you .	多數人說: 「 我們不相信你 。
we don't need it . we don't like it .	我們不需要它 , 我們不喜歡它 。
you're scaring us . "	你害怕我們 。 」
what if they had said , " if you're the kind of person who likes to have total control over every aspect of your life , boy , do we have a product for you .	如果他們說: 「 如果你是那種想要完全掌控生活的人們 , 天啊 , 我們有你的產品給你 。
it pauses live tv , skips commercials , memorizes your viewing habits , etc . , etc . "	它會暫停現場電視、跳過廣告 , 記住你的視覺習慣等等 。 」
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it , and what you do simply serves as the proof of what you believe .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼 , 而你所做的就是證明你所相信的 。
now let me give you a successful example of the law of diffusion of innovation .	現在讓我給你們一個成功的例子 , 說明創新的傳播法則 。
in the summer of 1963 , 250 , 000 people showed up on the mall in washington to hear dr . king speak .	1963年夏天 , 有25萬人出現在華盛頓大廳 , 聽見金恩博士演講 。
they sent out no invitations , and there was no website to check the date .	他們沒有發送邀請 , 沒有網站去查看日期 。
how do you do that ?	你是怎麼做到的 ?
well , dr . king wasn't the only man in america who was a great orator .	金恩博士不是美國唯一一個是偉大的演說者 。
he wasn't the only man in america who suffered in a precivil rights america .	他不是美國唯一受過公民權威的男人 。
in fact , some of his ideas were bad .	事實上 , 他的一些想法很糟 。
but he had a gift .	但他有一個禮物 。
he didn't go around telling people what needed to change in america .	他沒有到處告訴人們美國需要什麼才能改變 。
he went around and told people what he believed .	他四處去告訴人們他所相信的 。
" i believe , i believe , i believe , " he told people .	「 我相信 , 我相信 , 我相信 , 」 他告訴人們 。
and people who believed what he believed took his cause , and they made it their own , and they told people .	相信他所相信的成因的人 , 讓他成為自己 , 他們告訴人們 。
and some of those people created structures to get the word out to even more people .	其中一些人創造了結構 , 讓更多人發出這個詞 。
and lo and behold , 250 , 000 people showed up on the right day at the right time to hear him speak .	沒錯 , 有25萬人在對的日子 , 聽到他說話 。
how many of them showed up for him ?	有多少人為他出現 ?
they showed up for themselves .	他們為了自己而出現 。
it's what they believed about america that got them to travel in a bus for eight hours to stand in the sun in washington in the middle of august .	這是他們相信的美國 , 讓他們在巴士旅行了八個小時 , 站在華盛頓中期 , 站在華盛頓 。
it's what they believed , and it wasn't about black versus white: 25 percent of the audience was white .	這是他們所相信的 , 重點不是黑人和白人:百分之二十五的觀眾是白人 。
dr . king believed that there are two types of laws in this world: those that are made by a higher authority and those that are made by man .	金恩博士相信在這個世界上有兩種法律:由較高權威所製成的 , 以及由人類所製造的那些法律 。
and not until all the laws that are made by man are consistent with the laws that are made by the higher authority will we live in a just world .	除非人類所制定的所有法律都與較高權威所制定的法律一致 , 不管我們生活在一個公平的世界裡 。
it just so happened that the civil rights movement was the perfect thing to help him bring his cause to life .	剛好發生了 , 民權運動是幫助他帶來生命的完美目標 。
we followed , not for him , but for ourselves .	我們追隨 , 不是為了他 , 而是為了我們自己 。
and , by the way , he gave the " i have a dream " speech , not the " i have a plan " speech .	順帶一提 , 他給了 「 我有一個夢想 」 演講 , 而不是 「 我有一個計畫 」 。
listen to politicians now , with their comprehensive 12point plans .	現在聽聽政治人物 , 他們全面的12點計劃 。
they're not inspiring anybody .	他們沒有啟發任何人 。
because there are leaders and there are those who lead .	因為有領導者 , 也有領導者 。
leaders hold a position of power or authority , but those who lead inspire us .	領導者掌握了權力或權威的位置 , 但那些領導者鼓舞了我們的人 。
whether they're individuals or organizations , we follow those who lead , not because we have to , but because we want to .	不論是個人或組織 , 我們會追隨那些領導者 , 不是因為我們需要 , 而是因為我們想要 。
we follow those who lead , not for them , but for ourselves .	我們遵循那些領導的人 , 不是為了他們 , 而是為了我們自己 。
and it's those who start with " why " that have the ability to inspire those around them or find others who inspire them .	那些從 「 為什麼 」 開始的人 , 能夠啟發他們周遭的人 , 或找到啟發他們的人 。
how do you remember where you parked your car ? how do you know if you're moving in the right direction ? neuroscientist neil burgess studies the neural mechanisms that map the space around us , and how they link to memory and imagination .	你怎麼記得你在哪裡停車 ? 你怎麼知道你在正確的方向上移動 ? 神經科學家尼爾堡堡 , 研究我們周圍的神經機制 , 以及它們如何連結記憶力和想像力 。
brain , cognitive science , exploration , neuroscience , science	大腦、認知科學、探索、神經科學、科學、科學、科學 。
neil burgess: how your brain tells you where you are	尼爾堡:你的大腦如何告訴你你現在的位置 。
when we park in a big parking lot , how do we remember where we parked our car ?	當我們在大停車場停車時 , 我們要如何記住我們停車的位置 ?
here's the problem facing homer .	這是荷馬所面臨的問題 。
and we're going to try to understand what's happening in his brain .	我們會試著去了解他腦中發生了什麼事 。
so we'll start with the hippocampus , shown in yellow , which is the organ of memory .	我們先從黃色的海馬體開始 , 也就是記憶的器官 。
if you have damage there , like in alzheimer's , you can't remember things including where you parked your car .	如果你有損害 , 比如阿茲海默症 , 你就無法記住事物 , 包括你停車的地方 。
it's named after latin for " seahorse , " which it resembles .	它是用拉丁文命名為 「 海馬 」 , 它是相似的 。
and like the rest of the brain , it's made of neurons .	和其他的大腦一樣 , 它是由神經元組成的 。
so the human brain has about a hundred billion neurons in it .	人類的大腦大約有一千億個神經元 。
and the neurons communicate with each other by sending little pulses or spikes of electricity via connections to each other .	神經元會彼此溝通 , 藉由發送電脈衝 , 或透過連結 , 彼此溝通 。
the hippocampus is formed of two sheets of cells , which are very densely interconnected .	海馬體是由兩片細胞組成 , 非常密集的相互連結 。
and scientists have begun to understand how spatial memory works by recording from individual neurons in rats or mice while they forage or explore an environment looking for food .	科學家已經開始了解空間記憶如何運作 , 藉由記錄老鼠或老鼠的個別神經元 , 來記錄老鼠的記錄 , 或探索環境尋找食物 。
so we're going to imagine we're recording from a single neuron in the hippocampus of this rat here .	所以 , 我們要想像我們正在記錄老鼠的單一神經元 。
and when it fires a little spike of electricity , there's going to be a red dot and a click .	當它發電時 , 會有紅點和點擊 。
so what we see is that this neuron knows whenever the rat has gone into one particular place in its environment .	所以 , 我們看到這個神經元知道老鼠何時進入一個特定的環境中 。
and it signals to the rest of the brain by sending a little electrical spike .	它會藉由發送電脈衝訊號到大腦的其他部位 。
so we could show the firing rate of that neuron as a function of the animal's location .	所以 , 我們可以把神經元的激發率當作動物所在位置的功能 。
and if we record from lots of different neurons , we'll see that different neurons fire when the animal goes in different parts of its environment , like in this square box shown here .	如果我們從許多不同的神經元記錄下來 , 我們會看到不同的神經元發出訊號 , 當動物進入不同的環境時 , 比如這個正方形的盒子 。
so together they form a map for the rest of the brain , telling the brain continually , " where am i now within my environment ? "	所以他們一起組成大腦的地圖 , 不斷地告訴大腦: 「 我現在在哪裡 ? 」
place cells are also being recorded in humans .	位置細胞也被記錄在人類身上 。
so epilepsy patients sometimes need the electrical activity in their brain monitoring .	癲癇患者有時會需要腦部監控的電訊活動 。
and some of these patients played a video game where they drive around a small town .	有些病人在玩電玩遊戲 , 他們在小鎮裡開車 。
and place cells in their hippocampi would fire , become active , start sending electrical impulses whenever they drove through a particular location in that town .	海馬體中的細胞會被激發 , 活躍地開始發送電脈衝 , 只要他們開車穿過特定的小鎮 。
so how does a place cell know where the rat or person is within its environment ?	那麼 , 一個地方細胞怎麼知道老鼠或人的環境在哪裡 ?
well these two cells here show us that the boundaries of the environment are particularly important .	這兩個細胞告訴我們 , 環境的界線特別重要 。
so the one on the top likes to fire sort of midway between the walls of the box that their rat's in .	最上方的這個 , 喜歡在老鼠的牆壁間打火 。
and when you expand the box , the firing location expands .	當你擴展盒子時 , 激發的位置就會擴展 。
the one below likes to fire whenever there's a wall close by to the south .	下面的一面就是火災 , 每當它靠近南邊的一面牆 。
and if you put another wall inside the box , then the cell fires in both place wherever there's a wall to the south as the animal explores around in its box .	如果你把另一面牆放進盒子裡 , 細胞就會被激發 , 不論在哪裡 , 都有牆在南方 , 動物都在盒子裡探索 。
so this predicts that sensing the distances and directions of boundaries around you extended buildings and so on is particularly important for the hippocampus .	這預測了在你周遭的建築物間的距離和方向的距離 , 等等對海馬體而言是特別重要的 。
and indeed , on the inputs to the hippocampus , cells are found which project into the hippocampus , which do respond exactly to detecting boundaries or edges at particular distances and directions from the rat or mouse as it's exploring around .	的確 , 在海馬體的輸入值中 , 細胞會發現海馬體投射到海馬體中 , 它的確會完全反應出特定的距離和邊緣 , 特別是從老鼠或老鼠的方向來偵測 。
