so the cell on the left , you can see , it fires whenever the animal gets near to a wall or a boundary to the east , whether it's the edge or the wall of a square box or the circular wall of the circular box or even the drop at the edge of a table , which the animals are running around .	左邊的細胞 , 你可以看到 , 當動物靠近一面牆 , 或對東邊的邊緣 , 不管是方形的邊緣或圓形的牆壁 , 或是桌子的邊緣 , 那些動物跑來跑去 。
and the cell on the right there fires whenever there's a boundary to the south , whether it's the drop at the edge of the table or a wall or even the gap between two tables that are pulled apart .	右邊的細胞當南邊緣有限時會發出螢火 , 不論是桌邊的邊緣或牆壁 , 或甚至是兩張桌子之間的落差 。
so that's one way in which we think place cells determine where the animal is as it's exploring around .	所以 , 這就是我們認為位置細胞的一種方式 , 決定動物在何處探索 。
we can also test where we think objects are , like this goal flag , in simple environments or indeed , where your car would be .	我們也能測試我們認為物品的位置 , 像是這個目標旗 , 在簡單的環境中 , 或你的車子會在哪裡 。
so we can have people explore an environment and see the location they have to remember .	所以 , 我們可以讓人們探索一個環境 , 看到他們必須記住的地點 。
and then , if we put them back in the environment , generally they're quite good at putting a marker down where they thought that flag or their car was .	然後 , 如果我們把它們放回環境中 , 通常它們很擅長把標記放在他們認為旗子或車子的位置 。
but on some trials , we could change the shape and size of the environment like we did with the place cell .	但在某些試驗中 , 我們能改變環境的形狀和大小 , 像我們在安定細胞一樣 。
in that case , we can see how where they think the flag had been changes as a function of how you change the shape and size of the environment .	在這樣的情況下 , 我們可以看到他們認為旗幟在哪裡改變 , 作為改變環境的形狀和大小的功能 。
and what you see , for example , if the flag was where that cross was in a small square environment , and then if you ask people where it was , but you've made the environment bigger , where they think the flag had been stretches out in exactly the same way that the place cell firing stretched out .	舉例來說 , 如果你看到旗幟在一個小平方的環境中交叉 , 然後如果你問人們在哪裡 , 但你讓環境變大 , 他們認為旗幟已經延伸出去 , 和那個位置細胞爆發的方式完全一樣 。
it's as if you remember where the flag was by storing the pattern of firing across all of your place cells at that location , and then you can get back to that location by moving around so that you best match the current pattern of firing of your place cells with that stored pattern .	這就好像你記住旗幟的位置 , 藉由儲存你所有的位置細胞的模式 , 然後你就可以回到那個位置 , 這樣你就可以配合你所在位置細胞的發射模式 。
that guides you back to the location that you want to remember .	這引導你回到你想要記住的地點 。
but we also know where we are through movement .	但我們也知道我們在移動的哪裡 。
so if we take some outbound path perhaps we park and we wander off we know because our own movements , which we can integrate over this path roughly what the heading direction is to go back .	所以 , 如果我們採取一些不受限的路徑 , 或許我們停車 , 我們就會知道 , 因為我們自己的運動 , 我們可以整合這條路徑 , 大約是往前走的方向 。
and place cells also get this kind of path integration input from a kind of cell called a grid cell .	位置細胞也能從一種稱為網狀細胞的細胞中獲得這種整合 。
now grid cells are found , again , on the inputs to the hippocampus , and they're a bit like place cells .	現在 , 網格細胞在海馬體的輸入中發現 , 它們有點像是位置細胞 。
but now as the rat explores around , each individual cell fires in a whole array of different locations which are laid out across the environment in an amazingly regular triangular grid .	但當老鼠四處探索時 , 每個單獨的細胞會發出一系列不同的位置 , 在一個非常規則的三角形格子中 , 每個位置會發出一系列的能量 。
and if you record from several grid cells shown here in different colors each one has a gridlike firing pattern across the environment , and each cell's gridlike firing pattern is shifted slightly relative to the other cells .	如果你從幾個格子細胞中紀錄 , 顯示在不同的顏色中 , 每個細胞都有類似發射模式的格狀圖案 , 而每個細胞的發射圖案都和其他細胞有一點點相似 。
so the red one fires on this grid and the green one on this one and the blue on on this one .	紅色的則在這個格子上開火 , 綠色的就是這個 , 藍色在這個上面 。
so together , it's as if the rat can put a virtual grid of firing locations across its environment a bit like the latitude and longitude lines that you'd find on a map , but using triangles .	所以 , 同心協力 , 就好像老鼠可以在它的環境中放置虛擬的電網 , 有點像是地圖上所發現的緯度和長度線 , 而是用三角形 。
and as it moves around , the electrical activity can pass from one of these cells to the next cell to keep track of where it is , so that it can use its own movements to know where it is in its environment .	當它移動時 , 電活動可以從其中一個細胞傳遞到下一個細胞 , 來追蹤它的位置 , 這樣它就可以利用它自己的動作 , 知道它在其環境的位置 。
do people have grid cells ?	有人有網格細胞嗎 ?
well because all of the gridlike firing patterns have the same axes of symmetry , the same orientations of grid , shown in orange here , it means that the net activity of all of the grid cells in a particular part of the brain should change according to whether we're running along these six directions or running along one of the six directions in between .	由於所有像格狀的發射模式都有相同的對稱性 , 相同的網格 , 在橘色中顯示 , 網格細胞在某個特定的區域 , 應該根據六個方向來運作 , 或在六個方向進行跑 。
so we can put people in an mri scanner and have them do a little video game like the one i showed you and look for this signal .	所以我們可以把人放進磁共振掃描儀 , 讓他們做個小遊戲 , 像我給你們看的一樣 , 尋找這個信號 。
and indeed , you do see it in the human entorhinal cortex , which is the same part of the brain that you see grid cells in rats .	的確 , 你在人腦皮質中看到的 , 也就是你在老鼠身上看到的網格細胞的同一部分 。
so back to homer .	回到荷馬 。
he's probably remembering where his car was in terms of the distances and directions to extended buildings and boundaries around the location where he parked .	他可能還記得他車子的位置 , 距離和方向 , 以延伸建築和界線 , 延伸到他停車的地方 。
and that would be represented by the firing of boundarydetecting cells .	這會被邊界偵測細胞的激發所代表 。
he's also remembering the path he took out of the car park , which would be represented in the firing of grid cells .	他還記得他走出車站公園的路徑 , 可以用格子細胞來表示 。
now both of these kinds of cells can make the place cells fire .	兩種細胞都能使位置細胞激發 。
and he can return to the location where he parked by moving so as to find where it is that best matches the firing pattern of the place cells in his brain currently with the stored pattern where he parked his car .	他可以回溯到他停車的地方 , 這樣他就可以找到最符合他腦中的位置細胞的發射模式 , 目前他停車的地方 。
and that guides him back to that location irrespective of visual cues like whether his car's actually there .	這引導他回到那個不尊重視覺暗示的位置 , 像他的車到底是不是真的 。
maybe it's been towed .	也許它被綁住了 。
but he knows where it was , so he knows to go and get it .	但他知道它在哪裡 , 所以他知道要去抓它 。
so beyond spatial memory , if we look for this gridlike firing pattern throughout the whole brain , we see it in a whole series of locations which are always active when we do all kinds of autobiographical memory tasks , like remembering the last time you went to a wedding , for example .	所以 , 除了空間記憶以外 , 如果我們觀察整個大腦發射的這個格狀圖案 , 我們會在一系列的地點上看到 , 當我們在做各種自傳記憶任務時 , 會很活躍 , 比如 , 記住你上次去婚禮時 。
so it may be that the neural mechanisms for representing the space around us are also used for generating visual imagery so that we can recreate the spatial scene , at least , of the events that have happened to us when we want to imagine them .	所以 , 代表我們周遭空間的神經機制也被用來產生視覺影像 , 如此一來 , 我們就可以重新創造出空間場景 , 至少在我們想要想像的時候 , 發生在我們身上的事件 。
so if this was happening , your memories could start by place cells activating each other via these dense interconnections and then reactivating boundary cells to create the spatial structure of the scene around your viewpoint .	所以如果發生了這一切 , 你的記憶可以從細胞開始活化 , 透過這些密集的連接 , 然後重新啟動邊界細胞 , 來創造你觀點周圍的空間結構 。
and grid cells could move this viewpoint through that space .	網格細胞可以透過這個空間移動這個視野 。
another kind of cell , head direction cells , which i didn't mention yet , they fire like a compass according to which way you're facing .	我還沒提到另一種細胞 , 頭部導向細胞 , 根據你面臨的方向 , 它們會發出一道激素 。
they could define the viewing direction from which you want to generate an image for your visual imagery , so you can imagine what happened when you were at this wedding , for example .	他們可以定義你想要為你的視覺圖像產生的視覺方向 , 所以你可以想像當你在這個婚禮時發生了什麼事 。
so this is just one example of a new era really in cognitive neuroscience where we're beginning to understand psychological processes like how you remember or imagine or even think in terms of the actions of the billions of individual neurons that make up our brains .	這只是一個新時代的例子 , 在認知神經科學中 , 我們開始了解心理學的過程 , 例如你如何記住、想像 , 或甚至是以數十億個獨立的神經元為構成我們的大腦的行為來思考 。
thank you very much .	非常謝謝各位 。
imagine a global security driven by collaboration among agencies , government , the private sector and the public . that's not just the distant hope of opensource fans , it's the vision of james stavridis , the supreme commander of nato , who shares vivid moments from recent military history to explain why security of the future should be built with bridges rather than walls .	想像一下 , 全球安全是由機構、政府、私營機構所驅動的 , 和公眾所驅動的 。 這不僅僅是開放資源的粉絲的遠端希望 , 它是詹姆士史蒂夫里迪迪迪斯的最高指揮官 , 他分享了來自近期的軍事史 , 來解釋未來的安全性 , 而不是牆 。
collaboration , global issues , opensource , peace , politics , social media , violence , war	合作、全球議題、開源、和平、政治、社群媒體、暴力、戰爭、戰爭 。
james stavridis: how nato's supreme commander thinks about global security	詹姆士•斯特維里迪斯:nato的最高指揮官如何看待全球安全問題 。
i'm gonna talk a little bit about opensource security , because we've got to get better at security in this 21st century .	我打算談開放源的安全性 , 因為在21世紀 , 我們必須更加擅長安全 。
let me start by saying , let's look back to the 20th century , and kind of get a sense of how that style of security worked for us .	讓我開始說 , 讓我們回顧二十世紀 , 了解這對我們來說是如何運作的 。
this is verdun , a battlefield in france just north of the nato headquarters in belgium .	這是verdun , 一位在法國北部的戰場 , 位在比利時總部 。
at verdun , in 1916 , over a 300day period , 700 , 000 people were killed , so about 2 , 000 a day .	1916年 , 在verdun , 超過三百天的時期 , 有七十萬人被殺 , 所以每天大約兩千人死亡 。
if you roll it forward 20thcentury security into the second world war , you see the battle of stalingrad , 300 days , 2 million people killed .	如果你向前推行20世紀的安全 , 進入第二次世界大戰 , 你會看到三百天的戰役 , 兩百萬人死亡 。
we go into the cold war , and we continue to try and build walls .	我們進入冷戰 , 我們繼續嘗試建造牆 。
we go from the trench warfare of the first world war to the maginot line of the second world war , and then we go into the cold war , the iron curtain , the berlin wall .	我們從第一場世界大戰的戰場 , 到第二次世界大戰的馬基線 , 然後我們進入冷戰、鐵幕、柏林牆 。
my thesis for us today is , instead of building walls to create security , we need to build bridges .	我今天的論點是 , 與其建造牆來創造安全 , 我們需要建造橋樑 。
this is a famous bridge in europe .	這是歐洲的一座有名橋 。
it's the bridge over the drina river , the subject of a novel by ivo andrić , and it talks about how , in that very troubled part of europe and the balkans , over time there's been enormous building of walls .	這座橋是draina河流的橋樑 , 由ivoandrics的小說主題 , 它談的是歐洲和巴爾幹半島的一部分 , 長久以來 , 圍牆都是巨大的 。
more recently , in the last decade , we begin to see these communities start , hesitatingly , to come together .	更近期 , 在過去十年 , 我們開始看到這些社區開始猶豫地 , 聚集在一起 。
i would argue , again , opensource security is about connecting the international , the interagency , the privatepublic , and lashing it together with strategic communication , largely in social networks .	我認為 , 同樣的 , 開放式安全是關於將國際、國際、私人之間的連結起來 , 並將它和策略性的溝通結合在一起 , 主要是在社交網路上 。
so let me talk a little bit about why we need to do that , because our global commons is under attack in a variety of ways , and none of the sources of threat to the global commons will be solved by building walls .	讓我來談談為什麼我們需要這麼做 , 因為我們的全球公有物以各種方式受到攻擊 , 而沒有任何威脅到全球公有物的來源 , 都不會由建造牆來解決 。
now , i'm a sailor , obviously .	很顯然 , 我是水手 。
this is a ship , a liner , clipping through the indian ocean .	這是一艘船 , 一條線 , 穿過印度洋 。
what's wrong with this picture ?	這張照片有什麼問題 ?
it's got concertina wire along the sides of it .	它的旁邊有certina電線 。
that's to prevent pirates from attacking it .	這是為了防止海盜攻擊它 。
piracy is a very active threat today around the world . this is in the indian ocean .	piracy今天是全世界非常積極的威脅 。 這是在印度洋 。
piracy is also very active in the strait of malacca .	piracy也非常活躍在馬拉卡的位置 。
it's active in the gulf of guinea .	它在幾內亞灣活躍 。
we see it in the caribbean .	我們在加勒比海看到它 。
it's a $10billionayear discontinuity in the global transport system .	它是全球運輸系統的一千億年不連續性 。
last year , at this time , there were 20 vessels , 500 mariners held hostage .	去年 , 當時有20艘船 , 500名遊客舉行 。
this is an attack on the global commons .	這是對全球公有物的攻擊 。
we need to think about how to address it .	我們需要考慮如何處理它 。
let's shift to a different kind of sea , the cyber sea .	咱們來轉移到另一種海洋 , 網路大海 。
here are photographs of two young men .	這裡有兩個年輕人的照片 。
at the moment , they're incarcerated .	目前 , 他們被監禁了 。
they conducted a credit card fraud that netted them over 10 billion dollars .	他們做了一個信用卡詐欺 , 將他們淨化超過一百億美金 。
this is part of cybercrime which is a $2trillionayear discontinuity in the global economy .	這是網路犯罪的一部分 , 它是全球經濟中2兆美金的損失 。
two trillion a year .	一年兩兆美元 。
that's just under the gdp of great britain .	這只是英國的國內生產總值 。
so this cyber sea , which we know endlessly is the fundamental piece of radical openness , is very much under threat as well .	所以 , 我們所知的網路大海是極端開放的基本一部分 , 也受到威脅 。
another thing i worry about in the global commons is the threat posed by trafficking , by the movement of narcotics , opium , here coming out of afghanistan through europe over to the united states .	我擔心全球公有物的另一件事 , 就是人口販賣的威脅 , 是因為毒品、鴉片、阿富汗從阿富汗到美國 。
we worry about cocaine coming from the andean ridge north .	我們擔心從安第斯山脊到北部的古柯鹼 。
we worry about the movement of illegal weapons and trafficking . above all , perhaps , we worry about human trafficking , and the awful cost of it .	我們擔心非法武器和人口販賣運動 。 最重要的是 , 我們擔心人口販賣 , 以及它的花費 。
trafficking moves largely at sea but in other parts of the global commons .	人口販賣主要在海上移動 , 但在全球公有物的其他地方 。
this is a photograph , and i wish i could tell you that this is a very hightech piece of us navy gear that we're using to stop the trafficking .	這是一張照片 , 我希望我能告訴你們這是一張非常高科技的海軍裝備 , 我們用它來阻止人口販賣 。
the bad news is , this is a semisubmersible run by drug cartels .	壞消息是 , 這是販毒集團所經營的半潛水器 。
it was built in the jungles of south america .	它是在南美叢林建造的 。
we caught it with that lowtech raft — — and it was carrying six tons of cocaine .	我們用那低科技的升降機抓住了它 , 帶著六噸的古柯鹼 。
crew of four . sophisticated communications sweep .	船員四個 , 精密的溝通 。
this kind of trafficking , in narcotics , in humans , in weapons , god forbid , in weapons of mass destruction , is part of the threat to the global commons .	這種販賣 , 在毒癮中 , 在人類身上 , 在武器中 , 上帝禁止在大規模毀滅性的武器中 , 是全球公有物的威脅之一 。
and let's pull it together in afghanistan today .	讓我們在阿富汗總結一下 。
this is a field of poppies in afghanistan .	這是阿富汗的小馬田 。
eighty to 90 percent of the world's poppy , opium and heroin , comes out of afghanistan .	全世界百分之八十到九十的寶寶、鴉片和海洛因都來自阿富汗 。
we also see there , of course , terrorism .	當然 , 我們也看到了恐怖主義 。
this is where al qaeda is staged from .	這是基地組織的起源 。
we also see a very strong insurgency embedded there .	我們也看到一個非常強的緊急狀況 。
so this terrorism concern is also part of the global commons , and what we must address .	所以 , 這種恐怖主義的擔憂也是全球公有物的一部分 , 我們必須解決的 。
so here we are , 21st century .	所以 , 我們在這裡 , 21世紀 。
we know our 20thcentury tools are not going to work .	我們知道20世紀的工具無法運作 。
what should we do ?	我們該怎麼做 ?
i would argue that we will not deliver security solely from the barrel of a gun .	我認為我們不會只從槍的桶子裡提供安全 。
we will not deliver security solely from the barrel of a gun .	我們不會只從槍的桶子裡提供安全 。
we will need the application of military force .	我們需要軍事力量的應用 。
when we do it , we must do it well , and competently .	當我們這麼做時 , 我們必須做得很好 , 並且更有力 。
but my thesis is , opensource security is about international , interagency , privatepublic connection pulled together by this idea of strategic communication on the internet .	但我的論點是 , 開放式安全是關於國際、國際、私人公開的聯繫 , 由網路上策略通訊的概念所組成 。
let me give you a couple of examples of how this works in a positive way .	讓我舉幾個例子說明這如何以正面的方式運作 。
this is afghanistan . these are afghan soldiers .	這是阿富汗 。 這些是阿富汗的士兵 。
they are all holding books .	他們都拿著書 。
you should say , " that's odd . i thought i read that this demographic , young men and women in their 20s and 30s , is largely illiterate in afghanistan . "	你應該說: 「 這很奇怪 。 我想我讀到這個人口統計 , 二十三十幾歲的年輕男女 , 大部分都是在阿富汗的文盲 。 」
you would be correct .	你是對的 。
eightyfive percent cannot read when they enter the security forces of afghanistan .	85%的人無法讀取阿富汗的安全力量 。
why ? because the taliban withheld education during the period of time in which these men and women would have learned to read .	為什麼 ? 因為塔利班在這些男人和女人都學會閱讀 。
so the question is , so , why are they all standing there holding books ?	所以問題是 , 為什麼他們都站在那裡拿著書 ?
the answer is , we are teaching them to read in literacy courses by nato in partnership with private sector entities , in partnership with development agencies .	答案是 , 我們教導他們閱讀讀讀文學課程 , 透過納托和私營機構合作 , 與發展機構合作 。
we've taught well over 200 , 000 afghan security forces to read and write at a basic level .	我們已經教導超過二十萬阿富汗的安全力量 , 以基本的角度閱讀和寫 。
when you can read and write in afghanistan , you will typically put a pen in your pocket .	當你在阿富汗讀和寫字時 , 你通常會把一支筆放在口袋裡 。
at the ceremonies , when these young men and women graduate , they take that pen with great pride , and put it in their pocket .	在儀式中 , 當這些年輕人和女生畢業時 , 他們很驕傲地拿著這筆筆筆 , 把它放在口袋裡 。
this is bringing together international — there are 50 nations involved in this mission — interagency — these development agencies — and privatepublic , to take on this kind of security .	這使得國際間有50個國家涉及這項任務 , 這些發展機構 , 以及私人公開 , 來採取這種安全 。
now , we are also teaching them combat skills , of course , but i would argue , opensource security means connecting in ways that create longer lasting security effect .	當然 , 我們也在教導他們對抗技能 , 但我認為 , 開放式安全意味著連結 , 創造更長的安全效應 。
this is a us navy warship .	這是美國海軍戰艦 。
it's called the comfort .	它叫做舒適 。
there's a sister ship called the mercy .	有個姐妹船叫做 「 慈悲 」 。
they are hospital ships .	他們是醫院的船 。
this one , the comfort , operates throughout the caribbean and the coast of south america conducting patient treatments .	這個 , 舒適的 , 在加勒比海和南美洲的海岸進行病人治療 。
on a typical cruise , they'll do 400 , 000 patient treatments .	通常他們會做四十萬個病人治療 。
it is crewed not strictly by military but by a combination of humanitarian organizations: operation hope , project smile .	軍隊不是嚴格的 , 而是人道主義組織的結合: 「 希望 」 , 計畫微笑 。
other organizations send volunteers .	其他組織發送志願者 。
interagency physicians come out .	國際醫師來了 。
they're all part of this .	全部都是這樣 。
to give you one example of the impact this can have , this little boy , eight years old , walked with his mother two days to come to the eye clinic put on by the comfort .	舉個例子 , 這個小男孩 , 8歲 , 帶著他的母親走進舒適圈的眼科診所 。
when he was fitted , over his extremely myopic eyes , he suddenly looked up and said , " mama , veo el mundo . "	當他被配合時 , 他的眼睛突然抬起頭 , 說: 「 老媽 , veoelmundo 。 」
" mom , i see the world . "	「 媽 , 我看見這個世界 。 」
multiply this by 400 , 000 patient treatments , this privatepublic collaboration with security forces , and you begin to see the power of creating security in a very different way .	將這方法乘以四十萬名病人治療 , 這種私人和安全合作的私人合作 , 你開始以截然不同的角度來看創造安全的力量 。
here you see baseball players .	這是棒球選手 。
can you pick out the two us army soldiers in this photograph ?	你能否從這張照片中挑出兩位美國軍人士 ?
they are the two young men on either side of these young boys . this is part of a series of baseball clinics , where we have explored collaboration between major league baseball , the department of state , who sets up the diplomatic piece of this , military baseball players , who are real soldiers with real skills but participate in this mission , and they put on clinics throughout latin america and the caribbean , in honduras , in nicaragua , in all of the central american and caribbean nations where baseball is so popular , and it creates security .	他們是這些男孩兩邊的兩個年輕人 。 這是一系列棒球診所的一員 , 我們在加勒比大聯盟 , 國家的部門 , 他們設立了外交棒球隊 , 和真正的技能合作 , 他們在加勒比美洲和加勒比海的診所中 , 穿過拉丁美洲和加勒比海岸 , 開了全美各國的巴拉美洲 , 並且在加勒比美洲 , 創造了貧民區 。
it shows role models to young men and women about fitness and about life that i would argue help create security for us .	它展現了年輕男性和女性的角色 , 關於健身和生活的重要性 , 讓我主張 , 協助為我們創造安全 。
another aspect of this partnership is in disaster relief .	這種合作關係的另一個面向是災難救援 。
this is a us air force helicopter participating after the tsunami in 2004 which killed 250 , 000 people .	這是美國空軍直升機在2004年通過海嘯殺死了25萬人
in each of these major disasters — the tsunami in 2004 , 250 , 000 dead , the kashmiri earthquake in pakistan , 2005 , 85 , 000 dead , the haitian earthquake , about 300 , 000 dead , more recently the awful earthquaketsunami combination which struck japan and its nuclear industry — in all of these instances , we see partnerships between international actors , interagency , privatepublic working with security forces to respond to this kind of natural disaster .	在每一次重大災難中海嘯在2004年 , 死亡250 , 000人 , 巴基斯坦的kamiri地震 , 2005年 , 8萬5千人死亡 , 海地地震近30萬人 , 更近期 , 震撼日本和核子產業 , 在所有這些例子中 , 我們都看到國際行業、國際行業、國際行業、國際行業、國際間的合作夥伴關係 , 和這種自然災害的合作關係 。
so these are examples of this idea of opensource security .	這些是開放式安全的例子 。
we tie it together , increasingly , by doing things like this .	我們逐漸把它們綁在一起 , 透過這樣的做法 , 把它們綁在一起 。
now , you're looking at this thinking , " ah , admiral , these must be sea lanes of communication , or these might be fiber optic cables . "	現在你看到的是這個想法: 「 啊 , 阿 , 阿 , 這些必須是溝通的海道 , 或者這些可能是光纖電纜 。 」
no . this is a graphic of the world according to twitter .	不 , 這是根據推特的圖表 。
purple are tweets . green are geolocation .	紫色是推特綠色是地理分配
white is the synthesis .	白色是合成 。
it's a perfect evocation of that great population survey , the six largest nations in the world in descending order: china , india , facebook , the united states , twitter and indonesia .	這是一項很棒的民眾調查 , 全世界的六個國家 , 以下降順序:中國、印度、印度、facebook、美國、推特和印尼 。
why do we want to get in these nets ?	為什麼我們要去這些蚊帳呢 ?
why do we want to be involved ?	為什麼我們想要參與 ?
we talked earlier about the arab spring , and the power of all this .	我們先前談到阿拉伯之春 , 以及這一切的力量 。
i'll give you another example , and it's how you move this message .	我會再舉另一個例子 , 就是你如何移動這個訊息 。
i gave a talk like this in london a while back about this point . i said , as i say to all of you , i'm on facebook . friend me .	我在倫敦做過這樣的演講 。 我說 , 就如同我對你們說的 , 我在facebook , 朋友我 。
got a little laugh from the audience .	聽到觀眾的笑聲 。
there was an article which was run by ap , on the wire .	有一篇文章是阿普在電線上運行的 。
got picked up in two places in the world: finland and indonesia .	被帶到世界上兩個地方:芬蘭和印尼 。
the headline was: nato admiral needs friends .	標題是:納托需要朋友 。
and the story was a catalyst , and the next morning i had hundreds of facebook friend requests from indonesians and finns , mostly saying , " admiral , we heard you need a friend , and oh , by the way , what is nato ? "	故事是催化劑 , 第二天早上 , 我有數百名臉書朋友請求來自印尼人和芬蘭人 , 大多都說: 「 邁進份子 , 我們聽說你需要朋友 , 喔 , 順便說一下 , nato是什麼 ? 」
yeah , we laugh , but this is how we move the message , and moving that message is how we connect international , interagency , privatepublic , and these social nets to help create security .	沒錯 , 我們笑了 , 但這就是我們傳遞訊息的方式 , 傳遞訊息就是我們如何連結國際、國際、私人公開 , 而這些社交網路協助創造安全 。
now , let me hit a somber note .	現在 , 讓我明白一件事 。
this is a photograph of a brave british soldier .	這是一個勇敢的英國士兵的照片 。
he's in the scots guards .	他在蘇格蘭警衛隊 。
he's standing the watch in helmand , in southern afghanistan .	他站在阿富汗南方的helmand 。
i put him here to remind us , i would not want anyone to leave the room thinking that we do not need capable , competent militaries who can create real military effect .	我把他放在這裡提醒我們 , 我不會讓任何人離開房間 , 認為我們不需要有能力、有能力的軍隊 , 可以創造真正的軍事效應 。
that is the core of who we are and what we do , and we do it to protect freedom , freedom of speech , all the things we treasure in our societies .	這就是我們所做的事的核心 , 我們要保護自由、言論自由 , 我們在我們的社會中珍視的一切 。
but , you know , life is not an onandoff switch .	但 , 你知道 , 生命不是開關 。
you don't have to have a military that is either in hard combat or is in the barracks .	你不需要有軍隊 , 不管是戰鬥 , 或在戰場上 。
i would argue life is a rheostat .	我會說生命是圓形的 。
you have to dial it in , and as i think about how we create security in this 21st century , there will be times when we will apply hard power in true war and crisis , but there will be many instances , as we've talked about today , where our militaries can be part of creating 21stcentury security , international , interagency , privatepublic , connected with competent communication .	你必須將它導入 , 如同我所想的 , 我們在21世紀創造安全 , 將會有時 , 我們會用真實戰爭和危機來應用真正的力量 , 但 , 如同我們今天所談的 , 我們的軍隊可以成為創造21世紀安全的一部分 , 國際、國際間、私人、私人公開 , 與能力的溝通連結 。
i would close by saying that we heard earlier today about wikipedia . i use wikipedia all the time to look up facts , and as all of you appreciate , wikipedia is not created by 12 brilliant people locked in a room writing articles .	最後 , 我會說 , 我們今天聽說我們有關維基百科的知識 。 我常常常會用維基百科搜尋事實 , 就像你們所欣賞的一樣 , 維基百科並不是由12個出色的人 , 關在房間寫文章中 。
wikipedia , every day , is tens of thousands of people inputting information , and every day millions of people withdrawing that information .	維基百科 , 每天有數萬人在輸入資訊 , 每天有數百萬人在編寫這些資訊 。
it's a perfect image for the fundamental point that no one of us is as smart as all of us thinking together .	對基本的意義來說 , 沒有人和所有人一起思考都一樣聰明 。
no one person , no one alliance , no one nation , no one of us is as smart as all of us thinking together .	沒有一個人 , 沒有一個聯盟 , 沒有一個國家 , 沒有一個像我們所有人一起思考一樣聰明 。
the vision statement of wikipedia is very simple: a world in which every human being can freely share in the sum of all knowledge .	維基百科的宣言很簡單:一個每個人都能自由地分享所有知識的世界 。
my thesis for you is that by combining international , interagency , privatepublic , strategic communication , together , in this 21st century , we can create the sum of all security .	我的論點是 , 把國際、跨國、私人、私人、策略性的溝通結合在一起 , 在21世紀 , 我們就能創造出所有安全的總結 。
thank you very much . thank you . thank you .	非常謝謝各位 。 謝謝 。
